when you say she's a programmer , she did do some , but the real thing is to have said the future is going to be much , much more than this .	當你說她是程式設計師 , 她的確做了一些 , 但真正重要的是要說未來會是非常非常重要的事 。
now , a hundred years later , this guy comes along , alan turing , and in 1936 , and invents the computer all over again .	一百年後 , 這個人出現了alanturing在1936年 , 發明了電腦之後
now , of course , babbage's machine was entirely mechanical .	當然 , babbage的機器是完全機械化的
turing's machine was entirely theoretical .	turing的機器完全理論化了 。
both of these guys were coming from a mathematical perspective , but turing told us something very important .	這兩位都是來自數學的觀點 , 但turing告訴我們非常重要的一點 。
he laid down the mathematical foundations for computer science , and said , " it doesn't matter how you make a computer . "	他奠定了計算機科學的數學基礎 , 說: 「 不論你怎麼製造電腦 。 」
it doesn't matter if your computer's mechanical , like babbage's was , or electronic , like computers are today , or perhaps in the future , cells , or , again , mechanical again , once we get into nanotechnology .	不管你的電腦是機械的 , 像babbage的原始電腦 , 或是電子的 , 像現今的電腦 , 或未來的電腦 , 細胞的 , 又或者 , 再次的 , 機械的 , 一旦我們進入了奈米科技 。
we could go back to babbage's machine and just make it tiny . all those things are computers .	我們可以回到babbage的機器 , 讓它變得很小 。 這些東西都是電腦 。
there is in a sense a computing essence .	計算本質上是存在的 。
this is called the church–turing thesis .	這稱為 「 教堂培養論 」 。
and so suddenly , you get this link where you say this thing babbage had built really was a computer .	突然間 , 你會看到一個聯繫 , 你說babbage建造的這個東西真的是一台電腦 。
in fact , it was capable of doing everything we do today with computers , only really slowly .	事實上 , 它能夠做到我們現今用電腦做的所有事 , 只是真的很慢 。
to give you an idea of how slowly , it had about 1k of memory .	為了讓你們知道有多慢 , 大約1k的記憶體有多慢 。
it used punch cards , which were being fed in , and it ran about 10 , 000 times slower the first zx81 .	它使用打孔卡 , 也就是進食 , 它的速度比第一台zx81要慢一萬倍 。
it did have a ram pack .	它的確有一個拉姆包 。
you could add on a lot of extra memory if you wanted to .	如果你想要的話 , 你可以增加大量的記憶力 。
so , where does that bring us today ?	所以 , 今天這會帶我們到哪裡 ?
so there are plans .	所以有計畫 。
over in swindon , the science museum archives , there are hundreds of plans and thousands of pages of notes written by charles babbage about this analytical engine .	在swindon科學博物館的檔案中有上百個計劃和上千頁文章是charlesbabbage寫的關於這個分析引擎的筆記
one of those is a set of plans that we call plan 28 , and that is also the name of a charity that i started with doron swade , who was the curator of computing at the science museum , and also the person who drove the project to build a difference engine , and our plan is to build it .	其中一個計畫是我們稱作計劃28這也是我和doronswade所創立的一個慈善機構的名字他是科學博物館的管理者也是主導了這個計劃的人他負責建造一個不同的引擎我們的計劃就是建造它
here in south kensington , we will build the analytical engine .	在肯辛頓南部 , 我們會建造分析引擎 。
the project has a number of parts to it .	這個專案有好幾個部分 。
one was the scanning of babbage's archive .	其中之一是掃描babbage的檔案
that's been done . the second is now the study of all of those plans to determine what to build .	已經完成了 。 第二個是研究所有計劃的相關研究 , 來決定要建造什麼 。
the third part is a computer simulation of that machine , and the last part is to physically build it at the science museum .	第三部分是關於那機器的電腦模擬 , 最後一部分是將它做成在科學博物館 。
when it's built , you'll finally be able to understand how a computer works , because rather than having a tiny chip in front of you , you've got to look at this humongous thing and say , " ah , i see the memory operating , i see the cpu operating , i hear it operating . i probably smell it operating . "	當它建完後 , 你終於能夠理解電腦是如何運作的 , 因為與其在你面前建一個微小的晶片 , 你必須看著這個巨大的東西然後說: 「 啊 , 我看到記憶體在運作 , cpu在運作 , 我聽見它運作的聲響 。 我大概在聞到它的味道 。 」
but in between that we're going to do a simulation .	但在那之間我們要做一個模擬 。
babbage himself wrote , he said , as soon as the analytical engine exists , it will surely guide the future course of science .	babbage自己寫的 , 他說 , 當分析引擎存在的時候 , 它一定會引導未來的科學發展 。
of course , he never built it , because he was always fiddling with new plans , but when it did get built , of course , in the 1940s , everything changed .	當然 , 他從來沒有成功做出來 , 因為他總是在和新計畫保持距離 , 但當它真的被建成的時候 , 當然 , 在1940年代 , 一切都改變了 。
now , i'll just give you a little taste of what it looks like in motion with a video which shows just one part of the cpu mechanism working .	現在 , 我讓各位稍微體驗一下它的樣子 , 用一段影片顯示出局部的cpu機制運作的一部分 。
so this is just three sets of cogs , and it's going to add . this is the adding mechanism in action , so you imagine this gigantic machine .	所以 , 這只是三組齒輪 , 它會加上去 。 這是加上行動的機制 , 所以你想像這個巨大的機器 。
so , give me five years .	所以 , 給我五年 。
before the 2030s happen , we'll have it .	在2030年代以前 , 我們會
thank you very much .	謝謝大家 。
in this imagefilled talk , yann arthusbertrand displays his three most recent projects on humanity and our habitat stunning aerial photographs in his series " the earth from above , " personal interviews from around the globe featured in his web project " 6 billion others , " and his soontobereleased movie , " home , " which documents human impact on the environment through breathtaking video .	在這個充滿著影像的演講中 , 尤恩•阿修斯伯特蘭展示了他最近的三個計畫 , 關於人類和棲息地 , 令人震驚的空拍照片 , 在他的系列《地球來自地球》中 , 來自全球各地的個人訪談 , 在他的網路專案《六十億人》中 , 他很快就推出了 , 《家園》 , 這部影片記錄了人類對於環境的影響 , 透過一張讓人震驚的影片 。
art , climate change , environment , film , future , humanity , media , photography	藝術、氣候變化、環境、電影、未來、人類、媒體、攝影 。
yann arthusbertrand captures fragile earth in wideangle	yannarth-husbertrand以寬廣角度捕捉地球的脆弱性 。
i have a big impact on the planet to travel here by plane .	我對地球有很大的影響 , 可以靠飛機來到這裡 。
i emitted , in the atmosphere , nine tons of co2 ; that is the weight of two elephants .	我在大氣中排放了九噸的二氧化碳那是兩隻大象的重量 。
i came here to speak about ecology , and i emitted as much co2 as a frenchman in one year .	我來這裡是為了談談生態學 , 我在一年內排放的二氧化碳量就和法國人一樣多 。
so what do i have to do ?	那我得做什麼呢 ?
i have to kill a frenchman when i come back at home ?	我必須在家裡殺一個法國人 ?
i have to do my carbon offset in another way , like i do every time .	我必須用另一種方式來抵銷我的碳 , 就像我每次做的一樣 。
in fact my work is to show our impact on our planet .	事實上 , 我的作品是要展示我們對地球的影響 。
i'm going to show you some examples of the last pictures i've done in the last year .	我要給你們看一些例子 , 關於我過去一年拍攝的最後幾張照片 。

in alberta people work nonstop , 24 hours by seven to extract as much oil as they can .	在亞伯達省的人們不停工作24小時7小時盡可能的抽取石油

but we use three times more oil than we find every year .	但我們每年使用的石油量是發現的三倍 。

coral reef in new caledonia .	新喀里多尼亞州的珊瑚礁

we all share the same need for the earth's gifts the same wish to rise above ourselves , and become better .	我們都分享同樣的需求 , 希望能讓地球的禮物超越我們自己 , 變得更好 。
and yet we carry on raising walls to keep us apart .	然而 , 我們還是繼續築起牆來保持距離 。

our energy sources are not sustainable .	我們的能源來源是不永續的 。
the climate is changing .	氣候正在變遷 。
we are endangering ourselves .	我們正在危害自己 。

dna , biotech , health care , science , technology	dna、生物科技、醫療保健、科學、技術、
richard resnick: welcome to the genomic revolution	理查•雷斯尼克:歡迎來到基因革命時代 。
ladies and gentlemen , i present to you the human genome .	各位先生女士 , 我給各位看人類基因組 。
chromosome one , top left .	染色體一 , 左上角
bottom right are the sex chromosomes .	右下方的是性染色體 。
women have two copies of that big x chromosome ; men have the x and , of course , that small copy of the y .	女性有兩份大的x染色體 ; 男性則有x染色體 , 當然還有小小的y染色體 。
sorry boys , but it's just a tiny little thing that makes you different .	對不起男孩 , 但這只是件小事讓你與眾不同
so if you zoom in on this genome , then what you see , of course , is this double helix structure the code of life spelled out with these four biochemical letters , or we call them bases , right: a , c , g and t .	如果你放大這個基因組的圖片 , 你就會看到這個雙螺旋結構--生命的編碼有這四個生化字母 , 我們稱之為鹼基 , 對 , 對 , 就是a , c , g和t 。
how many are there in the human genome ? three billion .	人類基因組中有多少人 ? 30億人 。
is that a big number ?	這是一個很大的數字嗎 ?
well , everybody can throw around big numbers .	嗯 , 每個人都可以丟出很大的數字 。
but in fact , if i were to place one base on each pixel of this 1280 by 800 resolution screen , we would need 3 , 000 screens to take a look at the genome .	但事實上 , 如果我把這1280像素的每一個像素上放上一個基對 , 到800個解析度的螢幕上 , 我們就需要3000個螢幕來檢視基因組 。
so it's really quite big .	所以它真的是相當大 。
and perhaps because of its size , a group of people all , by the way , with y chromosomes decided they would want to sequence it .	也許是因為它的大小 , 順便一提 , 有一群y染色體的人 , 決定想要為它排序 。
and so 15 years , actually , and about four billion dollars later , the genome was sequenced and published .	實際上 , 15年後 , 約40億美元的基因組被定序並出版 。
in 2003 , the final version was published , and they keep working on it .	2003年 , 最後一版發行了 , 他們繼續致力於此 。
that was all done on a machine that looks like this .	都是在這樣的機器上完成的 。
it costs about a dollar for each base a very slow way of doing it .	每個鹼基的成本大約是一美元──這是非常慢的一種做法 。
well folks , i'm here to tell you that the world has completely changed and none of you know about it .	各位 , 我來這裡告訴各位 , 這個世界已經完全改變了 , 各位都不知道 。
so now what we do is we take a genome , we make maybe 50 copies of it , we cut all those copies up into little 50base reads , and then we sequence them , massively parallel .	現在我們做的是 , 拿出一個基因組 , 把它複製50份 , 我們把這些複本都切成小小的50個基對 , 然後大量平行排序 。
and then we bring that into software , and we reassemble it and we tell you what the story is .	然後我們把這套軟體融入其中 , 再重新組合 , 告訴大家故事是什麼 。
and so just to give you a picture of what this looks like , the human genome project: 3 gigabases , right .	為了讓大家看看這個圖像 , 人類基因組計畫:3gabes , 對 。
one run on one of these machines: 200 gigabases in a week .	其中一台機器:一個禮拜內跑200gabass 。
and that 200 is going to change to 600 this summer , and there's no sign of this pace slowing .	今年夏天 , 這兩百年將會改變到6000年 , 沒有任何跡象顯示 , 這種步調會慢下來 。
so the price of a base , to sequence a base , has fallen 100 million times .	所以一個基對排序的價格已經下跌一億倍 。
that's the equivalent of you filling up your car with gas in 1998 , waiting until 2011 , and now you can drive to jupiter and back twice .	這就等於你在1998年給汽車加滿一次油的錢 , 等到2011年 , 現在你可以開到木星 , 開兩次車回來 。
world population , pc placements , the archive of all the medical literature , moore's law , the old way of sequencing , and here's all the new stuff .	世界人口、pc地點、檔案庫 , 所有醫學文獻、摩爾定律、以舊方式排序的方式 , 這裡都是新東西 。
guys , this is a log scale ; you don't typically see lines that go up like that .	各位 , 這是對數刻度 , 你們通常不會看到那樣的線上升 。
so the worldwide capacity to sequence human genomes is something like 50 , 000 to 100 , 000 human genomes this year .	全世界用於人類基因組測序的能力大約在今年五萬到十萬個人類基因組 。
and we know this based on the machines that are being placed .	我們知道這個基於被放置的機器 。
this is expected to double , triple or maybe quadruple year over year for the foreseeable future .	預計在可預見的未來中 , 每年都會增加一倍、三倍、甚至四倍 。
in fact , there's one lab in particular that represents 20 percent of all that capacity .	事實上 , 有一間實驗室特別代表20%的產能 。
it's called the beijing genomics institute .	叫做北京基因研究所 。
the chinese are absolutely winning this race to the new moon , by the way .	順帶一提 , 中國人絕對是贏了這場比賽給新月球看的比賽 。
what does this mean for medicine ?	這對醫學有何意義 ?
so a woman is age 37 .	所以一個女人37歲 ,
she presents with stage 2 estrogen receptorpositive breast cancer .	她呈現的是第二期雌激素受體陽性乳腺癌 。
she is treated with surgery , chemotherapy and radiation .	她接受了手術 , 化療和放射治療 。
two years later , she comes back with stage three c ovarian cancer .	兩年後她又回來了第三期 「 卵巢癌 」
unfortunately , treated again with surgery and chemotherapy .	不幸的是 , 再次接受手術和化療 ,
she comes back three years later at age 42 with more ovarian cancer , more chemotherapy .	三年後她42歲生的卵巢癌 , 接受更多的化療 。
six months later , she comes back with acute myeloid leukemia .	六個月後 , 她回來時患上了急性骨髓性白血病 。
she goes into respiratory failure and dies eight days later .	她進入呼吸道衰竭並在八天後死去 。
so first , the way in which this woman was treated , in as little as 10 years , will look like bloodletting .	首先 , 這位女性接受治療的方式 , 只要不到十年 , 她們就會看起來像在流血 。
and it's because of people like my colleague , rick wilson , at the genome institute at washington university , who decided to take a look at this woman postmortem .	也是因為有像我同事rickwilson在華盛頓大學的基因研究所決定要看一下這個婦女的後遺症
and he sequenced , he took skin cells , healthy skin , and cancerous bone marrow , and he sequenced the whole genomes of both of them in a couple of weeks , no big deal .	然後他做定序 , 取出皮膚細胞 , 健康的皮膚 , 和癌骨髓 , 將它們兩者的基因組排序在幾週後 , 沒什麼大不了的 。
and then he compared those two genomes in software , and what he found , among other things , was a deletion , a 2 , 000base deletion across three billion bases in a particular gene called tp53 .	然後他把這兩組基因組的比對在軟體中 , 他發現在其他事物中 , 是種刪除 , 是兩千個鹼基在一個特定的基因上 , 一個叫做tp53的基因上 。
if you have this deleterious mutation in this gene , you're 90 percent likely to get cancer in your life .	如果你在這個基因上有這種嚇人的突變 , 你一生中有90%的可能性會罹患癌症 。
so unfortunately , this doesn't help this woman , but it does have severe , profound if you will , implications to her family .	所以 , 不幸的是 , 這對這位女性並沒有幫助 , 但這對她的家庭也確實有嚴重、深刻的影響 。
i mean , if they have the same mutation , and they get this genetic test , and they understand it , then they can go and get regular screens , and they can catch cancer early and potentially live a significantly longer life .	我的意思是 , 如果他們有相同的突變 , 且他們會得到這基因測試 , 且他們了解它 , 那麼他們就可以去做定期的篩檢 , 能夠及早發現癌症 , 且有可能過更長壽 。
let me introduce you now to the beery twins , diagnosed with cerebral palsy at the age of two .	讓我來介紹你們現在所在的啤酒對雙胞胎 , 在兩歲的時候被診斷出大腦性麻痺 。
their mom is a very brave woman who didn't believe that the symptoms weren't matching up , and through some heroic efforts and a lot of internet searching , she was able to convince the medical community that , in fact , they had something else .	他們的母親是一位非常勇敢的女性 , 她不相信這些症狀和以前的情形是不吻合的 , 透過一些英勇的努力和大量的網路搜尋 , 她才得以說服醫學界 , 事實上 , 他們還有一些其他的東西 。
what they had was doparesponsive dystonia .	他們所擁有的 , 是肌張力不全症 。
and so they were given ldopa , and their symptoms did improve , but they weren't totally asymptomatic .	於是他們就這樣被告發了 。 他們的症狀確實有所改善 , 但並非全然的症狀 。
turns out the gentleman in this picture is a guy named joe beery , who was lucky enough to be the cio of a company called life technologies .	照片裡的這位先生名叫joebeery他很幸運地成為一家名為生命科技公司的執行長
they're one of the two companies that makes these massive whole genome sequencing tools .	它們是兩間製造這些大規模完整基因定序工具的公司之一 。
and so what he did was he got his kids sequenced .	所以他做的是 , 他讓他的孩子做定序 。
and what they found was a series of mutations in a gene called spr , which is responsible for producing serotonin , among other things .	他們發現一個叫做spr的基因有一系列變異 , 負責製造血清素 , 和其他東西之間的變異性 。
so on top of ldopa , they gave these kids a serotonin precursor drug , and they're effectively normal now .	所以在左上角 , 他們給這些孩子一種血清素的前兆藥物 , 他們現在很正常 。
guys , this would never have happened without whole genome sequencing .	各位 , 如果沒有全基因組的測序 , 這種狀況就永遠不會發生 。
and at the time this was a few years ago it cost $100 , 000 .	而在幾年前--這只花了十萬美金--
today it's $10 , 000 . next year it's $1 , 000 .	今天是一萬元 。 明年是一千元 。
the year after it's $100 , give or take a year .	在價格達到100美元後的一年 , 給予或一年 。
that's how fast this is moving .	這就是移動的速度 。
so here's little nick likes batman and squirt guns .	這裡有個小小的尼克喜歡蝙蝠俠和噴槍 。
and it turns out nick shows up at the children's hospital with this distended belly like a famine victim .	尼克結果發現 , 尼克在兒童醫院出現了這不為人知的肚子 , 像個饑荒的受害者 。
and it's not that he's not eating , it's that when he eats , his intestine basically opens up and feces spill out into his gut .	這並不是說他不吃東西 , 而是他吃東西的時候 , 他的腸道基本上打開了 , 排泄物溢出到他的腸道 。
so a hundred surgeries later , he looks at his mom and says , " mom , please pray for me . i'm in so much pain . "	所以一百場手術後 , 他看著他的媽媽 , 說: 「 媽媽 , 請為我祈禱 。 我真的有這麼多的痛苦 。 」
his pediatrician happens to have a background in clinical genetics and he has no idea what's going on , but he says , " let's get this kid's genome sequenced . "	他的兒科醫師恰巧有臨床遺傳學的背景他完全不知道發生什麼事 , 但他說: 「 讓這個孩子做基因測序吧 。 」
and what they find is a singlepoint mutation in a gene responsible for controlling programmed cell death .	它們會發現一個單點突變 , 負責控制細胞死亡的基因 。
so the theory is that he's having some immunological reaction to what's going on to the food essentially , and that's a natural reaction , which causes some programmed cell death .	所以這個理論是說 , 他對發生在食物中的一切事物產生了一些免疫反應 , 本質上這是一種自然反應 , 這種反應會造成一些被編譯的細胞死亡 。
but the gene that regulates that down is broken .	但是管控那個下的基因 , 卻是壞掉的 。
and so this informs , among other things , of course , a treatment for bone marrow transplant , which he undertakes .	當然 , 這也是個用來治療骨髓移植的療法 , 這是他在做的事 。
and after nine months of grueling recovery , he's now eating steak with a1 sauce .	經過九個月的可怕康復之後 , 他現在要用a1醬汁來吃牛排了 。
the prospect of using the genome as a universal diagnostic is upon us today .	使用基因組來當作通用診斷的前景 , 今天就在我們身上 。
today , it's here .	今天 , 就在這裡 。
and what it means for all of us is that everybody in this room could live an extra five , 10 , 20 years just because of this one thing .	對所有人而言 , 這意味著在座的各位 , 能夠多活五年、十年、二十年 , 僅僅因為這一件事 。
which is a fantastic story , unless you think about humanity's footprint on the planet and our ability to keep up food production .	這是個很棒的故事 , 除非你想到人類在地球上的足跡 , 以及我們持續增加糧食生產的能力 。
so it turns out that the very same technology is also being used to grow new lines of corn , wheat , soybean and other crops that are highly tolerant of drought , of flood , of pests and pesticides .	所以 , 結果發現 , 同樣的技術也被用來培育新一類的玉米、小麥、黃豆 , 及其它高度包容的乾旱、洪水、害蟲和殺蟲劑 。
now look , as long as we continue to increase the population , we're going to have to continue to grow and eat genetically modified foods , and that's the only position that i'll take today .	現在 , 看 , 只要我們繼續增加人口 , 我們就得繼續種植和吃著基因改造過的食物 , 這是我今天將要帶到的唯一位置 。
unless there's anybody in the audience that would like to volunteer to stop eating ?	除非在座的各位有任何人願意自願不再吃東西 ?
none , not one .	沒有 , 一個都沒有 。
this is a typewriter , a staple of every desktop for decades .	這是一台打字機 , 數十年來 , 每個桌面的一個主題 。
and in fact , the typewriter was essentially deleted by this thing .	而事實上 , 打字機基本上被這個東西刪除了
and then more general versions of word processors came about .	之後 , 更普遍的文字處理器出現了 。
but ultimately , it was a disruption on top of a disruption .	但最終 , 它在顛覆性的上是個顛覆 。
it was bob metcalfe inventing the ethernet and the connection of all these computers that fundamentally changed everything .	bobmetcalfe發明了ethernet和所有電腦的連結從根本上改變了一切 。
and suddenly we had netscape , and we had yahoo and we had , indeed , the entire dotcom bubble .	突然間 , 我們有了netscape , 我們有了yahoo , 整個網路泡沫化了 。
not to worry though , that was quickly rescued by the ipod , facebook and , indeed , angry birds .	不用擔心 , 很快就被ipod , facebook和憤怒的小鳥拯救了
look , this is where we are today .	看看 , 這是我們今天所在之處 。
this is the genomic revolution today . this is where we are .	這是今天的基因革命 。 這是我們現在所處的位置 。
so what i'd like you to consider is: what does it mean when these dots don't represent the individual bases of your genome , but they connect to genomes all across the planet ?	所以 , 我想請各位思考的是:當這些點不代表你個人基因組的基對 , 而是和全世界各地的基因組連結在一起時 , 有什麼意涵 ?
so i just recently had to buy life insurance .	所以我最近只好買了生活保險 。
and i was required to answer: a . i have never had a genetic test , b . i've had one , here you go , and c . i've had one and i'm not telling .	我被要求回答:a.我從來沒有做過基因測試 , b.我有過一個 , 在這裡 , c.我有過一個 , 我沒說過
thankfully , i was able to answer a , and i say that honestly in case my life insurance agent is listening .	謝天謝地 , 我得以回答a , 我說實話 , 以防我的保險經紀人正在傾聽 。
but what would have happened if i had said c ?	但如果我有c怎麼辦呢 ?
consumer applications for genomics , they will flourish .	用於基因組的消費者應用 , 他們會蓬勃發展 。
do you want to see whether you're genetically compatible with your girlfriend ? sure .	你想看看你是不是跟女友基因相容呢 ? 當然 。
dna sequencing on your iphone ? there's an app for that .	dna在你的iphone上做排序 ? 有一個應用程式 。
personalized genomic massage anyone ?	有沒有人做個人基因按摩 ?
there's already a lab today that tests for allele 334 of the avpr1 gene , the socalled cheating gene .	現今已經有實驗室在測試avpr1基因的allele334 , 也就是所謂的欺騙基因 。
so anybody who's here today with your significant other , just turn over to them and swab their mouth , send it to the lab and you'll know for sure .	所以今天在場的任何一位有你重要的人 , 轉向他們 , 換嘴巴 , 送到實驗室 , 你會知道的 。
do you really want to elect a president whose genome suggests cardiomyopathy ?	你真的要選出一位總統他的基因組建議心臟病變嗎 ?
now think of it , it's 2016 and the leading candidate releases not only her four years of back tax returns , but also her personal genome .	現在想想 , 2016年 , 領先的候選人不僅釋放了她的四年稅收 , 也釋放了她的個人基因組 。
and it looks really good .	而且看起來非常好 。
and then she challenges all of her competitors to do the same .	接著 , 她挑戰她的所有競爭者都要做同樣的事 。
do you think that's not going to happen ?	你認為這不會發生 ?
do you think it would have helped john mccain ?	你認為這會有幫助約翰馬侃嗎 ?
how many people in the audience have the last name resnick like me ? raise your hand .	觀眾中有多少人有和我一樣的姓氏resnick ? 請舉手 。
typically , there's one or two .	通常有一兩位
so my father's father was one of 10 resnick brothers .	所以我父親的父親是10個resnick兄弟之一 。
they all hated each other .	都討厭對方
and they all moved to different parts of the planet .	並且它們都搬到地球的不同區域 。
so it's likely that i'm related to every resnick that i ever meet , but i don't know .	所以很可能我在每一次我遇見的每個resnick都會有關係 , 但我不知道 。
but imagine if my genome were deidentified , sitting in software , and a third cousin's genome was also sitting there , and there was software that could compare these two and make these associations .	但想像一下 , 如果我的基因被辨識出來 , 坐在軟體中 , 第三個表兄弟的基因組也坐在那 , 有軟體可以比較這兩者並做出關聯 。
not hard to imagine . my company has software that does this right now .	不難想像 。 我的公司有軟體現在就這麼做了 。
and so imagine one more thing: that that software is able to ask both parties for mutual consents , " would you be willing to meet your third cousin ? "	所以 , 想像一件事:這個軟體可以要求雙方同意 , 「 你願意與你的第三表兄見面嗎 ? 」
and if we both say yes , voila ! welcome to chromosomally linkedin .	如果我們都答對了 , 瞧 ! 歡迎來到染色體linkedin 。
now this is probably a good thing , right ?	這可能是件好事 , 對吧 ?
you have bigger clan gatherings and so on .	你有更大的族群聚集之類的 。
but maybe it's a bad thing as well .	但這也可能是壞事 。

okay , so experts think that one to three percent of you are not actually the father of your child .	好吧 , 專家們認為你們中有1%到3%其實不是孩子的父親
look these genomes , these 23 chromosomes , they don't in any way represent the quality of our relationships or the nature of our society at least not yet .	看看這些基因組 , 這23對染色體 , 它們並不能以任何方式呈現我們的人際關係 , 或我們社會的本質──至少現在還不能 。
and like any new technology , it's really in humanity's hands to wield it for the betterment of mankind , or not .	和任何新科技一樣 , 它真的是人類的手上握著它以改善人類的福祉 。
and so i urge you all to wake up and to tune in and to influence the genomic revolution that's happening all around you .	所以 , 我呼籲各位 , 喚醒大家 , 調整一下 , 影響你們身邊正在發生的基因革命 。
daniel kraft demos his marrow miner a new device that quickly harvests lifesaving bone marrow with minimal pain to the donor . he emphasizes that the adult stem cells found in bone marrow can be used to treat many terminal conditions , from parkinson's to heart disease .	丹尼爾•克拉夫向他的骨髓採取一種新裝置 , 它能快速採集救命的骨髓 , 以對捐贈者的最小痛苦來收集救命的骨髓 。 他強調 , 在骨髓中發現的成體幹細胞 , 可以用來治療許多臨終的條件 , 從帕金森氏症到心臟病 。
biology , biotech , health , health care , medicine , science , technology	生物科技 , 生物科技 , 健康 , 醫療 , 醫學 , 科學 , 科技
daniel kraft invents a better way to harvest bone marrow	danielkraft發明了更好的方式來收割骨髓 。
so i am a pediatric cancer doctor and stemcell researcher at stanford university where my clinical focus has been bone marrow transplantation .	我是小兒科癌醫生 , 史丹佛大學的幹細胞研究員 , 我的臨床研究專注是骨髓移植 。
now , inspired by jill bolte taylor last year , i didn't bring a human brain , but i did bring a liter of bone marrow .	現在 , 受到去年jillboltetaylor的啟發 , 我沒有帶一個人腦 , 但我確實帶了一公升的骨髓 。
and bone marrow is actually what we use to save the lives of tens of thousands of patients , most of whom have advanced malignancies like leukemia and lymphoma and some other diseases .	而骨髓 , 則是我們用來拯救數萬名病人的生命 , 大部分是惡性腫瘤 , 如白血病和淋巴瘤 , 以及其他一些疾病 。
so , a few years ago , i'm doing my transplant fellowship at stanford .	所以 , 幾年前 , 我在史丹佛做移植研究 。
i'm in the operating room . we have bob here , who is a volunteer donor .	我在手術房裡 。 我們這裡有bob , 他是志願捐贈者 。
we're sending his marrow across the country to save the life of a child with leukemia .	我們把他的骨髓發送到全國各地 , 來拯救白血病孩童的生命 。
so actually how do we harvest this bone marrow ?	所以實際上我們如何收集這些骨髓呢 ?
well we have a whole o . r . team , general anesthesia , nurses , and another doctor across from me .	我們有一個完整的o.r.團隊 , 麻醉醫師 , 護士 , 以及另一位來自我旁邊的醫生 。
bob's on the table , and we take this sort of small needle , you know , not too big .	bob躺在桌上 , 我們拿著小針 , 你知道 , 不要太大 。
and the way we do this is we basically place this through the soft tissue , and kind of punch it into the hard bone , into the tuchus that's a technical term and aspirate about 10 mls of bone marrow out , each time , with a syringe .	基本上 , 我們的做法是從軟組織放入軟骨 , 用針筒刺穿硬骨頭 , 刺入tuchus , 每次用針筒吸出大概10mlmarrow的骨髓 。
and hand it off to the nurse . she squirts it into a tin .	然後把針筒遞給護士 , 她把針筒放進一個針筒裡 。
hands it back to me . and we do that again and again .	把信件遞給我 。 我們一而再 , 再而三地這樣做 。
about 200 times usually .	大約兩百次 。
and by the end of this my arm is sore , i've got a callus on my hand , let alone bob , whose rear end looks something more like this , like swiss cheese .	在這時我的手臂末端 , 我手上有一台呼叫器 , 更不用說bob了 , 他的屁股看起來更像這個樣子 , 像瑞士起司 。
so i'm thinking , you know , this procedure hasn't changed in about 40 years .	所以我在想 , 你知道的 , 這個程序在大約40年後都沒有改變 。
and there is probably a better way to do this .	可能會有更好的方法 。
so i thought of a minimally invasive approach , and a new device that we call the marrow miner .	所以我想到了一個微創傷的方法 , 和一個我們稱為 「 骨髓採取器 」 的新裝置 。
and the marrow miner , the way it works is shown here .	而骨髓採取器 , 它的運作方式如下所示 。
our standard seethrough patient .	我們的標準看診病人
instead of entering the bone dozens of times , we enter just once , into the front of the hip or the back of the hip .	我們不再進到骨頭數十次 , 只進到骨頭前面或後面的骨頭 。
and we have a flexible , powered catheter with a special wire loop tip that stays inside the crunchy part of the marrow and follows the contours of the hip , as it moves around .	我們有一個靈活的導管 , 一個特殊的導管管 , 它會停留在骨髓的脆弱部分 , 跟著臀部的輪廓 , 隨著它四處移動 。
so it enables you to very rapidly aspirate , or suck out , rich bone marrow very quickly through one hole .	所以它會讓你非常快速地渴望 , 或吸乾 , 富有的骨髓很快就穿過了一個洞 。
we can do multiple passes through that same entry .	我們可以多次通過同一個入口
and , so , very quickly , bob can just get one puncture , local anesthesia , and do this harvest as an outpatient .	很快地 , 鮑勃就能買到一個穿刺衣服 , 局部麻醉 , 做為門診病人的門診 。
so i did a few prototypes . i got a small little grant at stanford .	所以我做了幾個原型 。 我在史丹佛拿到一個小額貸款 。
and played around with this a little bit .	稍微玩一下 。
and our team members developed this technology .	我們團隊的成員開發了這項技術 。
and eventually we got two large animals , and pig studies .	最後我們得到了兩大動物 , 以及豬的研究 。
and we found , to our surprise , that we not only got bone marrow out , but we got 10 times the stem cell activity in the marrow from the marrow miner , compared to the normal device .	我們發現 , 令我們驚訝的是 , 我們不僅僅取出骨髓 , 而且我們從骨髓採取器中 , 得到了10倍的幹細胞活動 , 相對於正常的裝置 。
this device was just fda approved in the last year .	這裝置在去年剛剛被美國食品藥物管理局批准 ,
here is a live patient . you can see it following the flexible curves around .	這是一位活生生的病人 。 你可以看到它跟隨四周的曲線 。
there will be two passes here , in the same patient , from the same hole .	會有兩位從同一個病人身上穿過的洞 。
this was done under local anesthesia , as an outpatient .	這是局部麻醉劑 , 作為門診病人 。
and we got , again , about three to six times more stem cells than the standard approach done on the same patient .	比起標準的方法 , 我們得到的幹細胞數目大約是同一個病人的三到六倍 。
so why should you care ? bone marrow is a very rich source of adult stem cells .	那為什麼要關心 ? 骨髓是非常豐富的成體幹細胞來源 。
you all know about embryonic stem cells .	各位都知道胚胎幹細胞
they've got great potential but haven't yet entered clinical trials .	他們有很大的潛力 , 但尚未進入臨床試驗階段 。
adult stem cells are throughout our body , including the bloodforming stem cells in our bone marrow , which we've been using as a form of stemcell therapy for over 40 years .	成體幹細胞遍佈我們身體各處 , 包括我們骨髓內的血液循環幹細胞 , 它是我們已使用的一種幹細胞療法 , 這種療法已經超過四十年了 。
in the last decade there's been an explosion of use of bone marrow stem cells to treat the patient's other diseases such as heart disease , vascular disease , orthopedics , tissue engineering , even in neurology to treat parkinson's and diabetes .	在過去的十年間 , 骨髓幹細胞的爆發已經出現了 , 用來治療病人其它疾病 , 如心臟病、血管疾病、組織工程、甚至神經學 , 用來治療帕金森氏症和糖尿病 。
we've just come out , we're commercializing , this year , generation 2 . 0 of the marrow miner .	我們剛剛出櫃 , 正在商業化 , 這一年 , 第二代 「 骨髓採取器 」 。
the hope is that this gets more stem cells out , which translates to better outcomes .	希望能將更多幹細胞取出 , 轉化成更好的結果 。
it may encourage more people to sign up to be potential livesaving bone marrow donors .	可能會鼓勵更多人登記成為能拯救生命的骨髓捐贈者 。
it may even enable you to bank your own marrow stem cells , when you're younger and healthier , to use in the future should you need it .	甚至可能可以讓你在年輕及健康的時期 , 禁止使用你自己的骨髓幹細胞 , 未來還可以使用它 。
and ultimately and here's a picture of our bone marrow transplant survivors , who come together for a reunion each year at stanford .	最後 , 這是一張我們骨髓移植手術受試者的照片 , 他們每年都會在史丹佛聚會 。
hopefully this technology will let us have more of these survivors in the future .	希望這項技術能讓我們在未來能有更多這樣的倖存者 。
physicist and surfer garrett lisi presents a controversial new model of the universe that just maybe answers all the big questions . if nothing else , it's the most beautiful 8dimensional model of elementary particles and forces you've ever seen .	物理學家和衝浪家葛瑞特利西提出了一種有爭議的新宇宙模型 , 也許可以解答所有大哉問 。 如果沒別的 , 它就是最漂亮的8d模型 , 既是基本粒子和力 。
physics , science , technology	物理、科學、技術 ,
garrett lisi on his theory of everything	garretlisi在他對所有事物的理論上
whoa , dude . check out those killer equations . sweet .	哇 , 老兄 。 看看那些致命的方程式 。 甜美 。
actually , for the next 18 minutes i'm going to do the best i can to describe the beauty of particle physics without equations .	其實 , 接下來的18分鐘 , 我要盡可能不用方程式 , 描述粒子物理學之美 。
it turns out there's a lot we can learn from coral .	結果發現 , 我們可以從珊瑚身上學到許多東西 。
coral is a very beautiful and unusual animal .	珊瑚是種非常美麗且不尋常的動物 。
each coral head consists of thousand of individual polyps .	每一塊珊瑚蟲由成千上萬的珊瑚組成 。
these polyps are continually budding and branching into genetically identical neighbors .	這些珊瑚會持續發出和分支 , 變成基因相同的鄰居 。
if we imagine this to be a hyperintelligent coral , we can single out an individual and ask him a reasonable question .	如果我們想像這些珊瑚可以是超級聰明的珊瑚 , 我們可以分散出一個個體 , 問他一個合理的問題 。
we can ask how exactly he got to be in this particular location compared to his neighbors if it was just chance , or destiny , or what ?	我們可以問他與鄰居相比之下他到底是如何處在這個特定位置的 ? 相較之下如果只是機率 , 還是命運 , 還是什麼 ?
now , after admonishing us for turning the temperature up too high , he would tell us that our question was completely stupid .	在我們招募溫度升高之後 , 他告訴我們 , 我們的問題完全是愚蠢 。
these corals can be quite kind of mean , you see , and i have surfing scars to prove that .	這些珊瑚可以很像 , 你看 , 我有衝浪的疤痕 , 可以證明這一點 。
but this polyp would continue and tell us that his neighbors were quite clearly identical copies of him .	但這片珊瑚會繼續告訴我們 , 他的鄰居對他來說是一模一樣的 。
that he was in all these other locations as well , but experiencing them as separate individuals .	他也在其他的地點 , 以獨特的個體體來體驗 。
for a coral , branching into different copies is the most natural thing in the world .	對珊瑚來說分支成不同的複製品是世界上最自然的東西
unlike us , a hyperintelligent coral would be uniquely prepared to understand quantum mechanics .	和我們不同的是高智商的珊瑚對量子力學有獨特的準備
the mathematics of quantum mechanics very accurately describes how our universe works .	量子力學的數學用來非常準確地描述我們宇宙的運行方式 。
and it tells us our reality is continually branching into different possibilities , just like a coral .	它告訴我們 , 我們的現實是持續地擴展到不同的可能性 , 就像珊瑚一樣 。
it's a weird thing for us humans to wrap our minds around , since we only ever get to experience one possibility .	對我們人類來說 , 這是一件很奇怪的事情 , 把我們的思維包裹起來 , 因為我們只能經歷一種可能性 。
this quantum weirdness was first described by erwin schrödinger and his cat .	這種量子詭異的現象最早是由薛丁格和他的貓提出來的
the cat likes this version better .	貓更喜歡這個版本
in this setup , schrödinger is in a box with a radioactive sample that , by the laws of quantum mechanics , branches into a state in which it is radiated and a state in which it is not .	在這個環境中 , 薛丁格待在一個具有放射性的盒子裡 , 用量子力學的定律來解釋 , 用量子力學的分支 , 進入一種它被放射的狀態 , 一種它並不是的狀態 。
in the branch in which the sample radiates , it sets off a trigger that releases poison and schrödinger is dead .	在樣本散發出的分支裡 , 它啟動了一種會釋放毒藥和薛丁格等死因的觸發器 。
but in the other branch of reality , he remains alive .	但在現實的另一個分支 , 他還是活著 。
these realities are experienced separately by each individual .	這些實相是被每個個體分開所體驗的 。
as far as either can tell , the other one doesn't exist .	相反的 , 另一種不存在 。
this seems weird to us , because each of us only experiences an individual existence , and we don't get to see other branches .	這對我們來說似乎很奇怪 , 因為我們每個人都只會體驗到個別的存在 , 而我們沒有機會看到其他的分支 。
it's as if each of us , like schrödinger here , are a kind of coral branching into different possibilities .	這就好像每個人 , 像薛丁格待在這裡一樣 , 是一種珊瑚在不同的可能性上分支出來 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics tells us this is how the world works at tiny scales .	量子力學的數學告訴我們這就是微小世界的運作方式 。
it can be summed up in a single sentence: everything that can happen , does .	可以用單一句話來總結:所有可能發生的一切 , 都可以 。
but this does not mean everything happens .	但這並不表示每件事都會發生 。
the rest of physics is about describing what can happen and what can't .	其他的物理則是描述哪些可以發生 , 哪些不可以 。
what physics tells us is that everything comes down to geometry and the interactions of elementary particles .	物理學告訴我們一切都可用幾何學以及基本粒子的相互作用
and things can happen only if these interactions are perfectly balanced .	只有在這些互動是完全平衡的情況下 , 事情才有可能發生 。
now i'll go ahead and describe how we know about these particles , what they are and how this balance works .	現在我來描述一下我們對這些粒子的認識它們是什麼以及它的平衡機制如何運作
in this machine , a beam of protons and antiprotons are accelerated to near the speed of light and brought together in a collision , producing a burst of pure energy .	在這台機器中 , 一束質子和反質子都被加速到接近光速的速度 , 並在對撞中聚合在一起 , 產生出一股巨大的純能量 。
this energy is immediately converted into a spray of subatomic particles , with detectors and computers used to figure out their properties .	這些能量立刻被轉換成亞原子粒子噴射出來 , 探測器和電腦用來找出它們的特性 。
this enormous machine the large hadron collider at cern in geneva has a circumference of 17 miles and , when it's operating , draws five times as much power as the city of monterey .	這個巨大的機器-在日內瓦的歐洲核子研究中心的大型強子對撞機有長達17英哩的圓周長 , 當它在運作時 , 吸引的力量是蒙特雷市的五倍 。
we can't predict specifically what particles will be produced in any individual collision .	我們無法明確預測哪些粒子會在任何個別的撞擊中產生
quantum mechanics tells us all possibilities are realized .	量子力學告訴我們所有可能性 , 都被實現了 。
but physics does tell us what particles can be produced .	但物理學告訴我們哪些粒子是可以產生的
these particles must have just as much mass and energy as is carried in by the proton and antiproton .	這些粒子的質量和能量必定與質子和反質子相同 。
any particles more massive than this energy limit aren't produced , and remain invisible to us .	任何比這個能量極限更巨大的粒子都沒有產生 , 且對我們來說仍然是隱形的 。
this is why this new particle accelerator is so exciting .	這就是為什麼這種新型粒子加速器如此令人興奮 。
it's going to push this energy limit seven times beyond what's ever been done before , so we're going to get to see some new particles very soon .	會把這個能量限制在以前所做過的七倍之外 , 所以我們很快就會看到新的粒子 。
but before talking about what we might see , let me describe the particles we already know of .	但在討論我們可能看到的現象之前 , 讓我先描述一下我們已知的粒子 。
there's a whole zoo of subatomic particles .	有一整個亞原子粒子的動物園
most of us are familiar with electrons .	我們大部分人都很熟悉電子
a lot of people in this room make a good living pushing them around .	在座的很多人都在過得很好的生活把他們推來推去了 。
but the electron also has a neutral partner called the neutrino , with no electric charge and a very tiny mass .	但電子有個中子伴侶叫 「 微中子 」 , 沒有電荷 , 質量很小 。
in contrast , the upanddown quarks have very large masses , and combine in threes to make the protons and neutrons inside atoms .	相對的 , 上夸克有非常大的質量 , 三者結合 , 使得原子裏的質子和中子都成了中子 。
all of these matter particles come in left and righthanded varieties , and have antiparticle partners that carry opposite charges .	所有這些物質粒子分成左旋和右旋它們都有攜帶相反電荷的反粒子
these familiar particles also have less familiar second and third generations , which have the same charges as the first but have much higher masses .	這些熟悉的粒子還有比較不熟悉的第二代和第三代擁有和第一代相同的載荷但有更高的質量
these matter particles all interact with the various force particles .	這些粒子都和各種力量粒子互相作用
the electromagnetic force interacts with electrically charged matter via particles called photons .	電磁力通過光子傳遞質子相互作用
there is also a very weak force called , rather unimaginatively , the weak force , that interacts only with lefthanded matter .	還有一種非常微弱的力 , 叫做弱力 , 只和左撇子物質交互作用 。
the strong force acts between quarks which carry a different kind of charge , called color charge , and come in three different varieties: red , green and blue .	夸克之間的強力作用 , 夸克帶有另一種電荷 , 叫做 「 色荷 」 , 分別有三種不同的形狀:紅、綠、藍 。
you can blame murray gellmann for these names they're his fault .	你可以怪罪murraygell-mann這些名字-這是他的錯 。
finally , there's the force of gravity , which interacts with matter via its mass and spin .	最後 , 還有重力透過質量與物質相互作用
the most important thing to understand here is that there's a different kind of charge associated with each of these forces .	最重要的是 , 在這裡要了解的是 , 每一種力都有不同的載荷 。
these four different forces interact with matter according to the corresponding charges that each particle has .	這四種不同的力量會根據每個粒子都有相對的載荷來與物質作用 。
a particle that hasn't been seen yet , but we're pretty sure exists , is the higgs particle , which gives masses to all these other particles .	一個還沒被看見的粒子但我們很確定的存在希格斯粒子就是希格斯粒子它讓所有其他粒子有了質量
the main purpose of the large hadron collider is to see this higgs particle , and we're almost certain it will .	大型強子對撞機的主要目的就是看到這個希格斯粒子我們幾乎確定它會發生
but the greatest mystery is what else we might see .	但最偉大的奧秘是我們還會看到什麼 。
and i'm going to show you one beautiful possibility towards the end of this talk .	我將向你們展示這個演講的結尾 , 一個漂亮的可能性 。
now , if we count up all these different particles using their various spins and charges , there are 226 .	現在 , 如果我們用不同的自旋和載荷計算這些不同的粒子總共有226種 。
that's a lot of particles to keep track of .	也就是許多粒子持續追蹤
and it seems strange that nature would have so many elementary particles .	大自然擁有這麼多的基本粒子似乎很奇怪 。
but if we plot them out according to their charges , some beautiful patterns emerge .	但如果我們依據它們的載荷把它們畫出來 , 就會出現一些美麗的圖案 。
the most familiar charge is electric charge .	最熟悉的電荷是電荷
electrons have an electric charge , a negative one , and quarks have electric charges in thirds .	電子有一個負電荷 , 夸克擁有1/3的電荷 。
so when two up quarks and a down quark are combined to make a proton , it has a total electric charge of plus one .	所以當兩個上夸克和一個下夸克相加時 , 會產生一個質子 , 它的電荷是一體的 。
these particles also have antiparticles , which have opposite charges .	這些粒子還有反粒子它們具有相反電荷
now , it turns out the electric charge is actually a combination of two other charges: hypercharge and weak charge .	結果發現 , 電荷實際上是兩種載荷的結合:超荷和弱荷 。
if we spread out the hypercharge and weak charge and plot the charges of particles in this twodimensional charge space , the electric charge is where these particles sit along the vertical direction .	如果我們把超荷和弱荷分開在這個二度載荷空間中畫出粒子的載荷電荷就是這些粒子在垂直方向的位置
the electromagnetic and weak forces interact with matter according to their hypercharge and weak charge , which make this pattern .	電磁力和弱力通過超荷和弱荷與物質相互作用而形成這個圖案
this is called the unified electroweak model , and it was put together back in 1967 .	這叫做通用電擊模型 , 它在1967年被組裝回來 。
the reason most of us are only familiar with electric charge and not both of these is because of the higgs particle .	我們之所以只熟悉電荷 , 並非這兩個都歸功於希格斯粒子 。
the higgs , over here on the left , has a large mass and breaks the symmetry of this electroweak pattern .	左邊的希格斯粒子有很大的質量並打破這顆電弱圖案的對稱性 。
it makes the weak force very weak by giving the weak particles a large mass .	通過給弱子較大的質量使弱力變得非常微弱
since this massive higgs sits along the horizontal direction in this diagram , the photons of electromagnetism remain massless and interact with electric charge along the vertical direction in this charge space .	由於大量的希格斯粒子在水平方向以來就是電磁作用的光子仍然沒有質量而且與帶電的載荷沿著電荷的方向相互作用
so the electromagnetic and weak forces are described by this pattern of particle charges in twodimensional space .	所以電磁力和弱力在二度空間中被粒子載荷所描述的這種模式
we can include the strong force by spreading out its two charge directions and plotting the charges of the force particles in quarks along these directions .	我們能將強力通過通過將兩種載荷的方向分散出去 , 將載荷用夸克示意粒子沿著這些方向進行描繪 。
the charges of all known particles can be plotted in a fourdimensional charge space , and projected down to two dimensions like this so we can see them .	所有已知粒子的載荷可以在四度載荷空間中畫出來然後投影到二度空間這樣我們就可以看見
whenever particles interact , nature keeps things in a perfect balance along all four of these charge directions .	無論粒子相互作用大自然在四個載荷方向上保持完美的平衡
if a particle and an antiparticle collide , it creates a burst of energy and a total charge of zero in all four charge directions .	如果一個粒子和反粒子相撞會產生能量和四個電荷方向的載荷疊加變為零
at this point , anything can be created as long as it has the same energy and maintains a total charge of zero .	在這個時點 , 任何東西都可以被創造 , 只要它有相同的能量 , 並保持一個總載荷總量為零 。
for example , this weak force particle and its antiparticle can be created in a collision .	比如 , 這個弱子和它的反粒子可以在撞擊中產生 。
in further interactions , the charges must always balance .	在進一步的互動中 , 載荷必須總是保持平衡
one of the weak particles could decay into an electron and an antineutrino , and these three still add to zero total charge .	一個弱子可以衰退成一個電子和一個反中微子而這三個的總載荷仍然是零
nature always keeps a perfect balance .	大自然總是保持完美的平衡 。
so these patterns of charges are not just pretty .	所以這些電荷的型式不僅漂亮
they tell us what interactions are allowed to happen .	它們告訴我們什麼樣的交互作用是被允許的 。
and we can rotate this charge space in four dimensions to get a better look at the strong interaction , which has this nice hexagonal symmetry .	我們可以在四度空間中旋轉這個載荷空間 , 以便更好地觀察強相互作用 , 這有一個不錯的對稱性 。
in a strong interaction , a strong force particle , such as this one , interacts with a colored quark , such as this green one , to give a quark with a different color charge this red one .	在強相互作用中強子 , 比如這個 , 會和有色夸克相互作用 , 比如這個綠色的夸克 , 會讓夸克帶上不同的色荷這個紅色 。
and strong interactions are happening millions of times each second in every atom of our bodies , holding the atomic nuclei together .	強相互作用每秒鐘會發生幾百萬次 , 在我們身體的各個原子裏 , 把原子核拿在一起 。
but these four charges corresponding to three forces are not the end of the story .	但三種力相對應的這四種載荷並非故事的結尾
we can also include two more charges corresponding to the gravitational force .	我們還可以把兩個載荷對應到重力的作用
when we include these , each matter particle has two different spin charges , spinup and spindown .	包括這些 , 每個物質粒子都有兩種不同的旋轉載荷 , 旋轉和旋轉 。
so they all split , and give a nice pattern in sixdimensional charge space .	所以它們都分開了 , 在六度載荷空間中賦予一個很好的圖案 。
we can rotate this pattern in six dimensions , and see that it's quite pretty .	我們可以在六度空間中旋轉這個模式 , 看到它是相當漂亮的 。
right now , this pattern matches our best current knowledge of how nature is built at the tiny scales of these elementary particles .	目前 , 這個圖案將我們目前所知的大自然如何在這些基本粒子的尺度中建構出來 。
this is what we know for certain .	這是我們很確定知道的 。
some of these particles are at the very limit of what we've been able to reach with experiments .	其中有些粒子的極限是我們在實驗中到達的極限 。
from this pattern , we already know the particle physics of these tiny scales . the way the universe works with these tiny scales is very beautiful .	從這個模式 , 我們已經知道這些微小尺度的粒子物理學 。 宇宙的運作方式與這些微小的尺度是非常美麗的 。
but now i'm going to discuss some new and old ideas about things we don't know yet .	但現在我要來談談我們還不知道的事物一些新古老的想法 。
we want to expand this pattern using mathematics alone , and see if we can get our hands on the whole enchilada .	我們想要把這個模式單獨用數學來拓展看看我們能否把手放在整個enchilada上 。
we want to find all the particles and forces that make a complete picture of our universe .	我們希望找到構成宇宙的所有粒子和力量
and we want to use this picture to predict new particles that we'll see when experiments reach higher energies .	我們希望利用這張圖來預測當實驗達到更高能量時我們會看到的新粒子 。
so there's an old idea in particle physics that this known pattern of charges , which is not very symmetric , could emerge from a more perfect pattern that gets broken similar to how the higgs particle breaks the electroweak pattern to give electromagnetism .	粒子物理學的舊觀念就是這種已知的載荷模式這種不對稱的型態可以從一個更完美的模式突顯出來就像希格斯粒子如何打破電弱型態以產生電磁力
in order to do this , we need to introduce new forces with new charge directions .	為了做到這一點 , 我們需要引入新的力量 , 帶有新的載荷方向 。
when we introduce a new direction , we get to guess what charges the particles have along this direction , and then we can rotate it in with the others .	當我們導入一個新方向時 , 我們要猜測粒子在這個方向上帶什麼樣的載荷 , 然後我們就能讓它和其他粒子一起旋轉 。
if we guess wisely , we can construct the standard charges in six charge dimensions as a broken symmetry of this more perfect pattern in seven charge dimensions .	如果我們猜得更明智 , 我們能在六度載荷空間中建構出標準載荷的對稱性在七度載荷空間中建構出更完美的圖案 。
this particular choice corresponds to a grand unified theory introduced by pati and salam in 1973 .	這種特殊的選擇 , 與1973年帕蒂和薩拉姆提出的大統一理論相對應 。
when we look at this new unified pattern , we can see a couple of gaps where particles seem to be missing .	當我們看到這個新的統一模式 , 我們可以看到一些空隙 , 粒子似乎缺少了些空隙 。
this is the way theories of unification work .	這是統一理論的研究方式 。
a physicist looks for larger , more symmetric patterns that include the established pattern as a subset .	物理學家在尋找更大、更對稱的模式時 , 包括了已建立的模式 , 作為一個子集 。
the larger pattern allows us to predict the existence of particles that have never been seen .	更大的模式讓我們能夠預測那些從未被看見的粒子的存在
this unification model predicts the existence of these two new force particles , which should act a lot like the weak force , only weaker .	這個統一模型預測了這兩種新力粒子的存在 , 它應該很像弱力 , 只會比較弱 。
now we can rotate this set of charges in seven dimensions and consider an odd fact about the matter particles: the second and third generations of matter have exactly the same charges in sixdimensional charge space as the first generation .	現在我們可以在七度空間中旋轉這組電荷 , 並考慮到關於粒子的奇怪事實:在六度載荷空間中物質的第二代和第三代具有完全相同的載荷 , 和第一代物質相同的電荷 。
these particles are not uniquely identified by their six charges .	這些粒子並非單一的由它們的六個載荷所識別
they sit on top of one another in the standard charge space .	他們坐在一個標準載荷空間的頂端 。
however , if we work in eightdimensional charge space , then we can assign unique new charges to each particle .	然而 , 如果我們在八度載荷空間中工作 , 我們可以將獨一無二的新載荷分給每個粒子 。
then we can spin these in eight dimensions , and see what the whole pattern looks like .	然後我們可以在八度空間中旋轉 , 看看整個圖案是什麼樣的 。
here we can see the second and third generations of matter now related to the first generation by a symmetry called " triality . "	在這裡我們可以看到物質的第二代和第三代通過一種叫做 " 三重性 " 的對稱性來與第一代相關聯
this particular pattern of charges in eight dimensions is actually part of the most beautiful geometric structure in mathematics .	在八度中的這個特殊的載荷圖案是數學中最為漂亮的幾何結構之一 。
it's a pattern of the largest exceptional lie group , e8 .	這是最大的例外型李群e8的圖案
this lie group is a smooth , curved shape with 248 dimensions .	謊言小組是個平滑、彎曲的形狀加上248的維度
each point in this pattern corresponds to a symmetry of this very complex and beautiful shape .	圖案中的每個點都對應到這個複雜而又美麗的形狀的對稱性 。
one small part of this e8 shape can be used to describe the curved spacetime of einstein's general relativity , explaining gravity .	e8中的一小部分可以用來描述愛因斯坦廣義相對論中用來解釋重力的扭曲時空
together with quantum mechanics , the geometry of this shape could describe everything about how the universe works at the tiniest scales .	和量子力學 , 這個形狀的幾何學可以用最小的尺度描述宇宙如何運作 。
the pattern of this shape living in eightdimensional charge space is exquisitely beautiful , and it summarizes thousands of possible interactions between these elementary particles , each of which is just a facet of this complicated shape .	這種形狀的圖案生活在八度載荷空間中非常美麗 , 它總結了數千種這些基本粒子之間可能的交互作用 , 每一種都只是這個複雜形狀的一個面向 。
as we spin it , we can see many of the other intricate patterns contained in this one .	當我們在旋轉它時 , 我們可以看到其中很多錯綜複雜的圖案 。
and with a particular rotation , we can look down through this pattern in eight dimensions along a symmetry axis and see all the particles at once .	有了特定的旋轉我們可以在八度空間沿一個對稱軸方向觀察這個圖案並且一次看盡所有粒子
it's a very beautiful object , and as with any unification , we can see some holes where new particles are required by this pattern .	它是一個非常美麗的物體 , 如同任何統一 , 我們可以看到一些孔 , 在這個圖案中 , 新的粒子是需要的 。
there are 20 gaps where new particles should be , two of which have been filled by the patisalam particles .	新粒子應該有20個空格 , 其中兩個已被派遣的粒子填補 。
from their location in this pattern , we know that these new particles should be scalar fields like the higgs particle , but have color charge and interact with the strong force .	從它們的位置在這個模式中 , 我們知道這些新粒子應該是像希格斯粒子一樣的稀有場地 , 卻有色荷和和強力相互作用 。
filling in these new particles completes this pattern , giving us the full e8 .	填入這些新粒子使圖案完整 , 給我們完整的e8 。
this e8 pattern has very deep mathematical roots .	這個e8圖案有著很深的數學根
it's considered by many to be the most beautiful structure in mathematics .	它被許多人認為是數學中最美麗的結構 。
it's a fantastic prospect that this object of great mathematical beauty could describe the truth of particle interactions at the smallest scales imaginable .	這個數學美麗的理論可以用最小的尺度來描述粒子相互作用的真相 。
and this idea that nature is described by mathematics is not at all new .	而這種自然被數學所描述的觀念 , 並不是全新的 。
in 1623 , galileo wrote this: " nature's grand book , which stands continually open to our gaze , is written in the language of mathematics .	1623年伽利略寫道: " 大自然的宏偉書 , 一直以來都對我們的觀點保持開放態度 , 用數學的語言寫道 。
its characters are triangles , circles and other geometrical figures , without which it is humanly impossible to understand a single word of it ; without these , one is wandering around in a dark labyrinth . "	它的角色是三角形、圓形 , 和其他幾何形狀 , 沒有了它 , 人類不可能理解其中的一個字 ; 若沒有這些 , 就會在黑暗的迷宮中四處遊蕩 。 」
i believe this to be true , and i've tried to follow galileo's guidance in describing the mathematics of particle physics using only triangles , circles and other geometrical figures .	我相信這是真的 , 我曾試著去遵循伽利略的指導 , 只用三角形、圓形和其他幾何形狀來描述粒子物理的數學 。
of course , when other physicists and i actually work on this stuff , the mathematics can resemble a dark labyrinth .	當然 , 當其他物理學家和我真的致力於研究這些東西時 , 數學可以和一個黑暗的迷宮相似 。
but it's reassuring that at the heart of this mathematics is pure , beautiful geometry .	但是確保數學的核心是純粹、美麗的幾何學 。
joined with quantum mechanics , this mathematics describes our universe as a growing e8 coral , with particles interacting at every location in all possible ways according to a beautiful pattern .	加入了量子力學 , 這個數學把我們的宇宙描述成一個正在成長的e8珊瑚 , 粒子在每個可能的位置進行互動 , 根據美麗的模式 。
and as more of the pattern comes into view using new machines like the large hadron collider , we may be able to see whether nature uses this e8 pattern or a different one .	當圖案更進一步地用像是大型強子對撞機的新機器觀察時 , 我們也許可以觀察到 , e8圖案或另一種圖案的大自然是否會使用這種圖案 。
this process of discovery is a wonderful adventure to be involved in .	這個發現的過程 , 是一段很棒的探險 , 能夠參與其中 。
if the lhc finds particles that fit this e8 pattern , that will be very , very cool .	如果lhc發現了符合e8圖案的粒子那會非常非常酷
if the lhc finds new particles , but they don't fit this pattern well , that will be very interesting , but bad for this e8 theory .	如果對lhc發現了新粒子但不符合這個模式那會非常有趣但是對e8理論不利
and , of course , bad for me personally .	當然 , 對我個人來說是不好的 。
now how bad would that be ?	那會有多糟 ?
well , pretty bad .	嗯 , 非常糟糕 。
but predicting how nature works is a very risky game .	但是 , 預測大自然如何運作是一個很冒險的遊戲 。
this theory and others like it are long shots .	這個理論和其他類似的例子都是很長的投籃動作 。
one does a lot of hard work knowing that most of these ideas probably won't end up being true about nature .	其中一項艱難得知大部分的想法可能最後對自然界一無所知
that's what doing theoretical physics is like: there are a lot of wipeouts .	理論物理就是這樣子的:有很多的不規則 。
in this regard , new physics theories are a lot like startup companies .	在這方面 , 新物理理論很像新創公司 。
as with any large investment , it can be emotionally difficult to abandon a line of research when it isn't working out .	如同任何大型投資 , 在不出問題時 , 要放棄一行研究是情緒上的困難 。
but in science , if something isn't working , you have to toss it out and try something else .	但在科學界 , 如果有什麼不管用 , 你得把它丟出去 , 再試試別的 。
now , the only way to maintain sanity and achieve happiness in the midst of this uncertainty is to keep balance and perspective in life .	現在唯一能維持理智並達到幸福的方法就是在生命中保持平衡和觀點
i've tried the best i can to live a balanced life .	我已經竭盡所能地生活著一個平衡的人生 。
i try to balance my life equally between physics , love and surfing my own three charge directions .	我試著在物理、愛和衝浪中平衡我自己的三個載荷方向
this way , even if the physics i work on comes to nothing , i still know i've lived a good life .	這麼一來 , 就算我所從事的物理工作已一無所有 , 我仍然知道我已經過得很好 。
and i try to live in beautiful places .	我試著住在美麗的地方 。
for most of the past ten years i've lived on the island of maui , a very beautiful place .	過去十年我大部分時間都住在毛伊島一個非常美麗的地方
now it's one of the greatest mysteries in the universe to my parents how i managed to survive all that time without engaging in anything resembling fulltime employment .	現在這是宇宙中最偉大的謎題之一 , 給我父母──我如何能在沒有全職工作的情況下生存下去 。
i'm going to let you in on that secret .	我要告訴你們這個秘密 。
this was a view from my home office on maui .	這是我在毛伊島上的家庭辦公室的照片
and you may have noticed that these beautiful views are similar , but in slightly different places .	你們可能已經注意到 , 這些美麗的景色是相似的 , 但在略有不同的地方 。
that's because this used to be my home and office on maui .	那是因為這曾是我在毛伊島的家和辦公室
i've chosen a very unusual life .	我選擇了一段很不尋常的生活 。
but not worrying about rent allowed me to spend my time doing what i love .	但不擔心房租讓我花時間做我愛做的事 。
living a nomadic existence has been hard at times , but it's allowed me to live in beautiful places and keep a balance in my life that i've been happy with .	過著遊牧生活有時候很辛苦 , 但它讓我能住在很美的地方 , 讓我能在生活中保持平衡 , 讓我很開心 。
it allows me to spend a lot of my time hanging out with hyperintelligent coral .	讓我可以花大量的時間在超級聰明的珊瑚上 。
but i also greatly enjoy the company of hyperintelligent people .	但我也很享受超級聰明人才的公司 。
so i'm very happy to have been invited here to ted .	所以我很高興能被邀請來ted演講 。
chris anderson: i probably understood two percent of that , but i still absolutely loved it . so i'm going to sound dumb .	克里斯•安德森:我大概知道其中的2% , 但我仍然非常喜歡 。 所以我要聽起來很蠢 。
your theory of everything garrett lisi: i'm used to coral .	你的萬物理論我很習慣珊瑚理論
ca: that's right . the reason it's got a few people at least excited is because , if you're right , it brings gravity and quantum theory together .	克:沒錯 。 至少有少數人興奮的原因是因為 , 如果你答對了 , 它會把重力和量子理論結合在一起 。
so are you saying that we should think of the universe , at its heart that the smallest things that there are , are somehow an e8 object of possibility ?	所以 , 你是不是說我們應該把宇宙當作是最微小的事物 , 最有可能是e8的可能性呢 ?
i mean , is there a scale to it , at the smallest scale , or . . . ?	我是說 , 有最小的比例嗎 ?
gl: well , right now the pattern i showed you that corresponds to what we know about elementary particle physics that already corresponds to a very beautiful shape .	亨利:嗯 , 我剛剛給你們看的圖案 , 是對應到我們所知的基本粒子物理學 , 它們已經對應到了一個非常美麗的圖形 。
and that's the one that i said we knew for certain .	這也是我說的我們很確定就知道的事 。
and that shape has remarkable similarities and the way it fits into this e8 pattern could be the rest of the picture .	而那個形狀與e8圖案有著明顯的相似之處 , 也可能是這張圖片的其他部分 。
and these patterns of points that i've shown for you actually represent symmetries of this highdimensional object that would be warping and moving and dancing over the space time that we experience .	我給你們看的這些點的圖案 , 實際上代表了這個高維物體的對稱性 , 在我們所體驗的時空中移動、移動和舞蹈 。
and that would be what explains all these elementary particles that we see .	這也解釋了我們所見的所有這些基本粒子 。
ca: but a string theorist , as i understand it , explains electrons in terms of much smaller strings vibrating i know you don't like string theory vibrating inside it .	克里斯:但是弦理論家 , 正如我所理解的 , 用更小的弦震動來解釋電子 , 我知道你不喜歡弦理論在裡面震動 。
how should we think of an electron in relation to e8 ?	我們該如何看待電子與e8的關係 ?
gl: no , it would be one of the symmetries of this e8 shape .	不對 , 這會是這個e8形狀對稱之一
so what's happening is , as the shape is moving over spacetime , it's twisting . and the direction it's twisting as it moves is what particle we see . so it would be ca: the size of the e8 shape , how does that relate to the electron ?	所以 , 當這個形狀在時空中移動時 , 它的扭曲 。 當移動時 , 它的扭曲方向就是我們看到的粒子 。 所以...克里斯:e8形狀的大小 , 那和電子的大小是怎樣的關係 ?
i kind of feel like i need that for my picture .	我覺得我需要這張照片 。
is it bigger ? is it smaller ?	變大了嗎 ? 變小了嗎 ?
gl: well , as far as we know electrons are point particles , so this would be going down to the smallest possible scales .	亨利:嗯 , 據我們所知 , 電子是點粒子 , 所以這是最小的尺度 。
so the way these things are explained in quantum field theory is , all possibilities are expanding and developing at once .	所以 , 在量子場理論中 , 這些東西的解釋方式是 , 所有的可能性都在同時展開和發展 。
and this is why i use the analogy to coral .	這就是我為什麼使用珊瑚的類比機制 。
and in this way , the way that e8 comes in is it will be as a shape that's attached at each point in spacetime .	依此類推 , e8的進入方式是它會依時空的每一點連接在一起的形狀
and , as i said , the way the shape twists the directional along which way the shape is twisting as it moves over this curved surface is what the elementary particles are , themselves .	如我所說的 , 形狀在經過這個彎曲的表面時會改變方向 , 形狀也就是基本粒子本身 。
so through quantum field theory , they manifest themselves as points and interact that way .	通過量子場理論 , 它們以點代表並以此方式互動 。
i don't know if i'll be able to make this any clearer .	我不知道我能不能再講得更清楚了 。
ca: it doesn't really matter .	克:這真的不重要 。
it's evoking a kind of sense of wonder , and i certainly want to understand more of this .	它激起了一種奇蹟的感覺 , 我肯定想瞭解更多 。
but thank you so much for coming . that was absolutely fascinating .	但非常感謝你們的到來 。 那真的很吸引人 。
the legendary chimpanzee researcher jane goodall talks about tacare and her other community projects , which help people in booming african towns live sidebyside with threatened animals .	傳奇性的黑猩猩研究者珍.古德談及了塔卡爾和她的其他社區計畫 , 這幫助了非洲新興城鎮的居民 , 與受到威脅的動物並肩同行 。
africa , animals , biodiversity , environment , global issues , pollution , primates , science	非洲、動物、生物多樣性、環境、全球議題、污染、靈長類、科學 。
jane goodall helps humans and animals live together	珍.古德幫助人類和動物生活在一起
good afternoon , good evening , whatever .	午安 , 晚安 , 無論如何 。
we can go , jambo , guten abend , bonsoir , but we can also ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh .	我們可以這樣 , 嗯 , 嗯 , 嗯 , 嗯 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 !
that is the call that chimpanzees make before they go to sleep in the evening .	那是黑猩猩的叫聲 , 在晚上牠們去睡覺之前 。
you hear it going from one side of the valley to the other , from one group of nests to the next .	你聽到它從山谷的一端傳到另一端 , 從一群蜂巢傳到另一端 。
and i want to pick up with my talk this evening from where zeray left off yesterday .	我今天晚上就要跟大家分享我昨天在哪裡做的演講 。
he was talking about this amazing , threeyearold australopithecine child , selam .	他談到這個神奇、三歲的澳大利亞孩子 , selam 。
and we've also been hearing about the history , the family tree , of mankind through dna genetic profiling .	我們也聽說過透過基因側寫人類的歷史、族譜 , 人類的族譜 。
and it was a paleontologist , the late louis leakey , who actually set me on the path for studying chimpanzees .	是一位古生物學家 , 已故的路易斯.李基 , 他讓我走上研究黑猩猩的道路 。
and it was pretty extraordinary , way back then .	在那之前 , 實在是相當不平凡 。
it's kind of commonplace now , but his argument was because he'd been searching for the fossilized remains of early humans in africa .	現在很常見了 , 但他的論點是 , 因為他一直在尋找非洲早期人類的化石遺跡 。
and you can tell an awful lot about what those beings looked like from the fossils , from the shape of the muscle attachments , something about the way they lived from the various artifacts found with them .	你可以從化石得知那些生物的長相 , 從肌肉的形狀判斷出 , 與其一起共存的各種手工藝 。
but what about how they behaved ? that's what he wanted to know .	但他們的行為呢 ? 這是他想知道的 。
and of course , behavior doesn't fossilize .	當然 , 行為並不會化石 。
he argued and it's now a fairly common theory that if we found behavior patterns similar or the same in our closest living relatives , the great apes , and humans today , then maybe those behaviors were present in the apelike , humanlike ancestor some seven million years ago .	他主張-而現在這是一個相當普遍的理論如果我們在現存的近親物種和人類之間找到了相似的行為模式或相同的行為模式 , 現今的人類 , 也許那些行為會出現在猿類和人類祖先身上-大約在七百萬年前 。
and therefore , perhaps we had brought those characteristics with us from that ancient , ancient past .	因此 , 也許我們將這些特質從古至今的歷史中帶入了 。
well , if you look in textbooks today that deal with human evolution , you very often find people speculating about how early humans may have behaved , based on the behavior of chimpanzees .	嗯 , 如果你看現今的教科書處理人類進化的過程你會經常發現人們依據黑猩猩的行為來推測早期人類的行為
they are more like us than any other living creature , and we've heard about that during this ted conference .	他們比其他生物更像我們 , 在ted大會上我們都聽過了 。
so it remains for me to comment on the ways in which chimpanzees are so like us , in certain aspects of their behavior .	所以 , 我想要表達的是黑猩猩在某些方面和我們是很相像的 。
every chimpanzee has his or her own personality .	每一隻黑猩猩都有他/她自己的個性 。
of course , i gave them names . they can live to be 60 years or more , although we think most of them probably don't make it to 60 in the wild .	當然 , 我會給牠們取名字 。 牠們可以活到六十年或更久 , 雖然我們認為大部份牠們可能不會在野外活到六十歲 。
mr . wurzel . the female has her first baby when she's 11 or 12 .	mr.wurzel , 雌性在十一或十二歲時就生了第一胎 。
thereafter , she has one baby only every five or six years , a long period of childhood dependency when the child is nursing , sleeping with the mother at night , and riding on her back .	在那之後 , 她每五、六年才有一個嬰兒 , 童年長期依賴期 , 當孩子在療養期時 , 晚上和母親一起睡覺 , 背靠背靠著她 。
and we believe that this long period of childhood is important for chimpanzees , just as it is for us , in relation to learning .	我們相信這段長時間的幼兒時期對黑猩猩很重要 , 就像對我們而言 , 與學習有關 。
as the brain becomes ever more complex during evolution in different forms of animals , so we find that learning plays an ever more important role in an individual's life history .	隨著大腦在不同形式的動物進化上有更複雜的變化 , 所以我們發現 , 學習在個體的生命歷史中扮演著一個更重要的角色 。
and young chimpanzees spend a lot of time watching what their elders do .	年輕的黑猩猩花很多時間觀察長者的行為 。
we know now that they're capable of imitating behaviors that they see .	我們現在知道牠們有能力模仿他們所看到的行為 。
and we believe that it's in this way that the different toolusing behaviors that have now been seen in all the different chimpanzee populations studied in africa how these are passed from one generation to the next , through observation , imitation and practice , so that we can describe these toolusing behaviors as primitive culture .	我們相信 , 用這種方式 , 如今在所有不同種類的黑猩猩族群中 , 已經看到不同的使用工具的行為 , 如同我們在非洲所研究的 , 這些行為是如何從一個世代傳到下一個世代的 , 透過觀察、模仿和練習 , 以便我們能把這些使用工具的行為描述成原始文化 。
chimpanzees don't have a spoken language . we've talked about that .	黑猩猩沒有口說的語言 。 我們剛剛談過 。
they do have a very rich repertoire of postures and gestures , many of which are similar , or even identical , to ours and formed in the same context . greeting chimpanzees embracing .	牠們的確有非常豐富的肢體動作和姿勢 , 其中許多與我們是相似的 , 甚至與我們相同的 , 並在同樣的情境下形成 。 歡迎黑猩猩擁抱 。
they also kiss , hold hands , pat one another on the back .	他們還親吻、握手、拍手 。
and they swagger and they throw rocks .	牠們大力士 , 扔石頭 。
in chimpanzee society , we find many , many examples of compassion , precursors to love and true altruism .	在黑猩猩的社會裡 , 我們發現很多很多的例子都是同情心的前兆 , 是愛和真正的利他行為 。
unfortunately , they , like us , have a dark side to their nature .	不幸的是 , 他們和我們一樣 , 對他們的本性有黑暗的一面 。
they're capable of extreme brutality , even a kind of primitive war .	他們有著極度殘暴的能力 , 甚至是種原始的戰爭 。
and these really aggressive behaviors , for the most part , are directed against individuals of the neighboring social group .	而這些極具攻擊性的行為 , 大部分的情況下 , 都是和鄰近社會群體的個體對抗的 。
they are very territorially aggressive .	牠們非常有攻擊性 。
chimpanzees , i believe , more than any other living creature , have helped us to understand that , after all , there is no sharp line between humans and the rest of the animal kingdom .	我相信黑猩猩們 , 比起其它的生物 , 已經讓我們了解 , 畢竟人類和動物界之間並沒有一條明顯的界線 。
it's a very blurry line , and it's getting more blurry all the time as we make even more observations .	這是一條非常模糊的線 , 而且每時每刻都在變得更加模糊 , 因為我們會做更多的觀察 。
the study that i began in 1960 is still continuing to this day .	我在1960年開始進行的研究 , 至今仍持續著 。
and these chimpanzees , living their complex social lives in the wild , have helped more than anything else to make us realize we are part of , and not separated from , the amazing animals with whom we share the planet .	而這些黑猩猩 , 生活在野外生活著複雜的社交生活 , 幫助比任何事物都還要多 , 使我們意識到 , 我們也是其中的一份子 , 而不是被分開 , 是我們與地球共享的奇妙動物 。
so it's pretty sad to find that chimpanzees , like so many other creatures around the world , are losing their habitats .	所以 , 發現黑猩猩 , 跟世界上其他許多生物一樣 , 是相當令人難過的 , 正在失去牠們的棲息地 。
this is just one photograph from the air , and it shows you the forested highlands of gombe .	這只是一張來自空氣的照片 , 它向你展示了戈姆貝森林的高地 。
and it was when i flew over the whole area , about 16 years ago , and realized that outside the park , this forest , which in 1960 had stretched almost unbroken along the eastern shore of lake tanganyika , which is where the tiny , 30squaremile gombe national park lies , that a question came to my mind .	就在大約16年前 , 我飛越了整個區域 , 才發現這片森林之外在1960年 , 沿著塔根尼卡湖的東岸 , 那裡是小小的 , 30平方公園國家公園的所在地 , 那裡有個疑問 。
" how can we even try to save these famous chimpanzees , when the people living around the national park are struggling to survive ? "	「 我們要如何拯救這些著名的黑猩猩 ? 當居住在國家公園附近的居民都在掙扎求生存 ? 」
more people are living there than the land could possibly support .	比土地能承受更多人居住在那裡 。
the numbers increased by refugees pouring in from burundi and over the lake from congo .	難民的數量增加 , 從蒲隆地、從剛果湖上方倒進來 。
and very poor people they couldn't afford to buy food from elsewhere .	而且非常貧窮的人們他們負擔不起從其他地方購買食物 。
this led to a program , which we call tacare .	這就帶出了一個計畫 , 我們稱之為tacare 。
it's a very holistic way of improving the lives of the people living in the villages around the park .	以一種全面的方式提高人們的生活品質 , 改善公園附近村莊的人們的生活 。
it started small with 12 villages . it's now in 24 .	一開始是小的有12個村莊現在是24個村莊
there isn't time to go into it , but it's including things like tree nurseries , methods of farming most suitable to this now very degraded , almost desertlike land up in these mountains .	時間不夠多了 , 但這包含了像樹木護理這類的東西 , 最適合耕種方法 , 如今已被嚴重退化 , 幾乎像沙漠一樣的土地堆積在山中 。
ways of controlling , preventing soil erosion .	控制和預防土壤侵蝕的方法 。
ways of reclaiming overused farmland , so that within two years they can again be productive .	重新取得過度使用農地的方法 , 如此一來 , 在兩年內 , 它們就能夠再度生產 。
working to help the villagers obtain fresh water from wells .	致力於幫助村民們從井裡取得新鮮的水源 。
perhaps build some schoolrooms .	或許建造一些學校教室
most important of all , i believe , is working with small groups of women , providing them with opportunities for microcredit loans .	最重要的是 , 我相信 , 與一小群婦女合作 , 提供她們取得微型貸款的機會 。
and we've got , as is the case around the world , about 95 percent of all loans returned .	身為全世界的案例 , 我們有大約95%的貸款都歸還了 。
empowering women , working with education , providing scholarships for girls so they can finish secondary school , in the clear understanding that , all around the world , as women's education improves , family size drops .	賦予女性能力 , 和教育工作 , 提供獎學金給女孩 , 讓他們能夠完成中學 , 清楚了解這一點 , 在全世界 , 隨著女性的教育改善 , 家庭規模也下降 。
we provide information about family planning and about hiv/aids .	我們提供家庭規劃和愛滋病等知識 。
and as a result of this program , something's happening for conservation .	由於這個計畫的成果 , 保育過程也發生了一些事 。
what's happening for conservation is that the farmers living in these 24 villages , instead of looking on us as a bunch of white people coming to study a whole bunch of monkeys and by the way , many of the staff are now tanzanian but when we began the tacare program , it was a tanzanian team going into the villages .	保護區的情況是 , 在這24個村落裡的農夫 , 與其以一群白種人來研究一大群猴子--順道一提 , 很多工作人員現在都是坦尚尼亞人--但當我們開始坦尚尼亞造車計劃時 , 卻是一個坦尚尼亞人進入村落 。
it was a tanzanian team talking to the villagers , asking what they were interested in .	那是一個坦尚尼亞的團隊與村民對話 , 問他們對什麼有興趣 。
were they interested in conservation ? absolutely not .	他們對保育感興趣嗎 ? 絕對不是 。
they were interested in health ; they were interested in education .	他們對健康有興趣 ; 他們對教育有興趣 。
and as time went on , and as their situation began to improve , they began to understand ever more about the need for conservation .	隨著時間過去 , 隨著他們的情況開始改善 , 他們開始更加了解對保育的需求 。
they began to understand that as the upper levels of the hills were denuded of trees , so you've got this terrible soil erosion and mudslides .	他們開始了解 , 隨著山坡的高度被砍伐樹木 , 所以你有這片可怕的土壤流失和爛泥 。
today , we are developing what we call the greater gombe ecosystem .	現今 , 我們正在開發所謂的 「 更偉大的岡貝生態系統 」 。
this is an area way outside the national park , stretching out into all these very degraded lands .	這是在國家公園之外的一塊區域 , 向外延伸到所有這些非常退化的土地上 。
and as these villages have a better standard of life , they are actually agreeing to put between 10 percent and 20 percent of their land in the highlands aside , so that once again , as the trees grow back , the chimpanzees will have leafy corridors through which they can travel to interact as they must for genetic viability with other remnant groups outside the national park .	當這些村落有更好的生活水準時 , 他們其實同意將百分之十到二十的高地一帶回去 , 隨著樹木再次長回去 , 黑猩猩們就會有傳單的走廊 , 穿過這條路 , 黑猩猩們就可以在國家公園外面交流 , 為了基因上的可行性 , 和其他殘存的族群交流 。
so tacare is a success .	因此 , 托兒所是一個成功的國家 。
we're replicating it in other parts of africa , around other wilderness areas which are faced with extreme population pressure .	我們在非洲的其它地方複製它 , 其它野生的地方 , 都面臨極端的人口壓力 。
the problems in africa , however , as we've been discussing for the whole of these first couple of days of ted , are major problems .	然而 , 非洲的問題 , 正如我們前幾天在ted所討論的 , 都是重大的問題 。
there is a great deal of poverty .	貧窮的情況也很嚴重 。
and when you get large numbers of people living in land that is not that fertile , particularly when you cut down trees , and you leave the soil open to the wind for erosion , as desperate populations cut down more and more trees , so that they can try and grow food for themselves and their families , what's going to happen ? something's got to give .	當你讓大量居住在沒那麼肥沃的土地上的人 , 尤其是當你砍掉樹木 , 把土壤留在風中 , 順道而論 , 隨著絕望的人們砍掉越來越多的樹木 , 如此一來他們就能自己和家人種食物 , 又會變成什麼樣子 ? 一定得有所作為 。
and the other problems in not only africa , but the rest of the developing world and , indeed , everywhere what are we doing to our planet ?	另外一個問題 , 不只在非洲 , 其他的發展中國家 , 甚至在各地我們對地球做了什麼事 ?
you know , the famous scientist , e . o . wilson said that if every person on this planet attains the standard of living of the average european or american , we need three new planets .	你知道的 , 著名的科學家 , 愛德華.威爾森曾說過 , 如果地球上每個人都有生活在歐洲或美國的標準 , 我們需要三個新的地球 。
today , they are saying four . but we don't have them . we've got one .	今天 , 他們說的是四個 。 但我們沒有他們 。 我們還有一個 。
and what's happened ? i mean , the question here is , here we are , arguably the most intelligent being that's ever walked planet earth , with this extraordinary brain , capable of the kind of technology that is so well illustrated by these ted conferences , and yet we're destroying the only home we have .	到底發生了什麼 ? 我的意思是 , 我們這裡的問題是 , 可以說是走路的地球上最有智慧的生物 , 擁有這個非凡的大腦 , 能夠以這些科技為優秀的ted會議所闡述的技術 , 然而我們卻要破壞我們唯一擁有的家園 。
the indigenous people around the world , before they made a major decision , used to sit around and ask themselves , " how does this decision affect our people seven generations ahead ? "	全世界的原住民 , 在他們做了重大的決定之前 , 常常坐著問自己: 「 這個決定會如何影響我們未來的七代人 ? 」
today , major decisions and i'm not particularly talking about africa here , but the developed world major decisions involving millions of dollars , and millions of people , are often based on , " how will this affect the next shareholders' meeting ? "	今天 , 重大的決策 , 我不是特別談論非洲 , 而是已開發國家重大的決策 , 包含了數百萬美元 , 數百萬人 , 通常是基於 「 這會如何影響到下一次股東的會議 ? 」
and these decisions affect africa .	而這些決定影響著非洲 。
as i began traveling around africa talking about the problems faced by chimpanzees and their vanishing forests , i realized more and more how so many of africa's problems could be laid at the door of previous colonial exploitation .	當我開始在非洲各地旅行時 , 談及黑猩猩所面臨的問題 , 以及它們正在消失的森林 。 我發現 , 越來越多非洲的問題 , 竟然有這麼多的問題被擺放在前殖民地的門上 。
so i began traveling outside africa , talking in europe , talking in the united states , going to asia .	所以我開始在非洲之外旅行 , 到歐洲演講 , 到美國演講 , 到亞洲去 。
and everywhere there were these terrible problems .	到處都有這些可怕的問題 。
and you know the kind i'm talking about . i'm talking about pollution .	你知道我說的那種 , 我說的污染 ,
the air that we breathe that often poisons us .	我們所呼吸的空氣 , 往往毒害著我們 。
the earth is poisoning our foods .	地球正在毒害著我們的食物 。
the water water is perhaps one of the most crucial issues that we're going to face in this century and everywhere water is being polluted by agricultural , industrial and household chemicals that still are being sprayed around the world , seemingly with the inability to profit from past experience .	水資源也許是其中一個我們將要面臨的最關鍵的議題這個世紀到處都有水正在被農業、工業和家庭用化學物污染的污染這些污染物依然在世界各地流通似乎是過去不可獲利的產物
the mangroves are being cut down ; the effects of things like the tsunami get worse .	紅樹林正在被砍伐 , 影響海嘯 。
we've talked about the soil erosion .	我們已經談過了土壤的侵蝕 ,
we have the reckless burning of fossil fuels along with other greenhouse gasses , so called , leading to climate change .	我們不計後果的燃燒著石化燃料還有其他溫室氣體也因此被稱為 , 導致氣候變遷
finally , all around the world , people have begun to believe that there is something going on very wrong with our climate .	最後 , 全世界各地 , 人們開始相信 , 我們的氣候面臨了一些問題 。
all around the world climates are mixed up .	全世界的氣候都被混為一談 。
and it's the poor people who are affected worse .	而且是那些受到影響較嚴重的窮人
it's africa that already is affected .	而是非洲已經受影響了 。
in many parts of subsaharan africa , the droughts are so much worse .	在撒哈拉以南的非洲許多地區 , 乾旱的情況更糟糕許多 。
and when the rain does come , it so often leads to flooding and added distress , and the cycle of poverty and hunger and disease .	當雨季真的到來時 , 它經常會導致洪水 , 加上一些苦惱 , 造成貧窮、飢餓、和疾病的惡性循環 。
and the numbers of people living in an area that the land cannot support , who are too poor to buy food , who can't move away because the whole land is degraded .	至於住在無法供應土地的人數 , 貧窮到無法購買食物 , 因為整片土地都被降解了 。
and so you get desertification creeping , creeping , creeping as the last of the trees are cut down .	所以 , 當樹木最後一棵樹木被砍倒 , 就會產生沙漠化的分解 。
and this kind of thing is not just in africa . it's all over the world .	這樣的事不只發生在非洲 , 全世界都有
so it wasn't surprising to me that as i was traveling around the world i met so many young people who seemed to have lost hope .	所以 , 我一點也不意外 , 當我在世界各地旅行時 , 我遇到許多失去希望的年輕人 。
we seem to have lost wisdom , the wisdom of the indigenous people .	我們似乎失去了智慧 , 失去了原住民的智慧 。
i asked a question . " why ? "	我問了一個問題: 「 為什麼 ? 」
well , do you think there could be some kind of disconnect between this extraordinarily clever brain , the kind of brain that the ted technologies exemplify , and the human heart ? talking about it in the nonscientific term , in terms of love and compassion . is there some disconnect ?	嗯 , 你認為這種極聰明的大腦之間會有某種差異嗎 ? ted的科技是可以表達的 , 而人類的心臟呢 ? 用非科學的角度來說 , 以愛和同情的角度來說 , 是否有某些缺點呢 ?
and these young people , when i talk to them , basically they were either depressed or apathetic , or bitter and angry . and they said more or less the same thing , " we feel this way because we feel you've compromised our future and there's nothing we can do about it . "	這些年輕人 , 當我和他們談話時 , 基本上 , 他們不是憂鬱症、漠不關心 , 或痛苦和憤怒 。 他們說的或多或少是一樣的 , 「 我們會感同身受 , 是因為我們覺得你在我們自己的未來中妥協 , 無能為力 。 」
we have compromised their future .	我們已經妥協了他們的未來 。
i've got three little grandchildren , and every time i look at them and i think how we've harmed this beautiful planet since i was their age , i feel this desperation .	我有三個小孫子 , 每當我看著他們時 , 心裡想著我們如何危害這個美麗的星球 , 從我還是他們的年代開始 , 我就感受到這種絕望 。
and that led to this program we call roots and shoots , which began right here in tanzania and has now spread to 97 countries around the world .	這就形成了一個計畫 , 我們稱之為根與芽的計畫 , 這個計畫始於坦尚尼亞 , 現在已擴及全球97個國家 。
it's symbolic . roots make a firm foundation .	它具有象徵性 。 根源能做堅實的基礎 。
shoots seem tiny ; to reach the sun they can break through a brick wall .	芽看起來似乎很微小 ; 為了到達太陽 , 它們能穿破磚牆 。
see the brick wall as all these problems we've inflicted on the planet , environmental and social . it's a message of hope .	把磚牆看成我們在地球上所面臨的所有問題 , 環保及社會問題 。 這是一個充滿希望的訊息 。
hundreds and thousands of young people around the world can break through and can make this a better world for all living things .	世界各地成千上萬的年輕人能夠突破這些生命體 , 讓這世界變得更美好 。
the most important message of roots and shoots: every single one of us makes a difference , every single day .	根與芽想傳達的最重要的訊息是:我們每一個人 , 每一天都做些改變 。
we have a choice . every one of us in this room , we have a choice as to what kind of difference we want to make .	我們有選擇 。 在座的每一位 , 我們都有選擇 , 我們想要做出什麼樣的改變 。
the very poor have no choice . it's up to us to change things so that the poor have choice as well .	非常貧窮的人別無選擇 。 這是我們要改變現狀 , 讓窮人也有選擇 。
the roots and shoots groups all choose three projects .	根與芽計畫團體都選擇三個項目 。
it depends on how old they are , and which country , whether they're in a city or rural , as to what kinds of projects .	這取決於他們幾歲 , 還有哪個國家 , 無論他們是在城市或鄉村 , 看他們是哪個項目 。
but basically , we have programs now from preschool right through university , with more and more adults starting their own roots and shoots groups .	但基本上 , 我們現在有從幼兒園到大學的計畫 , 有越來越多的成人開始他們自己的根與芽的群體 。
and every group chooses , between them , three different kinds of project to make this a better world , recognizing that all these different problems are interconnected and impinge on each other .	每個團體都選擇這三個不同的項目 , 來讓這個更美好的世界 , 讓大家知道 , 所有這些不同的問題都是互相關聯的 , 會互相影響的 。
so one of their projects will be to help their own human community .	所以 , 他們的其中一個計畫 , 將是要協助他們自己的人類社區 。
and then , if they're able , they may raise money to help communities in other parts of the world .	然後 , 如果他們能夠的話 , 他們就能夠籌措資金 , 幫助世界上其他地區的社區 。
one of their projects will be to help animals not just wildlife , domestic animals as well .	他們的其中一個計畫是幫助動物們-不僅僅是野生動物 , 還有家養動物 。
and one of their projects will be to help the environment that we all share .	他們的其中一個計畫 , 將是要幫助我們所共享的環境 。
and woven throughout all of this is a message of learning to live in peace and harmony within ourselves , in our families , in our communities , between nations , between cultures , between religions and between us and the natural world .	把這一切交織在一起就是一個關於學習如何在和平、和諧中生活的訊息在我們的家庭、在我們的社區、在國家之間、在文化與宗教之間、在我們之間、在我們之間、在我們之間、在我們之間、以及在自然世界中 。
we need the natural world . we cannot go on destroying it at the rate we are .	我們需要自然世界 。 我們不能以我們的速度 , 繼續破壞它 。
we not do have more than this one planet .	我們沒有超過這個星球 。
just picking one or two of the projects right here in africa that the roots and shoots groups are doing , one or two projects only in tanzania , in uganda , kenya , south africa , congobrazzaville , sierra leone , cameroon and other groups . and as i say , it's in 97 countries around the world .	只是挑出一兩個在非洲的計畫根與芽的團體正在進行的計畫一、兩個計畫僅限於坦尚尼亞、烏干達、肯亞、南非、剛果巴拉薩維爾、獅子山共和國、喀麥隆和其他團體 。 正如我說的 , 它在世界上九十七個國家實行 。
of course , they're planting trees . they're growing organic vegetables .	當然 , 他們在種樹 。 他們種有機蔬菜 。
they're working in the refugee camps , with chickens and selling the eggs for a little amount of money , or just using them to feed their families , and feeling a sense of pride and empowerment , because they're no longer helpless and depending on others with their vegetables and their chickens .	他們在難民營工作 , 和雞隻一起 , 並賣掉一小筆錢 , 或僅僅是用它們來餵飽他們的家庭 , 並感受到一種自豪和自主的感覺 , 因為它們不再無助 , 取決於他人 , 用他們種植的蔬菜和他們的雞隻 。
it's being used in uganda to give some psychological help to exchild soldiers .	它被用在烏干達 , 給予某些心理上的幫助 , 給予一些野兵兵的心理上的幫助 。
doing projects like this is bringing them out of themselves .	做像這樣的計畫是把他們自己帶出來 。
once again , they're useful members of society .	再一次 , 他們是有用的社會成員 。
we have this program in prisons as well .	我們在監獄裡也有這個計畫 。
so , there's no time for more roots and shoots now .	所以 , 現在沒有更多根與芽的時機 。
but oh , they're also working on hiv/aids .	但 , 喔 , 他們也在研究愛滋病 。
that's a very important component of roots and shoots , with older kids talking to younger ones .	那是根與芽成分非常重要的部分 , 讓年長的孩子和年紀較小的孩子交談 。
and unwanted pregnancies and things like that , which young people listen to better from other youth , rather than adults .	而不必要的懷孕和類似的事情 , 那些年輕人會更傾聽其他年輕人的心聲 , 而不是成年人 。
hope . that's the question i get asked as i'm going around the world: " jane , you've seen so many terrible things , you've seen your chimpanzees decrease in number from about one million , at the turn of the century , to no more than 150 , 000 now , and the same with so many other animals .	希望 。 那是我在世界各地會被問到的問題: 「 珍 , 你見過這麼多可怕的事 , 你見到你的黑猩猩們的數量減少 , 從一百萬 , 到一百五十萬 , 到現在不超過十五萬 , 和許多其他動物都一樣 。
forests disappearing , deserts where once there was forest .	森林消失 , 曾經是森林的沙漠 。
do you really have hope ? " well , yes .	你真的有希望嗎 ? " 嗯 , 是的 。
you can't come to a conference like ted and not have hope , can you ?	你不能來參加像ted一樣的研討會 , 沒有希望 , 你能嗎 ?
and of course , there's hope . one is this amazing human brain .	當然 , 還有希望 。 一個是這令人驚奇的人類大腦 。
and i mean , think of the technologies .	我的意思是 , 想一想那些科技
and i've just been so thrilled , finally , to come to people talking about compost latrines .	最後 , 我實在太激動了 , 要來找人談堆肥式廁所 。
it's one of my hobbyhorses .	它是我的一個嗜好 。
we just flush all this water down the lavatory , it's terrible .	我們只要把這些水往下沖就好 , 真是糟糕 。
and then talking about renewable energy desperately important .	再來談再生能源絕對是很重要的 。
do we care about the planet for our children ?	我們要為我們的孩子關心地球嗎 ?
how many of us have children or grandchildren , nieces , nephews ?	我們當中有多少人有小孩、孫子、姪子、姪子 ?
do we care about their future ?	我們關心他們的未來嗎 ?
