and if we care about their future , we , as the elite around the world , we can do something about it . we can make choices as to how we live each day .	如果我們關心他們的未來 , 我們身為這世界的精英 , 我們能做點什麼 。 我們能做出選擇 , 決定我們每天怎麼過生活 。
what we buy . what we wear .	我們買什麼、穿什麼
and choose to make these choices with the question , how will this affect the environment around me ?	選擇以問題做這些選擇 , 這將如何影響我周遭的環境 ?
how will it affect the life of my child when he or she grows up ?	會如何影響我孩子長大後的生活 ?
or my grandchild , or whatever it is .	或是我的孫子 , 或任何
so the human brain , coupled with the human heart , and we join hands around the world .	所以人腦 , 與人心結合 , 我們加入世界各地的人腦 。
and that's what ted is helping so well with , and google who help us , and esri are helping us with mapping in gombe national park .	這就是ted對此的幫助 , google也幫助我們 , esri也幫助我們繪製岡貝國家公園的地圖 。
all of these technologies we can use .	所有這些我們可以運用的科技
now let's link them , and it's beginning to happen , isn't it ?	現在讓我們把它們串連起來 , 而它也開始發生了 , 不是嗎 ?
you've heard about it this afternoon . it's beginning to happen .	今天下午你們都聽過它 , 開始發生了 。
this change , this change . to see change that we must have if we care about the future .	這樣的改變、這樣的改變、如果我們關心未來 , 我們一定要看到的改變 。
and the next reason for hope nature is amazingly resilient .	下一個理由是對大自然的期望是驚人的恢復力 。
you can take an area that's absolutely destroyed , with time and perhaps some help it can regenerate .	你可以將一個絕對毀滅的地區 , 利用時間 , 也許還能協助它再生 。
and an example is the tacare program .	而一個例子是養護方案 。
i told you , where a seemingly dead tree stump if you stop hacking them for firewood , which you don't need to because you have wood lots , then in five years you can have a 30foot tree .	我剛說過 , 看似死去的樹木殘渣--如果你停止為了生火 , 那你就不需要因為你擁有很多木質 , 然後在五年內 , 你就可以有一棵三十英尺高的樹 。
and animals , almost on the brink of extinction , can be given a second chance . that's my next book .	而動物 , 幾乎在絕種的邊緣可以得到第二次機會 。 這是我的下一本書 。
it's inspiring . and it brings me to my last category of hope , and we've heard about this so much in the last two days: this indomitable human spirit . this determination of people , the resilience of the human spirit , so that people who you would think would be battered by poverty , or disease , or whatever , can pull themselves up out of it , sometimes with a helping hand , and take their part in society , and take their part in changing the world .	這是很鼓舞人心的 。 這也帶出了我最後一類的希望 。 我們在過去兩天都聽說了這許多事情:這種不屈不撓的人類精神 。 這種人們對人類精神的堅韌決心 , 以致於人們 , 那些你認為是貧窮、疾病 , 或其他 , 將他們自己從貧窮中抽離出來的人們 , 有時還能幫忙 , 並且帶著他們的部份在社會上 , 帶著他們的部份在改變世界 。
and just to think of one or two people out of africa who are just really inspiring .	想想那些真正激勵人心的非洲人物 。
we could make a very long list , but obviously nelson mandela , emerging from 17 years of hard physical labor , 23 years of imprisonment , with this amazing ability to forgive , so that he could lead his nation out the evil regime of apartheid without a bloodbath .	我們可以列出很長的清單 , 但很明顯的 , 納爾遜•曼德拉 , 從17年的辛苦勞力 , 監禁期間 , 由這驚人的原諒人 , 讓他能夠帶領他的國家走出沒有血液的種族隔離政權 。
ken sarowiwa , in nigeria , who took on the giant oil companies , and although people around the world tried their best , was executed .	奈及利亞的沙羅維瓦對巨大的石油公司取消了 , 雖然全世界的人都嘗試過最好的辦法 , 但卻被處決了 。
people like this are so inspirational .	像這樣的人如此激勵人心 。
people like this are the role models we need for young africans .	像這樣的人就是我們需要年輕非洲青年的典範 。
and we need some environmental role models as well , and i've been hearing some of them today .	我們也需要一些環保的榜樣 , 我今天也已經聽過了一些 。
so i'm really grateful for this opportunity to share this message again , with everyone at ted .	所以 , 我真的很感激有這個機會再次與ted的每個人分享這個訊息 。
and i hope that some of us can get together and talk about some of these things , especially the roots and shoots program .	我希望我們當中的一些人能聚在一起討論這些事情 , 特別是根與芽的計畫 。
and just a last word on that the young woman who's running this entire conference center , i met her today .	最後我要跟那位經營這整場會議中心的年輕女子談話 , 我今天見到她 。
she came up so excited , with her certificate . she was [in] roots and shoots .	她很興奮 , 拿著她的證書 。 她是根與芽成員 。
she was in the leadership in dar es salaam .	她在daressalaam的領導階層
she said it's helped her to do what she's doing .	她說這可以幫助她做到她正在做的事 。
and it was very , very exciting for me to meet her and see just one example of how young people , when they are empowered , given the opportunity to take action , to make the world a better place , truly are our hope for tomorrow .	對我來說 , 非常興奮 , 讓我看到一個例子 , 說明年輕人在被賦予能力時 , 能有機會採取行動 , 讓世界變得更好 , 真正是我們未來的希望 。
artist dianna cohen shares some tough truths about plastic pollution in the ocean and in our lives and some thoughts on how to free ourselves from the plastic gyre .	藝術家戴安娜.柯恩分享了一些堅韌的真理 , 關於塑膠污染在海洋和生活中 , 以及一些思想在如何將我們自己從塑膠垃圾漩渦中解放 。
consumerism , global issues , green , mission blue , oceans , plastic	消費主義、全球性議題、綠色、使命藍色、海洋、塑膠製品 。
dianna cohen: tough truths about plastic pollution	diannacohen:關於塑膠污染的堅韌真相
i'm a visual artist , and i'm also one of the cofounders of the plastic pollution coalition .	我是視覺藝術家 , 同時也是塑膠污染聯盟的發起人之一 。
i've been working with plastic bags , which i cut up and sew back together as my primary material for my artwork for the last 20 years .	我一直在使用塑膠袋 , 我剪開和縫合拼湊起來 , 做為我藝術作品的主要材料 , 過去二十年來 。
i turn them into two and threedimensional pieces and sculptures and installations .	我把它們變成二維立體的雕塑和裝置藝術品 。
upon working with the plastic , after about the first eight years , some of my work started to fissure and break down into smaller little bits of plastic .	前八年左右 , 我的工作開始產生裂縫 , 分解成更小的塑膠塊 。
and i thought , " great .	我心想: 「 太棒了 。
it's ephemeral just like us . "	跟我們一樣 , 是短暫的 。 」
upon educating myself a little further about plastics , i actually realized this was a bad thing .	等我對塑膠的教育再多了一點 , 我其實意識到這是件壞事 。
it's a bad thing that plastic breaks down into smaller little bits , because it's always still plastic .	塑膠會分解成小一點的壞東西 , 因為它總是塑膠的 。
and what we're finding is that a lot of it is in the marine environment .	我們發現 , 很多在海洋環境裡 ,
i then , in the last few years , learned about the pacific garbage patch and the gyre .	在過去幾年 , 我學到了太平洋垃圾環流和垃圾環流的概念 。
and my initial reaction and i think this is a lot of people's first reaction to learning about it is , " oh my god !	而我最初的反應我想這是很多人對學習的第一反應 , " 天哪 !
we've got to go out there and clean this thing up . "	我們必須到外面去清理這個東西 。 」
so i actually developed a proposal to go out with a cargo ship and two decommissioned fishing trawlers , a crane , a chipping machine and a coldmolding machine .	所以我真的提出了一個提案 , 去搭配一艘貨船 , 和兩艘退休的漁船 , 一座起重機 , 一座起重機和一台冷模機 。
and my intention was to go out to the gyre , raise awareness about this issue and begin to pick up the plastic , chip it into little bits and cold mold it into bricks that could potentially be used as building materials in underdeveloped communities .	我打算要出去健身房 , 提高對這個議題的認知 , 開始拿起塑膠 , 將塑膠製成小塊 , 讓塑膠在未開發的社區中 , 能夠被用作建築材料 。
i began talking with people who actually had been out to the gyre and were studying the plastic problem in the marine environment and upon doing so , i realized actually that cleaning it up would be a very small drop in the bucket relative to how much is being generated every day around the world , and that actually i needed to back up and look at the bigger picture .	我開始跟實際去過垃圾漩渦的人談話他們正在研究海洋裡的塑膠問題接著我意識到 , 把塑膠清乾淨是和全世界每天生產的垃圾相對的一小滴而我需要退一步審視更大的規模
and the bigger picture is: we need to find a way to turn off the faucet .	而更大的情況是:我們需要找到一種方式 , 把水龍頭關掉 。
we need to cut the spigot of singleuse and disposable plastics , which are entering the marine environment every day on a global scale .	我們需要切開這些用過即丟的塑膠製品 , 這些塑膠每天都在海洋環境中 , 以全球的規模進入 。
so in looking at that , i also realized that i was really angry .	所以 , 看著這個 , 我也了解到 , 我真的很憤怒 。
i wasn't just concerned about plastic that you're trying to imagine out in the middle of the pacific ocean of which i have learned there are now 11 gyres , potentially , of plastic in five major oceans in the world .	我不只關心塑膠你還想在太平洋中間想像一下現在有11個塑膠垃圾漩渦遍佈世界上五大洋
it's not just that gyre of plastic that i'm concerned about it's the gyre of plastic in the supermarket .	不僅僅是那個我關心的塑膠垃圾漩渦還有那個超市裡塑膠的漩渦
i'd go to the supermarket and all of my food is packaged in plastic .	我會去超市 , 食物全都是用塑膠包裝的 。
all of my beverages are packaged in plastic , even at the health food market .	我所有的飲料都用塑膠包裝 , 即使在健康食品市場也一樣 。
i'm also concerned about the plastic in the refrigerator , and i'm concerned about the plastic and the toxins that leach from plastic into us and into our bodies .	我也很關心冰箱裡的塑膠以及從塑膠包裝進入我們體內的塑膠和毒素 。
so i came together with a group of other people who were all looking at this issue , and we created the plastic pollution coalition .	所以我跟其他一群人聚在一起他們都在關注這個議題我們創造了塑膠污染聯盟
we have many initiatives that we're working on , but some of them are very basic .	我們有許多我們正在努力的計畫 , 但有些是非常基本的 。
one is: if 80 to 90 percent of what we're finding in the ocean of the marine debris that we're finding in the ocean is plastic , then why don't we call it what it is .	其一是:如果我們在海洋中所發現的80% ~ 90%是塑膠 , 那麽我們就不叫它塑膠了 。
recycling everybody kind of ends their books about being sustainable and greening with the idea of recycling .	把所有人都回收利用回收的書作為永續經營和環保的概念 。
you put something in a bin and you don't have to think about it again .	把東西放進一個桶子裡 , 不用再想了 。
what is the reality of that ?	什麼是實際情況呢 ?
in the united states , less than seven percent of our plastics are recycled .	在美國 , 塑膠回收的比例不到7% 。
and if you really look into it , particularly when it comes to plastic bottles , most of it is only downcycled , or incinerated , or shipped to china .	如果你真的去看它 , 特別是塑膠瓶 , 大部分的塑膠只有回收或燒開 , 或運到中國去 。
it is downcycled and turned into lesser things , while a glass bottle can be a glass bottle again or can be used again a plastic bottle can never be a plastic bottle again .	它會被降級回收 , 轉換成比較少的東西 , 雖然玻璃瓶可以再次變成玻璃瓶 , 或者再次使用塑膠瓶 , 卻不會再變成塑膠瓶 。
so this is a big issue for us .	所以這對我們來說是個重大的問題 。
another thing that we're looking at and asking people to think about is we've added a fourth r onto the front of the " reduce , reuse , recycle , " three r's , and that is refuse .	我們還看到另一件事 , 並要求大家去思考 , 我們已經在 「 減少、再利用、回收 」 前面加上第四個r , 也就是拒絕 。
whenever possible , refuse singleuse and disposable plastics .	無論何時 , 拒絕單一使用及可丟棄的塑膠 。
alternatives exist ; some of them are very oldschool .	替代方案是存在的 ; 有些是非常老派的 。
i myself am now collecting these cool pyrex containers and using those instead of glad and tupperware containers to store food in .	我現在在收集這些很酷的pyrex容器 , 並使用那些不用塑膠、不用塑膠的容器來儲存食物 。
and i know that i am doing a service to myself and my family .	我知道我在為自己和我的家人做服務 。
it's very easy to pick up a stainlesssteel bottle or a glass bottle , if you're traveling and you've forgotten to bring your stainlesssteel bottle and fill that up with water or filtered water , versus purchasing plastic bottled water .	很容易拿起一個不銹鋼瓶或玻璃瓶 , 如果你在旅行 , 卻忘了帶你的不銹鋼瓶裝水 , 把它裝滿水或過濾水 , 而不是購買塑膠瓶裝水 。
i guess what i want to say to everybody here and i know that you guys know a lot about this issue is that this is a huge problem in the oceans , but this is a problem that we've created as consumers and we can solve .	我猜我想對在座的各位說的──我知道在座的各位都知道這議題很多──這在海洋是個很大的問題 , 但這是身為消費者的我們所造成的問題 , 且我們能解決 。
we can solve this by raising awareness of the issue and teaching people to choose alternatives .	我們可以藉由提高對這個議題的認知 , 並教導大家選擇替代方案 。
so whenever possible , to choose alternatives to singleuse plastics .	所以 , 無論何時 , 要選擇用過的塑膠替代品 。
we can cut the stem tide the stem of this into our oceans and in doing so , save our oceans , save our planet , save ourselves .	我們可以把這首詩的潮汐切成我們的海洋 , 這樣做 , 拯救我們的海洋 , 拯救我們的地球 , 拯救我們自己 。
this demo from pattie maes' lab at mit , spearheaded by pranav mistry was the buzz of ted . it's a wearable device with a projector that paves the way for profound interaction with our environment . imagine " minority report " and then some .	帕蒂馬斯在麻省理工學院的實驗室發表此項展示 , 帕納•密斯是ted的鬥士 。 它是一種穿戴式裝置 , 配上投影機 , 為我們與環境的互動鋪路 。 想像 「 少數民族報告 」 然後 , 有些 。
demo , design , interface design , technology	展示 , 設計 , 介面設計 , 科技
pattie maes and pranav mistry demo sixthsense	帕蒂馬斯和帕納夫錯誤在第六感時呈現了第六感 。
i've been intrigued by this question of whether we could evolve or develop a sixth sense a sense that would give us seamless access and easy access to metainformation or information that may exist somewhere that may be relevant to help us make the right decision about whatever it is that we're coming across .	我一直對這個問題很有興趣 , 關於我們能否演化出或發展出第六感──一種能夠讓我們無縫接觸、容易取得的代謝或訊息 , 可能存在於某處 , 可能與我們息息相關 , 協助我們做出正確的決定 , 決定我們所面對的是什麼 。
and some of you may argue , well , don't today's cell phones do that already ?	有些人可能會說 , 嗯 , 現今的手機不就有這種功能嗎 ?
but i would say no .	但我會說不是 。
when you meet someone here at ted and this is the top networking place , of course , of the year you don't shake somebody's hand and then say , " can you hold on for a moment while i take out my phone and google you ? "	當你在ted與某人會面時 , 當然這是第一年的網路排名你不和某人握手然後說: 「 你能否在我剛剛拿出手機和谷歌的時候保持住一下 ? 」
or when you go to the supermarket and you're standing there in that huge aisle of different types of toilet papers , you don't take out your cell phone , and open a browser , and go to a website to try to decide which of these different toilet papers is the most ecologically responsible purchase to make .	或是當你到超級市場站在那條巨大的馬桶遊走道中 , 你不會拿出手機 , 打開瀏覽器 , 到一個網站 , 試著決定這些不同的衛生紙中 , 哪些是最環保的購買方式 , 哪些是最環保的 。
so we don't really have easy access to all this relevant information that can just help us make optimal decisions about what to do next and what actions to take .	所以我們並不容易取得所有相關的資訊 , 能夠協助我們做出最佳決策 , 決定接下來要做什麼、要採取什麼行動 。
and so my research group at the media lab has been developing a series of inventions to give us access to this information in a sort of easy way , without requiring that the user changes any of their behavior .	所以我在媒體實驗室的研究團隊一直在開發一系列的發明 , 讓我們能以簡單的方式取得這些資訊 , 不用要求使用者改變他們的行為 。
and i'm here to unveil our latest effort , and most successful effort so far , which is still very much a work in process .	我來這裡就是要揭開我們最新的努力 , 目前為止最成功的努力 , 這個過程還是很成功的 。
i'm actually wearing the device right now and we've sort of cobbled it together with components that are off the shelf and that , by the way , only cost 350 dollars at this point in time .	其實我現在穿著這套裝置我們有點像把它和那些從架子上拿出來的零件結合在一起--順帶一提 , 這套裝置現在的成本只有350美元 。
i'm wearing a camera , just a simple webcam , a portable , batterypowered projection system with a little mirror .	我戴著相機 , 只是簡單的網路攝影機 , 一個攜帶電池、電池驅動的投影系統 , 配上一個小鏡子 。
these components communicate to my cell phone in my pocket which acts as the communication and computation device .	這些元件是我口袋裡的手機 , 用來當作通訊和計算的裝置 。
and in the video here we see my student pranav mistry , who's really the genius who's been implementing and designing this whole system .	在這段影片中 , 我們看到我的學生帕納•密特里 , 他真的是正在實施及設計這整個系統的天才 。
and we see how this system lets him walk up to any surface and start using his hands to interact with the information that is projected in front of him .	我們看到這個系統讓他走到任何表面上 , 開始用他的手來和前面投影出來的資訊互動 。
the system tracks the four significant fingers .	系統會追蹤這四隻重要的手指
in this case , he's wearing simple marker caps that you may recognize .	在這個案例中 , 他穿著你可能認得的簡單馬克杯 。
but if you want a more stylish version you could also paint your nails in different colors .	但如果你想要比較時髦的版本 , 你也可以把指甲塗成不同顏色 。
and the camera basically tracks these four fingers and recognizes any gestures that he's making so he can just go to , for example , a map of long beach , zoom in and out , etc .	攝影機基本上能追蹤這四隻手指並且辨識出他的任何手勢舉例來說 , 他可以直接去看一個長灘的地圖 , 放大等等 。
the system also recognizes iconic gestures such as the " take a picture " gesture , and then takes a picture of whatever is in front of you .	這個系統還能辨識出具象徵性的手勢例如 「 拿一張照片 」 這個手勢 , 然後拍下你眼前的事物 。
and when he then walks back to the media lab , he can just go up to any wall and project all the pictures that he's taken , sort through them and organize them , and resize them , etc . , again using all natural gestures .	當他走回媒體實驗室後 , 他可以走到任何一面牆前投影他拍的照片 , 經過他們 , 分類管理 , 然後整理這些照片 , 再一次 , 使用全然的手勢 。
so , some of you most likely were here two years ago and saw the demo by jeff han or some of you may think , " well , doesn't this look like the microsoft surface table ? "	所以 , 你們當中可能有些人兩年前就在這裡看到傑夫漢的展示 , 或你們當中可能有人會想: 「 這不像微軟的平面桌子嗎 ? 」
and yes , you also interact using natural gestures , both hands , etc .	是的 , 你也會用自然的手勢互動 , 雙手等等 。
but the difference here is that you can use any surface , you can walk to up to any surface , including your hand if nothing else is available and interact with this projected data .	但這裡的不同點是 , 你可以用任何表面 , 你可以走到任何表面 , 包括你的手 , 如果有什麼其他的資料是可以用的 , 且和投影的資料做互動 。
the device is completely portable , and can be . . .	裝置是完全可攜帶的 , 也可以是...
so one important difference is that it's totally mobile .	所以 , 有一個重要的不同點是 , 它是完全移動的 。
another even more important difference is that in mass production this would not cost more tomorrow than today's cell phones and would actually not sort of be a bigger packaging could look a lot more stylish than this version that i'm wearing around my neck .	另一個更重要的不同點是 , 大量生產的成本不會比現今的手機來得高 , 更不會是像這樣大型的包裝 , 會比我脖子上戴的這個版本還要時髦的多 。
but other than letting some of you live out your fantasy of looking as cool as tom cruise in " minority report , " the reason why we're really excited about this device is that it really can act as one of these sixthsense devices that gives you relevant information about whatever is in front of you .	除了讓你們其中一些人活出自己的幻想 , 像是在《關鍵報告》裡 , 湯姆克魯斯 , 我們對這個裝置感到非常興奮的原因是 , 它真的能夠扮演第六感的裝置的角色 , 它能提供你關於眼前事物的相關資訊 。
so we see pranav here going into the supermarket and he's shopping for some paper towels .	我們看到帕納進入超級市場 , 他要購買一些紙巾 。
and , as he picks up a product the system can recognize the product that he's picking up , using either image recognition or marker technology , and give him the green light or an orange light .	當他拿起一樣產品時 , 系統可以辨識出他所撿到的產品 , 用的是影像辨識或是標記技術 , 給他綠燈或橘燈 。
he can ask for additional information .	他可以尋求額外的資訊 。
so this particular choice here is a particularly good choice , given his personal criteria .	根據他的個人標準 , 這個特殊的選擇是特別好的選擇 。
some of you may want the toilet paper with the most bleach in it rather than the most ecologicallyresponsible choice .	有些人可能會想用最漂白的衛生紙 , 而不是最環保的選擇 。
if he picks up a book in the bookstore , he can get an amazon rating it gets projected right on the cover of the book .	如果他在書店裡拿起一本書 , 他可以拿到亞馬遜的評分--它會直接投影到書的封面上 。
this is juan's book , our previous speaker , which gets a great rating , by the way , at amazon .	這是胡安的書 , 我們之前的講者 , 順帶一提 , 在亞馬遜 , 得到了很好的評分 。
and so , pranav turns the page of the book and can then see additional information about the book reader comments , maybe sort of information by his favorite critic , etc .	所以 , 帕納把書的這一頁翻過來 , 就能看到額外的資訊──讀者評論 , 可能是他最喜歡的評論家評論 , 等等 。
if he turns to a particular page he finds an annotation by maybe an expert of a friend of ours that gives him a little bit of additional information about whatever is on that particular page .	如果他翻到特定的一頁 , 找到我們朋友的專家寫的註解 , 會給他一點額外的資訊 , 知道那一頁有什麼 。
reading the newspaper it never has to be outdated .	閱讀報紙--它永遠不用過時--
you can get video annotations of the event that you're reading about you can get the latest sports scores etc .	你可以收集到關於你正在閱讀的事件的影片註解--你可以得到最新的運動分數等等 。
this is a more controversial one .	這是更具爭議性的 。
as you interact with someone at ted , maybe you can see a word cloud of the tags , the words that are associated with that person in their blog and personal web pages .	當你在ted與某人互動時 , 也許你能看到一個字雲 , 一個與那個人在部落格和個人網頁連結的字 。
in this case , the student is interested in cameras , etc .	在這種情況下 , 學生對相機很有興趣 , 等等 。
on your way to the airport , if you pick up your boarding pass , it can tell you that your flight is delayed , that the gate has changed , etc .	在你前往機場的路上 , 如果你拿起你的登機證 , 它可以告訴你你的航班被延遲了 , 登機門已經改變了 , 等等 。
and , if you need to know what the current time is it's as simple as drawing a watch on your arm .	如果你需要知道現在的時間 , 就如同在你手臂上畫一支手錶一樣簡單 。
so that's where we're at so far in developing this sixth sense that would give us seamless access to all this relevant information about the things that we may come across .	這就是我們目前正在開發的第六感能夠讓我們對即將到來的所有相關資訊無縫地取得 。
my student pranav , who's really , like i said , the genius behind this .	我的學生帕納 , 他真的 , 就像我說的 , 這背後的天才 。
he does deserve a lot of applause because i don't think he's slept much in the last three months , actually .	他確實應該得到許多掌聲 , 因為我不認為他在過去三個月中睡在那段時間 。
and his girlfriend is probably not very happy about him either .	他的女朋友大概也不太高興他 。
but it's not perfect yet , it's very much a work in progress .	但這還不是最完美的 , 這可是一件很不完美的事 。
and who knows , maybe in another 10 years we'll be here with the ultimate sixth sense brain implant .	誰知道呢 , 或許再過十年我們將會與植入腦內的終極第六感來這裡 。
phyllis rodriguez and aicha elwafi have a powerful friendship born of unthinkable loss . rodriguez' son was killed in the world trade center attacks on september 11 , 2001 ; elwafi's son zacarias moussaoui was convicted of a role in those attacks and is serving a life sentence . in hoping to find peace , these two moms have come to understand and respect one another .	phyllisrodriguez和aichaelwafi有一個強大的友誼 , 由於難以想像的損失而產生 。 rodriguez的兒子在2001年9月11日受到世貿中心攻擊 , elwafi的兒子zacariasmoussaoui被定罪 , 在這些攻擊中 , 被判有很大的好友誼 。 希望能找到和平的人生 。 這兩個媽媽的母親 , 希望能了解並尊重他 。
culture , global issues , politics	文化、全球議題、政治、
9/11 healing: the mothers who found forgiveness , friendship	911的療癒:那些發現寬恕、友情的母親
phyllis rodriguez: we are here today because of the fact that we have what most people consider an unusual friendship .	phyllisrodriguez:我們今天來到這裡是因為我們擁有大多數人所認為的非比尋常的友誼 。
and yet , it feels natural to us now .	然而 , 現在對我們來說卻是自然的 。
i first learned that my son had been in the world trade center on the morning of september 11th , 2001 .	我第一次得知我兒子在世界貿易中心在2001年9月11日的早晨 。
we didn't know if he had perished yet until 36 hours later .	我們不知道他是否真的死了 , 直到36小時之後 。
at the time , we knew that it was political .	當時 , 我們知道那是政治 。
we were afraid of what our country was going to do in the name of our son my husband , orlando , and i and our family .	我們害怕我們的國家將會做些什麼事以我們兒子的名字──我的丈夫奧蘭多 , 我和我們的家人 。
and when i saw it and yet , through the shock , the terrible shock , and the terrible explosion in our lives , literally , we were not vengeful .	當我看到它 , 然而 , 經歷了巨大的衝擊 , 和我們生命中可怕的爆炸 , 真的 , 我們並沒有復仇 。
and a couple of weeks later when zacarias moussaoui was indicted on six counts of conspiracy to commit terrorism , and the u . s . government called for a death penalty for him , if convicted , my husband and i spoke out in opposition to that , publicly .	幾個星期後當zacariasmoussaoui被指控六項恐怖主義的陰謀時 , 美國政府呼籲對他判死刑 , 如果定罪的話 , 我和我的丈夫對公開反對這點 。
through that and through human rights groups , we were brought together with several other victims' families .	透過這些以及透過人權組織 , 我們和其他幾個受害者家屬團體聚在一起 。
when i saw aicha in the media , coming over when her son was indicted , and i thought , " what a brave woman .	當我在媒體上看到aicha , 看到她兒子被指控說出來時 , 我心想: 「 這真是個勇敢的女人 。
someday i want to meet that woman when i'm stronger . "	總有一天 , 當我更強壯時 , 我想跟那女人見面 。 」
i was still in deep grief ; i knew i didn't have the strength .	我仍然在深深的悲傷中 , 我知道我沒有力量 。
i knew i would find her someday , or we would find each other .	我知道有一天我會找到她 , 或我們會找到彼此 。
because , when people heard that my son was a victim , i got immediate sympathy .	因為 , 當人們聽到我兒子是受害者時 , 我馬上得到了同情 。
but when people learned what her son was accused of , she didn't get that sympathy .	但當人們知道她兒子被指控的事 , 她卻沒有得到那份同情 。
but her suffering is equal to mine .	但她的痛苦是等同於我的痛苦 。
so we met in november 2002 , and aicha will now tell you how that came about .	我們在2002年11月認識 , aicha現在會告訴你這一切是怎麼一回事 。
aicha elwafi: good afternoon , ladies and gentlemen .	aichaelwafi:午安 , 各位先生女士 。
i am the mother of zacarias moussaoui .	我是zacariasmoussaoui的母親 。
and i asked the organization of human rights to put me in touch with the parents of the victims .	我也請人權組織讓我聯絡上了受害者的父母 。
so they introduced me to five families .	所以他們介紹我給五個家庭認識 。
and i saw phyllis , and i watched her .	我看到phyllis , 看著她
she was the only mother in the group .	她是小組裡唯一的媽媽
the others were brothers , sisters .	其他則是兄弟姐妹 。
and i saw in her eyes that she was a mother , just like me .	我看到在她眼中 , 她是一位母親 , 就像我一樣 。
i suffered a lot as a mother .	我作為一個媽媽很痛苦 。
i was married when i was 14 .	我十四歲時結婚 ,
i lost a child when i was 15 , a second child when i was 16 .	我在十五歲時失去了一個孩子 , 當我十六歲時 , 第二個孩子 。
so the story with zacarias was too much really .	所以zacarias的故事真的太多了 。
and i still suffer , because my son is like he's buried alive .	而我仍然在受苦 , 因為我兒子就像是被活埋了一樣 。
i know she really cried for her son .	我知道她真的為兒子而哭泣 。
but she knows where he is .	但她知道他在哪裡 。
my son , i don't know where he is .	我的兒子 , 我不知道他在哪裡 。
i don't know if he's alive . i don't know if he's tortured .	我不知道他是否還活著 , 不知道他是否受到折磨 ,
i don't know what happened to him .	我不知道他發生了什麼事 。
so that's why i decided to tell my story , so that my suffering is something positive for other women .	所以這就是為什麼我決定要說我的故事 , 這樣我的痛苦對其他女性來說是很正面的 。
for all the women , all the mothers that give life , you can give back , you can change .	對所有的女人 , 所有賦予生命的母親 , 你可以回饋 , 你可以改變 。
it's up to us women , because we are women , because we love our children .	取決於我們女人 , 因為我們是女人 , 因為我們愛我們的孩子 。
we must be handinhand and do something together .	我們一定要手牽手一起做些什麼 。
it's not against women , it's for us , for us women , for our children .	這不是反對女性這是為我們 , 為我們女人、為我們的孩子 。
i talk against violence , against terrorism .	我反對暴力 , 反對恐怖主義 。
i go to schools to talk to young , muslim girls so they don't accept to be married against their will very young .	我去學校跟年青的穆斯林女孩說話 , 這樣她們就不接受被她們的意志所傷 。
so if i can save one of the young girls , and avoid that they get married and suffer as much as i did , well this is something good .	所以如果我能拯救其中一個小女孩 , 並且避免她們跟我一樣結婚 , 遭受痛苦 , 這是件好事 。
this is why i'm here in front of you .	這就是為什麼我會在你們面前 。
pr: i would like to say that i have learned so much from aicha , starting with that day we had our very first meeting with other family members which was a very private meeting with security , because it was november 2002 , and , frankly , we were afraid of the superpatriotism of that time in the country those of us family members .	pr:我想說我從aicha身上學到好多東西從那天開始我們第一次與其他的家庭成員會面---這是一個非常私密的會議 , 因為當時是2002年的11月 , 而且 , 坦白說 , 我們害怕當時的超級愛國主義---我們這些家庭成員國內的成員 。
but we were all so nervous .	但我們都好緊張 。
" why does she want to meet us ? "	「 她為什麼想跟我們見面 ? 」
and then she was nervous .	後來她很緊張

then we sat in a circle with support , with help , from people experienced in this kind of reconciliation .	然後我們圍成一個圓圈 , 圍著支援 , 從人們在這種和解過程中所經歷的 。
and aicha started , and she said , " i don't know if my son is guilty or innocent , but i want to tell you how sorry i am for what happened to your families .	aicha開始了 , 她說: 「 我不知道我的兒子是有罪還是無辜 , 但我想告訴你們 , 我對你們家發生的事有多麼不好意思 。
i know what it is to suffer , and i feel that if there is a crime , a person should be tried fairly and punished . "	我知道這是怎樣的痛苦 , 我覺得如果有罪 , 一個人應該被公平的審判和懲罰 。 」
but she reached out to us in that way , and it was , i'd like to say , it was an icebreaker .	但她以那種方式與我們聯絡 , 當時的確 , 我想說 , 這是個破冰的破冰者 。
and what happened then is we all told our stories , and we all connected as human beings .	接下來發生的是 , 我們都說出了自己的故事 , 我們都以人類的身分來連結 。
by the end of the afternoon it was about three hours after lunch we'd felt as if we'd known each other forever .	到了下午完結的時候--大概是午餐後的三小時--我們覺得好像彼此認識了一輩子 。
now what i learned from her , is a woman , not only who could be so generous under these present circumstances and what it was then , and what was being done to her son , but the life she's had .	我從她身上學到的 , 她是一個女人 , 不只可以在現狀和當時的情況下如此慷慨 , 和正在對她兒子所做的事情 , 也是她所經歷的人生 。
i never had met someone with such a hard life , from such a totally different culture and environment from my own .	我從來沒有遇過某個人有著如此艱難的生活 , 和我的文化和環境截然不同 。
and i feel that we have a special connection , which i value very much .	我覺得我們有一種特別的聯繫 , 這是我非常重視的 。
and i think it's all about being afraid of the other , but making that step and then realizing , " hey , this wasn't so hard .	我認為這一切都是因為害怕對方 , 但做出那一步 , 接著就意識到: 「 嘿 , 這沒那麼難 。
who else can i meet that i don't know , or that i'm so different from ? "	我還能跟誰見面我不知道 , 或我和誰是如此不同 ? 」
so , aicha , do you have a couple of words for conclusion ?	所以 , aicha , 你有幾個字的結論嗎 ?
because our time is up .	因為我們的時間到了 。
aw: i wanted to say that we have to try to know other people , the other .	aw:我想說我們必須試著去認識其他人 。

i , like most of you , was sitting down , the day after christmas in 2004 , when i was watching the devastating news of the asian tsunami as it rolled in , playing out on tv .	我 , 和你們多數人一樣 , 在2004年聖誕節後的那天 , 我看著亞洲海嘯摧殘在電視上播出 。

that really stuck with me .	這令我印象深刻 。

okay , now for the science bit .	好的 , 現在對科學領域
before lifesaver , the best hand filters were only capable of filtering down to about 200 nanometers .	在lifesaver濾水之前 , 最好的手動過濾器只能過濾大小至200奈米 。
the smallest bacteria is about 200 nanometers .	最小的細菌大約是200奈米 。
so a 200nanometer bacteria is going to get through a 200nanometer hole .	所以一個200奈米的細菌將會穿過一個200奈米大的洞 。
the smallest virus , on the other hand , is about 25 nanometers .	另一方面 , 最小的病毒大約是25奈米 。
so that's definitely going to get through those 200 nanometer holes .	那絕對會穿過那200奈米大小的洞 。
lifesaver pores are 15 nanometers .	lifesaver濾水孔是15奈米 。
so nothing is getting through .	所以什麼都沒有經過 。

instead of shipping water , and using manmade processes to do it , let's use mother nature . she's got a fantastic system .	與其運送水和使用人造過程去做 , 不如利用大自然 。 她有一個絕妙的系統 。
she picks the water up from there , desalinates it , for free , transports it over there , and dumps it onto the mountains , rivers , and streams .	她從那裡取水 , 免費下水 , 將水運送到那邊 , 傾倒在山地、河川、以及溪流中 。

paddy ashdown claims that we are living in a moment in history where power is changing in ways it never has before . in a spellbinding talk at tedxbrussels he outlines the three major global shifts that he sees coming .	paddyashdown的說法:我們正生活在歷史上的這一刻 , 權力正在改變 , 以它從未有過的方式改變 。 在一次tedxbrusel的演說中 , 他提出三個全球重大的轉變 。

there's a poem written by a very famous english poet at the end of the 19th century .	有一首詩這麼寫道這是一個非常有名的英國詩人在十九世紀末寫的
it was said to echo in churchill's brain in the 1930s .	在30年代 , 據說在邱吉爾的腦袋裡起共鳴 。
and the poem goes: " on the idle hill of summer , lazy with the flow of streams , hark i hear a distant drummer , drumming like a sound in dreams , far and near and low and louder on the roads of earth go by , dear to friend and food to powder , soldiers marching , soon to die . "	這首詩是這麼寫的: 「 在夏日的小山丘上 , 帶著溪流的潮濕 , 我聽到了遠方的鼓聲 , 像夢中一樣鼓聲 , 遠、近、低沉、聲音低沉 , 走在路上 , 親愛的 , 親愛的食物 , 向粉末遊行 , 士兵們馬上就要死了 。 」
those who are interested in poetry , the poem is " a shropshire lad " written by a . e . housman .	那些對詩有興趣的人 , 這首詩叫做 「 許佛瑞拉斯拉夫人 」 , 由艾姆•豪斯曼寫的 。
but what housman understood , and you hear it in the symphonies of nielsen too , was that the long , hot , silvan summers of stability of the 19th century were coming to a close , and that we were about to move into one of those terrifying periods of history when power changes .	但是豪斯曼所理解的你也在尼爾森的交響曲中聽過就是十九世紀那漫長 , 炎熱的夏天即將來臨而我們即將邁向一個可怕的歷史時期那就是權力的改變
and these are always periods , ladies and gentlemen , accompanied by turbulence , and all too often by blood .	這些時期 , 各位先生女士 , 伴隨著騷動 , 常常都是血肉之軀 。
and my message for you is that i believe we are condemned , if you like , to live at just one of those moments in history when the gimbals upon which the established order of power is beginning to change and the new look of the world , the new powers that exist in the world , are beginning to take form .	我想傳達給大家的訊息是 , 我相信我們會被譴責 , 如果你們喜歡 , 生活在歷史上的那些時刻之一 , 那些已經建立的權力秩序已經開始改變世界的新樣貌 , 世界上存在的新勢力已經開始形成 。
and these are and we see it very clearly today nearly always highly turbulent times , highly difficult times , and all too often very bloody times .	這些是--而我們今天看到的很明顯--幾乎總是高度不安、高度艱難的時代 , 甚至是非常血腥的時代 。
by the way , it happens about once every century .	順帶一提 , 它每個世紀都發生一次 。
you might argue that the last time it happened and that's what housman felt coming and what churchill felt too was that when power passed from the old nations , the old powers of europe , across the atlantic to the new emerging power of the united states of america the beginning of the american century .	你也許會主張 , 最後一次發生的那就是豪斯曼所感覺到的而且邱吉爾也感覺到當權者從古老的國家傳到歐洲的舊勢力跨越大西洋傳到美國的新興權力就在美國的世紀初
and of course , into the vacuum where the tooold european powers used to be were played the two bloody catastrophes of the last century the one in the first part and the one in the second part: the two great world wars .	當然 , 在以前歐洲權力過剩的真空地區 , 曾被兩場血腥的災難給打中 , 在上個世紀 , 第一部份和第二部分:兩次世界大戰 。
mao zedong used to refer to them as the european civil wars , and it's probably a more accurate way of describing them .	毛澤東曾以 「 歐洲內戰 」 形容他們 , 這或許是比較正確的形容方式 。
well , ladies and gentlemen , we live at one of those times .	各位先生女士 , 我們生活在這些時代的其中之一 。
but for us , i want to talk about three factors today .	但對我們來說 , 我今天想談三個因素 。
and the first of these , the first two of these , is about a shift in power .	首先 , 上述兩者的差異在權力的轉移 。
and the second is about some new dimension which i want to refer to , which has never quite happened in the way it's happening now .	第二個是關於一些新的維度 , 我想要說明的 , 這種新的維度從來沒有像現在這樣發生過 。
but let's talk about the shifts of power that are occurring to the world .	但 , 咱們先來談談權力在全世界發生的轉變 。
and what is happening today is , in one sense , frightening because it's never happened before .	而今天的狀況是 , 在某種意義上 , 令人恐懼的 , 因為它從來沒有發生過 。
we have seen lateral shifts of power the power of greece passed to rome and the power shifts that occurred during the european civilizations but we are seeing something slightly different .	我們看到了橫向的權力轉變 , 希臘的權力傳到羅馬 , 以及在歐洲文明期間發生的權力移轉 , 但我們看到的有些稍微不同 。
for power is not just moving laterally from nation to nation .	權力不只是國與國之間的橫向移轉 。
it's also moving vertically .	同時垂直移動 。
what's happening today is that the power that was encased , held to accountability , held to the rule of law , within the institution of the nation state has now migrated in very large measure onto the global stage .	今日的情況是所投入的權力 , 受到責任的牽制 , 受到法治的牽制 , 在這個國家的制度下 , 如今已大幅度地遷移至全球階段 。
the globalization of power we talk about the globalization of markets , but actually it's the globalization of real power .	全球化的權力我們談論的是全球化的市場 , 但事實上 , 它是全球化的權力 。
and where , at the nation state level that power is held to accountability subject to the rule of law , on the international stage it is not .	哪裡呢 ? 在國家層面 , 權力是被賦予法律規範的責任 , 在國際舞台上則否 。
the international stage and the global stage where power now resides: the power of the internet , the power of the satellite broadcasters , the power of the money changers this vast moneygoround that circulates now 32 times the amount of money necessary for the trade it's supposed to be there to finance the money changers , if you like , the financial speculators that have brought us all to our knees quite recently , the power of the multinational corporations now developing budgets often bigger than mediumsized countries .	國際舞台就是現在的權力:網際網路的權力 , 衛星廣播的權力 , 貨幣的權力改變了這些巨大的經費 , 使得交易成為現在必須的32倍這些錢是應該要投入資金改變的人才行 。 如果你喜歡的話 , 我們的金融管道 , 最近常常常被忽略了一個多國企業所龐大的權力 。
these live in a global space which is largely unregulated , not subject to the rule of law , and in which people may act free of constraint .	這些居住在一個全球化的空間這實在是很大程度上是沒有規範的 , 不受法律規範的規範影響 , 而且人們可能不受限制的影響 。
now that suits the powerful up to a moment .	現在這套裝備將強大到一個時刻 。
it's always suitable for those who have the most power to operate in spaces without constraint , but the lesson of history is that , sooner or later , unregulated space space not subject to the rule of law becomes populated , not just by the things you wanted international trade , the internet , etc . but also by the things you don't want international criminality , international terrorism .	這總是適合那些擁有最強權的人不受約束的限制 , 但歷史的教訓是 , 遲早 , 未受規範的空間 , 不受法律規範的規則所規範 , 不僅僅是來自國際貿易、網路、等等 。 還有你不想要國際犯罪、國際恐怖主義等 。
the revelation of 9/11 is that even if you are the most powerful nation on earth , nevertheless , those who inhabit that space can attack you even in your most iconic of cities one bright september morning .	9•11事件的揭示就是 , 即使你是地球上最強大的國家 , 從此 , 那些居住空間的人 , 能夠攻擊你甚至在九月的最具代表性的城市──一個亮度的早晨 。
it's said that something like 60 percent of the four million dollars that was taken to fund 9/11 actually passed through the institutions of the twin towers which 9/11 destroyed .	據說 , 大約400萬美金的費用當中 , 有60%是用在911之前之前 , 911恐怖攻擊基金會的費用實際上是通過雙子星大樓的機構來支付911摧毀的目標 。
you see , our enemies also use this space the space of mass travel , the internet , satellite broadcasters to be able to get around their poison , which is about destroying our systems and our ways .	要知道 , 我們的敵人也會用這個空間──大眾旅行、網路、衛星廣播的空間 , 來破壞它們的毒害 , 也就是破壞我們的系統和方式 。
sooner or later , sooner or later , the rule of history is that where power goes governance must follow .	遲早、晚 , 歷史的規則就是權力走向何方 。
and if it is therefore the case , as i believe it is , that one of the phenomenon of our time is the globalization of power , then it follows that one of the challenges of our time is to bring governance to the global space .	如果我相信是這樣的 , 我們這個時代的其中一個現象就是權力全球化 , 那麼我們這個時代的一個挑戰就是把統治者帶上國際舞台 。
and i believe that the decades ahead of us now will be to a greater or lesser extent turbulent the more or less we are able to achieve that aim: to bring governance to the global space .	我相信未來幾十年 , 我們將有更好或更少的動亂 , 我們將能達成這個目標:把統治權帶到全球 。
now notice , i'm not talking about government .	現在請注意 , 我不是在說政府
i'm not talking about setting up some global democratic institution .	我不是在說要設立一些全球民主機構 ,
my own view , by the way , ladies and gentlemen , is that this is unlikely to be done by spawning more u . n . institutions .	順帶一提 , 各位先生女士 , 我自己認為透過推動更多的聯合國機構來實現這不太可能 。
if we didn't have the u . n . , we'd have to invent it .	如果沒有聯合國 , 我們就得發明
the world needs an international forum .	世界需要一個國際論壇
it needs a means by which you can legitimize international action .	它需要一個手段 , 讓你可以合法地將國際行動合法化 。
but when it comes to governance of the global space , my guess is this won't happen through the creation of more u . n . institutions .	但 , 談到全球空間的管理 , 我猜 , 這不會發生在聯合國建立更多的機構之前 。
it will actually happen by the powerful coming together and making treatybased systems , treatybased agreements , to govern that global space .	它會發生在強權聚在一起 , 建立以條約為基礎的制度 , 以條約為基礎的協議 , 來統治這個全球空間 。
and if you look , you can see them happening , already beginning to emerge .	如果你去看 , 你可以看到它們正在發生 , 已經開始出現了 。
the world trade organization: treatybased organization , entirely treatybased , and yet , powerful enough to hold even the most powerful , the united states , to account if necessary .	世界貿易組織:以條約為基礎的組織 , 完全是條約為基礎的 , 而且 , 強大到足以包容最強大的 , 美國 , 如果有必要的話 。
kyoto: the beginnings of struggling to create a treatybased organization .	京都議定書:努力奮鬥以創立一個條約為基礎的組織 。
the g20: we know now that we have to put together an institution which is capable of bringing governance to that financial space for financial speculation .	二十國集團現在知道 , 我們得建立一個能夠把統治權帶到金融空間的機構去做推測 。
and that's what the g20 is , a treatybased institution .	這就是g20 , 一個以條約為基礎的機構 。
now there's a problem there , and we'll come back to it in a minute , which is that if you bring the most powerful together to make the rules in treatybased institutions , to fill that governance space , then what happens to the weak who are left out ?	現在有個問題了 , 我們等一下會再回來談 , 就是如果你把最強大的力量集合在一起 , 做成以條約為基礎的制度的規則 , 來填補這方面的統治空間 , 那麼 , 剩下的那些弱者會怎麼樣 ?
and that's a big problem , and we'll return to it in just a second .	這是個大問題 , 我們等一下就會回到這問題上 。
so there's my first message , that if you are to pass through these turbulent times more or less turbulently , then our success in doing that will in large measure depend on our capacity to bring sensible governance to the global space .	所以 , 我的第一條信息是 , 如果你要在這些亂流中 , 多或少動盪一下 , 那麼我們在做這件事的成功 , 會取決於我們把合理的統治權帶到全球 。
and watch that beginning to happen .	請注意這開始發生 。
my second point is , and i know i don't have to talk to an audience like this about such a thing , but power is not just shifting vertically , it's also shifting horizontally .	我的第二點是 , 我知道我不需要像這樣跟觀眾談這件事 , 但權力不只是直向移轉 , 還能橫向移轉 。
you might argue that the story , the history of civilizations , has been civilizations gathered around seas with the first ones around the mediterranean , the more recent ones in the ascendents of western power around the atlantic .	你可能會爭辯說 , 這個故事 , 文明的歷史 , 一直都是文明聚集在海洋中 , 最早圍繞著地中海 , 是比較近期在大西洋的西方後裔 , 比較像大西洋 。
well it seems to me that we're now seeing a fundamental shift of power , broadly speaking , away from nations gathered around the atlantic [seaboard] to the nations gathered around the pacific rim .	在我看來 , 我們現在看到了基本權力的轉變 , 廣泛地說 , 遠離聚在大西洋岸邊的國家 , 聚集在太平洋上 。
now that begins with economic power , but that's the way it always begins .	這要從經濟權開始 , 但這才是真正的開始 。
you already begin to see the development of foreign policies , the augmentation of military budgets occurring in the other growing powers in the world .	你已經開始看到外交政策的發展 , 軍事預算的擴增 , 發生在世界上其他不斷增長的勢力 。
i think actually this is not so much a shift from the west to the east ; something different is happening .	我覺得這其實不是從西方移轉到東方不同的 ; 有些事正在發生 。
my guess is , for what it's worth , is that the united states will remain the most powerful nation on earth for the next 10 years , 15 , but the context in which she holds her power has now radically altered ; it has radically changed .	我的猜測是 , 對於它的價值 , 就是美國在接下來的十年 , 仍然是世界上最強大的國家 , 十五年 , 但她掌握的權力背景現在已經徹底改變了 。 它已經徹底改變了 。
we are coming out of 50 years , most unusual years , of history in which we have had a totally monopolar world , in which every compass needle for or against has to be referenced by its position to washington a world bestrode by a single colossus .	50年來 , 最不尋常的是歷史 , 我們有一個非常獨特的世界 , 每一個羅盤都需要指向一個華盛頓的最佳地位 。
but that's not a usual case in history .	但這在歷史上並不是常見的情況 。
in fact , what's now emerging is the much more normal case of history .	事實上 , 現在正在浮現的是一個更正常的歷史案例 。
you're beginning to see the emergence of a multipolar world .	你也開始看到多極化世界的出現 。
up until now , the united states has been the dominant feature of our world .	到目前為止 , 美國一直是我們這個世界的主導特徵 。
they will remain the most powerful nation , but they will be the most powerful nation in an increasingly multipolar world .	它們會保留最強的國家 , 但它們會是最強大的國家 , 在一個越來越極端的世界中 。
and you begin to see the alternative centers of power building up in china , of course , though my own guess is that china's ascent to greatness is not smooth .	然後你會開始看到 , 中國其他地方的權力建設中心 , 當然 , 我自己猜測 , 中國要達到偉大的目的並不是平順的 。
it's going to be quite grumpy as china begins to democratize her society after liberalizing her economy .	一切都會很糟糕 , 因為中國在解放她的經濟後 , 開始將她的社會民主化 。
but that's a subject of a different discussion .	但那是不同的討論主題 。
you see india , you see brazil .	你看印度、巴西
you see increasingly that the world now looks actually , for us europeans , much more like europe in the 19th century .	你可以看到 , 對我們歐洲人來說 , 世界看起來越來越像十九世紀的歐洲 。
europe in the 19th century: a great british foreign secretary , lord canning , used to describe it as the " european concert of powers . "	十九世紀的歐洲:英國的外交大秘書長 , 大法王坎寧 , 曾經形容它為 「 歐洲人的權力音樂會 」 。
there was a balance , a fivesided balance .	當時有一個平衡 , 一邊是五邊的平衡 。
britain always played to the balance .	英國向來平衡 。
if paris got together with berlin , britain got together with vienna and rome to provide a counterbalance .	如果巴黎跟柏林合作 , 英國就和維也納及羅馬合作 , 提供平衡 。
now notice , in a period which is dominated by a monopolar world , you have fixed alliances nato , the warsaw pact .	現在請注意 , 在這個被單一世界支配的時期 , 你有固定的加盟國-北約組織 , 也就是戰爭事務 。
a fixed polarity of power means fixed alliances .	固定兩極一致的權力代表固定的盟國 。
but a multiple polarity of power means shifting and changing alliances .	但 , 權力的多重兩極化就表示要轉移、改變盟國 。
and that's the world we're coming into , in which we will increasingly see that our alliances are not fixed .	這就是我們即將進入的世界 , 我們將看到我們的同盟國並非固定不變的 。
canning , the great british foreign secretary once said , " britain has a common interest , but no common allies . "	偉大的英國外交部長坎寧曾說過: 「 英國有一個共同的利益 , 但沒有共同的盟友 。 」
and we will see increasingly that even we in the west will reach out , have to reach out , beyond the cozy circle of the atlantic powers to make alliances with others if we want to get things done in the world .	我們也會看到 , 即使在西方國家也會伸出援手 , 不得不伸出援手 , 超越大西洋的舒適圈 , 與他人結盟 , 只要我們想在這個世界上完成 。
note , that when we went into libya , it was not good enough for the west to do it alone ; we had to bring others in .	注意 , 當我們進入利比亞時 , 光是西方國家是不夠的 ; 我們還得把其他人帶進來 。
we had to bring , in this case , the arab league in .	我們必須把阿拉伯聯盟也引進來
my guess is iraq and afghanistan are the last times when the west has tried to do it themselves , and we haven't succeeded .	我猜伊拉克和阿富汗是西方國家中最後一次嘗試自己做 , 我們還沒成功 。
my guess is that we're reaching the beginning of the end of 400 years i say 400 years because it's the end of the ottoman empire of the hegemony of western power , western institutions and western values .	我的猜測是 , 我們已經到達了400年年底 , 我說400年 , 因為這是鄂圖曼帝國的結束 , 代表西方的權力、西方的制度 , 以及西方的價值觀 。
you know , up until now , if the west got its act together , it could propose and dispose in every corner of the world .	你知道的 , 到目前為止 , 如果西方國家聯手了 , 它在世界各個角落都可以提出和反駁 。
but that's no longer true .	但這已經不是事實了 。
take the last financial crisis after the second world war .	以最後一次世界大戰後的金融危機為例 。
the west got together the bretton woods institution , world bank , international monetary fund the problem solved .	西方國家齊聚了布雷頓森林機構 , 世界銀行 , 國際貨幣基金組織--問題解決了 。
now we have to call in others .	現在我們必須號召他人
now we have to create the g20 .	現在我們必須創造出g20
now we have to reach beyond the cozy circle of our western friends .	現在我們必須超越西方的舒適圈 。
let me make a prediction for you , which is probably even more startling .	讓我為各位做個預測 , 這可能更讓人吃驚 。
i suspect we are now reaching the end of 400 years when western power was enough .	我猜我們現在已經達到400年後的終點 , 當時的西方強權已經足夠了 。
people say to me , " the chinese , of course , they'll never get themselves involved in peacemaking , multilateral peacemaking around the world . "	人們對我說: " 中國人當然永遠不會參與調停 , 和世界各地的調停調停 。 "
oh yes ? why not ?	有嗎 ? 為什麼不 ?
how many chinese troops are serving under the blue beret , serving under the blue flag , serving under the u . n . command in the world today ?	有多少中國軍隊在藍色貝雷斯底下服務 , 在藍色的旗幟下服務 , 在聯合國的指令下服務呢 ?
how many americans ? 11 .	美國有多少 ? 11個 。
what is the largest naval contingent tackling the issue of somali pirates ?	什麼是最大型的海軍陸戰隊在處理索馬利海盜的議題 ?
the chinese naval contingent .	中國海軍陸戰隊的內容 。
of course they are , they are a mercantilist nation .	當然他們是 , 他們是一個商人的國家 。
they want to keep the sea lanes open .	他們想讓海道保持開放 ,
increasingly , we are going to have to do business with people with whom we do not share values , but with whom , for the moment , we share common interests .	漸漸地 , 我們得要和那些不分享價值觀的人做生意 , 但和他們在一起 , 現在 , 我們會共享利益 。
it's a whole new different way of looking at the world that is now emerging .	用一個全新的角度來看現在正在興起的世界 。
and here's the third factor , which is totally different .	接下來是第三個因素 , 完全不同 。
today in our modern world , because of the internet , because of the kinds of things people have been talking about here , everything is connected to everything .	今天在我們的現代世界 , 由於網際網路 , 人們一直在談論的各式各樣的東西 , 每件事都與每件事有關 。
we are now interdependent .	我們現在是相互依賴的 。
we are now interlocked , as nations , as individuals , in a way which has never been the case before , never been the case before .	我們現在是相互關聯的國家 , 以個人的身分 , 以一個從未發生過的方式 , 從未發生過的方式 。
the interrelationship of nations , well it's always existed .	國家之間的相互關係 , 嗯 , 它一直都存在 。
diplomacy is about managing the interrelationship of nations .	外交就是管理國家之間的相互關係 。
but now we are intimately locked together .	但現在我們密切鎖在一起了 。
you get swine flu in mexico , it's a problem for charles de gaulle airport 24 hours later .	你在墨西哥得到了豬流感 , 24小時後對查爾斯•戴高爾的機場出問題了 。
lehman brothers goes down , the whole lot collapses .	雷曼兄弟下來了 , 整體來說 , 整個崩潰了 。
there are fires in the steppes of russia , food riots in africa .	俄羅斯的大草原發生火災非洲的糧食暴動
we are all now deeply , deeply , deeply interconnected .	我們現在都深深地、深深地緊緊相連 。
and what that means is the idea of a nation state acting alone , not connected with others , not working with others , is no longer a viable proposition .	意思就是 , 一個國家獨自行動 , 沒有與他人建立聯繫 , 不再與他人合作 , 這已經不是一個可行的主張了 。
because the actions of a nation state are neither confined to itself , nor is it sufficient for the nation state itself to control its own territory , because the effects outside the nation state are now beginning to affect what happens inside them .	因為一個國家的作為都不只侷限在自己國 , 也不足以讓國家本身來掌控自己的領土 , 因為國家外部的影響現在已經開始影響他們內在的一切 。
i was a young soldier in the last of the small empire wars of britain .	我年輕時曾在大英帝國戰爭時當過兵
at that time , the defense of my country was about one thing and one thing only: how strong was our army , how strong was our air force , how strong was our navy and how strong were our allies .	那時 , 我國的辯護是關於一件事的 , 只有一件事:我們的軍隊有多強 , 我們的空軍有多強 , 我們的海軍有多強 , 我們的盟友有多強 。
that was when the enemy was outside the walls .	那是敵人在城牆外
now the enemy is inside the walls .	現在敵人卻在牆內
now if i want to talk about the defense of my country , i have to speak to the minister of health because pandemic disease is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of agriculture because food security is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of industry because the fragility of our hitech infrastructure is now a point of attack for our enemies as we see from cyber warfare i have to speak to the minister of home affairs because who has entered my country , who lives in that terraced house in that inner city has a direct effect on what happens in my country as we in london saw in the 7/7 bombings .	現在 , 如果我想談談我的國家的國防 , 我必須要和健康部談談 , 因為全球性疾病對我來說是一個威脅 , 我必須和農業部談談 , 因為糧食安全對我的國家造成威脅 , 我必須和工業部談談 , 因為高科技公共設施的脆弱性對我們的敵人造成威脅 , 就如同我們從網路戰場上所看到的 , 我必須和國內的婦女們談談 , 因為我的房子受到威脅性影響 , 那是因為我們進入了倫敦的房子 。
it's no longer the case that the security of a country is simply a matter for its soldiers and its ministry of defense .	不再是這樣 , 一個國家的安全性只對軍人和國防部有影響 。
it's its capacity to lock together its institutions .	鎖定其機構的能力 。
and this tells you something very important .	而這告訴你非常重要的一點 。
it tells you that , in fact , our governments , vertically constructed , constructed on the economic model of the industrial revolution vertical hierarchy , specialization of tasks , command structures have got the wrong structures completely .	它告訴你 , 事實上 , 我們的政府垂直架構 , 建構在工業革命的經濟模式縱向層級制度 , 專門處理工作任務 , 指令結構已經完全錯了 。
you in business know that the paradigm structure of our time , ladies and gentlemen , is the network .	在商界 , 你們都知道我們這個時代的典範結構 , 各位先生女士 , 就是這個網路 。
it's your capacity to network that matters , both within your governments and externally .	重要的是你有能力網絡 , 無論在你的政府內部或外部 。
so here is ashdown's third law .	這是第三個法則 。
by the way , don't ask me about ashdown's first law and second law because i haven't invented those yet ; it always sounds better if there's a third law , doesn't it ?	對了 , 別問我第一法則和第二法則因為我還沒發明這些法則 , 如果第三法則總是比較好聽 , 不是嗎 ?
ashdown's third law is that in the modern age , where everything is connected to everything , the most important thing about what you can do is what you can do with others .	ashdown的第三定律是 , 在現代 , 每件事都與一切有關連 , 最重要的是你能做什麼 , 就是你能和他人做什麼 。
the most important bit about your structure whether you're a government , whether you're an army regiment , whether you're a business is your docking points , your interconnectors , your capacity to network with others .	關於你自己的結構 , 無論你是政府 , 還是軍隊的機構 , 無論你是商人 , 代表你與他人的交集 , 你的交集 , 你與他人交流的能力 。
you understand that in industry ; governments don't .	你了解在工業上 ; 政府不會 。
but now one final thing .	但現在最後一件事
if it is the case , ladies and gentlemen and it is that we are now locked together in a way that has never been quite the same before , then it's also the case that we share a destiny with each other .	如果是的話 , 各位先生女士--我們現在被鎖在一起 , 以前所未有的方式鎖定著--那麼 , 事實就是我們彼此有著命運 。
suddenly and for the very first time , collective defense , the thing that has dominated us as the concept of securing our nations , is no longer enough .	忽然間 , 這是頭一次 , 集體的防禦 , 那些主導我們這個 「 保障我們國家 」 的概念已經不夠了 。
it used to be the case that if my tribe was more powerful than their tribe , i was safe ; if my country was more powerful than their country , i was safe ; my alliance , like nato , was more powerful than their alliance , i was safe .	過去就是這樣 , 如果我的部落比他們的部落更強大 , 我就安全了 ; 如果我的國家比他們的國家更強大 , 我就安全了 ; 我的盟國 , 像北約 , 比他們的同盟還強大 , 我就安全了 。
it is no longer the case .	不再是如此了 。
the advent of the interconnectedness and of the weapons of mass destruction means that , increasingly , i share a destiny with my enemy .	大規模毀滅性武器的相互關聯性進步意謂著 , 逐漸地 , 我和我的敵人分享了一個命運 。
when i was a diplomat negotiating the disarmament treaties with the soviet union in geneva in the 1970s , we succeeded because we understood we shared a destiny with them .	當我還是外交官的時候 , 在1970年代日內瓦與蘇聯外交官的協商 , 我們成功是因為我們了解我們和他們有著共同的命運 。
collective security is not enough .	集體的安全是不夠的 。
peace has come to northern ireland because both sides realized that the zerosum game couldn't work .	和平也來到北愛爾蘭 , 因為雙方了解 , 零和遊戲是行不通的 。
they shared a destiny with their enemies .	他們與敵人有著共同的命運
one of the great barriers to peace in the middle east is that both sides , both israel and , i think , the palestinians , do not understand that they share a collective destiny .	阻礙著中東和平的其中一個要素就是 , 以色列和巴勒斯坦人 , 不了解他們有共同的命運 。
and so suddenly , ladies and gentlemen , what has been the proposition of visionaries and poets down the ages becomes something we have to take seriously as a matter of public policy .	所以 , 各位先生女士 , 對於有遠見的、詩人的提議 , 各個年齡層都成了我們必須認真看待的公共政策 。
i started with a poem , i'll end with one .	我以一首詩作為開場 , 將以一首
the great poem of john donne's .	約翰•多恩的偉大詩作
" send not for whom the bell tolls . "	「 不要讓鈴聲響到哪裡去 。 」
the poem is called " no man is an island . "	這首詩叫做 " 沒有人是孤島 "
and it goes: " every man's death affected me , for i am involved in mankind , send not to ask for whom the bell tolls , it tolls for thee . "	上面寫著: 「 每個人的死亡都影響著我 , 因為我是涉入人類 , 不是去問鐘聲是誰響的 , 是為誰響的 。 」
for john donne , a recommendation of morality .	對約翰•多恩來說 , 一個道德建議
for us , i think , part of the equation for our survival .	對我們來說 , 我認為 , 對於我們生存的方程式的一部分
to find the path to long life and health , dan buettner and team study the world's " blue zones , " communities whose elders live with vim and vigor to recordsetting age . at tedxtc , he shares the 9 common diet and lifestyle habits that keep them spry past age 100 .	為了找到長久生活和健康的道路 , 丹.buettner和團隊研究世界的 " 藍寶區 " , 這些社區的長者與vim同住並具有紀錄年齡的族群 。 在tedxtc , 他共享九種常見的飲食和生活習慣 , 這些習慣使得他們在一百歲以後才得以繁衍 。
biology , culture , exploration , food , health , life , science	生物、文化、探索、食物、生命、科學、
dan buettner: how to live to be 100+	danbuetner:如何活到100+100+100 ?
something called the danish twin study established that only about 10 percent of how long the average person lives , within certain biological limits , is dictated by our genes .	丹麥雙胞胎的研究指出 , 一般人平均壽命只有百分之十的時間限制在特定的生物限制下 , 基因決定了我們的壽命
the other 90 percent is dictated by our lifestyle .	其他90%則被生活方式支配了 。
so the premise of blue zones: if we can find the optimal lifestyle of longevity we can come up with a de facto formula for longevity .	所以藍寶地的前提是:如果我們能找到長壽的最佳生活方式我們就能得出一個實際的長壽方程式
but if you ask the average american what the optimal formula of longevity is , they probably couldn't tell you .	但如果你問一般美國人平均壽命最佳的公式是什麼 , 他們大概不會告訴你的 。
they've probably heard of the south beach diet , or the atkins diet .	他們可能聽說過南灘減肥法 , 或是阿特金減肥法 。
you have the usda food pyramid .	你有美國食物金字塔 。
there is what oprah tells us .	歐普拉告訴我們的是
there is what doctor oz tells us .	奧茲醫生告訴我們
the fact of the matter is there is a lot of confusion around what really helps us live longer better .	事實是 , 對於什麼真正能幫助我們活得更好 , 有很大的困惑 。
should you be running marathons or doing yoga ?	你應該跑馬拉松還是做瑜珈 ?
should you eat organic meats or should you be eating tofu ?	應該吃有機肉還是豆腐 ?
when it comes to supplements , should you be taking them ?	當提到營養品時 , 你該吃嗎 ?
how about these hormones or resveratrol ?	荷爾蒙或白斑呢 ?
and does purpose play into it ?	目的也能發揮作用嗎 ?
spirituality ? and how about how we socialize ?	靈性呢 ? 我們的社交方式如何 ?
well , our approach to finding longevity was to team up with national geographic , and the national institute on aging , to find the four demographically confirmed areas that are geographically defined .	嗯 , 我們找到長壽的方法是和國家地理還有國家老化研究院合作找出四個人口確定地理界限的地區
and then bring a team of experts in there to methodically go through exactly what these people do , to distill down the crosscultural distillation .	接著 , 把一群專家團隊帶到那裡 , 用方法來處理這些人的所做所為 , 來提煉出跨文化的精華 。
and at the end of this i'm going to tell you what that distillation is .	最後我要告訴你們精華是什麼 。
but first i'd like to debunk some common myths when it comes to longevity .	但首先我想打破一些常見的迷思 , 談到長壽 。
and the first myth is if you try really hard you can live to be 100 .	第一個迷思是如果你非常努力去活到一百歲
the problem is , only about one out of 5 , 000 people in america live to be 100 .	問題是 , 美國只有五千分之一的人能活到一百歲 。
your chances are very low .	你的機會非常低 。
even though it's the fastest growing demographic in america , it's hard to reach 100 .	即使它是美國人口成長最快的地區 , 也很難達到一百歲 。
the problem is that we're not programmed for longevity .	問題是我們並不是為了長壽才設計出來的
we are programmed for something called procreative success .	我們被設計為一種叫做 " 繁殖成功 " 的產品 。
i love that word .	我很愛這個字 。
it reminds me of my college days .	這讓我想起大學生活 。
biologists term procreative success to mean the age where you have children and then another generation , the age when your children have children .	生物學家把繁衍的成功定義在你有了孩子的年齡然後另一個世代 , 當你的孩子有了孩子時的年齡
after that the effect of evolution completely dissipates .	在那之後 , 演化的效應就完全消失了 。
if you're a mammal , if you're a rat or an elephant , or a human , in between , it's the same story .	如果你是哺乳類 , 如果你是老鼠或是大象 , 或人類 , 在兩者之間 , 這都是同樣的故事 。
so to make it to age 100 , you not only have to have had a very good lifestyle , you also have to have won the genetic lottery .	所以 , 要讓它活到一百歲 , 你不只得有個很好的生活方式 , 你還得拿到基因彩票 。
the second myth is , there are treatments that can help slow , reverse , or even stop aging .	第二個迷思是 , 有療程可以幫助緩慢、反轉 , 或甚至停止老化 。
when you think of it , there is 99 things that can age us .	當你想一想 , 有99件事可以讓我們老化 。
deprive your brain of oxygen for just a few minutes , those brain cells die , they never come back .	只要短短幾分鐘 , 你的腦部缺氧 , 那些腦細胞就會死 , 從不復返 。
play tennis too hard , on your knees , ruin your cartilage , the cartilage never comes back .	打網球太用力 , 在膝蓋上 , 毀了軟骨 , 軟骨就沒回來 。
our arteries can clog . our brains can gunk up with plaque , and we can get alzheimer's .	我們的動脈會堵塞 。 我們的大腦可以用斑塊噴射 , 我們就可以得到阿茲海默症 。
there is just too many things to go wrong .	有太多事情會出錯了 。
our bodies have 35 trillion cells , trillion with a " t . " we're talking national debt numbers here .	我們的身體有35兆個細胞 , 用的是t的數量 , 我們現在在說的是國債 。
those cells turn themselves over once every eight years .	那些細胞每八年就會自轉一次 。
and every time they turn themselves over there is some damage . and that damage builds up .	每當它們自己轉身 , 就會產生一些損害 , 造成損害 。
and it builds up exponentially .	並且以指數增加的速度增長 。
it's a little bit like the days when we all had beatles albums or eagles albums and we'd make a copy of that on a cassette tape , and let our friends copy that cassette tape , and pretty soon , with successive generations that tape sounds like garbage .	有點像以前我們都有披頭四或老鷹專輯 , 我們會在錄音帶上複製 , 讓朋友複製那錄音帶 , 很快就有了成功的世代 , 錄音帶就聽起來像垃圾一樣 。
well , the same things happen to our cells .	同樣的事情也發生在我們的細胞上 。
that's why a 65yearold person is aging at a rate of about 125 times faster than a 12yearold person .	這就是為什麼一個65歲的人老化的速度 , 比一個12歲的人快125倍 。
so , if there is nothing you can do to slow your aging or stop your aging , what am i doing here ?	所以 , 如果你沒辦法減緩老化或停止老化 , 我在這裡幹嘛 ?
well , the fact of the matter is the best science tells us that the capacity of the human body , my body , your body , is about 90 years , a little bit more for women .	嗯 , 事情的真相是最好的科學告訴我們 , 人體的能力 , 我的身體 , 你的身體 , 大約有90年 , 再為女人多做一點 。
but life expectancy in this country is only 78 .	但這個國家的預期壽命只有78歲
so somewhere along the line , we're leaving about 12 good years on the table .	所以在某個時點 , 我們正要離開大約十二年的好時光 。
these are years that we could get .	這些年可以讓我們
and research shows that they would be years largely free of chronic disease , heart disease , cancer and diabetes .	研究顯示 , 牠們大多能免於慢性病、心臟病、癌症和糖尿病 。
we think the best way to get these missing years is to look at the cultures around the world that are actually experiencing them , areas where people are living to age 100 at rates up to 10 times greater than we are , areas where the life expectancy is an extra dozen years , the rate of middle age mortality is a fraction of what it is in this country .	我們認為 , 要讓這些消失的年齡 , 最好的方式就是看看世界各地的文化實際體驗 , 人們活到一百歲以上比我們多出十倍的地方 , 平均壽命多了十幾年 , 中年死亡率是這個國家的一小部分 。
we found our first blue zone about 125 miles off the coast of italy , on the island of sardinia .	我們發現我們的第一個藍寶地是在義大利海岸外約125英哩處 , 薩丁尼亞島上
and not the entire island , the island is about 1 . 4 million people , but only up in the highlands , an area called the nuoro province .	不是整座島 , 整座島約有一百四十萬人 , 但只在高地上 , 一個叫做努奧羅省的地區 。
and here we have this area where men live the longest , about 10 times more centenarians than we have here in america .	這裡是男人最長壽的地區 , 大約比美國人口百歲人瑞的數目多出十倍 。
and this is a place where people not only reach age 100 , they do so with extraordinary vigor .	這個地方的人們不僅活到一百歲 , 他們還帶著特別的活力 。
places where 102 year olds still ride their bike to work , chop wood , and can beat a guy 60 years younger than them .	一百零二歲的孩子仍然騎自行車上班 , 砍柴 , 還能打敗比他們年輕六十年的男人 。
their history actually goes back to about the time of christ .	他們的歷史實際上可以追溯到大約基督的時代 。
it's actually a bronze age culture that's been isolated .	其實是孤立無援的青銅器時代文化
because the land is so infertile , they largely are shepherds , which occasions regular , lowintensity physical activity .	因為土地非常貧瘠 , 大多是牧羊人 , 常規的、低強度的物理活動 。
their diet is mostly plantbased , accentuated with foods that they can carry into the fields .	牠們的飲食主要以植物為主 , 以牠們可攜帶的食物為中心 。
they came up with an unleavened whole wheat bread called carta musica made out of durum wheat , a type of cheese made from grassfed animals so the cheese is high in omega3 fatty acids instead of omega6 fatty acids from cornfed animals , and a type of wine that has three times the level of polyphenols than any known wine in the world .	他們想出一種未發酵的全麥麵包叫做 " 卡達麥香 " 用小麥製作的一種乳酪這種乳酪是由草原生的動物所製成的這種乳酪富含omega-3脂肪酸而非omega-6脂肪酸來自於玉米類動物種類還有一種葡萄酒含量比世上任何已知的酒都多三倍
but the real secret i think lies more in the way that they organize their society .	但我認為真正的秘密是他們組織社會的方式 。
and one of the most salient elements of the sardinian society is how they treat older people .	薩丁尼亞社會最突出的元素之一就是他們對待老年人的方式
you ever notice here in america , social equity seems to peak at about age 24 ?	你有沒有注意到 , 在美國 , 社會平等似乎在24歲達到高峰 ?
just look at the advertisements .	只要看看那些廣告 ,
here in sardinia , the older you get the more equity you have , the more wisdom you're celebrated for .	在薩丁尼亞這裡 , 你越是平等 , 你就越是被讚頌的智慧 。
you go into the bars in sardinia , instead of seeing the sports illustrated swimsuit calendar , you see the centenarian of the month calendar .	你走進薩丁尼亞的酒吧裡 , 而不是看到運動畫面描繪游泳裝日曆 , 而是看到百歲人瑞的月曆 。
this , as it turns out , is not only good for your aging parents to keep them close to the family it imparts about four to six years of extra life expectancy research shows it's also good for the children of those families , who have lower rates of mortality and lower rates of disease .	結果發現 , 這不只適用於你老化的父母親讓他們跟家人親近還能增加大約四到六年的預期壽命研究顯示這對那些家庭的孩子也是好的 , 他們的死亡率和患病率較低 , 還有患病的比率較低 。
that's called the grandmother effect .	也就是所謂的奶奶效應 。
we found our second blue zone on the other side of the planet , about 800 miles south of tokyo , on the archipelago of okinawa .	我們發現行星另一端的第二個藍寶地 , 位於東京南方八百英里處 , 就在琉球的阿基拉戈 。
okinawa is actually 161 small islands .	琉球實際上有161個小島
and in the northern part of the main island , this is ground zero for world longevity .	而在主島的北端 , 這是世界長壽的起點 。
this is a place where the oldest living female population is found .	這個地方是當地最古老的女性被發現的地方 。
it's a place where people have the longest disabilityfree life expectancy in the world .	這個地方是人們擁有世界上最長壽的預期壽命
they have what we want .	他們有我們要的 。
they live a long time , and tend to die in their sleep , very quickly , and often , i can tell you , after sex .	他們活得很久 , 往往會在睡眠時死得很快 , 通常 , 我可以告訴你 , 在性交之後 ,
they live about seven good years longer than the average american .	他們比一般美國人多快活七年 。
five times as many centenarians as we have in america .	美國百歲人瑞的五倍之多
one fifth the rate of colon and breast cancer , big killers here in america .	大腸癌和乳癌的比率是五分之一 , 在美國是大型的殺手 。
and one sixth the rate of cardiovascular disease .	心血管疾病的比率是第六名 。
and the fact that this culture has yielded these numbers suggests strongly they have something to teach us .	這種文化能產生這些數字的事實 , 強烈表示他們有教導我們的道理 。
what do they do ?	他們會怎麼做 ?
once again , a plantbased diet , full of vegetables with lots of color in them .	再一次 , 以植物為主的飲食 , 充滿著多種顏色的蔬菜 。
and they eat about eight times as much tofu as americans do .	而且他們吃大約八倍多的豆腐比起美國人來說
more significant than what they eat is how they eat it .	比起他們吃什麼更重要的是他們吃的方式 。
they have all kinds of little strategies to keep from overeating , which , as you know , is a big problem here in america .	他們有各種小策略來避免過食 , 如你所知 , 在美國這是個大問題 。
a few of the strategies we observed: they eat off of smaller plates , so they tend to eat fewer calories at every sitting .	我們觀察到的一些策略:他們吃的盤子比較小 , 所以他們每次吃的卡路里就比較少 。
instead of serving family style , where you can sort of mindlessly eat as you're talking , they serve at the counter , put the food away , and then bring it to the table .	與其以家庭風格為出發點 , 你可以隨心所欲的吃點東西 , 他們會在櫃台服務 , 把食物拿走 , 然後再把食物帶到桌上 。
they also have a 3 , 000yearold adage , which i think is the greatest sort of diet suggestion ever invented .	他們還有一部三千年的格言 , 我認為是最棒的飲食建議 。
it was invented by confucius .	由fucius發明的 。
and that diet is known as the hara , hatchi , bu diet .	那個飲食就是大家所知的哈拉、哈蒂、布丁 ,
it's simply a little saying these people say before their meal to remind them to stop eating when their stomach is [80] percent full .	只是一個小小的說 , 這些人在用餐前說 , 提醒他們要吃的時候 , 80%滿時要吃的 。
it takes about a half hour for that full feeling to travel from your belly to your brain .	那完整的感覺要花半小時才能從你的肚子傳到你的大腦 。
and by remembering to stop at 80 percent it helps keep you from doing that very thing .	藉由記住去阻止百分之八十的發生 , 它能幫助你不去做那件事情 。
but , like sardinia , okinawa has a few social constructs that we can associate with longevity .	但 , 像薩丁尼亞 , 琉球有一些社會結構 , 可以讓我們長壽的社會結構連結在一起 。
we know that isolation kills .	我們知道孤立會扼殺
fifteen years ago , the average american had three good friends .	十五年前 , 美國平均有三個好朋友 。
we're down to one and half right now .	我們現在已經下降到一半了 。
if you were lucky enough to be born in okinawa , you were born into a system where you automatically have a half a dozen friends with whom you travel through life .	如果你幸運生在琉球你生在一個系統自動擁有半打朋友與你共渡生命的旅程
they call it a moai . and if you're in a moai you're expected to share the bounty if you encounter luck , and if things go bad , child gets sick , parent dies , you always have somebody who has your back .	他們稱之為moai 。 如果你正處於一個你預期會分享好運的moai身上 , 如果你碰到好運 , 而如果事情不好 , 孩子生病 , 父母去世 , 你總是有人背負你 。
this particular moai , these five ladies have been together for 97 years .	這位特別的莫艾 , 這五位女士已經在一起九十七年了 。
their average age is 102 .	他們的平均年齡是102歲 。
typically in america we've divided our adult life up into two sections .	通常在美國我們把成人生活分成兩部分
there is our work life , where we're productive .	工作就是我們有生產力的地方 。
and then one day , boom , we retire .	然後有一天 , 砰 , 我們退休了 。
and typically that has meant retiring to the easy chair , or going down to arizona to play golf .	通常這表示退休後要擺好椅子 , 或去亞利桑那州打高爾夫球 。
in the okinawan language there is not even a word for retirement .	在琉球語裡甚至沒有退休這個詞
instead there is one word that imbues your entire life , and that word is " ikigai . "	取而代之的是一個詞彙充斥著你整個人生 , 這個詞就是 「 ikigai 」 。
and , roughly translated , it means " the reason for which you wake up in the morning . "	大約翻譯過來 , 意思是 「 早上起床的理由 」 。
for this 102yearold karate master , his ikigai was carrying forth this martial art .	對這位一百零二歲的空手道大師他的生存價值就是這位武術
for this hundredyearold fisherman it was continuing to catch fish for his family three times a week .	對這一百歲的漁夫來說 , 一週要捕三次魚 。
and this is a question . the national institute on aging actually gave us a questionnaire to give these centenarians .	這是個問題 , 國家老化研究院給我們一個百歲人瑞的問卷 ,
and one of the questions , they were very culturally astute , the people who put the questionnaire .	其中一個問題 , 他們在文化上非常敏銳 , 就是那些問卷調查員 。
one of the questions was , " what is your ikigai ? "	其中一個問題是: 「 你的生存價值是什麼 ? 」
they instantly knew why they woke up in the morning .	他們馬上就知道為何早上起床
for this 102 year old woman , her ikigai was simply her greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	對這位一百零二歲的老婦人來說 , 她的生智只是她的曾曾曾曾曾孫女 。
two girls separated in age by 101 and a half years .	兩個女孩在101歲半前分開 。
and i asked her what it felt like to hold a greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	我問她 , 抱著一個曾曾曾孫女的感覺是什麼樣子 。
and she put her head back and she said , " it feels like leaping into heaven . "	她回頭說: 「 感覺就像飛躍上天堂 。 」
i thought that was a wonderful thought .	我以為那是很棒的一個想法 。
my editor at geographic wanted me to find america's blue zone .	我在地理的編輯要我去找美國的藍寶地 。
and for a while we looked on the prairies of minnesota , where actually there is a very high proportion of centenarians .	有一陣子我們看的是明尼蘇達的草原這裡的百歲人瑞比例非常高
but that's because all the young people left .	但那是因為所有的年輕人都離開了 。
so , we turned to the data again .	所以 , 我們又轉向資料
and we found america's longestlived population among the seventhday adventists concentrated in and around loma linda , california .	我們發現 , 美國最長壽的居民是加州的第七天 , 加州的洛瑪林達市 。
adventists are conservative methodists .	冒險家是保守派的方法論者
they celebrate their sabbath from sunset on friday till sunset on saturday .	他們把安息日從日落到星期六日出為止 。
a " 24hour sanctuary in time , " they call it .	他們稱之為 「 二十四小時的避難所 」 。
and they follow five little habits that conveys to them extraordinary longevity , comparatively speaking .	他們遵循五個小習慣 , 相對來說他們能傳達出非凡的長壽習慣 。
in america here , life expectancy for the average woman is 80 .	在美國這裡 , 女性平均壽命是80歲 。
but for an adventist woman , their life expectancy is 89 .	但對一個冒險家的女性來說 , 她們的預期壽命是89歲 。
and the difference is even more pronounced among men , who are expected to live about 11 years longer than their american counterparts .	男性之間的差異更明顯他們預期能多活十一年比起美國同伴來說
now , this is a study that followed about 70 , 000 people for 30 years .	這個研究追蹤了大約七萬人三十年 。
sterling study . and i think it supremely illustrates the premise of this blue zone project .	很驚人的研究 。 而且我認為 , 它成功地說明了這個藍寶地計畫的前提 。
this is a heterogeneous community .	這是一個異性戀的社區 。
it's white , black , hispanic , asian .	是白人、黑人、西班牙裔、亞洲人
the only thing that they have in common are a set of very small lifestyle habits that they follow ritualistically for most of their lives .	他們唯一的共通點是一套非常小的生活習慣他們一生中大部份的時間都跟著做 。
they take their diet directly from the bible .	他們直接取自聖經中的飲食 。
genesis: chapter one , verse [29] , where god talks about legumes and seeds , and on one more stanza about green plants , ostensibly missing is meat .	創世紀的第一章 , 第29篇 , 上帝談到豆腐和種子 , 還有另一篇則是有關綠色植物 , 很明顯少了肉 。
they take this sanctuary in time very serious .	他們非常認真地看待這個保護區 。
for 24 hours every week , no matter how busy they are , how stressed out they are at work , where the kids need to be driven , they stop everything and they focus on their god , their social network , and then , hardwired right in the religion , are nature walks .	每週24小時 , 不管他們有多忙碌 , 他們工作的壓力多大 , 孩子需要被驅逐 , 他們會停下一切 , 專注在他們的上帝、他們的社交網路 , 接著 , 宗教中的硬體 , 就是走路 。
and the power of this is not that it's done occasionally , the power is it's done every week for a lifetime .	而它的力量並不是它偶爾可以做 , 它的力量是每週都要做一輩子 。
none of it's hard . none of it costs money .	一點都不困難 。 一點都不花錢 。
adventists also tend to hang out with other adventists .	冒險家也傾向跟其他的冒險家見面 。
so , if you go to an adventist's party you don't see people swilling jim beam or rolling a joint .	所以 , 如果你去參加一個冒險家的派對 , 你不會看到有人在揮動jimbeam或打滾一個聯合體 。
instead they're talking about their next nature walk , exchanging recipes , and yes , they pray .	反之 , 他們在談的是他們的下一個自然步行、交換食譜 , 以及 , 是的 , 他們會祈禱 。
but they influence each other in profound and measurable ways .	但它們以深刻、可測量的方式互相影響著彼此 。
this is a culture that has yielded ellsworth whareham .	這個文化造就了埃爾斯沃•偉倫這樣的人 。
ellsworth whareham is 97 years old .	埃爾斯沃•偉倫九十七歲
he's a multimillionaire , yet when a contractor wanted 6 , 000 dollars to build a privacy fence , he said , " for that kind of money i'll do it myself . "	他是一個千萬富翁 , 但當承包商要六千美元來建造一個隱私的圍籬時 , 他說: 「 為了這類的錢 , 我會自己來幹嘛 。 」
so for the next three days he was out shoveling cement , and hauling poles around .	所以接下來的三天他都在外頭鏟水泥把杆子拖到附近
and predictably , perhaps , on the fourth day he ended up in the operating room .	可以預料的是 , 也許第四天他會在手術室裡 。
but not as the guy on the table ; the guy doing openheart surgery .	但不是手術台上那個人而是做開心手術的人
at 97 he still does 20 openheart surgeries every month .	九十七歲的他每個月仍然動二十次開心手術 。
ed rawlings , 103 years old now , an active cowboy , starts his morning with a swim .	艾德•羅林斯 , 現在一百三歲 , 是個活躍的牛仔 , 早上就開始游泳 。
and on weekends he likes to put on the boards , throw up rooster tails .	在他喜歡踏上衝浪板的週末 , 丟棄腐爛的尾巴 。
her grandson actually lives in the twin cities here .	她的孫子 , 其實就住在雙胞胎城市裡 。
she starts her day with lifting weights .	她每天由舉重開始
she rides her bicycle .	她騎腳踏車
and then she gets in her rootbeer colored 1994 cadillac seville , and tears down the san bernardino freeway , where she still volunteers for seven different organizations .	接著 , 她在1994年根部塞維利亞凱迪拉克的高速公路上流下了聖貝納迪諾高速公路 , 在那裡 , 她仍是七個不同組織的志工 。
i've been on 19 hardcore expeditions .	我曾在十九次的探險活動上
i'm probably the only person you'll ever meet who rode his bicycle across the sahara desert without sunscreen .	我大概是唯一一個你會遇到的 , 他騎腳踏車穿越撒哈拉沙漠沒有防曬油 。
but i'll tell you , there is no adventure more harrowing than riding shotgun with marge deton .	但是我要告訴你 , 沒有任何探險比搭馬爾德頓騎車還更加恐怖的了 。
" a stranger is a friend i haven't met yet ! " she'd say to me .	「 陌生人是我還沒見面的朋友 ! 」 她會對我說:
so , what are the common denominators in these three cultures ?	那麼 , 這三個文化裡有什麼共同點呢 ?
what are the things that they all do ?	他們都做了什麼事 ?
and we managed to boil it down to nine .	我們成功的將它歸結為九重 。
in fact we've done two more blue zone expeditions since this and these common denominators hold true .	事實上 , 我們從這之後又做了兩次藍寶地考察 , 以及這些常見的調查是對的 。
and the first one , and i'm about to utter a heresy here , none of them exercise , at least the way we think of exercise .	第一項 , 我即將要提出一項離譜 , 沒有一項運動 , 至少是我們所認為的運動方式 。
instead , they set up their lives so that they are constantly nudged into physical activity .	取而代之的是 , 他們安排自己的生活 , 這樣他們才會持續推動身體活動 。
these 100yearold okinawan women are getting up and down off the ground , they sit on the floor , 30 or 40 times a day .	這些百歲的琉球女人每天都起床三十或四十次 。
sardinians live in vertical houses , up and down the stairs .	薩丁尼亞人住在垂直的房子裡 , 樓梯上上上下 ,
every trip to the store , or to church or to a friend's house occasions a walk .	每次去商店 , 或去教堂或去朋友家都要走路
they don't have any conveniences .	他們沒有任何方便 。
there is not a button to push to do yard work or house work .	沒有一個按鈕可以推動院子工作或房子工作 。
if they want to mix up a cake , they're doing it by hand .	如果他們要混蛋糕的話 , 他們是用手工做的 。
that burns calories just as much as going on the treadmill does .	跟跑步機一樣會燃燒卡路里 。
when they do do intentional physical activity , it's the things they enjoy . they tend to walk , the only proven way to stave off cognitive decline , and they all tend to have a garden .	當他們做有意的身體活動時 , 就是他們享受的東西 。 他們會走路 , 唯一證實能延遲認知能力下降的路上 , 他們都往往有個花園 。
they know how to set up their life in the right way so they have the right outlook .	他們知道如何以正確的方式安排自己的人生 , 讓他們有正確的人生觀 。
each of these cultures take time to downshift .	上述的每一種文化都需要時間慢慢往下移 。
the sardinians pray . the seventhday adventists pray .	薩丁尼亞人祈禱 。 第七天的教徒祈禱 。
the okinawans have this ancestor veneration .	琉球人有這種祖先的表情
but when you're in a hurry or stressed out , that triggers something called the inflammatory response , which is associated with everything from alzheimer's disease to cardiovascular disease .	但當你急著或緊張時 , 會引發一種稱為 「 發炎反應 」 的反應 , 這和所有一切都息相關 , 從阿茲海默症到心血管疾病 。
when you slow down for 15 minutes a day you turn that inflammatory state into a more antiinflammatory state .	當你一天放慢個十五分鐘 , 你就會把那發炎狀態轉變成更加抗炎的狀態 。
they have vocabulary for sense of purpose , ikigai , like the okinawans .	它們的詞彙很有目的性 , 很像琉球人的 「 生殖器 」 。
you know the two most dangerous years in your life are the year you're born , because of infant mortality , and the year you retire .	你知道自己生命中最危險的兩年是出生那年 , 因為嬰兒死亡率 , 以及退休那年 。
these people know their sense of purpose , and they activate in their life , that's worth about seven years of extra life expectancy .	這些人知道他們的目的感 , 也啟動了他們的生活 , 這大約是七年多的預期壽命 。
there's no longevity diet .	沒有長壽的飲食
instead , these people drink a little bit every day , not a hard sell to the american population .	相反的 , 這些人每天喝的有點小 , 不難賣給美國人口 。
they tend to eat a plantbased diet .	他們往往以植物為主的飲食
doesn't mean they don't eat meat , but lots of beans and nuts .	不是說他們不吃肉 , 而是吃很多豆類和堅果 。
and they have strategies to keep from overeating , little things that nudge them away from the table at the right time .	他們有策略 , 避免過量 , 一些小事在適當的時間將他們推離餐桌 。
and then the foundation of all this is how they connect .	然後這一切的基礎是他們如何聯繫 。
they put their families first , take care of their children and their aging parents .	他們把家人擺第一 , 照顧孩子及其年邁的父母 。
they all tend to belong to a faithbased community , which is worth between four and 14 extra years of life expectancy if you do it four times a month .	他們全都屬於一個以信仰為基礎的族群 , 這個族群價值四到十四年的壽命 , 如果你一個月做四次的話 。
and the biggest thing here is they also belong to the right tribe .	這裡最大的是 , 牠們也屬於對的部落.
they were either born into or they proactively surrounded themselves with the right people .	他們不是生來就有生來就是他們主動把自己和對的人聚在一起
we know from the framingham studies , that if your three best friends are obese there is a 50 percent better chance that you'll be overweight .	我們從佛明罕研究中得知 , 如果你三個最好的朋友都胖你有50%的機率會過重 。
so , if you hang out with unhealthy people , that's going to have a measurable impact over time .	所以 , 如果你跟不健康的人交談 , 隨時間過去 , 這將會有明顯的影響 。
instead , if your friend's idea of recreation is physical activity , bowling , or playing hockey , biking or gardening , if your friends drink a little , but not too much , and they eat right , and they're engaged , and they're trusting and trustworthy , that is going to have the biggest impact over time .	相反的 , 如果你朋友的休閒活動是體力活動 , 保齡球或打曲棍球、自行車或園藝如果你的朋友喝了點小酒 , 但不過量他們吃得恰當 , 他們投入的同時信賴和值得信賴這會隨時間產生最大的影響
diets don't work . no diet in the history of the world has ever worked for more than two percent of the population .	飲食是行不通的 。 世界歷史上沒有任何飲食可用於超過百分之二的人口 。
exercise programs usually start in january ; they're usually done by october .	運動計劃通常一月就開始了 ; 通常是十月份就完成的 。
when it comes to longevity there is no short term fix in a pill or anything else .	談到長壽 , 沒有短期的補救措施 , 只要是藥物或其他東西 。
but when you think about it , your friends are longterm adventures , and therefore , perhaps the most significant thing you can do to add more years to your life , and life to your years . thank you very much .	但當你仔細想想 , 你的朋友是長期的冒險 , 因此 , 也許你能做的最重要事項 , 能多增加年的壽命 , 及年復一年的壽命 。 非常感謝 。
ink that conducts electricity ; a window that turns from clear to opaque at the flip of a switch ; a jelly that makes music . all this stuff exists , and catarina mota says: it's time to play with it . mota leads us on a tour of surprising and cool new materials , and suggests that the way we'll figure out what they're good for is to experiment , tinker and have fun .	墨水導引電流 ; 一扇從清楚轉向不透明的窗戶 ; 一個轉換開關的果凍 , 一個製造音樂的果凍 。 所有這些東西都存在 , 而卡塔琳娜•莫塔說:是時候到了 。 莫塔會帶領我們一同參與驚喜和酷炫的新材料之旅 , 並暗示我們將弄清楚它們的好處 , 將來做實驗 , 錫克和帶給我們歡樂 。
creativity , design , technology	創意、設計、科技、
catarina mota: play with smart materials	catarinamota:用智慧型材料玩樂
i have a friend in portugal whose grandfather built a vehicle out of a bicycle and a washing machine so he could transport his family .	我在葡萄牙有位朋友他的祖父用腳踏車和洗衣機建造一台飛天車讓他能夠運輸家人
he did it because he couldn't afford a car , but also because he knew how to build one .	他這麼做是因為他負擔不起汽車 , 但也因為他知道如何建造一個
there was a time when we understood how things worked and how they were made , so we could build and repair them , or at the very least make informed decisions about what to buy .	曾有一段時間 , 我們了解事物如何運作 , 以及它們是如何被製造出來的 , 如此一來 , 我們就能建造和修復它們 , 或者 , 最少能夠得知關於購買什麼的資訊 。
many of these doityourself practices were lost in the second half of the 20th century .	這些自助手段很多都是在二十世紀後半時期失去的
but now , the maker community and the opensource model are bringing this kind of knowledge about how things work and what they're made of back into our lives , and i believe we need to take them to the next level , to the components things are made of .	但現在 , 自造者和開放原始碼的模式正將這種知識帶入我們的生活中而我相信我們需要將這些知識帶到下一個層級 , 到組成物的層次
for the most part , we still know what traditional materials like paper and textiles are made of and how they are produced .	大部分的時候 , 我們仍然知道紙和紡織品等傳統原料是由什麼製成的 , 以及如何生產出來的 。
