but now we have these amazing , futuristic composites plastics that change shape , paints that conduct electricity , pigments that change color , fabrics that light up .	但是現在我們有了這些令人驚嘆的未來複合材料--它會改變形狀 , 油漆會導電 , 會改變顏色的顏料 , 會發光的布等 。
let me show you some examples .	讓我給你們看一些例子 。
so conductive ink allows us to paint circuits instead of using the traditional printed circuit boards or wires .	所以導電油墨讓我們不需要用傳統印刷電路或電線 , 而是用傳統印刷電路或電線 。
in the case of this little example i'm holding , we used it to create a touch sensor that reacts to my skin by turning on this little light .	在我手上拿著的這個小例子中 , 我們用它來創造一個觸控感應器 , 藉由開啟這個小燈 , 來對我的皮膚產生反應 。
conductive ink has been used by artists , but recent developments indicate that we will soon be able to use it in laser printers and pens .	藝術家一直在用導電油墨 , 但近期的發展表示 , 我們很快就能將它用在雷射印表機和筆上面 。
and this is a sheet of acrylic infused with colorless lightdiffusing particles .	這塊丙烯酸纖維附滿了無色的散光粒子 。
what this means is that , while regular acrylic only diffuses light around the edges , this one illuminates across the entire surface when i turn on the lights around it .	這意味著 , 雖然普通的丙烯酸纖維只會在邊緣散光 , 這一片會在我開燈的時候整個表面散發光芒 。
two of the known applications for this material include interior design and multitouch systems .	這項材料有兩種已知的應用 , 包括室內設計和多點觸控系統 。
and thermochromic pigments change color at a given temperature .	熱色素則會在特定溫度下改變顏色 。
so i'm going to place this on a hot plate that is set to a temperature only slightly higher than ambient and you can see what happens .	所以 , 我把這個放在熱盤子上 , 它的溫度只比環境還要高一點點 , 你可以看到會發生什麼事 。
so one of the principle applications for this material is , amongst other things , in baby bottles , so it indicates when the contents are cool enough to drink .	所以 , 這項材料主要的應用是在嬰兒奶瓶中 , 它能顯示內容物是否涼了可以喝了 。
so these are just a few of what are commonly known as smart materials .	以上只是一些一般所知的智慧型材料 。
in a few years , they will be in many of the objects and technologies we use on a daily basis .	幾年內 , 它們會在我們日常生活中使用的許多物品和技術 。
we may not yet have the flying cars science fiction promised us , but we can have walls that change color depending on temperature , keyboards that roll up , and windows that become opaque at the flick of a switch .	我們可能還沒辦法擁有科幻小說中會出現的飛天汽車 , 但我們能用溫度改變顏色的牆壁 , 可以捲起來的鍵盤 , 能在開關上不透明的窗戶 。
so i'm a social scientist by training , so why am i here today talking about smart materials ?	我是一個社會科學家 , 藉由訓練 , 為什麼我今天來這裡講的是智慧型材料 ?
well first of all , because i am a maker .	首先 , 因為我是個製造者 。
i'm curious about how things work and how they are made , but also because i believe we should have a deeper understanding of the components that make up our world , and right now , we don't know enough about these hightech composites our future will be made of .	我很好奇事物如何運作 , 以及組成 。 但我相信 , 我們應該要對構成我們世界的組成部分有更深入的了解 , 而現在 , 我們對這些高科技的組合還不夠了解 , 我們的未來將如何構成 。
smart materials are hard to obtain in small quantities .	智慧型材料難以在少量下取得 。
there's barely any information available on how to use them , and very little is said about how they are produced .	如何使用它們幾乎沒有任何的資訊 , 幾乎沒有人知道它們是如何產生的 。
so for now , they exist mostly in this realm of trade secrets and patents only universities and corporations have access to .	所以 , 目前 , 它們大多都存在於貿易機密和專利領域中 , 只有大學和企業能夠取得專利 。
so a little over three years ago , kirsty boyle and i started a project we called open materials .	三年多前 , kirstybole和我開始一個我們稱之為 " 開放材料 " 的計劃
it's a website where we , and anyone else who wants to join us , share experiments , publish information , encourage others to contribute whenever they can , and aggregate resources such as research papers and tutorials by other makers like ourselves .	它是一個網站 , 我們 , 和任何任何想要加入我們的人 , 分享實驗 , 發表資訊 , 鼓勵他人隨時隨地有所貢獻 , 並收集資源 , 如研究論文和教學 , 由其他和自己一樣的製造者所收集 。
we would like it to become a large , collectively generated database of doityourself information on smart materials .	我們希望它成為一個龐大而豐富的集體生成資料庫 , 由智慧型材料下自行生成 。
but why should we care how smart materials work and what they are made of ?	但為什麼我們要關心智慧型材料的運作和組成呢 ?
first of all , because we can't shape what we don't understand , and what we don't understand and use ends up shaping us .	首先 , 因為我們無法塑造我們不了解的東西 , 最後我們不了解、使用的東西最終塑造了我們 。
the objects we use , the clothes we wear , the houses we live in , all have a profound impact on our behavior , health and quality of life .	我們用的物品 , 我們穿的衣服 , 我們居住的房子 , 都對我們的行為、健康和生活品質有著深遠的影響 。
so if we are to live in a world made of smart materials , we should know and understand them .	所以 , 如果我們要生活在由智慧型材料組成的世界 , 我們應該要知道且了解它們 。
secondly , and just as important , innovation has always been fueled by tinkerers .	第二點 , 同樣重要的是 , 創新總是靠著tinker發動的 。
so many times , amateurs , not experts , have been the inventors and improvers of things ranging from mountain bikes to semiconductors , personal computers , airplanes .	很多時候 , 業餘者 , 不是專家 , 是發明者和改進者 , 從登山腳踏車到半導體、個人電腦、飛機 。
the biggest challenge is that material science is complex and requires expensive equipment .	最大的挑戰是材料科學很複雜 , 需要昂貴的設備 。
but that's not always the case .	但並非總是如此 。
two scientists at university of illinois understood this when they published a paper on a simpler method for making conductive ink .	伊利諾州大學有兩名科學家便深入了解 , 當他們發表了一篇論文 , 用比較簡單的方法製作導電油墨 。
jordan bunker , who had had no experience with chemistry until then , read this paper and reproduced the experiment at his maker space using only offtheshelf substances and tools .	約旦•邦克沒有化學經驗 , 直到那時候 , 他讀了這篇論文 , 並在他的製造者空間中重現實驗 , 只用現成的物質和工具 。
he used a toaster oven , and he even made his own vortex mixer , based on a tutorial by another scientist/maker .	他用烤箱甚至製作了自己的渦流混合器 , 依據是另一位科學家的教學方式 。
jordan then published his results online , including all the things he had tried and didn't work , so others could study and reproduce it .	約旦後來在網路上公佈了他的成果 , 包括他曾經嘗試過和不成功的所有事情 , 所以其他人可以研究並複製它 。
so jordan's main form of innovation was to take an experiment created in a wellequipped lab at the university and recreate it in a garage in chicago using only cheap materials and tools he made himself .	所以 , 約旦的創新主要形式是把一個在上大學的有裝備的實驗室做出來的實驗 , 並在芝加哥的車庫裡重現 , 只用便宜的材料和工具 , 讓他自己完成 。
and now that he published this work , others can pick up where he left and devise even simpler processes and improvements .	現在 , 他發表了這項研究 , 其他人可以從他離開的地方 , 設計出更簡單的過程 , 並改善 。
another example i'd like to mention her project's goal is to highlight the expressive qualities of materials while focusing on the creativity and skills of the builder .	另一個我想提的例子是 , 她的專案計畫的目標是要強調材料的品質 , 同時要注重建設者的創造力和技能 。
electronics kits are very powerful in that they teach us how things work , but the constraints inherent in their design influence the way we learn .	電子設備非常強大 , 以便教導我們事物如何運作 , 但其設計的限制會影響我們學習的方式 。
so hannah's approach , on the other hand , is to formulate a series of techniques for creating unusual objects that free us from predesigned constraints by teaching us about the materials themselves .	所以漢娜的辦法 , 另一方面 , 是制定一系列的技術來創造不尋常的物品 , 能讓我們從設計限制中解放出來 , 教導我們自身的素材 。
so amongst hannah's many impressive experiments , this is one of my favorites .	在漢娜眾多令人印象深刻的實驗裡這是我最喜歡的一個
[ " paper speakers " ] what we're seeing here is just a piece of paper with some copper tape on it connected to an mp3 player and a magnet .	[紙喇叭]我們現在看到的只是一張紙上面貼了一些銅膠帶 , 連到mp3播放器和磁鐵上
so based on the research by marcelo coelho from mit , hannah created a series of paper speakers out of a wide range of materials from simple copper tape to conductive fabric and ink .	根據麻省理工學院的marcelocoelho的研究 , 漢娜用許多不同的材料製作出一系列的紙喇叭 , 從簡單的銅膠帶 , 到導電布及墨水 。
just like jordan and so many other makers , hannah published her recipes and allows anyone to copy and reproduce them .	就像喬登和許多其它的製造家漢娜將她的食譜出版 , 讓任何人都可以複製和繁殖 。
but paper electronics is one of the most promising branches of material science in that it allows us to create cheaper and flexible electronics .	但紙電子是材料科學中最被看好的分支之一 , 它讓我們能創造出更便宜且有彈性的電子 。
so hannah's artisanal work , and the fact that she shared her findings , opens the doors to a series of new possibilities that are both aesthetically appealing and innovative .	漢娜的手工藝成品 , 以及她分享了她的發現 , 為一系列新的可能性打開了一扇通往美感以及創新的通路 。
so the interesting thing about makers is that we create out of passion and curiosity , and we are not afraid to fail .	製造者有趣的地方在於我們創造出熱情和好奇心 , 而我們不怕失敗 。
we often tackle problems from unconventional angles , and , in the process , end up discovering alternatives or even better ways to do things .	我們通常從不因循守舊的角度來處理問題 , 過程中 , 最後發現了替代方案 , 甚至是更好的做事方式 。
so the more people experiment with materials , the more researchers are willing to share their research , and manufacturers their knowledge , the better chances we have to create technologies that truly serve us all .	所以 , 越多人在材料上做實驗 , 越多研究者願意分享他們的研究 , 並製造他們的知識 , 我們就越有機會創造出能為我們全體服務的科技 。
so i feel a bit as ted nelson must have when , in the early 1970s , he wrote , " you must understand computers now . "	我覺得有點像泰德.納爾遜在1970年代早期寫道: 「 你們現在一定要了解電腦 。 」
back then , computers were these large mainframes only scientists cared about , and no one dreamed of even having one at home .	那時 , 電腦是只有科學家在關心的大型電腦大型計算機 , 沒有人夢想過即使家中有一台這種電腦 。
so it's a little strange that i'm standing here and saying , " you must understand smart materials now . "	所以這有點奇怪 , 我站在這裡說: 「 你們現在必須要了解智慧型材料 。 」
just keep in mind that acquiring preemptive knowledge about emerging technologies is the best way to ensure that we have a say in the making of our future .	請記住 , 取得新興科技的先進知識是確保我們對於未來有發言權最好的方式 。
when we drive , we get into a glass bubble , lock the doors and press the accelerator , relying on our eyes to guide us even though we can only see the few cars ahead of and behind us . but what if cars could share data with each other about their position and velocity , and use predictive models to calculate the safest routes for everyone on the road ? jennifer healey imagines a world without accidents .	當我們開車時 , 我們會進入一個玻璃泡 , 鎖上房門 , 按下加速器 , 依靠雙眼即使我們只能看到少數幾輛車在我們身後 。 但如果汽車可以彼此分享資料 , 關於它們的位置和速度 , 並用可預知的模型來計算出最安全的路線 , 讓路上的人都走一趟 ? 珍妮佛•喜利想像一個沒有意外的世界 。
jennifer healey: if cars could talk , accidents might be avoidable	珍妮佛.喜利:如果車子能說話 , 意外可能是可避免的 。
let's face it: driving is dangerous .	面對現實吧開車是危險的
it's one of the things that we don't like to think about , but the fact that religious icons and good luck charms show up on dashboards around the world betrays the fact that we know this to be true .	這是我們不喜歡去思考的事情之一 , 但事實是 , 宗教偶像和好運的魅力出現在世界各地的儀表板上 , 被我們所知的事實背叛了 。
car accidents are the leading cause of death in people ages 16 to 19 in the united states leading cause of death and 75 percent of these accidents have nothing to do with drugs or alcohol .	車禍是美國16至19歲青年死亡的主因車禍是導致死亡的主因而當中75%與毒品或酒精無關
no one can say for sure , but i remember my first accident .	沒有人可以肯定的說 , 但我記得我的第一個意外 。
i was a young driver out on the highway , and the car in front of me , i saw the brake lights go on .	我當時還是個年輕的司機在高速公路上 , 前面的車子 , 我看到前面的煞車燈亮了 。
i'm like , " okay , all right , this guy is slowing down , i'll slow down too . "	我心想: 「 好吧 , 好吧 , 這傢伙慢了下來 , 我也會慢下來 。 」
i step on the brake .	我踩著剎車 。
but no , this guy isn't slowing down .	但不 , 這傢伙不是在放慢腳步 。
this guy is stopping , dead stop , dead stop on the highway .	這傢伙在高速公路上停車 , 停車 , 停車 。
it was just going 65 to zero ?	那時它才六十五歲 , 變成零 ?
i slammed on the brakes .	我踩著剎車 。
i felt the abs kick in , and the car is still going , and it's not going to stop , and i know it's not going to stop , and the air bag deploys , the car is totaled , and fortunately , no one was hurt .	我感覺到abs踢進去 , 車仍在前進 , 車子還沒停 , 我知道不會停下來 , 空氣袋就部署了 , 車子全開 , 幸運的是 , 沒有人受傷 。
but i had no idea that car was stopping , and i think we can do a lot better than that .	但我完全沒想到那輛車停了 , 我認為我們可以做得更好 。
i think we can transform the driving experience by letting our cars talk to each other .	我認為我們可以改造駕駛經驗 , 藉由讓車子彼此交談 ,
i just want you to think a little bit about what the experience of driving is like now .	我只想讓你們稍微想想現在開車的體驗是怎樣的 。
get into your car . close the door . you're in a glass bubble .	進入你的車 。 關上門 。 你在一個玻璃泡裡 。
you can't really directly sense the world around you .	你無法直接感受周圍的世界 。
you're in this extended body .	你就在這個延伸的身體裡
you're tasked with navigating it down partiallyseen roadways , in and amongst other metal giants , at superhuman speeds .	你的任務是將它導航 , 往下導航 , 沿著部分的道路 , 和其他的金屬巨人 , 以超人類的速度飛上軌道 。
okay ? and all you have to guide you are your two eyes .	好嗎 ? 你只需要引導你是你的兩個眼睛 。
okay , so that's all you have , eyes that weren't really designed for this task , but then people ask you to do things like , you want to make a lane change , what's the first thing they ask you do ?	好 , 這就是你們所有的眼睛 , 不是真的為這個任務而設計的眼睛 , 但人們請你做像這樣的事 , 你想要改變車道 , 他們要做的第一件事是什麼 ?
take your eyes off the road . that's right .	你的眼睛從路上脫下來 , 沒錯 。
stop looking where you're going , turn , check your blind spot , and drive down the road without looking where you're going .	不要看你要去哪裡 , 轉彎 , 檢查你的盲點 , 然後開車下馬路 , 不看你要去哪裡 。
you and everyone else . this is the safe way to drive .	在座各位和其他人 。 這是安全的駕駛方式 。
why do we do this ? because we have to , we have to make a choice , do i look here or do i look here ?	為什麼要這樣做 ? 因為我們必須做出選擇 , 我是要看這邊還是這邊 ?
and usually we do a fantastic job picking and choosing what we attend to on the road .	通常我們會做很棒的工作 , 選擇要走的路 。
but occasionally we miss something .	但偶爾我們也會漏掉一些
occasionally we sense something wrong or too late .	偶爾我們也會覺得有些不對勁或太晚了 。
in countless accidents , the driver says , " i didn't see it coming . "	在無數的意外中 , 駕駛說: 「 我沒看到它即將來臨 。 」
and i believe that . i believe that .	我相信這點 , 我相信這點 。
we can only watch so much .	我們只能眼睜睜看著
but the technology exists now that can help us improve that .	但是科技現在可以幫助我們改善這個狀況 。
in the future , with cars exchanging data with each other , we will be able to see not just three cars ahead and three cars behind , to the right and left , all at the same time , bird's eye view , we will actually be able to see into those cars .	未來 , 隨著汽車彼此交換資料 , 我們將能夠看到不只是三輛車在前面 , 三輛車在後面 , 右邊和左邊 , 全都在同一時間 , 鳥眼的視野之下 , 我們將能夠實際地看到在那些車裡面 。
we will be able to see the velocity of the car in front of us , to see how fast that guy's going or stopping .	我們可以看到前面車輛的速度 , 可以看出前面車輛的速度有多快或是停車位 。
if that guy's going down to zero , i'll know .	如果那人降到零 , 我就會知道 。
and with computation and algorithms and predictive models , we will be able to see the future .	加上運算、演算法和預測模型 , 我們將能夠預見未來 。
you may think that's impossible .	你們可能認為這不可能 。
how can you predict the future ? that's really hard .	你怎麼能預測未來 ? 那真的很難 。
actually , no . with cars , it's not impossible .	實際上 , 不是 。 對於汽車來說 , 這不是不可能的 。
cars are threedimensional objects that have a fixed position and velocity .	汽車是立體的物體有固定的位置和速度
they travel down roads .	他們沿著道路往下走
often they travel on prepublished routes .	通常他們在有預先發表的路線上行駛 。
it's really not that hard to make reasonable predictions about where a car's going to be in the near future .	要合理地預測車子在不遠的將來會去到哪裡 , 真的不難 。
even if , when you're in your car and some motorcyclist comes bshoom ! 85 miles an hour down , lanesplitting i know you've had this experience that guy didn't " just come out of nowhere . "	即使當你在你的車上 , 又來了摩托車 ! 以每小時85英里的速度下降 , 我知道你曾經有過這樣的經驗: 「 那傢伙不是無中生有 。 」
that guy's been on the road probably for the last half hour .	那個人在過去半個小時都在路上 。
right ? i mean , somebody's seen him .	對吧 ? 我的意思是 , 有人見過他
ten , 20 , 30 miles back , someone's seen that guy , and as soon as one car sees that guy and puts him on the map , he's on the map position , velocity , good estimate he'll continue going 85 miles an hour .	10 , 20 , 30英里前 , 有人看見了那個傢伙 , 只要有一部車看到了那個傢伙 , 然後把他放在地圖上 , 他的位置 , 速度 , 估計他會以每小時85英哩的速度持續前進 。
you'll know , because your car will know , because that other car will have whispered something in his ear , like , " by the way , five minutes , motorcyclist , watch out . "	你會知道 , 因為你的車會知道 , 因為其他車也會在他耳邊低語一些東西 , 比如: 「 順便一提 , 五分鐘 , 摩托車騎士 , 小心點 。 」
you can make reasonable predictions about how cars behave .	你可以合理地預測車子的行為 。
i mean , they're newtonian objects .	我的意思是 , 它們是牛頓的物品 。
that's very nice about them .	那對他們很有好處 。
so how do we get there ?	所以 , 我們要如何做到呢 ?
we can start with something as simple as sharing our position data between cars , just sharing gps .	我們可以從簡單的東西開始 , 分享我們在車子之間的位置資料 , 只是分享gps 。
if i have a gps and a camera in my car , i have a pretty precise idea of where i am and how fast i'm going .	如果我車上有gps和攝影機 , 我對於我現在在哪裡有很精準的看法 , 以及我未來有多快 。
with computer vision , i can estimate where the cars around me are , sort of , and where they're going .	有了電腦視覺 , 我可以估計我旁邊哪裡有車 , 哪裡有車 , 以及他們要往哪裡去 。
and same with the other cars .	其他車也一樣 。
they can have a precise idea of where they are , and sort of a vague idea of where the other cars are .	他們可以精確地知道自己身在何方 , 並且對其他車子的位置有點模糊 。
what happens if two cars share that data , if they talk to each other ?	如果兩部車子分享那些資料 , 如果他們彼此交談 , 會發生什麼事 ?
i can tell you exactly what happens .	我可以精確的告訴你會發生什麼事 。
professor bob wang and his team have done computer simulations of what happens when fuzzy estimates combine , even in light traffic , when cars just share gps data , and we've moved this research out of the computer simulation and into robot test beds that have the actual sensors that are in cars now on these robots: stereo cameras , gps , and the twodimensional laser range finders that are common in backup systems .	bobwang教授和他的團隊完成了電腦模擬測驗當模仿模擬後會發生什麼事即便是 「 輕型交通工具 」 當汽車只分享gps資訊我們將這個研究從電腦模擬和機器測試中移出具有現在這些機器人身上實際的感應器比如:音響相機、gps還有平面雷射測距儀這些都是常用的備用系統
we also attach a discrete shortrange communication radio , and the robots talk to each other .	我們也附上一個小小的短距電台 , 機器人會彼此交談 。
when these robots come at each other , they track each other's position precisely , and they can avoid each other .	當這些機器人來到彼此身邊時 , 它們會精準地追蹤彼此的位置 , 就可以避免彼此 。
we're now adding more and more robots into the mix , and we encountered some problems .	我們現在在這個混合物中加入了越來越多的機器人 , 我們遇到了一些問題 。
one of the problems , when you get too much chatter , it's hard to process all the packets , so you have to prioritize , and that's where the predictive model helps you .	其中一個問題 , 當你拿到太多話題 , 很難處理所有的封包 , 所以你必須優先考慮 , 這也是預測模型對你有幫助的地方 。
if your robot cars are all tracking the predicted trajectories , you don't pay as much attention to those packets .	如果你的機器人車都在追蹤著預測的軌跡 , 你就不會太注意那些封包了 。
you prioritize the one guy who seems to be going a little off course .	你優先考慮一個人 , 他看起來有點偏離軌道 。
that guy could be a problem .	那傢伙可能是個問題 。
and you can predict the new trajectory .	並且能夠預測新的軌道 。
so you don't only know that he's going off course , you know how .	所以你不只知道他要偏離航道了 , 你還知道他要怎麼偏 。
and you know which drivers you need to alert to get out of the way .	也知道要提醒哪些驅動力才能脫離哪些動力 。
and we wanted to do how can we best alert everyone ?	我們希望 , 我們要如何警告每個人 ?
how can these cars whisper , " you need to get out of the way ? "	這些車怎麼會悄悄地說: 「 你得趕緊離開路 ? 」
well , it depends on two things: one , the ability of the car , and second the ability of the driver .	嗯 , 這得靠兩件事:一 , 車子的性能二 , 駕駛的能力
if one guy has a really great car , but they're on their phone or , you know , doing something , they're not probably in the best position to react in an emergency .	如果一個人有一台很棒的車 , 但他們在手機上或者 , 你知道的 , 他們可能不是最適合在緊急情況下反應的 。
so we started a separate line of research doing driver state modeling .	所以 , 我們開始了一項研究 , 測試駕駛者的狀態模型 。
and now , using a series of three cameras , we can detect if a driver is looking forward , looking away , looking down , on the phone , or having a cup of coffee .	而現在 , 使用一系列的三相機 , 我們可以偵測到駕駛人向前看、往後看、往下看、往手機看 , 或是喝一杯咖啡 。
we can predict the accident and we can predict who , which cars , are in the best position to move out of the way to calculate the safest route for everyone .	我們可以預知事故我們可以預測是誰、是哪一台車子 , 都位在最好的位置 , 前進後 , 去計算每個人最安全的路線 。
fundamentally , these technologies exist today .	基本上 , 這些科技在今日仍然存在 。
i think the biggest problem that we face is our own willingness to share our data .	我認為 , 我們面臨的最大問題是我們自身的意願分享我們的資料 。
i think it's a very disconcerting notion , this idea that our cars will be watching us , talking about us to other cars , that we'll be going down the road in a sea of gossip .	我認為這是非常令人不安的概念 , 我們的車子會看著我們 , 跟其他車子談 , 我們將會一路從八卦流下 。
but i believe it can be done in a way that protects our privacy , just like right now , when i look at your car from the outside , i don't really know about you .	但我相信它可以用保護我們的隱私的方式來做到 , 就像現在一樣 , 當我從外面看你的車 , 我不太清楚你 。
if i look at your license plate number , i don't really know who you are .	如果我看你的牌照號碼我不太清楚你是誰
i believe our cars can talk about us behind our backs .	我相信我們的車子可以在背後談論我們
and i think it's going to be a great thing .	而我認為這將會是件很棒的事 。
i want you to consider for a moment if you really don't want the distracted teenager behind you to know that you're braking , that you're coming to a dead stop .	我希望各位花點時間想想 , 如果你真的不希望被分心的青少年在你身後 , 知道你要煞車 , 你要停下來了 。
by sharing our data willingly , we can do what's best for everyone .	透過自願分享我們的資料 , 我們可以為每個人做到最好 。
so let your car gossip about you .	所以讓你的車去八卦一下你 。
it's going to make the roads a lot safer .	將會讓道路更安全 。
x prize founder peter diamandis talks about how he helped stephen hawking fulfill his dream of going to space by flying together into the upper atmosphere and experiencing weightlessness at zero g .	xprize創辦人彼得.戴曼迪斯談到他如何幫助史蒂芬.霍金實現他的夢想透過飛進大氣層一起飛進大氣層上空 , 並在零g時體驗無重量 。
business , flight , science , short talk , space , technology , universe	商業、飛行、科學、簡短演講、空間、科技、宇宙 。
peter diamandis on stephen hawking in zero g	彼得•戴曼迪斯關於史提芬•霍金在無重力g-g-g-g-ro 。
those of you who know me know how passionate i am about opening the space frontier .	那些認識我的人知道我有多熱衷於打開太空門 。
so when i had the chance to give the world's expert in gravity the experience of zero gravity , it was incredible .	所以當我有機會給這位世界重力專家無重力的經驗時 , 這真是不可思議 。
and i want to tell you that story .	而我想要告訴你們那個故事 。
i first met him through the archon x prize for genomics .	我初次見到他是在基因組學archonx的獎項
it's a competition we're holding , the second x prize , for the first team to sequence 100 human genomes in 10 days .	這是我們所舉辦的競賽 , 第二個xprize , 第一個能在10天內完成100個人類基因組排序 。
we have something called the genome 100 100 individuals we're sequencing as part of that .	我們有個叫做 「 基因體一百個 」 的個體 , 我們正在對其中的一部分進行排序 。
craig venter chairs that event .	克萊格•凡特那事件的背後 。
and i met professor hawking , and he said his dream was to travel into space .	我遇到了霍金教授 , 他說他的夢想是去太空旅行 。
and i said , " i can't take you there , but i can take you into weightlessness into zerog .	我說: 「 我不能帶你去那裡 , 但我能帶你進入無重狀態 , 變成零重力 。
and he said , on the spot , " absolutely , yes . "	他說: 「 絕對可以 。 」
well , the only way to experience zerog on earth is actually with parabolic flight , weightless flight .	嗯 , 唯一可以在地球上體驗無重力的辦法 , 其實是有著拋物線飛行 , 無重力飛行 。
you take an airplane , you fly over the top , you're weightless for 25 seconds .	你搭飛機 , 飛過頂點 , 25秒的無重力 。
come back down , you weigh twice as much .	再下來 , 你體重兩倍 。
you do it again and again .	你一而再、再而三地做 。
you can get eight , 10 minutes of weightlessness how nasa's trained their astronauts for so long .	你可以得到8、10分鐘的無重力 , 相當於nasa如何訓練他們的太空人那麼久 。
we set out to do this .	我們打算這麼做 。
it took us 11 years to become operational .	我們花了11年才開始營運 。
and we announced that we were going to fly stephen hawking .	並且我們宣布我們要讓史蒂芬•霍金
we had one government agency and one company aircraft operator say , you're crazy , don't do that , you're going kill the guy .	我們有個政府機關和一家公司的營運人員說 , 你瘋了 , 別這樣做 , 你要殺了那傢伙 。
and he wanted to go .	而他也想去 。
we worked hard to get all the permissions .	我們努力取得所有的許可 。
and six months later , we sat down at kennedy space center .	六個月後 , 我們在甘迺迪太空中心坐下 。
we had a press conference , we announced our intent to do one zerog parabola , give him 25 seconds of zerog .	我們召開了一場記者會 , 我們宣佈我們的目標是做一個無重力拋物線 , 給他25秒的無重力 。
and if it went really well , we might do three parabolas .	如果順利的話 , 我們可能會做三個拋物線飛行 。
well , we asked him why he wanted to go up and do this .	我們問他為什麼他想去做這件事 。
and what he said , for me , was very moving .	而他所說的 , 對我來說 , 非常感人 。
he said , " life on earth is at an everincreasing risk of being wiped out by disaster . . .	他說: 「 地球上的生命總是有不斷增加的風險被災難所消滅...
i think the human race doesn't have a future if it doesn't go into space .	我認為如果人類不進入太空 , 人類就沒有未來 。
i therefore want to encourage public interest in space . "	因此我想要鼓勵公眾對空間的興趣 。 」
we took him out to the kennedy space center , up inside the nasa vehicle , into the back of the zerog airplane .	我們帶他到甘迺迪太空中心 , 在nasa的車子裡面 , 進入zero-g飛機的後方 。
we had about 20 people who made donations we raised $150 , 000 in donations for children's charities who flew with us .	我們有大約20個人捐款我們捐款了15萬美元作為兒童慈善事業之用他們跟著我們一起飛 。
a few tedsters here .	這裡有幾位ted會員 。
we set up a whole er .	我們設立了整間急診室 。
we had four emergency room doctors and two nurses on board the airplane .	我們有四位急診室醫生和兩位護士在飛機上 。
we were monitoring his po2 of his blood , his heart rate , his blood pressure .	我們在監測他的血液、心跳、血壓 。
we had everything all set in case of an emergency ; god knows , you don't want to hurt this worldrenowned expert .	我們擁有所有設備 , 以防緊急事件發生 , 天知道 , 你不想傷到這位世界知名的專家 。
we took off from the shuttle landing facility , where the shuttle takes off and lands .	我們從太空梭降落機構起飛 , 那裡是太空梭起降的地方 。
and my partner byron lichtenberg and i carefully suspended him into zerog .	而我的夥伴byronlichtenberg跟我小心地將他懸為零 。
once he was there , [we] let him go to experience what weightlessness was truly like .	一旦他在那裡 , 我們就讓他去體驗無重力的真正樣子 。
and after that first parabola , you know , the doc said everything is great . he was smiling , and we said go .	在第一個拋物線之後 , 你知道 , 醫生說一切都很棒 。 他在微笑 , 我們說去 。
so we did a second parabola .	所以我們做了第二個拋物線飛行 。
we actually floated an apple in homage to sir isaac newton because professor hawking holds the same chair at cambridge that isaac newton did .	我們其實是向艾薩克•牛頓爵士致敬 , 因為霍金教授在劍橋大學也拿著和牛頓一樣的椅子 。
and we did a fourth , and a fifth and a sixth .	然後我們又做了第四、五和第六次 。
and a seventh and an eighth .	以及第七次和第八次 。
and this man does not look like a 65yearold wheelchairbound man .	這個人看起來並不像一個65歲的輪椅的人 。
he was so happy .	他好高興 。
we are living on a precious jewel , and it's during our lifetime that we're moving off this planet .	我們住在一個珍貴的珠寶上 , 正是在我們有生之年 , 我們正要離開這個星球 。
please join us in this epic adventure .	請加入我們一起參與這史詩般的探險 。
medical animator david bolinsky presents 3 minutes of stunning animation that show the bustling life inside a cell .	醫療動畫師大衛•鮑林斯基呈現了三分鐘令人震驚的動畫 , 呈現出細胞內部的繁忙生活 。
design , entertainment , film , health , medicine , science , technology , visualizations	設計、娛樂、電影、健康、醫學、科學、科技、視覺化呈現 。
david bolinsky animates a cell	davidbolinsky動畫一個細胞
i'm a medical illustrator , and i come from a slightly different point of view .	我是醫學插圖師 , 我來自稍微不同的觀點 。
i've been watching , since i grew up , the expressions of truth and beauty in the arts and truth and beauty in the sciences .	我從小就一直在觀察 , 藝術中真與美的表現方式 , 科學中真與美的表現方式 。
and while these are both wonderful things in their own right they both have very wonderful things going for them truth and beauty as ideals that can be looked at by the sciences and by math are almost like the ideal conjoined twins that a scientist would want to date .	雖然這兩者都是獨一無二的好東西 , 它們都有非常美妙的東西 , 能帶給它們真與美 , 身為理想的一群 , 能被科學和數學所檢視的 , 幾乎就像是理想的一對雙胞胎 , 是科學家會想要約會的 。
these are expressions of truth as awefull things , by meaning they are things you can worship .	這些是真相的表達方式 , 像是令人敬畏的東西 , 意思是它們是你可以崇拜的事物 。
they are ideals that are powerful . they are irreducible .	它們是有力的、不可分量的理想 。
they are unique . they are useful sometimes , often a long time after the fact .	它們是獨一無二的 , 有時很有用 , 通常在事實之後很長一段時間 。
and you can actually roll some of the pictures now , because i don't want to look at me on the screen .	你現在其實可以滾出一些照片了 , 因為我不想在螢幕上看到我 。
truth and beauty are things that are often opaque to people who are not in the sciences .	對於不懂科學的人來說 , 真與美通常是不透明的 。
they are things that describe beauty in a way that is often only accessible if you understand the language and the syntax of the person who studies the subject in which truth and beauty is expressed .	它們是用來描述美的事物 , 通常只有在你理解這個主題的語言和語法時 , 才會描述真與美的表現 。
if you look at the math , e=mc squared , if you look at the cosmological constant , where there's an anthropic ideal , where you see that life had to evolve from the numbers that describe the universe these are things that are really difficult to understand .	如果你看數學 , e=mc平方 , 如果你看宇宙常數 , 那裡有個人類學的理想 , 在那裡 , 你看到生命必須由描述宇宙的數字進化出來這些是非常難以理解的事物 。
and what i've tried to do since i had my training as a medical illustrator since i was taught animation by my father , who was a sculptor and my visual mentor i wanted to figure out a way to help people understand truth and beauty in the biological sciences by using animation , by using pictures , by telling stories so that the things that are not necessarily evident to people can be brought forth , and can be taught , and can be understood .	自從我當醫學插畫師以來 , 一直以來 , 我試著要做的是我的父親 , 他是雕塑家 , 也是我的視覺導師 , 我想找出一種方法 , 幫助人們了解生物科學中的真與美 , 透過動畫 , 透過圖片 , 透過說故事 , 讓那些未必是顯而易見的人們可以被拿出來 , 並且可以被教導 , 並且可以被瞭解 。
students today are often immersed in an environment where what they learn is subjects that have truth and beauty embedded in them , but the way they're taught is compartmentalized and it's drawn down to the point where the truth and beauty are not always evident .	今天的學生常常沉浸在一種環境中 , 在這個環境中 , 他們所學的主題當中 , 真與美都蘊含在其中 , 但他們被教導的方式是相對的 , 被歸納為真與美 , 並不總是顯而易見的 。
it's almost like that old recipe for chicken soup where you boil the chicken until the flavor is just gone .	幾乎就像是用來煮雞湯的老食譜 , 直到香味不見了 。
we don't want to do that to our students .	我們不想對我們的學生這麼做 。
so we have an opportunity to really open up education .	所以我們有機會真正開啟教育 。
and i had a telephone call from robert lue at harvard , in the molecular and cellular biology department , a couple of years ago . he asked me if my team and i would be interested and willing to really change how medical and scientific education is done at harvard .	幾年前我接到哈佛大學分子與細胞生物學系的robertlue的電話 。 他問我 , 我和我的團隊是否會有興趣 , 而且願意真正改變哈佛大學的醫學和科學教育方式 。
so we embarked on a project that would explore the cell that would explore the truth and beauty inherent in molecular and cellular biology so that students could understand a larger picture that they could hang all of these facts on .	所以我們開始進行一個探索細胞的計畫 , 探究分子與細胞生物學中與生俱來的真與美 , 讓學生能了解所有這些事實的全貌 。
they could have a mental image of the cell as a large , bustling , hugely complicated city that's occupied by micromachines .	他們可能有心智圖像 , 將細胞作為一個大型、大型、大型、複雜的城市 , 被微機械佔據 。
and these micromachines really are at the heart of life .	這些微機械處於生命的核心 。
these micromachines , which are the envy of nanotechnologists the world over , are selfdirected , powerful , precise , accurate devices that are made out of strings of amino acids .	這些微機械 , 是世界各地奈米技術專家的羨慕 , 是能自我引導、強大、精確的裝置 , 用胺基酸串成的胺基酸 。
and these micromachines power how a cell moves .	這些微機械讓細胞動起來 。
they power how a cell replicates . they power our hearts .	它們驅動著細胞複製 。 它們驅動著我們的心臟 。
they power our minds .	它們驅使我們的思想 。
and so what we wanted to do was to figure out how we could make this story into an animation that would be the centerpiece of biovisions at harvard , which is a website that harvard has for its molecular and cellular biology students that will in addition to all the textual information , in addition to all the didactic stuff put everything together visually , so that these students would have an internalized view of what a cell really is in all of its truth and beauty , and be able to study with this view in mind , so that their imaginations would be sparked , so that their passions would be sparked and so that they would be able to go on and use these visions in their head to make new discoveries and to be able to find out , really , how life works .	所以我們想做的是想辦法把這個故事變成動畫我們想做的是哈佛大學生物維度中心的動畫它是一個哈佛為其分子與細胞生物學學生所設立的網站這個網站將除了所有的教學信息以外 , 所有東西都以視覺方式呈現所以這些學生能夠將細胞內化的真與美 , 並且能夠以此來研究這個觀點 , 以便他們的心靈能夠被激發、激發 , 以便獲得新生命的啟發 。
so we set out by looking at how these molecules are put together .	所以我們開始研究這些分子是如何組合在一起的 。
we worked with a theme , which is , you've got macrophages that are streaming down a capillary , and they're touching the surface of the capillary wall , and they're picking up information from cells that are on the capillary wall , and they are given this information that there's an inflammation somewhere outside , where they can't see and sense .	我們和一個主題合作過 , 就是你有一個巨噬細胞在微血管裡串流 , 它們在微血管壁的表面碰觸著微血管壁 , 它們從毛細管壁上取出的信息 , 這些信息被傳送出去之後 , 外面某處有發炎 , 看不見和感知 。
but they get the information that causes them to stop , causes them to internalize that they need to make all of the various parts that will cause them to change their shape , and try to get out of this capillary and find out what's going on .	但他們得到的資訊會讓他們停下來 , 造成他們內化──他們需要製造出各式各樣的零件 , 才能改變它們的形狀 , 試著脫離這個微血管 , 找出發生了什麼事 。
so these molecular motors we had to work with the harvard scientists and databank models of the atomically accurate molecules and figure out how they moved , and figure out what they did .	所以這些分子馬達我們必須與哈佛的科學家及原子間的數據庫模型合作 , 找出它們如何移動 , 找出它們的作用 。
and figure out how to do this in a way that was truthful in that it imparted what was going on , but not so truthful that the compact crowding in a cell would prevent the vista from happening .	然後想辦法以一種真理的方式去做這件事情 , 讓事情變得更真實 , 讓細胞中的擁擠人群 , 無法防止它發生 。
and so what i'm going to show you is a threeminute reader's digest version of the first aspect of this film that we produced . it's an ongoing project that's going to go another four or five years .	所以 , 我要給你們看的是我們製作的這部影片的第一個面向的三分鐘讀者版本 。 這是一個持續進行中的專案計畫 , 預計要再花四、五年 。
and i want you to look at this and see the paths that the cell manufactures these little walking machines , they're called kinesins that take these huge loads that would challenge an ant in relative size .	我希望你們能看著這邊 , 看到細胞製造這些步行機器的路徑 , 它們叫做動脈 , 承載著巨大的負荷 , 以相對大小的尺寸挑戰著螞蟻 。
run the movie , please .	請去跑這部電影 。
but these machines that power the inside of the cells are really quite amazing , and they really are the basis of all life because all of these machines interact with each other .	但這些驅動細胞內部的機器真的是相當驚人的 , 它們真的是所有生命的基礎 , 因為所有這些機器彼此之間的互動 。
they pass information to each other .	互相傳遞訊息 。
they cause different things to happen inside the cell .	它們會造成細胞內的不同事情 。
and the cell will actually manufacture the parts that it needs on the fly , from information that's brought from the nucleus by molecules that read the genes .	細胞會透過讀取基因的分子 , 來製造出果蠅身上所需的零件 。
no life , from the smallest life to everybody here , would be possible without these little micromachines .	沒有任何生命 , 從最小的生命到在座的各位 , 如果沒有這些小小的微機械 , 就有可能辦到 。
in fact , it would really , in the absence of these machines , have made the attendance here , chris , really quite sparse .	事實上 , 沒有這些機械時 , 克里斯 , 會很激烈的衝動 。
this is the fedex delivery guy of the cell .	這是細胞的fedex快遞小伙子 。
this little guy is called the kinesin , and he pulls a sack that's full of brand new manufactured proteins to wherever it's needed in the cell whether it's to a membrane , whether it's to an organelle , whether it's to build something or repair something .	這個小傢伙叫作kinesin , 他拉著一個包裝滿全新的製造蛋白質到細胞所需處的任何地方不論是到細胞膜、或是到器官、不論是用來製造東西或修復某些東西 。
and each of us has about 100 , 000 of these things running around , right now , inside each one of your 100 trillion cells .	我們每個人大約有十萬種這種細胞 , 目前在你一百兆個細胞中跑來跑去 。
so no matter how lazy you feel , you're not really intrinsically doing nothing .	所以 , 不論你感覺有多懶惰 , 本質上 , 你其實什麼都不做 。
so what i want you to do when you go home is think about this , and think about how powerful our cells are .	所以當你們回家後 , 我希望你們能想想這一點 , 想想我們的細胞多麼地強大 。
and think about some of the things that we're learning about cellular mechanics .	想想看 , 我們學到的一些關於細胞機械學的知識 。
once we figure out all that's going on and believe me , we know almost a percent of what's going on once we figure out what's going on , we're really going to be able to have a lot of control over what we do with our health , with what we do with future generations , and how long we're going to live .	一旦我們搞懂了這一切 , 相信我 , 我們便知道其中的百分之一 , 一旦我們搞懂了現況 , 我們將能對我們的健康做許多控制 , 配合我們未來的世代 , 及我們將活多久 。
and hopefully we'll be able to use this to discover more truth , and more beauty .	希望我們能利用這一點來發現更多的真理 , 和更多的美 。
but it's really quite amazing that these cells , these micromachines , are aware enough of what the cell needs that they do their bidding .	但非常驚人的是 , 這些細胞 , 這些微機械 , 足以意識到它們所需細胞的作用 。
they work together . they make the cell do what it needs to do .	它們同心協力 。 它們使細胞做出它所需的功能 。
and their working together helps our bodies huge entities that they will never see function properly .	它們一起工作 , 協助我們的身體 , 巨大的實體 , 它們永遠都看不清正常的功能 。
enjoy the rest of the show . thank you .	好好享受剩下的演出 。 謝謝 。
becky blanton planned to live in her van for a year and see the country , but when depression set in and her freelance job ended , her camping trip turned into homelessness . in this intimate talk , she describes her experience of becoming one of america's working homeless .	貝琪布蘭頓計畫要在她的休旅車上住一年 , 看到這個國家 , 但當憂鬱症出現時 , 她的自由工作結束了 , 她的營地旅行變成了無家可歸 。 在這個親密的演說中 , 她形容她經歷到美國正在無家可歸的工作 。
adventure , happiness , life , personal growth , poverty , social change , society , storytelling	冒險、快樂、生活、個人成長、貧窮、社會改變、社會、說故事 。
becky blanton: the year i was homeless	beckyblanton:我那年是流浪漢
i'm a writer and a journalist , and i'm also an insanely curious person , so in 22 years as a journalist , i've learned how to do a lot of new things .	我是作家和記者 , 同時也是一個出於好奇的人 , 所以身為記者 , 我已經學會了怎麼做很多新的事情 。
and three years ago , one of the things i learned how to do was to become invisible .	三年前 , 我學到如何做的事情之一就是變得隱形 。
i became one of the working homeless .	我變成了工作無家者之一 。
i quit my job as a newspaper editor after my father died in february of that same year , and decided to travel .	我辭去了報紙編輯的工作就在我父親同年二月去世之後 , 決定去旅行 。
his death hit me pretty hard .	他的死讓我非常難受 。
and there were a lot of things that i wanted to feel and deal with while i was doing that .	我在做這件事的時候 , 有很多事情想要感受和處理 。
i've camped my whole life . and i decided that living in a van for a year to do this would be like one long camping trip .	我一生都在露營 , 我決定要在旅行車中生活一年 , 做這件事就像一趟漫長的露營旅行 。
so i packed my cat , my rottweiler and my camping gear into a 1975 chevy van , and drove off into the sunset , having fully failed to realize three critical things .	我把我的貓、勞威爾和露營裝備塞進了一台1975年雪佛蘭旅行車 , 開車去過日落 , 沒想到三件很關鍵的事 。
one: that society equates living in a permanent structure , even a shack , with having value as a person .	一:社會等同生活在恆久不變的架構中 , 甚至是像一個人 , 擁有價值 。
two: i failed to realize how quickly the negative perceptions of other people can impact our reality , if we let it .	二:我沒有意識到 , 很快地 , 其他人的負面看法對我們的現實有多大的影響 , 如果我們放任它 。
three: i failed to realize that homelessness is an attitude , not a lifestyle .	三:我沒意識到 , 無家可歸是一種態度 , 而非生活方式 。
at first , living in the van was great .	一開始 , 住在旅行車是很棒的 。
i showered in campgrounds . i ate out regularly .	我在營地洗澡 , 我定期吃飯 。
and i had time to relax and to grieve .	我有時間放鬆 , 哀悼 。
but then the anger and the depression about my father's death set in .	但接著 , 父親去世的憤怒和沮喪 。
my freelance job ended . and i had to get a fulltime job to pay the bills .	我的自由工作結束了 。 而我必須找全職工作來支付帳單 。
what had been a really mild spring turned into a miserably hot summer .	一個溫和的春天 , 變成了極度炎熱的夏天 。
and it became impossible to park anywhere without being very obvious that i had a cat and a dog with me , and it was really hot .	要停在任何地方都不可能 , 要很明顯地知道我有一隻貓和一隻狗 , 而且這實在很熱 。
the cat came and went through an open window in the van .	那隻貓跑過來 , 經過了車窗 ,
the doggy went into doggy day care .	狗狗也進到日間護理中心 ,
whenever i could , i used employee showers in office buildings and truck stops .	每當我可以的時候 , 我會用辦公大樓和卡車站的員工淋浴 。
or i washed up in public rest rooms .	或在公共場所清理乾淨
nighttime temperatures in the van rarely dropped below 80 degrees fahrenheit , making it difficult or impossible to sleep .	夜間的車廂中很少在華氏80度以下的房間溫度會下降 , 讓睡眠變得很難或不可能 。
food rotted in the heat .	食物在高溫中腐爛 。
ice in my ice chest melted within hours , and it was pretty miserable .	我冰箱裡的冰塊在數小時內融化了 , 那真是慘不忍睹 。
i couldn't afford to find an apartment , or couldn't afford an apartment that would allow me to have the rottweiler and the cat .	我沒錢住進准許養貓狗的公寓 , 或根本負擔不起公寓 , 讓我有羅特韋爾和那隻貓 。
and i refused to give them up , so i stayed in the van .	而我拒絕放棄他們 , 所以我留在旅行車裡 。
and when the heat made me too sick to walk the 50 feet to the public restroom outside my van at night , i used a bucket and a trash bag as a toilet .	當熱氣使我無法在晚上在公共廁所外走了五十英尺我用桶子和垃圾袋當廁所
when winter weather set in , the temperatures dropped below freezing . and they stayed there .	當冬天來臨時 , 溫度下降的溫度會降到低於冷凍狀態 。 他們就待在那裏 。
and i faced a whole new set of challenges .	我又面臨了一整套全新的挑戰 。
i parked a different place every night so i would avoid being noticed and hassled by the police .	我每晚都在一個不同的地方停車 , 以免被警察發現和惹火 。
i didn't always succeed .	我並不總是成功的 。
but i felt out of control of my life .	但我卻覺得失控了我的人生 。
and i don't know when or how it happened , but the speed at which i went from being a talented writer and journalist to being a homeless woman , living in a van , took my breath away .	我不知道是何時、如何發生 , 但我從一個有才華的作家和記者 , 到一個無家可歸的女性 , 住在旅行車裡 , 把我的呼吸都消失了 。
i hadn't changed . my i . q . hadn't dropped .	我還沒變 , 我智商沒降
my talent , my integrity , my values , everything about me remained the same .	我的才華、我的正直、我的價值觀 , 所有關於我的價值觀 , 都還是一樣 。
but i had changed somehow .	但我某程度上改變了 。
i spiraled deeper and deeper into a depression .	我在憂鬱的過程中旋轉越來越深 。
and eventually someone referred me to a homeless health clinic .	最後有人提名我去一間無家可歸的健康診所 。
and i went . i hadn't bathed in three days .	我就去了 。 我三天沒洗澡了 。
i was as smelly and as depressed as anyone in line .	我跟排隊中的人一樣沮喪、一樣沮喪 。
i just wasn't drunk or high .	我就是不喝醉或者不高興 。
and when several of the homeless men realized that , including a former university professor , they said , " you aren't homeless . why are you really here ? "	當數不清的流浪漢發現 , 包括一個前任大學教授 , 他們說: 「 你不是無家可歸者 。 你為什麼要在這裡 ? 」
other homeless people didn't see me as homeless , but i did .	其他無家者不把我當成無家者 , 但我卻做了 。
then the professor listened to my story and he said , " you have a job . you have hope .	然後教授聽了我的故事 , 他說: 「 你有工作 , 你有希望 。
the real homeless don't have hope . "	真正的街友是沒有希望的 。 」
a reaction to the medication the clinic gave me for my depression left me suicidal . and i remember thinking , " if i killed myself , no one would notice . "	診所給我的抑鬱藥有種反應讓我有自殺傾向 , 我記得當時心想: 「 如果我殺了自己 , 沒有人會注意到 。 」
a friend told me , shortly after that , that she had heard that tim russert , a nationally renowned journalist , had been talking about me on national t . v .	不久之後 , 一位朋友告訴我 , 她聽說提姆•拉瑟斯特 , 一位全國知名的記者 , 曾在全國電視台上談到我 。
an essay i'd written about my father , the year before he died , was in tim's new book .	我寫的一篇有關我父親的文章在他去世的前一年在提姆的新書
and he was doing the talk show circuit . and he was talking about my writing .	他當時正在表演電路 , 他正在談我的寫作 。
and when i realized that tim russert , former moderator of " meet the press , " was talking about my writing , while i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , i started laughing .	當我意識到提姆•魯斯特曾主持《與媒體見面》前主持人談到我的寫作 , 當時我住在沃爾瑪超市停車場的旅行車裡 , 我開始大笑 。
i started laughing because it got to the point where , was i a writer , or was i a homeless woman ?	我開始笑了因為那時候我是個作家 , 還是一個無家可歸的女人 ?
so i went in the bookstore . and i found tim's book .	於是我走進書店 , 找到提姆的書
and i stood there . and i reread my essay .	我站在那裡 , 重讀了我的文章
because i was a writer .	因為我是個作家
i was a writer .	我是作家 。
shortly after that i moved back to tennessee .	不久之後我搬回了田納西 。
i alternated between living in a van and couch surfing with friends .	我住在旅行車中 , 和朋友家中的沙發衝浪有所替代 。
and i started writing again .	我又開始寫作了 。
by the summer of the following year i was a working journalist .	隔年夏天我擔任記者工作 。
i was winning awards . i was living in my own apartment .	我是贏家 。 我活在我自己的公寓裡 。
i was no longer homeless .	我不再無家可歸 。
and i was no longer invisible .	而我不再是隱形人 。
thousands of people work full and parttime jobs , and live in their cars .	數以千計的人全職工作 , 兼職工作 , 還住在他們的車裡 。
but society continues to stigmatize and criminalize living in your vehicle or on the streets .	但社會持續汙名化 , 犯罪化居住在你的車上或街上 。
so the homeless , the working homeless , primarily remain invisible .	所以無家可歸者 , 工作無家者 , 主要還是隱形的 。
but if you ever meet one , engage them , encourage them , and offer them hope .	但如果你曾經遇過他們 , 讓他們投入 , 鼓勵他們 , 並給他們希望 。
the human spirit can overcome anything if it has hope .	人類的精神可以克服任何事 , 只要有希望的話 。
and i'm not here to be the poster girl for the homeless .	我來這裡不是要當無家可歸者的海報女孩 。
i'm not here to encourage you to give money to the next panhandler you meet .	我不是來鼓勵你們把錢交給你們認識的下一個乞討者 。
but i am here to tell you that , based on my experience , people are not where they live , where they sleep , or what their life situation is at any given time .	但我來這裡告訴各位 , 根據我的經驗 , 大家不是住的地方、睡的地方 , 或生活處境 。
three years ago i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , and today i'm speaking at ted .	三年前 , 我住在旅行車上停在沃爾瑪超市的停車場 , 今天我在ted演講 。
hope always , always finds a way . thank you .	希望總是 , 總是找到一個辦法 。 謝謝 。
at tedxchange , thailand's " mr . condom , " mechai viravaidya , walks us through the country's bold plan to raise its standard of living , starting in the 1970s . first step: population control . and that means a lot of frank , funny and very effective talk about condoms .	在tedxchange , 泰國的 「 保險套先生 」 , mechaiviravaidya , 帶領我們走過全國大膽的計畫 , 去提升它的生活水準 , 從七○年代開始 。 第一步:人口控制 。 這意味著 , 許多法蘭克 , 很有趣也很有效的談論安全套 。
culture , global issues , health , population , science	文化、全球議題、健康、人口、科學、
mechai viravaidya: how mr . condom made thailand a better place	麥奇維拉瓦迪亞:保險套的先生如何讓泰國成為更好的地方 。
now , when i was a young man 40 years ago , the country was very , very poor with lots and lots and lots of people living in poverty .	四十年前 , 我還是個年輕人時 , 這個國家是非常非常貧窮的 , 有許多許多的人口生活在貧窮的環境中 。
we decided to do something about it , but we didn't begin with a welfare program or a poverty reduction program .	我們決定為此做點什麼 , 但我們不是從福利計劃開始 , 或是從貧窮減量計劃開始 。
but we began with a familyplanning program , following a very successful maternal child health activity , sets of activities .	但我們從一個家庭主導的計畫開始 , 遵循一套非常成功的婦女兒童健康活動 , 一組活動 。
so basically , no one would accept family planning if their children didn't survive .	所以 , 基本上 , 沒有人會接受節育計畫 , 如果他們的孩子沒有生存的話 。
so the first step: get to the children , get to the mothers , and then follow up with family planning .	所以 , 第一步:先接觸孩子 , 接觸母親 , 然後再接續家庭計畫 。
not just child mortality alone , you need also family planning .	不只是孩童死亡率 , 你還需要家庭計劃 。
now let me take you back as to why we needed to do it .	現在讓我帶各位回顧一下為什麼我們需要這麼做 。
in my country , that was the case in 1974 .	在我國 , 1974年就是如此 。
seven children per family tremendous growth at 3 . 3 percent .	每個家庭平均有7個小孩 , 成長率是3.3% 。
there was just no future .	沒有未來 。
we needed to reduce the population growth rate .	我們需要降低人口成長率 。
so we said , " let's do it . "	所以我們說: 「 就去做吧 。 」
the women said , " we agree . we'll use pills , but we need a doctor to prescribe the pills , " and we had very , very few doctors .	婦女說: " 我們同意 。 我們會用藥丸 , 但是我們需要一個醫生來開藥 。 " 而且我們有非常非常非常少的醫生 。
we didn't take no as an answer ; we took no as a question .	我們不接受沒有答案 , 我們沒有提出任何問題 。
we went to the nurses and the midwives , who were also women , and did a fantastic job at explaining how to use the pill .	我們找護士和助產士 , 她們也是女性 , 她們做了一件很棒的工作 , 解釋如何用藥 。

we introduced our first microcredit program in 1975 , and the women who organized it said , " we only want to lend to women who practice family planning .	我們在1975年推出了我們第一個小額貸款計畫 , 該計畫組織的女性說: 「 我們只想借給實行家庭計畫的女性 。
if you're pregnant , take care of your pregnancy .	如果你懷孕了 , 要好好照顧你的懷孕 。
if you're not pregnant , you can take a loan out from us . "	如果你不懷孕 , 你可以從我們這裡貸款 。 」
and that was run by them .	那就是他們經營的 。
and after 35/36 years , it's still going on .	35/36年後 , 還在持續進行中 。
it's a part of the village development bank ; it's not a real bank , but it's a fund microcredit .	它是村落發展銀行的一部分 ; 它不是真的銀行 , 但它是基金微型貸款 。

because poor people are business people who lack business skills and access to credit .	因為貧窮的人是商人 , 他們缺乏商業技能和取得功勞 。
those are the things to be provided by the business community .	那些是由商業社群提供的東西
we're trying to turn them into barefoot entrepreneurs , little business people .	我們試著將他們轉化為赤足企業家 , 小企業家 。
the only way out of poverty is through business enterprise .	脫離貧窮的唯一方法是透過企業企業
so , that was done .	完成了 。

and before you can borrow the money , you need to be trained .	而在你能借錢前 , 你需要先接受訓練 。
and we believe if you want to help the poor , those who are living in poverty , access to credit must be a human right .	我們相信 , 如果你想要幫助窮人 , 那些生活在貧窮之中的人 , 信用能力就必須要成為人權 。
access to credit must be a human right .	信用權利的取得 , 一定是人權 。
otherwise they'll never get out of poverty .	否則他們永遠脫離不了貧窮 。
and then before getting a loan , you must be trained .	然後在取得貸款之前 , 你必須要先接受訓練 。
here's what we call a " barefoot mba , " teaching people how to do business so that , when they borrow money , they'll succeed with the business .	以下是我們所謂的赤腳mba教導人們如何做生意如此一來 , 當他們借錢時 , 他們就會成功的完成生意

your smartphone may feel like a friend but a true friend would give you a smile once in a while . at ted2013 , keller rinaudo demos romo , the smartphonepowered mini robot who can motor along with you on a walk , slide you a cup of coffee across the table , and react to you with programmable expressions .	你的智慧手機可能會覺得像個朋友 , 但真正的朋友會給你微笑一會兒 。 在ted2013年的時候 , 凱勒•里納多•狄莫斯羅摩斯 , 智慧手機驅動的mini機器人會和你一起散步 , 滑動一杯咖啡 , 一杯咖啡跨過桌 , 用可編程的表達方式來回應你 。
keller rinaudo: a mini robot powered by your phone	kellerrinaudo:一個迷你機器人用手機發電 。
so just by a show of hands , how many of you all have a robot at home ?	請舉手 , 有多少人家裡都有機器人 ?
not very many of you .	不是很多人 。
okay . and actually of those hands , if you don't include roomba how many of you have a robot at home ?	好的 。 舉手來說 , 如果你不納入roomba有多少人家中有機器人 ?
that's the problem that we're trying to solve at romotive that i and the other 20 nerds at romotive are obsessed with solving .	這就是我們romotive公司想解決的問題我和其他二十位宅男在romotive做的 , 他們都熱衷於解決問題 。
so we really want to build a robot that anyone can use , whether you're eight or 80 .	所以我們真的想要打造一個人人都可以用的機器人不論你是八歲還是八十歲
and as it turns out , that's a really hard problem , because you have to build a small , portable robot that's not only really affordable , but it has to be something that people actually want to take home and have around their kids .	結果發現 , 這真的是很困難的問題 , 因為你必須打造一個小、可攜式的機器人 , 這不僅僅是真正負擔得起 , 而且它必須是人們真正想要帶回家 , 帶回家的東西 。
this robot can't be creepy or uncanny .	這個機器人不能令人毛骨悚然或不可思議 。
he should be friendly and cute .	他應該要友善和可愛 。
romo's a robot that uses a device you already know and love your iphone as his brain .	romo這個機器人 , 使用一種你已經知道且喜愛你的iphone做為他的大腦 。
and by leveraging the power of the iphone's processor , we can create a robot that is wifi enabled and computer visioncapable for 150 bucks , which is about one percent of what these kinds of robots have cost in the past .	藉由iphone處理器的力量 , 我們可以創造一個機器人 , 這個機器人能用wi-fi網路和電腦視覺容量一百五十美元 , 大約是過去這類機器人的花費的百分之一 。
when romo wakes up , he's in creature mode .	當romo被喚醒時 , 他正處於生物模式中 。
so he's actually using the video camera on the device to follow my face .	所以他其實是利用設備上的錄影機拍攝的 , 來追蹤我的臉 。
if i duck down , he'll follow me .	如果我躲下去 , 他就會跟著我 。
he's wary , so he'll keep his eyes on me .	他很疑惑 , 所以他會把目光放在我身上 。
if i come over here , he'll turn to follow me .	如果我來到這裡 , 他會轉向跟著我 。
if i come over here he's smart .	如果我來這裡 , 他很聰明 。
and if i get too close to him , he gets scared just like any other creature .	如果我太靠近他 , 他會感到害怕 , 就像任何其他生物一樣 。
so in a lot of ways , romo is like a pet that has a mind of his own .	所以 , romo像是一隻有自己想法的寵物 。

but the most important thing about romo is that we wanted to create something that was literally completely intuitive .	但關於romo最重要的事是我們想要創造一個完全依靠直覺的東西 。

so he actually streams twoway audio and video between any two smart devices .	所以他其實是將雙向音頻和影片串流在任何兩個智慧裝置之間 。
