so we were talking before about telepresence , and this is a really cool example .	所以我們之前談到遠端臨場 , 這是個很酷的例子 。
you can imagine an eightyearold girl , for example , who has an iphone , and her mom buys her a robot .	你可以想像一個八歲大的女孩 , 比如說 , 她有一支iphone , 她媽媽買給她一個機器人 。
that girl can take her iphone , put it on the robot , send an email to grandma , who lives on the other side of the country .	那個女孩可以拿著她的iphone , 把它放在機器人上 , 發送一封電子郵件給祖母 , 她住在國家的另一端 。
grandma can log into that robot and play hideandgoseek with her granddaughter for fifteen minutes every single night , when otherwise she might only be able to get to see her granddaughter once or twice a year .	奶奶可以登入那個機器人 , 和她的孫女一起玩捉迷藏 , 每晚十五分鐘 , 否則她一年可能只能看她的孫女一、兩次而已 。
so those are a couple of the really cool things that romo can do today .	所以這些是romo今天能做的幾個很酷的事 。
but i just want to finish by talking about something that we're working on in the future .	最後我想談談我們未來在努力的方向 。
this is actually something that one of our engineers , dom , built in a weekend .	這其實是我們的一個工程師 , dom , 在一個週末的時候做的 。
it's built on top of a google open framework called blockly .	它是建立在google一個稱為blockly的開放框架上的 。
this allows you to drag and drop these blocks of semantic code and create any behavior for this robot you want .	這可以讓你拖拉這些區塊的編碼和創造任何你想要這個機器人的行為 。
you do not have to know how to code to create a behavior for romo .	你不需要知道如何編寫程式才能為romo創造一個行為 。
and you can actually simulate that behavior in the browser , which is what you see romo doing on the left .	你實際上可以在瀏覽器中模擬這種行為 , 就是你看到romo在左邊做的事 。
and then if you have something you like , you can download it onto your robot and execute it in real life , run the program in real life .	如果你有你喜歡的東西 , 你可以下載它到你的機器人 , 並在現實生活中去執行它 , 在現實生活中運行這個程式 。
and then if you have something you're proud of , you can share it with every other person who owns a robot in the world .	如果你有值得驕傲的事物 , 你可以和世界上所有擁有機器人的人分享 。
so all of these wifi–enabled robots actually learn from each other .	所以 , 所有這些wi-fi讓機器人互相學習的機器人 。
the reason we're so focused on building robots that everyone can train is that we think the most compelling use cases in personal robotics are personal .	我們之所以太專注於建造一個大家都能訓練的機器人 , 是因為我們認為在個人機器人中 , 最能引人注目的使用方式 , 是個人的 。
they change from person to person .	它們會從人到人的改變 。
so we think that if you're going to have a robot in your home , that robot ought to be a manifestation of your own imagination .	所以 , 我們認為 , 如果你要在你的家中有個機器人 , 那個機器人應該是你自己想像出來的一種呈現出來 。
so i wish that i could tell you what the future of personal robotics looks like .	所以 , 我希望我能告訴你們個人機器人的未來是什麼樣子 。
to be honest , i have no idea .	老實說 , 我不知道 。
but what we do know is that it isn't 10 years or 10 billion dollars or a large humanoid robot away .	但我們知道的是 , 它不是10年或100億美元 , 也不是大型的類人型機器人 。
the future of personal robotics is happening today , and it's going to depend on small , agile robots like romo and the creativity of people like yourselves .	個人機器人的未來就發生在今天 , 這將會取決於像romo這樣的小型敏捷的機器人 , 以及像你這樣的人的創造力 。
so we can't wait to get you all robots , and we can't wait to see what you build .	所以我們迫不及待地想讓你們所有的機器人 , 我們迫不及待地想看你們建造的是什麼 。
author and activist isabel allende discusses women , creativity , the definition of feminism and , of course , passion in this talk .	作者和行動主義者伊莎貝•阿言德討論女性、創意、女性主義的定義 , 當然 , 還有這場演說的熱情 。
entertainment , global issues , love , parenting , storytelling , women , world cultures	娛樂、全球議題、愛、養育、說故事、女人、世界文化 。
isabel allende tells tales of passion	伊莎貝爾•阿言德講述激情的故事 。
thank you so much . it's really scary to be here among the smartest of the smart .	非常感謝大家 。 能來到這裡是最聰明的一個 。 真的很可怕 。
i'm here to tell you a few tales of passion .	我在這裡告訴你們幾個充滿熱情的故事 。
there's a jewish saying that i love .	有個猶太人說我愛
what is truer than truth ? answer: the story .	比真理更真誠的是什麼 ? 答案:故事 。
i'm a storyteller . i want to convey something that is truer than truth about our common humanity .	我是一個說故事的人 。 我想要傳達一個比事實更真誠的東西 , 關於我們共同的人性 。
all stories interest me , and some haunt me until i end up writing them .	所有故事都對我感興趣 , 有些甚至令我心煩意亂 , 直到我終於把它們寫出來 。
certain themes keep coming up: justice , loyalty , violence , death , political and social issues , freedom .	有些主題不斷出現:正義、忠誠、暴力、死亡、政治和社會議題、自由 。
i'm aware of the mystery around us , so i write about coincidences , premonitions , emotions , dreams , the power of nature , magic .	我意識到我們周遭的神祕 , 所以我寫下巧合、預兆、情緒、夢想、自然的力量、魔法 。
in the last 20 years i have published a few books , but i have lived in anonymity until february of 2006 , when i carried the olympic flag in the winter olympics in italy .	過去二十年 , 我出版了幾本書 , 但我一直活在匿名中 , 直到2006年二月 , 當我在義大利的冬季奧運會上 , 帶著奧運旗幟 。
that made me a celebrity . now people recognize me in macy's , and my grandchildren think that i'm cool .	這讓我成了名人 。 現在大家在macy的領域裡認得我 , 我的孫子們都覺得我很酷 。
allow me to tell you about my four minutes of fame .	讓我告訴你們我名聲的四分鐘 。
one of the organizers of the olympic ceremony , of the opening ceremony , called me and said that i had been selected to be one of the flagbearers .	一名籌辦奧運開幕式的籌辦人打電話給我說我被選為護旗手之一
i replied that surely this was a case of mistaken identity because i'm as far as you can get from being an athlete .	我回答 , 這肯定是個錯誤認同的案例 , 因為我到目前為止 , 從運動健兒那一刻起 。
actually , i wasn't even sure that i could go around the stadium without a walker .	其實 , 我甚至不確定我能繞著體育場跑一圈 , 沒有助行器 。
i was told that this was no laughing matter .	我被告知這不是在笑
this would be the first time that only women would carry the olympic flag .	這會是頭一次 , 只有女性會攜帶奧林匹克旗幟 。
five women , representing five continents , and three olympic gold medal winners .	五名女性 , 代表五大洲 , 和三位奧運金牌得主 ,
my first question was , naturally , what was i going to wear ?	我的第一個問題是 , 很自然地 , 我要穿什麼 ?
a uniform , she said , and asked for my measurements .	一件制服 , 她說 , 並尋求我的衡量標準 。
i had a vision of myself in a fluffy anorak , looking like the michelin man .	我有一個想法 , 讓我自己處在一個蓬鬆的大道上 , 看起來就像米其林 。
by the middle of february , i found myself in turin , where enthusiastic crowds cheered when any of the 80 olympic teams was in the street .	到了2月中旬 , 我發現自己身在杜林 , 在那裡 , 充滿熱情的群眾在街上 , 任何80個奧運團體都在歡呼 。
those athletes had sacrificed everything to compete in the games .	這些運動員犧牲了一切去比賽 。
they all deserved to win , but there's the element of luck .	他們都應得勝利 , 但也有運氣的要素 。
a speck of snow , an inch of ice , the force of the wind , can determine the result of a race or a game .	一塊雪、一英吋的冰、一股風力 , 就能決定比賽或比賽的結果 。
however , what matters most more than training or luck is the heart .	然而 , 最重要的是訓練或是運氣是心臟 。
only a fearless and determined heart will get the gold medal .	只有無懼且堅定的心才能得到金牌 。
it is all about passion .	一切都與熱情相關 。
the streets of turin were covered with red posters announcing the slogan of the olympics .	杜林街上滿是紅色海報 , 宣布奧運的標誌 。
passion lives here . isn't it always true ?	熱情就在這裡 。 它不是一直都是真的嗎 ?
heart is what drives us and determines our fate .	心是驅使我們及決定我們的命運的因素 。
that is what i need for my characters in my books: a passionate heart .	那是我書中角色所需要的:充滿熱情的心 。
i need mavericks , dissidents , adventurers , outsiders and rebels , who ask questions , bend the rules and take risks .	我需要maverick、異議者、冒險家、外人和反抗者 , 他們問問題、彎曲規則、冒險 。
people like all of you in this room .	像在座各位一樣的人 。
nice people with common sense do not make interesting characters .	有常識的好人不會創造有趣的人物 。
they only make good former spouses .	他們只會是好前夫
in the green room of the stadium , i met the other flag bearers: three athletes , and the actresses susan sarandon and sophia loren .	在體育館的綠色房間裡 , 我遇見了其他護旗手:三位運動員 , 演員蘇珊珊和蘇菲雅羅蘭 。
also , two women with passionate hearts: wangari maathai , the nobel prizewinner from kenya who has planted 30 million trees . and by doing so , she has changed the soil , the weather , in some places in africa , and of course the economic conditions in many villages .	還有兩位心中充滿熱情的女性:旺加里•馬塔伊 , 來自肯亞的諾貝爾獎得主 , 她種植了三千萬棵樹 。 透過這麼做 , 她已經改變了土壤 , 天氣 , 在非洲的某些地方 , 當然也改變了很多村莊的經濟狀況 。
and somaly mam , a cambodian activist who fights passionately against child prostitution .	還有柬埔寨活動家索馬利•瑪姆 , 他熱心地對抗兒童賣淫的抗爭 。
when she was 14 years old , her grandfather sold her to a brothel .	她14歲時 , 祖父將她賣到妓院
she told us of little girls raped by men who believe that having sex with a very young virgin will cure them from aids .	她告訴我們 , 小女孩們被男人強暴她們相信和年紀很小的處女做愛可以治好愛滋病
and of brothels where children are forced to receive five , 15 clients per day , and if they rebel , they are tortured with electricity .	孩子們被迫每天接客515次 , 如果他們反抗 , 就會被電擊折磨 。
in the green room i received my uniform .	在綠色房間裡我收到制服
it was not the kind of outfit that i normally wear , but it was far from the michelin man suit that i had anticipated . not bad , really .	這不是我平常會穿的那種衣服 , 但卻離我預期的米其林男子裝的還遠得很 。 其實不錯 。
i looked like a refrigerator .	我看起來像個冰箱 。
but so did most of the flagbearers , except sophia loren , the universal symbol of beauty and passion .	但大部分的旗幟都是 , 除了蘇菲雅羅蘭 , 通用的美麗和熱情的象徵 。
sophia is over 70 and she looks great .	蘇菲雅超過70歲 , 她看起來很棒 。
she's sexy , slim and tall , with a deep tan .	她很性感、很瘦、很高 , 有著很深的水槽 。
now , how can you have a deep tan and have no wrinkles ?	那麼 , 你如何能有一個很深的油箱卻沒有皺紋呢 ?
when asked in a tv interview , " how could she look so good ? "	在電視訪問中 , 當被問到: 「 她怎麼看起來這麼好 ? 」
she replied , " posture . my back is always straight , and i don't make old people's noises . "	她回答: 「 姿勢 。 我的背總是直直的 。 我沒有發出老人的聲音 。 」
so , there you have some free advice from one of the most beautiful women on earth .	所以 , 你們可以從地球上最美的女性之一得到免費的建議 。
no grunting , no coughing , no wheezing , no talking to yourselves , no farting .	不乏鬥志、咳嗽、不自言自語、不放屁 。
well , she didn't say that exactly .	嗯 , 她並沒有說得很清楚 。
at some point around midnight , we were summoned to the wings of the stadium , and the loudspeakers announced the olympic flag , and the music started by the way , the same music that starts here , the aida march .	在大概午夜的時候 , 我們被召喚去體育場 , 大聲說話者宣佈奧林匹克旗下 , 音樂也從這裡開始 , 同樣的音樂就是從這裡開始的 , aida遊行 。
sophia loren was right in front of me she's a foot taller than i am , not counting the poofy hair .	蘇菲雅羅蘭就在我面前 , 她的身高比我高 , 不算多毛 。
she walked elegantly , like a giraffe on the african savannah , holding the flag on her shoulder . i jogged behind on my tiptoes holding the flag on my extended arm , so that my head was actually under the damn flag .	她優雅地走著 , 就像非洲大草原上的長頸鹿將旗子舉在肩上 。 我在後面小跑步 , 用腳跟在手臂上拿著旗子 , 這樣我的頭就在那該死的旗子下 。
all the cameras were , of course , on sophia .	當然 , 所有的攝影機都在蘇菲亞 。
that was fortunate for me , because in most press photos i appear too , although often between sophia's legs .	那對我來說是幸運的 , 因為在大部分記者的照片中 , 我也會出現 , 雖然常常會出現在蘇菲雅的雙腿間 。
a place where most men would love to be .	一個多數男人會喜歡去的地方 。
the best four minutes of my entire life were those in the olympic stadium .	我一生中最棒的4分鐘就是那些在奧運體育館裡的人 。
my husband is offended when i say this although i have explained to him that what we do in private usually takes less than four minutes so he shouldn't take it personally .	我丈夫被冒犯了 , 雖然我向他解釋 , 我們私下作的事通常只花不到四分鐘 , 所以他不該獨自承受 。
i have all the press clippings of those four magnificent minutes , because i don't want to forget them when old age destroys my brain cells .	我擁有那4個偉大的分鐘數的所有按鈕 , 因為我不想忘記它們 , 當年紀大時摧毀了我的腦細胞 。
i want to carry in my heart forever the key word of the olympics passion .	我想要永遠帶著奧運的關鍵字 , 來永遠帶著我的心 。
so here's a tale of passion .	以下是關於熱情的故事 。
the year is 1998 , the place is a prison camp for tutsi refugees in congo .	時間是1998年 , 這個地方是一座囚營 , 地點是剛果的圖西族難民營 。
by the way , 80 percent of all refugees and displaced people in the world are women and girls .	順帶一提 , 世界上80%的難民和流離失所的人都是婦女和女孩 。
we can call this place in congo a death camp , because those who are not killed will die of disease or starvation .	我們可以稱這個地方為剛果的死亡集中營 , 因為沒有被殺的人 , 將會死於疾病或飢餓 。
the protagonists of this story are a young woman , rose mapendo , and her children .	這個故事的主角是個年輕女性蘿絲•瑪班多和她的孩子
she's pregnant and a widow .	她懷孕了 , 還有一個寡婦 。
soldiers have forced her to watch as her husband was tortured and killed .	士兵們迫使她視其為她的丈夫被虐待並被殺害 。
somehow she manages to keep her seven children alive , and a few months later , she gives birth to premature twins .	不知怎麼的 , 她竟然讓她的七個孩子活了下來 , 幾個月後 , 她生出了早產兒雙胞胎 。
two tiny little boys .	兩個小男孩
she cuts the umbilical cord with a stick , and ties it with her own hair .	她用棍子自己割斷臍帶然後用頭髮把它綁起來
she names the twins after the camp's commanders to gain their favor , and feeds them with black tea because her milk cannot sustain them .	她給陣營的指揮官取名字 , 以取得他們的喜好 , 並用黑色茶餵他們 , 因為她的牛奶無法維持他們的喜好 。
when the soldiers burst in her cell to rape her oldest daughter , she grabs hold of her and refuses to let go , even when they hold a gun to her head .	當士兵闖進她的牢房要強暴她大女兒時 , 她會抓住她並拒絕放手 , 即使他們手持一把槍抵著她的頭 。
somehow , the family survives for 16 months , and then , by extraordinary luck , and the passionate heart of a young american man , sasha chanoff , who manages to put her in a u . s . rescue plane , rose mapendo and her nine children end up in phoenix , arizona , where they're now living and thriving .	不知怎麼的 , 家人存活了16個月然後 , 靠著絕佳的運氣和一名美國男子的熱心臟-sashachnoff , 她設法把她放進一台美國救援機 , 蘿絲.marendo和她的九個孩子最後到了亞利桑那州鳳凰城他們現在在那裡生活和成長茁壯
mapendo , in swahili , means great love .	斯瓦希里語的馬丁歐語意指的是偉大的愛 。
the protagonists of my books are strong and passionate women like rose mapendo .	我書中的主角都是堅強且有熱情的女性 , 像蘿絲•瑪班多 。
i don't make them up . there's no need for that .	我不會捏造它們 , 不需要這些 。
i look around and i see them everywhere .	我環顧四周 , 到處看到他們 。
i have worked with women and for women all my life .	我一生都在與女性及女性合作 。
i know them well .	我對他們很了解 。
i was born in ancient times , at the end of the world , in a patriarchal catholic and conservative family .	我出生在古代 , 在世界末日 , 在父系天主教和保守家庭裡 。
no wonder that by age five i was a raging feminist although the term had not reached chile yet , so nobody knew what the heck was wrong with me .	難怪我五歲時是個憤怒的女權主義者雖然這個名詞還沒有接觸過智利 , 所以沒人知道我到底哪裡出了問題 。
i would soon find out that there was a high price to pay for my freedom , and for questioning the patriarchy .	很快地 , 我會發現 , 為了自由而付出的代價很高 , 以及對父權的質疑 。
but i was happy to pay it , because for every blow that i received , i was able to deliver two .	但我很高興能付出 , 因為每次我接到的一擊 , 我都能遞出二分錢 。
once , when my daughter paula was in her twenties , she said to me that feminism was dated , that i should move on .	有一次 , 當我的女兒寶拉在她二十多歲時 , 她對我說女權主義是約會的 , 我該繼續向前走 。
we had a memorable fight . feminism is dated ?	我們曾有場難忘的戰爭 。 女權主義是約會的嗎 ?
yes , for privileged women like my daughter and all of us here today , but not for most of our sisters in the rest of the world who are still forced into premature marriage , prostitution , forced labor they have children that they don't want or they cannot feed .	是的 , 對於像我女兒和在座各位這樣有特權的女性 , 至今仍然是如此 , 但對世界上大部分的姐妹來說 , 她們仍然被迫結婚、賣淫、強迫勞動 , 她們有不想要的孩子 , 或她們不能進食的孩子 。
they have no control over their bodies or their lives .	他們無法掌控自己的身體或人生 。
they have no education and no freedom .	他們沒有受教育而且沒有自由 。
they are raped , beaten up and sometimes killed with impunity .	他們被強暴、毆打 , 有時被懲罰殺 。
for most western young women of today , being called a feminist is an insult .	對現今大部分西方女性來說 , 被稱為女權主義者是一種侮辱 。
feminism has never been sexy , but let me assure you that it never stopped me from flirting , and i have seldom suffered from lack of men .	女權主義從來就不吸引人 , 但 , 讓我向各位保證 , 它從來不會阻止我調情 , 我很少有缺乏男性的痛苦 。
feminism is not dead , by no means .	女權主義不是死的 , 絕不是死的 。
it has evolved . if you don't like the term , change it , for goddess' sake .	它已經進化了 。 如果你不喜歡這個名詞 , 就改變它 , 為了女神的緣故 。
call it aphrodite , or venus , or bimbo , or whatever you want ; the name doesn't matter , as long as we understand what it is about , and we support it .	稱它為aphrodite , 或維納斯 , 或是布波 , 或任何你想要的都無所謂 ; 只要我們了解它是什麼 , 我們就會支持它 。
so here's another tale of passion , and this is a sad one .	所以這是另一個關於熱情的故事 , 這是個令人難過的故事 。
the place is a small women's clinic in a village in bangladesh .	這個地方是孟加拉某村落的一間小型女性診所 。
the year is 2005 .	時間是2005年 。
jenny is a young american dental hygienist who has gone to the clinic as a volunteer during her threeweek vacation .	珍妮是個年輕的美國衛生學家 , 她在三週的假期中擔任志工 。
she's prepared to clean teeth , but when she gets there , she finds out that there are no doctors , no dentists , and the clinic is just a hut full of flies .	她已經準備好清潔牙齒了 , 但當她到那裡時 , 她發現那裡沒有醫生 , 沒有牙醫 , 診所只是一個塞滿蒼蠅的小屋 。
outside , there is a line of women who have waited several hours to be treated .	在外面 , 有一行婦女等了幾個小時要被醫治 。
the first patient is in excruciating pain because she has several rotten molars .	第一個病人痛苦難當 , 因為她好幾個腐爛的臼齒 。
jenny realizes that the only solution is to pull out the bad teeth .	珍妮意識到唯一的解決方案就是拔掉那爛牙 。
she's not licensed for that ; she has never done it .	她不是被授權的 ; 她從來沒有這麼做過 。
she risks a lot and she's terrified .	她的風險很大 , 她嚇壞了 。
she doesn't even have the proper instruments , but fortunately she has brought some novocaine .	她連適當的樂器都沒有 , 但幸運的是 , 她已經帶了一些麻醉藥 。
jenny has a brave and passionate heart .	珍妮有顆勇敢而熱情的心
she murmurs a prayer and she goes ahead with the operation .	她怒氣活現 , 接受了手術 。
at the end , the relieved patient kisses her hands .	最後 , 病人鬆了一口氣吻了她的手 。
that day the hygienist pulls out many more teeth .	那天 , 衛生人員多拔了牙 。
the next morning , when she comes again to the socalled clinic , her first patient is waiting for her with her husband .	隔天早上 , 當她再次來到所謂的診所時 , 她的第一個病人在跟她的丈夫在等她 。
the woman's face looks like a watermelon .	那女人的臉看起來像是個西瓜 。
it is so swollen that you can't even see the eyes .	腫到看不見眼睛 。
the husband , furious , threatens to kill the american .	丈夫氣極了 , 威脅要殺了美國人 。
jenny is horrified at what she has done , but then the translator explains that the patient's condition has nothing to do with the operation .	珍妮對她所做的事感到震驚 , 但接著 , 翻譯解釋說病人的狀況和手術無關 。
the day before , her husband beat her up because she was not home in time to prepare dinner for him .	前一天 , 她丈夫打她 , 因為她沒有時間替他準備晚餐 。
millions of women live like this today .	現今有數百萬名女性過著這樣的生活 。
they are the poorest of the poor .	他們是最貧窮的人 。
although women do twothirds of the world's labor , they own less than one percent of the world's assets .	雖然全世界有三分之二的勞動力 , 她們擁有的資產卻不到世界財產的1% 。
they are paid less than men for the same work if they're paid at all , and they remain vulnerable because they have no economic independence , and they are constantly threatened by exploitation , violence and abuse .	她們的薪水低於男性如果她們有薪水 , 她們仍然是弱勢 , 因為她們沒有經濟獨立 , 她們不斷受到剝削、暴力和虐待的威脅 。
it is a fact that giving women education , work , the ability to control their own income , inherit and own property , benefits the society .	這是個給予女性教育、工作能力控制自己收入、繼承並擁有財產的事實 , 為社會帶來好處 。
if a woman is empowered , her children and her family will be better off .	如果一個女人被賦予能力 , 她的孩子和家人將會過得更好 。
if families prosper , the village prospers , and eventually so does the whole country .	如果家庭繁榮 , 村落也會繁榮 , 最終 , 整個國家也是如此 。
wangari maathai goes to a village in kenya .	wangarimaathai到肯亞的一個村子裡
she talks with the women and explains that the land is barren because they have cut and sold the trees .	她跟那裡的女人聊天 , 解釋說那裡的土地已經貧瘠 , 因為被砍伐 , 被賣掉的樹木 。
she gets the women to plant new trees and water them , drop by drop .	她讓婦女種植新的樹 , 澆水 , 下降 。
in a matter of five or six years , they have a forest , the soil is enriched , and the village is saved .	在僅僅5或6年的時間裡 , 他們有森林 , 土壤豐富了 , 村子因而得救了 。
the poorest and most backward societies are always those that put women down .	最貧窮和最落後的社會 , 總是那些讓女性放下身段的人 。
yet this obvious truth is ignored by governments and also by philanthropy .	然而 , 這個明顯的事實卻被政府及慈善事業所忽略 。
for every dollar given to a women's program , 20 dollars are given to men's programs .	給予女性相關計畫每一塊錢就有二十塊錢被交給男性 。
women are 51 percent of humankind .	女性佔人類51%的比例
empowering them will change everything more than technology and design and entertainment .	給予他們力量會改變一切比科技、設計和娛樂還要更重要的事
i can promise you that women working together linked , informed and educated can bring peace and prosperity to this forsaken planet .	我可以向各位保證 , 女性同心合力 , 連結、受過教育 , 能為這個理想的星球帶來和平與繁榮 。
in any war today , most of the casualties are civilians , mainly women and children . they are collateral damage .	今天的任何戰爭中 , 死傷最多的都是平民百姓 , 主要是婦女和兒童 。 他們是附帶傷害 。
men run the world , and look at the mess we have .	男人跑世界 , 看看我們有多混亂 。
what kind of world do we want ?	我們想要什麼樣的世界 ?
this is a fundamental question that most of us are asking .	這是我們大多數人都在問的基本問題 。
does it make sense to participate in the existing world order ?	參與現有的世界秩序後會合理嗎 ?
we want a world where life is preserved and the quality of life is enriched for everybody , not only for the privileged .	我們想要一個生命被保存的世界 , 生活品質被提升到每個人身上 , 不僅是為了特權 。
in january i saw an exhibit of fernando botero's paintings at the uc berkeley library .	一月我看到費南多•博特羅在加州大學伯克利圖書館的畫展 。
no museum or gallery in the united states , except for the new york gallery that carries botero's work , has dared to show the paintings because the theme is the abu ghraib prison .	美國沒有一間博物館或畫廊 , 只不過紐約畫廊攜帶巴特羅的作品 , 已經膽敢展示這幅畫 , 因為這幅畫的主題是阿布格萊布監獄 。
they are huge paintings of torture and abuse of power , in the voluminous botero style .	他們是巨大的畫作 , 以酷刑和虐待權力的方式呈現 , 以體面的方式呈現 。
i have not been able to get those images out of my mind or my heart .	我沒有辦法把那些影像從我的腦海或心中顯現出來 。
what i fear most is power with impunity .	最讓我害怕的是權力的障礙 。
i fear abuse of power , and the power to abuse .	我害怕濫用權力 , 以及濫用權力 。
in our species , the alpha males define reality , and force the rest of the pack to accept that reality and follow the rules .	在我們這個族群 , 雄性領袖定義了現實 , 強迫其他成員接受現實並遵守規則 。
the rules change all the time , but they always benefit them , and in this case , the trickledown effect , which does not work in economics , works perfectly .	規則常常在改變 , 但總是有好處 , 在這個例子中 , 在經濟上行不通的 「 滴漏效應 」 效應 。
abuse trickles down from the top of the ladder to the bottom .	從最上面的梯子一路延伸到最底部 。
women and children , especially the poor , are at the bottom .	婦女和兒童 , 尤其是貧窮的人 , 都位於海底 。
even the most destitute of men have someone they can abuse a woman or a child .	即使是最貧窮的男人也有人可以虐待女人或小孩
i'm fed up with the power that a few exert over the many through gender , income , race , and class .	我受夠了少數幾個人的力量 , 包括性別、收入、種族、階級 。
i think that the time is ripe to make fundamental changes in our civilization .	我認為現在是成熟的時候 , 能在我們的文明中做出根本的改變 。
but for real change , we need feminine energy in the management of the world .	但 , 若要真正改變 , 我們就需要全世界的女性能量管理 。
we need a critical number of women in positions of power , and we need to nurture the feminine energy in men .	我們需要關鍵數量的女性掌握權力我們需要培養男性心中的女性能量
i'm talking about men with young minds , of course .	我說的是有年輕心智的男人 , 當然 。
old guys are hopeless ; we have to wait for them to die off .	老傢伙是沒有希望的 ; 我們必須等他們死去 。
yes , i would love to have sophia loren's long legs and legendary breasts .	是的 , 我很想擁有蘇菲雅羅蘭的長腿及傳奇的乳房 。
but given a choice , i would rather have the warrior hearts of wangari maathai , somaly mam , jenny and rose mapendo .	但 , 就一個選擇來說 , 我寧願有顆勇士的心像瓦加里•馬塔伊、蘇曼麗•曼、珍妮和蘿絲
i want to make this world good .	我想要讓這個世界變好 。
not better , but to make it good .	不是更好 , 而是讓它良好 。
why not ? it is possible . look around in this room all this knowledge , energy , talent and technology .	為什麼不呢 ? 這是辦得到的 。 看看這房間裡所有的知識、能量、才華和科技 。
let's get off our fannies , roll up our sleeves and get to work , passionately , in creating an almost perfect world .	讓我們離開我們的歌迷 , 捲起袖子開始工作 , 熱情地 , 創造一個近乎完美的世界 。
every day , in a city the size of london , 30 million meals are served . but where does all the food come from ? architect carolyn steel discusses the daily miracle of feeding a city , and shows how ancient food routes shaped the modern world .	每天 , 在倫敦這麼大的城市裡 , 三千萬份餐都是用過的 。 但是哪裡有所有的食物呢 ? 建築師卡洛琳•史泰爾討論了城市的日常奇蹟 , 展現出古老的食物路線如何塑造出現代世界 。
cities , culture , food , global issues	城市、文化、食物、全球的議題
carolyn steel: how food shapes our cities	carolynsteel:食物如何塑造我們的城市 ?
how do you feed a city ?	如何養活一座城市
it's one of the great questions of our time .	這是我們這個時代最偉大的問題之一 。
yet it's one that's rarely asked .	但很少被問到這個 。
we take it for granted that if we go into a shop or restaurant , or indeed into this theater's foyer in about an hour's time , there is going to be food there waiting for us , having magically come from somewhere .	我們理所當然地認為 , 如果我們去商店或餐廳 , 或是在一小時內到戲院大廳 , 那裡將會有食物等待著我們 , 神奇地從某處來 。
but when you think that every day for a city the size of london , enough food has to be produced , transported , bought and sold , cooked , eaten , disposed of , and that something similar has to happen every day for every city on earth , it's remarkable that cities get fed at all .	但當你認為倫敦這麼大的城市 , 每一天 , 都有足夠的食物被製造、運送、買、買、賣、煮、吃、丟棄 , 類似的事 , 每天都會發生在地球上的每個城市 , 都會被餵養的程度非常驚人 。
we live in places like this as if they're the most natural things in the world , forgetting that because we're animals and that we need to eat , we're actually as dependent on the natural world as our ancient ancestors were .	我們生活在這些地方 , 彷彿它們是世界上最自然的東西 , 忘記了我們是動物、我們需要進食的地方 , 我們其實和我們古老的祖先一樣依賴自然世界 。
and as more of us move into cities , more of that natural world is being transformed into extraordinary landscapes like the one behind me it's soybean fields in mato grosso in brazil in order to feed us .	當更多人搬到城市中 , 更多的自然世界被改造成不平凡的景色 , 就像我身後的這個:在巴西的馬托格羅索的黃豆田裡 , 為了餵飽我們 。
these are extraordinary landscapes , but few of us ever get to see them .	這些景觀十分驚人 , 但很少人見過 。
and increasingly these landscapes are not just feeding us either .	愈來愈多的風景不只是餵飽我們 。
as more of us move into cities , more of us are eating meat , so that a third of the annual grain crop globally now gets fed to animals rather than to us human animals .	當更多人搬進城市時 , 更多人是吃肉的 , 所以每年全球的穀物作物有三分之一都被餵食給動物 , 而不是我們人類的動物 。
and given that it takes three times as much grain actually ten times as much grain to feed a human if it's passed through an animal first , that's not a very efficient way of feeding us .	由於它需要三倍的穀物事實上是十倍的穀物如果它首先是通過動物傳給人類的話這就不是一個非常有效的餵養方式
and it's an escalating problem too .	這也是一個日益增長的問題 。
by 2050 , it's estimated that twice the number of us are going to be living in cities .	到2050年 , 估計我們生活在都市的兩倍之多 。
and it's also estimated that there is going to be twice as much meat and dairy consumed .	另外 , 估計將會有兩倍的肉與乳製品所消耗的量
so meat and urbanism are rising hand in hand .	所以 , 肉類和城市主義在手中提升了 。
and that's going to pose an enormous problem .	這將是個巨大的問題 。
six billion hungry carnivores to feed , by 2050 .	要餵食六十億肉食性動物 , 到2050年 ,
that's a big problem . and actually if we carry on as we are , it's a problem we're very unlikely to be able to solve .	這是個大問題 。 而事實上 , 如果我們以我們身為人類的身分繼續走 , 這是我們不太可能解決的問題 。
nineteen million hectares of rainforest are lost every year to create new arable land .	每年有一千九百萬公頃的熱帶雨林消失 , 以創造新的可耕地 。
although at the same time we're losing an equivalent amount of existing arables to salinization and erosion .	雖然同時我們也失去相當於在鹽化和侵蝕上的可耕地
we're very hungry for fossil fuels too .	我們也非常渴望石化燃料
it takes about 10 calories to produce every calorie of food that we consume in the west .	每一卡路里要耗去我們消耗的食物 , 每一卡路里大約需要十卡路里 。
and even though there is food that we are producing at great cost , we don't actually value it .	雖然有糧食供給我們不計代價我們卻不重視
half the food produced in the usa is currently thrown away .	半數在美國生產的食物 , 目前都被丟棄了 。
and to end all of this , at the end of this long process , we're not even managing to feed the planet properly .	要終結這一切 , 在這漫長過程的最後 , 我們甚至還沒有適當的飲食 。
a billion of us are obese , while a further billion starve .	我們當中有十億人過胖 , 同時又過了十億人的壽命 。
none of it makes very much sense .	這一切都沒道理 。
and when you think that 80 percent of global trade in food now is controlled by just five multinational corporations , it's a grim picture .	當你認為現在全球百分之八十的糧食貿易只由五大跨國公司控制 , 那真是可怕的局面 。
as we're moving into cities , the world is also embracing a western diet .	隨著我們遷入城市 , 世界也擁抱著西方的飲食 。
and if we look to the future , it's an unsustainable diet .	如果我們展望未來 , 那將是不永續的飲食 。
so how did we get here ?	所以我們是怎麼走到這一步的 ?
and more importantly , what are we going to do about it ?	更重要的是 , 我們要怎麼做 ?
well , to answer the slightly easier question first , about 10 , 000 years ago , i would say , is the beginning of this process in the ancient near east , known as the fertile crescent .	嗯 , 要回答一個稍微簡單一點的問題 , 大約一萬年前 , 我會說 , 這是這個過程的開端 , 就在古老的近東地區 , 也就是所謂的 " 新月沃土 " 中 。
because , as you can see , it was crescent shaped .	因為 , 如你所見 , 它的形狀
and it was also fertile .	此外 , 它也很肥沃 。
and it was here , about 10 , 000 years ago , that two extraordinary inventions , agriculture and urbanism , happened roughly in the same place and at the same time .	大約在一萬年前 , 在這裡 , 有兩項非凡的發明 , 農業和城市化 , 大約在同一地點、同一時間發生 。
this is no accident , because agriculture and cities are bound together . they need each other .	這並不是意外 , 因為農業和城市是分界的 , 它們彼此需要 。
because it was discovery of grain by our ancient ancestors for the first time that produced a food source that was large enough and stable enough to support permanent settlements .	因為這是由古老祖先的祖先第一次發現的穀物產生足以支撐永久居住的糧食來源
and if we look at what those settlements were like , we see they were compact .	如果我們看一下這些居住地的樣子 , 就會發現它們是很小的 。
they were surrounded by productive farm land and dominated by large temple complexes like this one at ur , that were , in fact , effectively , spiritualized , central food distribution centers .	他們被農田圍繞並支配著像這一個在烏爾的大型寺廟的大型神殿在那邊事實上是神聖化的中央食物分配中心
because it was the temples that organized the harvest , gathered in the grain , offered it to the gods , and then offered the grain that the gods didn't eat back to the people .	因為是神殿安排了收割 , 收集在穀物上 , 將它獻給神 , 然後再將神沒吃的穀物獻給民眾 。
so , if you like , the whole spiritual and physical life of these cities was dominated by the grain and the harvest that sustained them .	所以 , 你也可以說 , 這些城市的精神及實體生活是由穀物和收成的穀物支配著 。
and in fact , that's true of every ancient city .	事實上 , 每個古老的城市也是如此 。
but of course not all of them were that small .	但當然不是全部都那麼小 。
famously , rome had about a million citizens by the first century a . d .	著名的例子是 , 早在西元一世紀 , 羅馬就有大約一百萬名居民 。
so how did a city like this feed itself ?	所以 , 像這樣的城市要如何滋養它們自己 ?
the answer is what i call " ancient food miles . "	答案就在我所謂的 「 古老食物哩 」
basically , rome had access to the sea , which made it possible for it to import food from a very long way away .	基本上 , 羅馬靠近海因此食物可以從很遠的地方運來
this is the only way it was possible to do this in the ancient world , because it was very difficult to transport food over roads , which were rough .	這是在古代唯一可能做到這一點的方式 , 因為運送食物是很困難的 , 這條路很粗糙 。
and the food obviously went off very quickly .	而且食物很快就掉下來了 。
so rome effectively waged war on places like carthage and egypt just to get its paws on their grain reserves .	所以羅馬有效地攻擊凱薩和埃及等地區 , 只為了取得他們的存糧 。
and , in fact , you could say that the expansion of the empire was really sort of one long , drawn out militarized shopping spree , really .	事實上 , 你可以說這個帝國的擴張真的是一場漫長的戰事 , 真的 。
in fact i love the fact , i just have to mention this: rome in fact used to import oysters from london , at one stage . i think that's extraordinary .	事實上 , 我很喜歡這個事實 , 我只需要提到這個:羅馬還曾經是從倫敦運輸牡蠣的動物 , 當時我覺得這很特別 。
so rome shaped its hinterland through its appetite .	所以羅馬透過它的胃口塑造了牠的後園
but the interesting thing is that the other thing also happened in the preindustrial world .	但有趣的是 , 另一件事也發生在工業化前的世界 。
if we look at a map of london in the 17th century , we can see that its grain , which is coming in from the thames , along the bottom of this map .	如果我們看看十七世紀的倫敦地圖 , 我們可以看到 , 它的穀物是從泰晤士河運進來的 , 沿著這張地圖的底部 。
so the grain markets were to the south of the city .	所以穀物市場就在城市的南方 ,
and the roads leading up from them to cheapside , which was the main market , were also grain markets .	這些路從它們變成便宜的 , 也是主要的市場 , 也是穀物市場 。
and if you look at the name of one of those streets , bread street , you can tell what was going on there 300 years ago .	如果你看其中一條街道的名字 , 麵包街 , 你可以看出三百年前那裡發生了什麼事 。
and the same of course was true for fish .	魚也是一樣 。
fish was , of course , coming in by river as well . same thing .	魚當然是從河裡來的 。 同樣的道理 。
and of course billingsgate , famously , was london's fish market , operating onsite here until the mid1980s .	當然 , billingsgate最有名的是倫敦的魚市場一直到1980年代中期都還在使用
which is extraordinary , really , when you think about it .	這真的很特別 , 真的 , 當你想到
everybody else was wandering around with mobile phones that looked like bricks and sort of smelly fish happening down on the port .	所有人都帶著手機遊蕩在港口 , 看起來像磚塊 , 有點臭味的魚在港口沿著 。
this is another thing about food in cities: once its roots into the city are established , they very rarely move .	這是城市食物的另一件事:一旦它的根源被建立起來 , 很少會動起來 。
meat is a very different story because , of course , animals could walk into the city .	肉類是一個非常不同的故事因為 , 當然 , 動物們可以走進城市
so much of london's meat was coming from the northwest , from scotland and wales .	所以倫敦的大部分肉品是從西北方來的從蘇格蘭及威爾斯來的
so it was coming in , and arriving at the city at the northwest , which is why smithfield , london's very famous meat market , was located up there .	所以它來了 , 抵達倫敦西北部的那座城市 , 這就是為什麼史密斯菲爾德 , 倫敦有名的肉市場 , 它就在那裡 。
poultry was coming in from east anglia and so on , to the northeast .	家禽類從東安格利亞來到東北方 ,
i feel a bit like a weather woman doing this . anyway , and so the birds were coming in with their feet protected with little canvas shoes .	我覺得這有點像是天氣女子在做這件事 。 不管怎樣 , 鳥兒都帶著腳踏進來 , 保護著小的畫布 。
and then when they hit the eastern end of cheapside , that's where they were sold , which is why it's called poultry .	然後當它們撞到便宜東方時 , 這就是它們被賣掉的原因 , 這就是它被稱為 「 家禽 」 的原因 。
and , in fact , if you look at the map of any city built before the industrial age , you can trace food coming in to it .	事實上 , 如果你看一下工業時代前建的任何城市地圖 , 你就可以追溯食物的來源 。
you can actually see how it was physically shaped by food , both by reading the names of the streets , which give you a lot of clues .	你實際上可以看到它是如何被食物所塑造 , 藉由閱讀街道的名稱 , 這給了你很多線索 。
friday street , in a previous life , is where you went to buy your fish on a friday .	星期五街 , 在以前是你在星期五去買魚的地方
but also you have to imagine it full of food .	但你也必須想像 , 它充滿了食物 。
because the streets and the public spaces were the only places where food was bought and sold .	因為街道和公共場所是唯一一處買賣食物的地方 。
and if we look at an image of smithfield in 1830 you can see that it would have been very difficult to live in a city like this and be unaware of where your food came from .	如果我們看1830年史密斯菲爾德的畫面 , 你可以看到 , 生活在這樣一個城市是非常困難的 , 而且還沒意識到你的食物從哪裡來 。
in fact , if you were having sunday lunch , the chances were it was mooing or bleating outside your window about three days earlier .	事實上 , 如果你在吃禮拜日午餐 , 可能你會在你的窗戶外面流血 , 大約是在三天前 。
so this was obviously an organic city , part of an organic cycle .	所以這顯然是一個有機的城市 , 是一個有機循環的一部分 。
and then 10 years later everything changed .	然後十年後一切都改變了 。
this is an image of the great western in 1840 .	這是1840年的偉大西方偉人形象 。
and as you can see , some of the earliest train passengers were pigs and sheep .	你們可以看到 , 最早的火車旅客當中有一些是豬和羊 。
so all of a sudden , these animals are no longer walking into market .	所以 , 突然間 , 這些動物不再走進市場 ,
they're being slaughtered out of sight and mind , somewhere in the countryside .	牠們從視覺和心靈中被屠殺掉 , 在鄉下的某處 。
and they're coming into the city by rail .	並且藉由欄杆進入城市 。
and this changes everything .	而這會改變一切 。
to start off with , it makes it possible for the first time to grow cities , really any size and shape , in any place .	首先 , 讓城市可以在任何地方 , 真正有任何大小、形狀 。
cities used to be constrained by geography ; they used to have to get their food through very difficult physical means .	過去 , 城市受限於地理條件 ; 過去 , 城市得要用很困難的實體手段來取得食物 。
all of a sudden they are effectively emancipated from geography .	突然間 , 它們從地理環境中被有效解放出來 。
and as you can see from these maps of london , in the 90 years after the trains came , it goes from being a little blob that was quite easy to feed by animals coming in on foot , and so on , to a large splurge , that would be very , very difficult to feed with anybody on foot , either animals or people .	你可以從倫敦的地圖上看到在火車通行的90年後倫敦從一個容易餵飽的小點一個動物走進來的東西 , 如此這般 , 再進一步 , 再進一步餵飽所有人 , 無論是對動物或是對人都是非常困難的 。
and of course that was just the beginning . after the trains came cars , and really this marks the end of this process .	當然 , 這只是開端 。 火車來了之後 , 真的是這過程的終點 。
it's the final emancipation of the city from any apparent relationship with nature at all .	這是城市最終的解放從大自然的透明關係中解放出來的 。
and this is the kind of city that's devoid of smell , devoid of mess , certainly devoid of people , because nobody would have dreamed of walking in such a landscape .	而這就是那種城市 , 沒有嗅覺、沒有混亂 , 肯定也沒有人 , 因為沒有人會夢到自己走在這樣的地景之中 。
in fact , what they did to get food was they got in their cars , drove to a box somewhere on the outskirts , came back with a week's worth of shopping , and wondered what on earth to do with it .	事實上 , 他們為了取得食物所做的是他們上車 , 開到郊區某處的一個箱子上 , 帶回一星期的商場去 , 想一想 , 到底要拿它怎麼辦 。
and this really is the moment when our relationship , both with food and cities , changes completely .	而這正是我們與食物和城市的關係改變的時刻 。
here we have food that used to be the center , the social core of the city at the periphery .	這裡曾經是中心 , 城市的社交核心位於邊緣 。
it used to be a social event , buying and selling food .	以前是社交活動 , 買賣食物、
we used to cook ; now we just add water , or a little bit of an egg if you're making a cake or something .	以前我們只是做飯 ; 現在我們只加點水 , 或一點點生蛋 , 如果你在做蛋糕之類的 。
we don't smell food to see if it's okay to eat .	我們不會聞到食物的味道 , 看看這是否可以吃 。
we just read the back of a label on a packet .	我們只需要讀包裝背後的一個標籤 。
and we don't value food . we don't trust it .	而且我們不重視食物 。 我們不信任它 。
so instead of trusting it , we fear it .	所以 , 我們不再信任它 , 而是害怕它 。
and instead of valuing it , we throw it away .	而且我們不珍惜它 , 反而丟棄了 。
one of the great ironies of modern food systems is that they've made the very thing they promised to make easier much harder .	現代的糧食體系最諷刺的一點是 , 他們已經把他們所承諾的做法弄得更加容易 。
by making it possible to build cities anywhere and any place , they've actually distanced us from our most important relationship , which is that of us and nature .	藉由在任何地方建造城市和任何地方的城市 , 他們其實已經讓我們與我們最重要的關係保持距離 , 那就是我們和大自然的關係 。
and also they've made us dependent on systems that only they can deliver , that , as we've seen , are unsustainable .	此外 , 它們讓我們依賴只有它們能提供的系統 , 如我們所見 , 是不可持續的 。
so what are we going to do about that ?	那麼 , 我們該怎麼辦呢 ?
it's not a new question .	這不是個新的問題 。
500 years ago it's what thomas more was asking himself .	五百年前湯瑪斯•更曾問過自己
this is the frontispiece of his book " utopia . "	這是他的《烏托邦》這本書的頭版 。
and it was a series of semiindependent citystates , if that sounds remotely familiar , a day's walk from one another where everyone was basically farmingmad , and grew vegetables in their back gardens , and ate communal meals together , and so on .	那是一系列半自主的城市 , 如果聽起來很熟悉 , 一天的走路 , 和彼此相處 , 基本上人人都是農田 , 在自家的後院種植蔬菜 , 一起吃公用餐等等 。
and i think you could argue that food is a fundamental ordering principle of utopia , even though more never framed it that way .	我想你們可以主張食物是烏托邦的基本原則 , 儘管更多從來沒有這樣看過 。
and here is another very famous " utopian " vision , that of ebenezer howard , " the garden city . "	還有另一個著名的烏托邦 , 也是ebenezerhoward的 " 花園城市 " 。
same idea: series of semiindependent citystates , little blobs of metropolitan stuff with arable land around , joined to one another by railway .	同樣的想法:一連串的半自主城市 , 小型的都會區 , 周圍有可耕地的土地 , 彼此結合 , 用鐵路連接 。
and again , food could be said to be the ordering principle of his vision .	同樣的 , 食物可以被說是他視覺的訂定原則 。
it even got built , but nothing to do with this vision that howard had .	它甚至被建造出來了 , 但和默斯克韋茲所擁有的這個願景沒有關係 。
and that is the problem with these utopian ideas , that they are utopian .	這就是烏托邦思想的問題 , 即他們是烏托邦 。
utopia was actually a word that thomas moore used deliberately .	烏托邦是湯瑪斯•摩爾刻意使用的一個詞 。
it was a kind of joke , because it's got a double derivation from the greek .	這是個笑話 , 因為希臘文裏面有雙重含意 。
it can either mean a good place , or no place .	它可以不是指一個好地方 , 就是沒有地方
because it's an ideal . it's an imaginary thing . we can't have it .	因為它是個理想的樣子 。 這是個幻想的樣子 。 我們無法擁有它 。
and i think , as a conceptual tool for thinking about the very deep problem of human dwelling , that makes it not much use .	我認為 , 做為一種概念工具 , 來思考人類居住的深層問題 , 會讓它不太有用 。
so i've come up with an alternative , which is sitopia , from the ancient greek , " sitos " for food , and " topos " for place .	所以我想出了一個替代方案 , 就是 「 希托邦 」 , 源自於古希臘 , 「 希托 」 是 「 食物 」 , 也是 「 地方 」 。
i believe we already live in sitopia .	我相信我們已經住在西托邦 。
we live in a world shaped by food , and if we realize that , we can use food as a really powerful tool a conceptual tool , design tool , to shape the world differently .	我們生活在一個被食物塑造的世界 , 如果我們意識到這一點 , 我們就可以把食物當作十分強大的工具一個概念性的工具 , 設計工具 , 來改變這個世界 。
so if we were to do that , what might sitopia look like ?	所以如果我們這麼做了 , 希托邦會是什麼樣子 ?
well i think it looks a bit like this .	嗯 , 我覺得它看起來有點像
i have to use this slide . it's just the look on the face of the dog .	我得用這張投影片 。 這只是狗的臉上的表情 。

weeks from the charter for compassion launch , karen armstrong looks at religion's role in the 21st century: will its dogmas divide us ? or will it unite us for common good ? she reviews the catalysts that can drive the world's faiths to rediscover the golden rule .	在 「 同情心 」 發行的數週後 , karenarmstrong在二十一世紀觀察宗教扮演的角色:它的教條會分裂我們嗎 ? 或它將我們團結起來 , 讓世界的信仰重新發現黃金法則 。
god , ted prize , global issues , politics , religion , tedglobal2009 , violence	上帝、ted大獎、全球議題、政治、宗教、tedglobal2009年的暴力 ,
karen armstrong: let's revive the golden rule	karenarmstrong:讓我們恢復黃金法則吧 。
for years i've been feeling frustrated , because as a religious historian , i've become acutely aware of the centrality of compassion in all the major world faiths .	多年來 , 我一直覺得很挫敗 , 因為 , 身為宗教歷史學家 , 我已經敏銳地意識到同情心在全世界的主要信仰中扮演的核心角色 。
every single one of them has evolved their own version of what's been called the golden rule .	每一個都進化出了他們自己所謂的黃金法則的版本 。
sometimes it comes in a positive version " always treat all others as you'd like to be treated yourself . "	有時會以正面的版本出現 , " 當你想被對待自己時 , " 永遠對待他人 。 "
and equally important is the negative version " don't do to others what you would not like them to do to you . "	同樣重要的是負面的版本 " 不要對其他人做那些你不會希望他們對你做的事情 。 "
look into your own heart , discover what it is that gives you pain and then refuse , under any circumstance whatsoever , to inflict that pain on anybody else .	看看自己的心 , 發現什麼能夠帶給你痛苦 , 然後不管在什麼情況下 , 都拒絕將痛苦折磨到別人身上 。
and people have emphasized the importance of compassion , not just because it sounds good , but because it works .	而且人們強調了慈悲心的重要性不只是因為它很好聽而是因為它有效
people have found that when they have implemented the golden rule as confucius said , " all day and every day , " not just a question of doing your good deed for the day and then returning to a life of greed and egotism , but to do it all day and every day , you dethrone yourself from the center of your world , put another there , and you transcend yourself .	人們發現當他們實施了黃金法則 , 如孔子所說的: 「 一整天和每一天 , 」 不只是一個關於做好事的一個問題 , 然後又回到貪婪和自大的一生 , 而是一整天都要做 , 你把自己從世界的中心 , 丟下另一條在那裡 , 然後超越自我 。
and it brings you into the presence of what's been called god , nirvana , rama , tao .	它會引領你到一個以往被稱為神的境界 , 涅盤 , 拉馬 , 塔羅 。
something that goes beyond what we know in our egobound existence .	超越我們所知的超越我們自我束縛的存在 。
but you know you'd never know it a lot of the time , that this was so central to the religious life .	但你知道 , 很多時候你永遠不會知道這對宗教生活來說是多麼的重要
because with a few wonderful exceptions , very often when religious people come together , religious leaders come together , they're arguing about abstruse doctrines or uttering a council of hatred or inveighing against homosexuality or something of that sort .	因為有一些美妙的例外 , 通常當宗教人士聚在一起 , 宗教領袖會聚在一起 , 他們會爭論abstrinese的教義 , 或說出一連串充滿仇恨或崇拜同性戀的詞彙 , 或這類的 。
often people don't really want to be compassionate .	通常人們並不真的想變得寬宏大量
i sometimes see when i'm speaking to a congregation of religious people a sort of mutinous expression crossing their faces because people often want to be right instead .	我有時會看到 , 當我和宗教人士談話時 , 我會看到 , 一個互相交流的表情 , 會跨過他們的臉 , 因為人們常常想對 。
and that of course defeats the object of the exercise .	那當然會打敗這運動的對象 。
now why was i so grateful to ted ?	為什麼我要感謝ted ?
because they took me very gently from my booklined study and brought me into the 21st century , enabling me to speak to a much , much wider audience than i could have ever conceived .	因為他們從我的書架上 , 輕柔地帶我走入21世紀 , 讓我能夠和更廣大的觀眾對話 , 遠遠超出我想像的範圍 。
because i feel an urgency about this .	因為我覺得這件事很急迫 。
if we don't manage to implement the golden rule globally , so that we treat all peoples , wherever and whoever they may be , as though they were as important as ourselves , i doubt that we'll have a viable world to hand on to the next generation .	如果我們不想辦法在全球實施黃金法則 , 不管在哪裡 , 不管在哪裡 , 不管在哪裡 , 如同我們自己一樣重要 , 我懷疑我們會有一個可行的世界 , 來接手下一代 。
the task of our time , one of the great tasks of our time , is to build a global society , as i said , where people can live together in peace .	我們這個時代的任務 , 我們這個時代的最偉大的任務之一 , 就是建立一個全球化的社會 , 如同我所說的 , 人們可以和平地生活在一起 。
and the religions that should be making a major contribution are instead seen as part of the problem .	而應該要做出重大貢獻的宗教 , 卻被視為問題的一部分 。
and of course it's not just religious people who believe in the golden rule .	當然不光是虔誠的人相信黃金法則
this is the source of all morality , this imaginative act of empathy , putting yourself in the place of another .	這是所有道德的源頭 , 這種富有想像力的同理心行為 , 把自己放在另一個地方 。
and so we have a choice , it seems to me .	所以我們有選擇 , 在我看來
we can either go on bringing out or emphasizing the dogmatic and intolerant aspects of our faith , or we can go back to the rabbis . rabbi hillel , the older contemporary of jesus , who , when asked by a pagan to sum up the whole of jewish teaching while he stood on one leg , said , " that which is hateful to you , do not do to your neighbor .	我們可以繼續帶出或強調我們信仰的教條或是不寬容的一面 , 或者 , 我們可以回到拉比聖戰者的拉比希爾 , 那個長者是耶穌 。 他問一位異教徒 , 當他站在單腿上時 , 要總結整個猶太人的教誨 , 他說: 「 這樣做對你來說很討厭 , 不要對你的鄰居做好事 。
that is the torah and everything else is only commentary . "	那就是托拉 , 其他的都只是評論而已 。 」
and the rabbis and the early fathers of the church who said that any interpretation of scripture that bred hatred and disdain was illegitimate .	而拉比和教會的早期父子們 , 他說任何解讀有關仇恨和輕視的經文都是違法的 。
and we need to revive that spirit .	而我們需要復興這樣的精神 。
and it's not just going to happen because a spirit of love wafts us down .	這不僅僅是因為愛的精神喚醒我們而發生 ,
we have to make this happen , and we can do it with the modern communications that ted has introduced .	我們必須讓這個計畫實現 , 我們可以利用ted所引發的現代通訊技術來實現 。
already i've been tremendously heartened at the response of all our partners .	我已經對我們所有伴侶的回應感到極大的鼓舞 。
in singapore , we have a group going to use the charter to heal divisions recently that have sprung up in singaporean society , and some members of the parliament want to implement it politically .	在新加坡 , 我們有一群人打算用憲章來治癒分歧 , 最近才在新加坡社會中流傳開來 , 議會的某些成員想要在政治上實施 。
in malaysia , there is going to be an art exhibition in which leading artists are going to be taking people , young people , and showing them that compassion also lies at the root of all art .	在馬來西亞 , 將來會有一場藝術展覽 , 主導藝術家將帶領人們 , 年輕人 , 向他們展示 , 慈悲也代表著所有藝術的根源 。
throughout europe , the muslim communities are holding events and discussions , are discussing the centrality of compassion in islam and in all faiths .	在整個歐洲 , 各個穆斯林社群舉辦活動和討論 , 討論以伊斯蘭和所有信仰為中心的慈悲心 。
but it can't stop there . it can't stop with the launch .	但它不能就此停止 。 它不能停止發射 。
religious teaching , this is where we've gone so wrong , concentrating solely on believing abstruse doctrines .	宗教的教誨 , 在這裡我們走錯了路 , 全神貫注地相信抽象的教義 。
religious teaching must always lead to action .	宗教教學一定會導致行動 。
and i intend to work on this till my dying day .	我打算在這個快要死去的日子裡工作 。
and i want to continue with our partners to do two things educate and stimulate compassionate thinking .	我還想繼續跟我們的另一半做兩件事--教育和刺激同情心的思想 。
education because we've so dropped out of compassion .	教育因為我們從同情心下降了 。
people often think it simply means feeling sorry for somebody .	人們常常認為那只是表示對某人感到抱歉 。
but of course you don't understand compassion if you're just going to think about it .	但你當然不明白憐憫之心如果你只是想一想
you also have to do it .	你還得做 。
i want them to get the media involved because the media are crucial in helping to dissolve some of the stereotypical views we have of other people , which are dividing us from one another .	我希望媒體能參與其中 , 因為媒體很重要 , 能協助破除我們對其他人的一些刻板印象 , 將我們彼此分離 。
the same applies to educators .	教育工作者也同樣適用 。
i'd like youth to get a sense of the dynamism , the dynamic and challenge of a compassionate lifestyle .	我希望年輕人能夠感受到一種富有同情心的生活方式的活力與挑戰 。
and also see that it demands acute intelligence , not just a gooey feeling .	同時也看到 , 這需要敏銳的智慧 , 而不僅僅是種愚蠢的感覺 。
i'd like to call upon scholars to explore the compassionate theme in their own and in other people's traditions .	我想要號召學者去探索他們自己以及他人的傳統中關於慈悲的主題 。
and perhaps above all , to encourage a sensitivity about uncompassionate speaking , so that because people have this charter , whatever their beliefs or lack of them , they feel empowered to challenge uncompassionate speech , disdainful remarks from their religious leaders , their political leaders , from the captains of industry .	也許最重要的是 , 為了鼓勵大家對於無情演講的敏感性 , 這麼一來 , 因為人們有這個特許權 , 不論他們的信仰為何 , 不論他們的信仰為何 , 他們會覺得自己有權力去挑戰不具同情心的演說、不守規則的論點 , 不論他們的宗教領袖、政治領袖、來自產業界的長官 。
because we can change the world , we have the ability .	因為我們可以改變世界 , 我們有能力 。

it's in his book " the four loves . "	在他的《四人之愛》書中
he said that he distinguished between erotic love , when two people gaze , spellbound , into each other's eyes .	他說他區別了愛情 , 當兩個人凝視彼此之間的咒語時 , 他凝視著對方的眼睛 。
and then he compared that to friendship , when two people stand side by side , as it were , shoulder to shoulder , with their eyes fixed on a common goal .	然後他把這與友情比較 , 當兩個人站在一起時 , 像這樣 , 肩並肩 , 雙眼固定在共同的目標上 。
we don't have to fall in love with each other , but we can become friends .	我們不需要愛上彼此 , 但我們可以成為朋友 。
and i am convinced .	我深信 ,
i felt it very strongly during our little deliberations at vevey , that when people of all different persuasions come together , working side by side for a common goal , differences melt away .	我強烈地感受到這一點 , 是因為在我們小小的意願下 , 當各種不同的說服者聚集在一起 , 為了共同的目標而努力 , 差異就會消融 。
and we learn amity .	並學習艾米 。

i've always managed my own extensions so it never even occurred to me to read the instructions , but i did finally figure it out . i had to figure it out , because along with the invitation came the frightening reminder that there would be no projector , so bringing those carousels would no longer be necessary but some alternate form of communication would .	我一直都在想辦法自己的延伸 , 以至於我從來沒想過要讀指示 , 但我終於明白了 。 我得弄清楚 , 因為接著邀請函 , 令人害怕的是 , 沒有投影機 , 所以帶著那些汽車旅館到來會不會有必要 , 只是某種另類的溝通方式而已 。

now , why would i care about rome , particularly ?	那麼 , 為什麼我會特別關心羅馬 ?
well , i went to rhode island school of design in the second half of the '60s to study architecture .	我在羅德島設計學院念建築時 , 在60年代的後半 ,
i was lucky enough to spend my last year , my fifth year , in rome as a student . it changed my life .	我很幸運 , 去年我在羅馬當學生的五年那天改變了我的一生
not the least reason was the fact that i had spent those first four years living at home , driving into risd everyday , driving back .	不是因為前四年我都住在家裡 , 每天開車去rsid附近 , 開回家 。
i missed the '60s . i read about them ; i understand they were pretty interesting . i missed them , but i did spend that extraordinary year in rome , and it's a place that is never far from my mind .	我錯過了1960年代 , 我讀了他們的故事 , 我知道他們相當有趣 , 但我錯過了他們 , 但我的確在羅馬度過了那不凡的一年 , 那是一個離我很遠的地方 。
so , whenever given an opportunity , i try to do something in it or with it or for it .	所以 , 只要有機會 , 我就會試著在其中做點什麼 , 或是為它做點什麼 。
i also make drawings to help people understand things .	我還會畫圖來幫助人們理解事物 。
things that i want them to believe i understand .	我希望他們相信我所理解的事物 。
and that's what i do as an illustrator , that's my job .	這就是我作為一個插畫家的工作 , 那是我的工作 。

part of the reason i'm showing you these is that it sort of helps illustrate this process i go through of trying to figure out what it is i feel about rome and why i feel it .	我給你們看其中一部分原因 , 它可以用來說明我所經歷的這個過程 , 試圖找出我對羅馬的感覺 , 以及我為什麼感受到 。

rome is a city full of surprises .	羅馬是個充滿驚喜的城市
i mean , we're talking about unusual perspectives , we're talking about narrow little winding streets that suddenly open into vast , sundrenched piazzas never , though , piazzas that are not humanly scaled .	我的意思是 , 我們在談不尋常的觀點 , 我們在談的是狹窄的小條街 , 突然通通開成廣闊、陽光充足的廣場 , 卻從未有過人性化的廣場大規模擴張 。
part of the reason for that is the fact that they grew up organically .	部分原因是因為它們在有機的環境中成長 。
that amazing juxtaposition of old and new , the bits of light that come down between the buildings that sort of create a map that's traveling above your head of usually blue especially in the summer compared to the map that you would normally expect to see of conventional streets .	新舊如此神奇的結合各式各樣的光線在兩棟建築物之間產生一幅在你頭頂的地圖--通常是藍色的--尤其是在夏天比起你平常會在街上看到的地圖

you see that i'm beginning to really lose control here and also hope .	你看我開始真正地失去控制 , 在這裡也失去希望 。
there's a very thin blue line of exhaust that sort of runs through this thing that would be kind of the trail that holds it all together .	有一條很細的藍線 , 有點像是路線 , 將所有的東西串連起來 。
then i thought , " wait a minute , what am i doing ? "	接著 , 我心想: 「 等等 , 我在做什麼 ? 」
a book is not only a neat way of collecting and storing information , it's a series of layers .	一本書不僅是蒐集和儲存資訊的很棒的方式 , 它還是一系列的層次 。
i mean , you always peel one layer off another ; we think of them as pages , doing it a certain way .	我的意思是 , 你總是把其中一層剝掉 ; 我們把它們看成網頁 , 用某種方式做 。
but think of them as layers . i mean , rome is a place of layers horizontal layers , vertical layers and i thought , well just peeling off a page would allow me to if i got you thinking about it the right way would allow me to sort of show you the depth of layers .	但把它們想成是層層 。 我的意思是 , 羅馬是一個有層次地層次空間的地方 , 縱向地層次--而我想 , 只要把一頁面剝下來 , 就可以讓我--如果我讓你們用正確的方式去思考的話 , 就能讓你們知道層次的深度 。
the stucco on the walls of most of the buildings in rome covers the scars ; the scars of centuries of change as these structures have been adapted rather than being torn down .	羅馬的大部分建築牆上的黏土覆蓋著疤痕 ; 數世紀來 , 這些結構一直在改變的疤痕 , 而不是被拆掉了 。
if i do a foldout page on the lefthand side and let you just unfold it , you see behind it what i mean by scar tissue .	如果我在左手邊做一個摺疊頁然後你將它展開你會看到背後所謂的傷口組織 。
you can see that in 1635 , it became essential to make smaller windows because the bad guys were coming or whatever .	你可以看到在1635年 , 製作出更小的窗戶就變得很重要 , 因為壞人就要來了或別的了 。
adaptations all get buried under the stucco .	適應力全都被埋在黏液之下
i could peel out a page of this palazzo to show you what's going on inside of it .	我可以從這一頁頁頁的 「 阿拉索 」 中解出來 , 讓大家看看裡面的狀況 。
but more importantly , i could also show you what it looks like at the corner of one of those magnificent buildings with all the massive stone blocks , or the fake stone blocks done with brick and stucco , which is more often the case .	更重要的是 , 我還可以給你們看看那些雄偉建築的角落那裡有各種巨大的石塊 , 或者是磚頭和黏土做的假石塊 , 比較常見 。
so it becomes slightly threedimensional .	所以它就變得有點立體感 。
i could take you down one of those narrow little streets into one of those surprising piazzas by using a double gate fold double foldout page which , if you were like me reading a popup book as a child , you hopefully stick your head into .	我可以把你們這條狹窄的街道帶到一塊令人驚訝的廣場上 , 通過使用雙扇摺疊紙的網頁──如果你和我一樣小時候讀著彈出版的書 , 希望你們可以把頭伸進去 。

so i went back to the notion of story , which is always a good thing to have if you're trying to get people to pay attention to a book and pick up information along the way .	所以我回到故事的概念 , 如果你想讓大家注意一本書並在過程中取得資訊 , 這永遠是件好事 。
" pigeon's progress " struck me as a catchy title .	「 鴿子的進步 」 擊敗了我 , 稱之為捕捉型態 。
if it was a homing pigeon , it would be called " homer's odyssey . "	如果是一隻回家的鴿子那就叫做《荷馬的奧德修紀》
but it was the journey of the . . .	但那是旅程......
i mean , if a title works , use it . but it would be a journey that went through rome and showed all the things that i like about rome .	我是說 , 如果有標題可用 , 但那會是一趟穿越羅馬的旅程 , 展示所有我喜歡的羅馬 。
it's a pigeon sitting on top of a church .	坐在教堂的頂樓的鴿子
goes off during the day and does normal pigeon stuff . comes back , the whole place is covered with scaffolding and green netting and there's no way this pigeon can get home .	白天走出去 , 做正常的鴿子動作 。 再回來 , 整個地方被鷹架和綠色內衣包覆著 , 沒有這種鴿子可以回家了 。
so it's a homeless pigeon now and it's going to have to find another place to live , and that allows me to go through my catalog of favorite things , and we start with the tall ones and so on .	所以這是一隻無家可歸的鴿子 , 它將必須再找一個居住地 , 這讓我得以從我喜愛的事物目錄中走出去 , 我們從最高的事物開始做起 。
maybe it has to go back and live with family members ; that's not always a good thing , but it does sort of bring pigeons together again .	也許它必須回去和家庭成員一起生活 ; 那並不總是件好事 , 但它還會讓鴿子們再次聚在一起 。
and i thought , that's sort of interesting , but maybe there's a person who should be involved in this in some way .	我心想 , 這有點意思 , 但或許有個人應該要用某種方式來參與 。
so i kind of came up with this old guy who spends his life looking after sick pigeons .	所以我想出了一個老傢伙 , 他一輩子都在照顧生病的鴿子 。

and he finally gets enough strength together to climb up the ladder onto the roof , and all the pigeons , a la red balloon , are there waiting for him and they carry him off over the walls of the city .	最後他得到足夠的力量來爬上梯子到屋頂 , 所有的鴿子 , 一個紅色的氣球 , 都在那兒等著他 , 然後他們把他載到城墻上去 。
and i forgot to mention this: whenever he lost a pigeon , he would take that pigeon out beyond the walls of the city .	我忘了提到這一點:每當他丟了一隻鴿子的時候 , 他就會把鴿子帶到城市的牆外 。
in the old roman custom , the dead were never buried within the walls .	在羅馬的習俗中 , 死者從來不埋在牆內 。
and i thought that's a really cheery story .	我覺得這是個很令人高興的故事 。
. that's really going to go a long way .	這真的會走很長的路 。
so anyway , i went through . . . and again , if packaging doesn't work and if the stories aren't going anywhere , i just come up with titles and hope that a title will sort of kick me off in the right direction .	總之 , 我經歷了一次 , 如果包裝不行 , 如果故事沒有在哪裡 , 我只能想出標題 , 希望書名能讓我朝對的方向看好 。
and sometimes it does focus me enough and i'll even do a title page .	有時 , 它的確會把我弄得夠重 , 我甚至會寫個標題頁 。
so , these are all title pages that eventually led me to the solution i settled on , which is the story of a young woman who sends a message on a homing pigeon she lives outside the walls of the city of rome to someone in the city .	所以 , 這些全部都是標題頁最終讓我找到了解決方案這個年輕女子的故事她用一隻寄來的信息給羅馬城牆外的居民
and the pigeon is flying down above the appian way here .	而鴿子正沿著亞洲的路徑往下飛 ,
you can see the tombs and pines and so on and so forth along the way .	你可以看到墳墓和松果之類的東西 。
if you see the red line , you are seeing the trail of the pigeon ; if you don't see the red line , you are the pigeon .	如果你看到這條紅線 , 你看到鴿子的小徑 ; 如果你看不見紅線 , 你就是那隻鴿子 。
and it becomes necessary and possible , at this point , to try to convey what that sense would be like of flying over the city without actually moving .	此時此刻 , 它變得有必要且可行 , 試圖傳達出那種飛越城市的感覺 , 而不用真的移動 。
past the pyramid of cestius these will seem very familiar to you , even if you haven't been to rome recently past the gatehouse .	過了賽斯提烏斯金字塔--這對你們來說應該很熟悉 , 即使你們最近沒去過羅馬渡口大門 。
this is something that's a little bit unusual .	這是有點不尋常 。
this pigeon does something that most homing pigeons do not do: it takes the scenic route , which was a device that i felt was necessary to actually extend this book beyond about four pages .	這隻鴿子做了一件大多數鴿子不會做的事:它採取我覺得很有必要的儀器去將這本書延長到大約四頁以外 。
so , we circle around the coliseum , past the church of santa maria in cosmedin and the temple of hercules towards the river .	所以 , 我們繞過羅馬競技場 , 穿過聖塔瑪利亞的教堂 , 和海克力士到河裡的神廟 。
we almost collide with the cornice of the palazzo farnese designed by michelangelo , built of stone taken from the coliseum narrow escape .	我們幾乎與由米開朗基羅設計的palazzfarnese " 的硬骨隨手打造的石頭由羅馬競技場窄路所採取
we swoop down over the campo de' fiori .	我們俯衝過campode'sfiori的上空
this is one of those things i show to my students because it's a complete bastardization a denial of any rules of perspective .	這是我給學生看的其中一件事 , 因為這完全是胡說八道 , 完全否認任何觀點的規則 。
the only rule of perspective that i think matters is if it looks believable , you've succeeded .	我認為唯一重要的觀點的規則就是如果它看起來是可信的 , 你就成功了 。
but you try and figure out where the vanishing points meet here ; a couple are on mars and a couple of others in cremona .	但你試著弄清楚這些消失點在哪裡 ; 有一對在火星上 , 還有另外幾位在克雷莫納州 。
but into the piazza in front of santa maria della pace , where invariably a soccer game is going on , and we're hit by a soccer ball .	但進入廣場 , 就在聖母堂前面 , 一場足球無人駕駛的比賽 , 我們被足球給打 。
now this is a terrible illustration of being hit by a soccer ball .	這是個被足球撞擊的可怕例子 。
i have all the pieces: there's santa maria della pace , there's a soccer ball , there's a little bit of a bird's wing nothing's happening , so i had to rethink it .	我有所有的作品 。 聖塔瑪莉亞•德拉的步伐 , 足球 , 鳥翅膀的一小部分沒有變化 , 所以我必須重新思考 。
and if you do want to see santa maria della pace , these books are really flexible , incredibly interactive just turn it around and look at it the other way .	如果你想看聖母堂 , 這些書就很有彈性 , 很具互動性 , 可以把它翻過來 , 用另一種方式去看它 。
through the alley , we can see the impact is captured in the red line .	穿過巷子 , 我們能看到撞擊的效果用紅線標示出來 。
and then bird manages to pull itself together past this medieval tower one of the few remaining medieval towers towards the church of sant'agnese and around the dome looking down into piazza navona which we've already mentioned and seen and flown over a couple of times ; there's the bernini statue of the four rivers and then past the wonderful borromini sant'ivo , stopping just long enough on the 26foot diameter oculus of the pantheon to catch our breath .	然後小鳥設法把自己拉到中世紀的塔子上 , 只剩下幾座中世紀塔樓 , 朝聖塔哥斯的教堂前進 , 在這個圓頂的旁邊 , 向下望向下方 , 我們已經看見、飛了好幾次 , 那裡有四條河流的伯尼座雕像 , 接著再去那美妙的布羅米尼聖提堂 , 就停止了足夠長的直徑 , 來抵達我們所說的萬神殿 。
and then we can swoop inside and around ; and because we're flying , we don't really have to worry about gravity at this particular moment in time , so this drawing can be oriented in any way on the page .	接著 , 我們在內裡到處飛 , 因為我們飛 , 我們不用擔心重力發生在這個特定的時刻 , 所以這幅圖能以任何方式在頁面上移動 。
we get a little exuberant as we pass gesu ; it's not surprising to sort of mimic the architecture in this way .	當我們通過gesu時 , 我們會很興奮 ; 用這種方式來模仿建築是一點也不意外的 。
past the wonderful wall filled with the juxtaposition that i was talking about ; beautiful carvings set into the walls above the neon " ristorante " sign , and so on .	過了一道美好的牆 , 充滿了我剛剛所講的對比 ; 美麗的雕塑在neon的 「 暴風雨 」 上方的牆 , 諸如此類 。
and eventually , we arrive at the courtyard of the palazzo , which is our destination .	最後我們到達palazzo的前庭也就是我們的目的地
straight up through the courtyard into a little window into the attic , where somebody is working at the drawing board .	直接穿過庭院 , 進入閣樓 , 在那裡有人在畫板上工作 。
he removes the message from the leg of the bird ; this is what it says .	他把這訊息從鳥兒的腿上除去 ; 這是他說的 。
as we look at the drawing board , we see what he's working on is , in fact , a map of the journey that the pigeon has just taken , and the red line extends through all the sights .	當我們看看畫板 , 我們看到他正在做的是 , 事實上 , 鴿子剛剛所拍攝的旅程地圖 , 紅線劃過所有視野 。
and if you want the information , so that we complete this cycle of understanding , all you have to do is read these paragraphs .	如果你想要這個資訊 , 這樣我們就完成了這個理解的循環 , 你只需要讀這些段落 。
thank you very much .	謝謝大家 。
mit researcher skylar tibbits works on selfassembly the idea that instead of building something , we can create materials that build themselves , much the way a strand of dna zips itself together . it's a big concept at early stages ; tibbits shows us three inthelab projects that hint at what a selfassembling future might look like .	麻省理工學院的天際兔子研究的是自我組裝的概念 , 與其建構出某種東西 , 我們能創造出一種材料 , 這種材料是一股dna將自己拉近在一起的方式 。 這是在初期階段的一個很大的概念 ; 兔子展示的是三個可以暗示未來自行組裝的計畫 。
skylar tibbits: can we make things that make themselves ?	天文數字:我們能創造出能自己做出來的東西嗎 ?
today i'd like to show you the future of the way we make things .	今天我想讓大家看看我們未來製造東西的方法 。
i believe that soon our buildings and machines will be selfassembling , replicating and repairing themselves .	我相信 , 很快的 , 我們的建築物和機器將可以自組 , 複製和修復自己 。
so i'm going to show you what i believe is the current state of manufacturing , and then compare that to some natural systems .	所以 , 我要給你們看 , 我相信是當前的製造業狀態 , 然後拿來和一些自然生態系統做比較 。
so in the current state of manufacturing , we have skyscrapers two and a half years [of assembly time] , 500 , 000 to a million parts , fairly complex , new , exciting technologies in steel , concrete , glass .	在當前的製造業狀態 , 我們有摩天大樓--兩年半的時間 , 五十萬至一百萬個部分 , 相當複雜 , 令人興奮的新技術在鋼鐵、水泥、玻璃 。
we have exciting machines that can take us into space five years [of assembly time] , 2 . 5 million parts .	我們有令人興奮的機器能夠帶領我們進入太空五年--250萬個部分 。
but on the other side , if you look at the natural systems , we have proteins that have two million types , can fold in 10 , 000 nanoseconds , or dna with three billion base pairs we can replicate in roughly an hour .	但在另一邊 , 如果你觀察自然系統 , 我們有兩百萬種蛋白質 , 可以在一萬納秒折疊 , 或是dna有三十億個鹼基對 , 我們可以在大約一個小時複製 。
so there's all of this complexity in our natural systems , but they're extremely efficient , far more efficient than anything we can build , far more complex than anything we can build .	所以 , 我們的自然系統有這麼複雜 , 但它們的效率非常高 , 遠遠超過任何我們可以建造的東西 , 遠遠超過任何我們可以建造出的東西 。
they're far more efficient in terms of energy .	它們在能源方面的效率更高 。
they hardly ever make mistakes .	他們幾乎不會犯錯 。
and they can repair themselves for longevity .	而且他們可以修復自己長壽 。
so there's something super interesting about natural systems .	所以自然系統有超級有趣的現象 。
and if we can translate that into our built environment , then there's some exciting potential for the way that we build things .	如果我們能將這些轉譯成我們的建築環境 , 那麼就有一些令人興奮的潛力在我們建造東西的方法上 。
and i think the key to that is selfassembly .	我認為關鍵是自我組裝 。
so if we want to utilize selfassembly in our physical environment , i think there's four key factors .	所以如果我們想利用我們的物理環境中的自組裝 , 我認為有四個關鍵因素 。
the first is that we need to decode all of the complexity of what we want to build so our buildings and machines .	首先 , 我們需要解碼所有我們想要建構的東西的複雜度 , 讓我們的建築物和機器能夠被解碼 。
and we need to decode that into simple sequences basically the dna of how our buildings work .	我們需要解碼成簡單的序列基本上是我們的建築物如何運作的dna 。
then we need programmable parts that can take that sequence and use that to fold up , or reconfigure .	接著 , 我們需要可編程的部分 , 可以把這個序列拿來使用 , 來折疊 , 或重新配置 。
we need some energy that's going to allow that to activate , allow our parts to be able to fold up from the program .	我們需要一些能量讓它啟動 , 讓我們的部件能夠折疊起來 , 從而使它啟動 。
and we need some type of error correction redundancy to guarantee that we have successfully built what we want .	我們需要某種類型的糾錯冗餘 , 來保證我們已經成功地建造我們想要的 。
so i'm going to show you a number of projects that my colleagues and i at mit are working on to achieve this selfassembling future .	所以我將向你們展示一些我在麻省理工學院的同事和我正在努力實現這個自我組裝的未來 。
the first two are the macrobot and decibot .	前兩名是macrobot和decibot 。
so these projects are largescale reconfigurable robots 8 ft . , 12 ft . long proteins .	所以這些項目都是大規模的可重構機器人--8英尺 , 12英尺長的蛋白質 。
they're embedded with mechanical electrical devices , sensors .	它們與機械電裝置 , 傳感器嵌入 。
you decode what you want to fold up into , into a sequence of angles so negative 120 , negative 120 , 0 , 0 , 120 , negative 120 something like that ; so a sequence of angles , or turns , and you send that sequence through the string .	你要解碼什麼才折疊成什麼 , 成序列的角度--負120 , 負120 , 0 , 0 , 120 , 負120--類似的東西 , 這樣的角度 , 或輪流順序 , 通過弦而發送序列 。
each unit takes its message so negative 120 it rotates to that , checks if it got there and then passes it to its neighbor .	每個單位都需要它的消息--負120會旋轉到那個位置 , 檢查它是否到了那裡 , 然後把它傳遞給它的鄰居 。
so these are the brilliant scientists , engineers , designers that worked on this project .	這些都是傑出的科學家、工程師、設計師在這個項目上工作 。
and i think it really brings to light: is this really scalable ?	我想這真的可以帶來光明:這真的可擴展嗎 ?
i mean , thousands of dollars , lots of man hours made to make this eightfoot robot .	我的意思是 , 數千美元 , 大量的男人小時來製造這8英尺的機器人 。
can we really scale this up ? can we really embed robotics into every part ?	我們可以擴大規模嗎 ? 我們真的能把機器人融入每個部分嗎 ?
the next one questions that and looks at passive nature , or passively trying to have reconfiguration programmability .	下一個問題 , 以及著眼於被動性本質 , 或被動地試圖重新配置可編程 。
but it goes a step further , and it tries to have actual computation .	但它又再進一步 , 試圖實際進行計算 。
it basically embeds the most fundamental building block of computing , the digital logic gate , directly into your parts .	它基本上是最基礎的構造 , 數位邏輯閘 , 直接嵌入到你的零件裡 。
so this is a nand gate .	所以這是nand邏輯閘 ,
you have one tetrahedron which is the gate that's going to do your computing , and you have two input tetrahedrons .	你有一個四面體 , 也就是門 , 會做你的計算 , 你有兩個會輸入的四面體 。
one of them is the input from the user , as you're building your bricks .	其中之一是來自使用者的輸入 , 如同你在製造你的磚塊一般 。
the other one is from the previous brick that was placed .	另外一塊是從之前放置的磚
and then it gives you an output in 3d space .	然後它給你一個3d空間的輸出 。
so what this means is that the user can start plugging in what they want the bricks to do .	所以 , 這意味著 , 使用者可以開始在他們希望磚頭能做什麼 。
it computes on what it was doing before and what you said you wanted it to do .	它計算著它之前做什麼 , 你說你想要它做什麼 。
and now it starts moving in threedimensional space so up or down .	現在它開始在三維空間裡移動--向上或向下 。
so on the lefthand side , [1 , 1] input equals 0 output , which goes down .	所以在左手邊 , [1 , 1]輸入等於輸出0 , 這個數字就會下降 。
on the righthand side , [0 , 0] input is a 1 output , which goes up .	在右手邊 , [0 , 0]輸入是1輸出 , 輸出的數字會上升 。
and so what that really means is that our structures now contain the blueprints of what we want to build .	這真正的意思是我們現在的結構包含了我們想要建造的藍圖 。
so they have all of the information embedded in them of what was constructed .	所以他們有了所有內建的信息 。
so that means that we can have some form of selfreplication .	所以這意味著我們可以有某種形式的自我複製 。
in this case i call it selfguided replication , because your structure contains the exact blueprints .	在這個案例中 , 我稱它為自我導向的複製 , 因為你的結構包含着確切的藍圖 。
if you have errors , you can replace a part .	如果你有錯誤 , 你可以換一個零件 。
all the local information is embedded to tell you how to fix it .	所有當地的資訊都被嵌入其中 , 告訴你怎麼去修復它 。
so you could have something that climbs along and reads it and can output at one to one .	所以 , 你可以擁有攀登的東西 , 並讀取它 , 一個對一個的輸出 。
it's directly embedded ; there's no external instructions .	它是直接嵌入的 ; 沒有任何外在的指令 。
so the last project i'll show is called biased chains , and it's probably the most exciting example that we have right now of passive selfassembly systems .	我將展示的最後一個項目叫做偏置鏈 , 它可能是目前被動自組裝系統中 , 最令人興奮的例子 。
so it takes the reconfigurability and programmability and makes it a completely passive system .	所以它把可重構性和可程式化的系統變成完全被動的系統 。
so basically you have a chain of elements .	所以基本上你有一連串的元素
each element is completely identical , and they're biased .	每個元素是完全相同的 , 而且它們是有偏見的 。
so each chain , or each element , wants to turn right or left .	所以每個鏈 , 或每個元素 , 都想向右或向左轉 。
so as you assemble the chain , you're basically programming it .	所以當你組裝鏈 , 基本上你就是在編程 。
you're telling each unit if it should turn right or left .	你是在告訴每個單位是否應該向右轉或者向左轉 。
so when you shake the chain , it then folds up into any configuration that you've programmed in so in this case , a spiral , or in this case , two cubes next to each other .	當你搖動鏈條 , 它便會折疊成你編程的任何組態 , 在這個案例中 , 一個螺旋 , 或在這個例子中 , 兩個立方體彼此相鄰 。
so you can basically program any threedimensional shape or onedimensional , twodimensional up into this chain completely passively .	基本上你可以將任何立體的形狀或一維的二維編碼 , 輸入這條鏈 , 完全處於被動的狀態 。
so what does this tell us about the future ?	所以這告訴我們什麼關於未來的事 ?
i think that it's telling us that there's new possibilities for selfassembly , replication , repair in our physical structures , our buildings , machines .	我認為這告訴我們有新的可能性可以自我組裝、複製、修復在我們的物理結構、建築物、機器上 。
there's new programmability in these parts .	這些部分有新的可編程性 。
and from that you have new possibilities for computing .	從那你會有新的計算可能性 。
we'll have spatial computing .	我們將有空間運算能力
imagine if our buildings , our bridges , machines , all of our bricks could actually compute .	想像一下 , 如果我們的建築物 , 我們的橋樑 , 機器 , 我們所有的磚其實都可以計算 。
that's amazing parallel and distributed computing power , new design possibilities .	那是驚人的並行和分佈式的計算能力 , 新的設計可能性 。
so it's exciting potential for this .	所以對此是令人興奮的潛力 。
so i think these projects i've showed here are just a tiny step towards this future , if we implement these new technologies for a new selfassembling world .	所以我認為 , 我在此展示的這些計畫 , 只是對於這個未來的一小步 , 如果我們實施這些新技術 , 為一個新的自組裝世界 。
we've been to the moon , we've mapped the continents , we've even been to the deepest point in the ocean twice . what's left for the next generation to explore ? biologist and explorer nathan wolfe suggests this answer: almost everything . and we can start , he says , with the world of the unseeably small .	我們已經登上了月球 , 繪製了大陸的地圖 , 我們甚至去過海裡最深的一點兩次 。 什麼是為了探討下一代 ? 生物學家和探險家南森沃爾夫人對這個答案提出了這個答案:幾乎所有一切都要開始 。 而我們可以開始 , 他說 , 與這個不可思議的微小世界 。
biodiversity , exploration , microbiology , science	生物多樣性、探索、微生物學、科學
nathan wolfe: what's left to explore ?	nathanwolfe:探索剩下的是什麼 ?
recently i visited beloit , wisconsin .	最近我去了威斯康辛州的貝洛伊特市 ,
and i was there to honor a great 20th century explorer , roy chapman andrews .	我在那裡向二十世紀偉大的探險家roychapmanandrews致敬 。
during his time at the american museum of natural history , andrews led a range of expeditions to uncharted regions , like here in the gobi desert .	在他任職於美國自然歷史博物館時 , andrews引領一系列未經探險的探險活動範圍出現在戈壁沙漠中 。
he was quite a figure .	他是個不錯的人物 。
he was later , it's said , the basis of the indiana jones character .	據說他後來成為印第安那瓊斯這個角色的基礎
and when i was in beloit , wisconsin , i gave a public lecture to a group of middle school students .	當我在威斯康辛州的貝洛伊特市時 , 我對一群中學學生發表了一段公開的演說 。
and i'm here to tell you , if there's anything more intimidating than talking here at ted , it'll be trying to hold the attention of a group of a thousand 12yearolds for a 45minute lecture .	我來這裡告訴各位 , 如果有任何事比在ted這裡演講還要嚇人 , 那就是試著要讓一群45分鐘的12歲孩子們的注意力吸引力 。
at the end of the lecture they asked a number of questions , but there was one that's really stuck with me since then .	在演說的尾聲 , 他們問了幾個問題 , 但從那時起 , 有一個問題深深吸引著我 。
there was a young girl who stood up , and she asked the question: " where should we explore ? "	有一個年輕女孩站起來 , 她問了這個問題: 「 我們應該要去哪裡探索 ? 」
i think there's a sense that many of us have that the great age of exploration on earth is over , that for the next generation they're going to have to go to outer space or the deepest oceans in order to find something significant to explore .	我認為 , 我們很多人都有那種偉大的地球探索年代已經結束了 , 對下一代來說 , 他們將必須去外太空或深海處尋求重要的探索 。
but is that really the case ?	但真的是這樣嗎 ?
is there really nowhere significant for us to explore left here on earth ?	地球上無處不在的重要探險嗎 ?
it sort of made me think back to one of my favorite explorers in the history of biology .	這有點讓我回想生物學歷史上我最喜愛的探險家之一 。
this is an explorer of the unseen world , martinus beijerinck .	這是未知世界的探險家 , martinusbeijerinck ,
so beijerinck set out to discover the cause of tobacco mosaic disease .	beijerinck一開始是為了發現菸草鑲嵌病的起因 。
what he did is he took the infected juice from tobacco plants and he would filter it through smaller and smaller filters .	他做的是從菸草植物中取出被感染的汁液 , 讓它能過濾更小更細的過濾器 。
and he reached the point where he felt that there must be something out there that was smaller than the smallest forms of life that were ever known bacteria , at the time .	他接觸到的那個時點 , 覺得一定有什麼東西比當時已知最小型的生命形式還要更小 。
he came up with a name for his mystery agent .	他為他的神秘媒介命名 。
he called it the virus latin for " poison . "	他稱之為 「 毒藥 」 拉丁文 。
and in uncovering viruses , beijerinck really opened this entirely new world for us .	在揭露病毒的過程中 , beijerinck真的為我們開啟了一個全新的世界 。
we now know that viruses make up the majority of the genetic information on our planet , more than the genetic information of all other forms of life combined .	我們現在知道病毒構成地球上大多數的基因信息 , 比起其它形式的生命體的基因信息加起來還多 。
and obviously there's been tremendous practical applications associated with this world things like the eradication of smallpox , the advent of a vaccine against cervical cancer , which we now know is mostly caused by human papillomavirus .	很顯然的 , 已經有很大的實際應用 , 和這個世界有關 , 像是天花的根除、疫苗對抗子宮頸癌的出現 , 我們現在知道主要是由人類乳突病毒所引起 。
and beijerinck's discovery , this was not something that occurred 500 years ago .	而beijerinck的發現不是500年前發生的事情 。
it was a little over 100 years ago that beijerinck discovered viruses .	大約是一百多年前 , beijerinck發現病毒 。
so basically we had automobiles , but we were unaware of the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	基本上 , 我們有汽車 , 但我們卻沒有意識到組成我們星球上大多數基因信息的生命形式 。
we now have these amazing tools to allow us to explore the unseen world things like deep sequencing , which allow us to do much more than just skim the surface and look at individual genomes from a particular species , but to look at entire metagenomes , the communities of teeming microorganisms in , on and around us and to document all of the genetic information in these species .	我們現在有了這些驚人的工具 , 讓我們可以探索未知的世界 , 例如深度定序 , 讓我們不只跳過表面 , 還能觀察特定物種的個別基因組 , 還能觀察整個節拍器 , 我們身邊充滿了微生物的群系 , 以及紀錄這些物種中所有的基因信息 。
we can apply these techniques to things from soil to skin and everything in between .	我們可以將這些技術應用在從土壤到皮膚間的事物上 。
in my organization we now do this on a regular basis to identify the causes of outbreaks that are unclear exactly what causes them .	在我的組織裡 , 我們現在常常這樣做 , 來辨識出造成疾病爆發的原因 , 不清楚到底是什麼原因 。
and just to give you a sense of how this works , imagine that we took a nasal swab from every single one of you .	為了讓大家了解這如何運作 , 想像一下 , 我們取代了你們每一個人的鼻腔 。
and this is something we commonly do to look for respiratory viruses like influenza .	這是我們通常會做的事 , 來尋找呼吸道融合類的病毒 , 如流感 。
the first thing we would see is a tremendous amount of genetic information .	首先 , 我們會看到非常大量的基因信息 。
and if we started looking into that genetic information , we'd see a number of usual suspects out there of course , a lot of human genetic information , but also bacterial and viral information , mostly from things that are completely harmless within your nose .	如果我們開始研究這些遺傳信息 , 我們會看到一些普通的可疑物--當然 , 很多的人類基因信息 , 還有細菌和病毒信息 , 大部分都來自你鼻子內完全無害的事物 。
but we'd also see something very , very surprising .	但我們也會看到非常非常令人驚訝的現象 。
as we started to look at this information , we would see that about 20 percent of the genetic information in your nose doesn't match anything that we've ever seen before no plant , animal , fungus , virus or bacteria .	當我們開始檢視這些資訊時 , 我們會看到你鼻子中大約20%的基因信息不符合任何我們以前曾經見過的東西--沒有植物、動物、真菌、病毒或細菌 。
basically we have no clue what this is .	基本上我們完全不知道這是什麼 。
and for the small group of us who actually study this kind of data , a few of us have actually begun to call this information biological dark matter .	對於我們這些實際在研究這種資料的小團體 , 其實我們當中少數人已經開始稱之為 「 資訊生物暗物質 」 。
we know it's not anything that we've seen before ; it's sort of the equivalent of an uncharted continent right within our own genetic information .	我們知道它不是任何以前我們看過的東西 。 它有點像是一個在我們自己的基因信息中未知的大陸 。
and there's a lot of it .	而且還有很多 。
if you think 20 percent of genetic information in your nose is a lot of biological dark matter , if we looked at your gut , up to 40 or 50 percent of that information is biological dark matter .	如果你認為你鼻腔中百分之二十的基因信息是許多生物暗物質 , 如果我們觀察你的腸道 , 高達百分之四十或五十的信息是生物暗物質 。
and even in the relatively sterile blood , around one to two percent of this information is dark matter can't be classified , can't be typed or matched with anything we've seen before .	即使是在相對比較下無菌的血液中 , 大約有1% ~ 2%的信息是暗物質無法被分類 , 不能和我們以前見過的任何東西匹配 。
at first we thought that perhaps this was artifact .	一開始我們認為也許這是人造物 。
these deep sequencing tools are relatively new .	這些深度定序的工具相對新穎 。
but as they become more and more accurate , we've determined that this information is a form of life , or at least some of it is a form of life .	但當它們變得愈來愈準確 , 我們已經判斷這個信息是一種生命型態 , 至少其中一部分是生命型態 。
and while the hypotheses for explaining the existence of biological dark matter are really only in their infancy , there's a very , very exciting possibility that exists: that buried in this life , in this genetic information , are signatures of as of yet unidentified life .	雖然解釋生物暗物質存在的假設 , 其實只是在其嬰兒期 , 有非常、非常令人興奮的可能性存在:那埋藏在生命中 , 在遺傳資訊中 , 是尚未被辨識出的生命的特徵 。
that as we explore these strings of a's , t's , c's and g's , we may uncover a completely new class of life that , like beijerinck , will fundamentally change the way that we think about the nature of biology .	當我們探索一連串的a、t、c、g , 我們可能會揭開一個全新的生命階段 , 就像beijerinck一樣 , 從根本上改變我們對生物學本質的看法 。
that perhaps will allow us to identify the cause of a cancer that afflicts us or identify the source of an outbreak that we aren't familiar with or perhaps create a new tool in molecular biology .	這也許能讓我們找出折磨人類的癌症病源 , 或找出我們不熟悉的爆發病症源頭 , 或也許能創造出分子生物學的新工具 。
i'm pleased to announce that , along with colleagues at stanford and caltech and ucsf , we're currently starting an initiative to explore biological dark matter for the existence of new forms of life .	我很高興地宣布 , 同時也與斯坦福大學、加州理工學院和加州大學舊金山分校的同事一起 , 我們現在正要開始探索生物暗物質 , 探索新的生命形式的存在 。
a little over a hundred years ago , people were unaware of viruses , the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	大約一百多年前 , 人們不知道病毒 , 一種組成我們星球上大多數基因信息的生命形態 。
a hundred years from now , people may marvel that we were perhaps completely unaware of a new class of life that literally was right under our noses .	一百年後 , 人們可能驚嘆我們可能完全不知道有一種新的生命種類 , 就在我們的鼻子底下 。
it's true , we may have charted all the continents on the planet and we may have discovered all the mammals that are out there , but that doesn't mean that there's nothing left to explore on earth .	這是真的 , 我們可能已經描繪了地球上所有的大陸 , 我們可能已經發現了所有在那裡的哺乳動物 , 但那並不表示地球上沒有任何東西可以探索 。
beijerinck and his kind provide an important lesson for the next generation of explorers people like that young girl from beloit , wisconsin .	beijerinck和他的同事為下一代的探險家提供了重要的一課 , 像來自威斯康辛州的貝洛伊特市的年輕女孩 。
