and i think if we phrase that lesson , it's something like this: don't assume that what we currently think is out there is the full story .	我認為如果我們把這一課說出來的話 , 應該是這樣的:不要假設我們目前認為有的就是完整的故事 。
go after the dark matter in whatever field you choose to explore .	追求任何你選擇要探索的領域中的暗物質 。
there are unknowns all around us and they're just waiting to be discovered .	我們身邊到處都有未知的事物 , 它們只是等著被發現 。
legendary scientist david deutsch puts theoretical physics on the back burner to discuss a more urgent matter: the survival of our species . the first step toward solving global warming , he says , is to admit that we have a problem .	傳說性科學家大衛.杜奇在背後放了理論物理 , 來討論一個更迫切的問題:我們人類的生存 。 解決全球暖化的第一步 , 他說 , 就是承認我們有一個問題 。
climate change , cosmos , culture , environment , global issues , physics , science , technology , universe	氣候變化、宇宙、文化、環境、全球議題、物理、科技、宇宙 。
david deutsch on our place in the cosmos	大衛描述我們在宇宙中的位置 。
we've been told to go out on a limb and say something surprising .	我們被告知走出肢體並說出令人驚訝的話 。
so i'll try and do that , but i want to start with two things that everyone already knows .	所以我會試著這麼做 , 但我想先從大家都知道的兩件事說起 。
and the first one , in fact , is something that has been known for most of recorded history .	而第一個 , 事實上 , 是多數以來記錄的歷史所廣為人知的東西 。
and that is that the planet earth , or the solar system , or our environment or whatever , is uniquely suited to sustain our evolution or creation , as it used to be thought and our present existence , and most important , our future survival .	那就是地球 , 或太陽系 , 或太陽系 , 或我們環境的等等 , 都獨一無二地適合維持我們的演化或創造 , 正如它以前的思維、現在的存在 , 最重要的是 , 我們未來的生存 。
nowadays this idea has a dramatic name: spaceship earth .	現今 , 這個想法有個戲劇性的名字:太空船地球 。
and the idea there is that outside the spaceship , the universe is implacably hostile , and inside is all we have , all we depend on .	我們的想法是 , 在太空船之外 , 宇宙是無可避免地充滿敵意的 , 內在是我們所有的一切 , 我們所賴以為生的一切 。
and we only get the one chance: if we mess up our spaceship , we've got nowhere else to go .	我們只有一次機會:如果我們搞砸我們的太空船 , 其他地方都沒有 。
now , the second thing that everyone already knows is that contrary to what was believed for most of human history , human beings are not , in fact , the hub of existence .	現在 , 第二件大家都已經知道的事 , 與我們所相信的人類歷史大多相反 , 人類事實上並不是存在的中心 。
as stephen hawking famously said , we're just a chemical scum on the surface of a typical planet that's in orbit around a typical star , which is on the outskirts of a typical galaxy , and so on .	正如stephenhawking的名言 , 我們只是典型的星球表面的化學污垢 , 繞著一個典型的恆星運行 , 就是在一個典型銀河系的邊緣 , 以此類推 。
now the first of those two things that everyone knows is kind of saying that we're at a very untypical place , uniquely suited and so on , and the second one is saying that we're at a typical place .	現在 , 大家都知道的第一件事 , 有點像是說我們是在一個非常不典型的地方 , 獨一無二地適合 。 第二件事是說我們是在一個典型的地方 。
and especially if you regard these two as deep truths to live by and to inform your life decisions , then they seem a little bit to conflict with each other .	尤其是當你把這兩個當作是深層的真理看待 , 並且告訴你的生命決策 , 那麼他們似乎彼此有些衝突 。
but that doesn't prevent them from both being completely false .	但這並不能防止兩者都是完全錯誤的 。
and they are . so let me start with the second one: typical . well is this a typical place ? well , let's look around , you know , and look in a random direction , and we see a wall , and chemical scum and that's not typical of the universe at all .	它們是 。 讓我從第二個開始:典型的 。 嗯 , 這是典型的地方嗎 ? 嗯 , 讓我們看看四周 , 你知道的 , 看看四周 , 看看一個隨機的方向 , 我們看到一面牆 , 還有一個化學污垢 , 那完全不是宇宙的典型 。
all you've got to do is go a few hundred miles in that same direction and look back , and you won't see any walls or chemical scum at all all you see is a blue planet . and if you go further than that , you'll see the sun , the solar system , and the stars and so on .	你只要朝著同一個方向走幾百英里 , 然後往回看 , 你將不會看到任何牆面或化學污垢你只會看到一個藍色的星球 。 如果你再更進一步 , 你會看到太陽、太陽系、恆星等等 。
but that's still not typical of the universe , because stars come in galaxies .	但那仍然不是宇宙中常態的現象 , 因為恆星在星系中來來來去去去去去了 。
and most places in the universe , a typical place in the universe , is nowhere near any galaxies .	宇宙中的大部分地方 , 宇宙中一個典型的地方 , 都沒有任何一個星系 。
so let's go out further , till we're outside the galaxy , and look back , and yeah , there's the huge galaxy with spiral arms laid out in front of us .	讓我們更進一步 , 直到我們走出銀河系 , 再回頭看 , 是的 , 巨大的銀河系中有螺旋手臂 , 擺在我們面前 。
and at this point we've come 100 , 000 light years from here .	就在這個時候 , 我們已經走了十萬光年 。
but we're still nowhere near a typical place in the universe .	但我們卻一點也不像宇宙中一個典型的地方.
to get to a typical place , you've got to go 1 , 000 times as far as that into intergalactic space .	要到達一個典型的地方 , 你要到達一個星系間空間的千倍之多 。
and so what does that look like ? typical .	那看起來是什麼樣子 ? 典型的 。
what does a typical place in the universe look like ?	宇宙中一個典型的地方是什麼樣子 ?
well , at enormous expense , ted has arranged a highresolution immersion virtual reality rendering of intergalactic space the view from intergalactic space .	嗯 , 在巨大的代價下 , ted已經安排了一種高解析度的中介空間的虛擬實境 , 也就是星系間空間的景觀 。
so can we have the lights off , please , so we can see it ?	請把燈關掉 , 看得出來嗎 ?
well , not quite , not quite perfect you see , in intergalactic space intergalactic space is completely dark , pitch dark .	嗯 , 不完全完美你可以看到在星系間的空間是完全黑暗的 。
it's so dark that if you were to be looking at the nearest star to you , and that star were to explode as a supernova , and you were to be staring directly at it at the moment when its light reached you , you still wouldn't be able to see even a glimmer .	它是如此的黑暗 , 如果你正看著離你最近的恆星 , 而那顆恆星正如一個超新星般爆炸 , 當光線抵達你的時候 , 你甚至會直接盯著它看 , 直到它抵達你的時候 , 你仍然無法看見甚至閃耀 。
that's how big and how dark the universe is .	這就是宇宙是多大又黑暗的 。
and that's despite the fact that a supernova is so bright , so brilliant an event , that it would kill you stone dead at a range of several light years .	儘管超新星的確是如此的明亮 , 一個非常聰明的事件 , 它會讓你在幾光年的範圍內打死 。
and yet from intergalactic space , it's so far away you wouldn't even see it .	然而在星系間的空間 , 它是如此的遙遠 , 你甚至看不到它 。
it's also very cold out there less than three degrees above absolute zero .	那裡也非常寒冷絕對零度不到三度 。
and it's very empty . the vacuum there is one million times less dense than the highest vacuum that our best technology on earth can currently create . so that's how different a typical place is from this place .	而且它是空的 。 真空的密度比目前地球上最好的科技所能創造的最高密度還要小一百萬倍 。 這就是從這個地方之後典型的情況 。
and that is how untypical this place is .	這就是這個地方最不典型的地方 。
so can we have the lights back on please ? thank you .	所以 , 我們能否把燈打回來 ? 謝謝 。
now how do we know about an environment that's so far away , and so different , and so alien , from anything we're used to ?	我們怎麼知道這麼遠的環境如此不同 , 如此不同 , 如此不同 , 如此不同於我們所習慣的一切 ?
well , the earth our environment , in the form of us is creating knowledge .	地球--我們的環境 , 以我們的形式存在--創造知識 。
well , what does that mean ? well , look out even further than we've just been i mean from here , with a telescope and you'll see things that look like stars .	嗯 , 那是什麼意思呢 ? 再往外看 , 比從這裡開始 , 用望遠鏡--你會看到類似恆星的東西 。
they're called " quasars . " quasars originally meant quasistellar object .	它們被稱為 「 石英 」 。 石英層原本是指特拉西斯的物體 。
which means things that look a bit like stars . but they're not stars .	這意味著有些像恆星的東西 。 但它們不是恆星 。
and we know what they are . billions of years ago , and billions of light years away , the material at the center of a galaxy collapsed towards a supermassive black hole .	而我們知道它們是什麼 。 數十億年前 , 以及數十億光年之外 , 一個星系中心的物質朝著一個超大質量黑洞瓦解 。
and then intense magnetic fields directed some of the energy of that gravitational collapse . and some of the matter , back out in the form of tremendous jets which illuminated lobes with the brilliance of i think it's a trillion suns .	然後密集的磁場引導了一些重力塌陷的能量 。 其中的一些物質 , 以巨大的噴射流的形式回到外面 , 照亮了額葉 , 上面照亮了一兆個太陽 。
now , the physics of the human brain could hardly be more unlike the physics of such a jet .	人類大腦的物理現象幾乎不像噴射機的物理原理 。
we couldn't survive for an instant in it . language breaks down when trying to describe what it would be like in one of those jets .	我們無法在一瞬間存活下來 。 語言在嘗試描述某一個噴流時 , 會崩解 。
it would be a bit like experiencing a supernova explosion , but at pointblank range and for millions of years at a time .	它會有點像經歷超新星爆炸 , 但在點伏特的範圍內 , 每次的數百萬年都如此 。
and yet , that jet happened in precisely such a way that billions of years later , on the other side of the universe , some bit of chemical scum could accurately describe , and model , and predict , and explain , above all there's your reference what was happening there , in reality .	然而 , 噴射流發生得如此精確 , 以至於數十億年後 , 在宇宙的另一端 , 一些化學污垢可以準確地描述 , 模型 , 和預測 , 並且解釋 , 最重要的是 , 有個你在參考那裡發生了什麼事 , 在現實中 。
the one physical system , the brain , contains an accurate working model of the other the quasar .	其中一個物理系統 , 大腦 , 包含了另一個 「 夸 」 的準確工作模型 。
not just a superficial image of it , though it contains that as well , but an explanatory model , embodying the same mathematical relationships and the same causal structure .	不僅僅是它的表面形象 , 雖然它包含了這一點 , 也包含了解釋性的模型 , 體現了相同的數學關係以及相同的因果結構 。
now that is knowledge . and if that weren't amazing enough , the faithfulness with which the one structure resembles the other is increasing with time . that is the growth of knowledge .	這就是知識 , 如果這還不夠驚人 , 對另一種結構的信心會隨著時間增加 。 這就是知識的增長 。
so , the laws of physics have this special property .	所以 , 物理定律有著這種特殊的特性 ,
that physical objects , as unlike each other as they could possibly be , can nevertheless embody the same mathematical and causal structure and to do it more and more so over time .	實體物品 , 儘管不盡然不同 , 但不論如何具體展現出同樣的數學和因果結構 , 且隨著時間的推移 , 能做得越來越多 。
so we are a chemical scum that is different . this chemical scum has universality .	所以 , 我們是化學污垢 , 這種化學污垢有著通用性 。
its structure contains , with everincreasing precision , the structure of everything . this place , and not other places in the universe , is a hub which contains within itself the structural and causal essence of the whole of the rest of physical reality . and so , far from being insignificant , the fact that the laws of physics allow this , or even mandate that this can happen , is one of the most important things about the physical world .	它的結構包含了不斷提升的精確度 , 所有東西的結構 。 這個地方 , 和宇宙中其他地方 , 是一個中心 , 裡面包含了整個物理現實的架構和因果關係 。 所以 , 與其它物理定律 , 物理定律允許這一切發生 , 甚至是 , 物理世界中最重要的事情之一 。
now how does the solar system and our environment , in the form of us acquire this special relationship with the rest of the universe ?	那麼太陽系和我們的環境 , 以我們自身習得的形式 , 與其他宇宙的特殊關係又是如何呢 ?
well , one thing that's true about stephen hawking's remark i mean , it is true , but it's the wrong emphasis . one thing that's true about it is that it doesn't do it with any special physics . there's no special dispensation , no miracles involved . it does it simply with three things that we have here in abundance .	關於史蒂芬•霍金的評論中有一點是對的 , 但這是錯誤的 。 有一點是正確的 , 就是它沒有特殊的物理 。 沒有特殊的干擾 , 沒有奇蹟的影響 。 它只用三件我們豐富的事物就可以辦到 。
one of them is matter , because the growth of knowledge is a form of information processing . information processing is computation , computation requires a computer there's no known way of making a computer without matter .	其中一個是物質 , 因為知識的增長是資訊處理的一種形式 。 資訊的處理是計算 , 電腦需要的是沒有物質的知識 。
we also need energy to make the computer , and most important , to make the media in effect onto which we record the knowledge that we discover .	我們也需要能量來製造電腦 , 最重要的是要讓媒體能夠有效地影響我們所發現的知識 。
and then thirdly , less tangible , but just as essential for the openended creation of knowledge , of explanations , is evidence .	第三點 , 比較不明顯 , 但對於知識開放、解釋的創造 , 也是很重要的 。
now , our environment is inundated with evidence .	現在 , 我們的環境充斥著證據 。
we happen to get round to testing , let's say , newton's law of gravity about 300 years ago .	我們剛好可以測試 , 比如說 , 牛頓的萬有引力定律大約在三百年前就有了 。
but the evidence that we used to do that was falling down on every square meter of the earth for billions of years before that , and will continue to fall on for billions of years afterwards . and the same is true for all the other sciences .	但是我們過去所做的證據 , 早在那之前就落在地球上每平方公尺上了 , 且數十億年後還會繼續落在地球上 。 所有其他的科學也同樣如此 。
as far as we know , evidence to discover the most fundamental truths of all the sciences is here just for the taking on our planet .	就我們所知 , 發掘所有科學最基本真理的證據就在我們的星球上 。
our location is saturated with evidence , and also with matter and energy .	我們的位置充滿了證據 , 也伴隨著物質和能量 。
out in intergalactic space , those three prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge are at their lowest possible supply .	在星系間的空間中 , 這三個開放式的知識創造的前提條件就在它們的可供度最低 。
as i said , it's empty ; it's cold ; and it's dark out there . or is it ?	就像我說的 , 那裡空無一物 , 寒冷 , 外面一片漆黑 , 還是 ?
now actually , that's just another parochial misconception .	其實那只是另一個狹隘的錯誤觀念 。
because imagine a cube out there in intergalactic space , the same size as our home , the solar system . now that cube is very empty by human standards , but that still means that it contains over a million tons of matter .	因為想像一個在星系間空間裡的立方體 , 和我們的房屋大小一樣 , 太陽系的大小 。 現在這個立方體被人類的標準所空了 , 但這仍然意味著這個立方體含有超過百萬噸的物質 。
and a million tons is enough to make , say , a selfcontained space station , on which there's a colony of scientists that are devoted to creating an openended stream of knowledge , and so on .	一百萬噸足以製作出 , 比方說 , 一個自給自足的太空站 , 有一群科學家 , 致力於創造開放式的知識流 , 諸如此類 。
now , it's way beyond present technology to even gather the hydrogen from intergalactic space and form it into other elements and so on .	現在遠超出當前的技術甚至將氫氣從星系間空間收集起來再將它轉化成其他元素等等
but the thing is , in a comprehensible universe , if something isn't forbidden by the laws of physics , then what could possibly prevent us from doing it , other than knowing how ?	但問題在於 , 在一個可理解的宇宙中 , 如果某樣東西不被物理定律所禁止 , 那麼 , 有什麼事情可能可以阻止我們做到 , 除了知道如何 ?
in other words , it's a matter of knowledge , not resources .	換句話說 , 這是關於知識的問題 , 而不是資源 。
and the same well , if we could do that we'd automatically have an energy supply , because the transmutation would be a fusion reactor and evidence ?	同樣地 , 如果我們可以自動做得到 , 我們就有能源供應 , 因為變異會是核融合反應爐和證據嗎 ?
well , again , it's dark out there to human senses . but all you've got to do is take a telescope , even one of presentday design , look out and you'll see the same galaxies as we do from here .	嗯 , 同樣的 , 對人類的感官是暗的 。 但你要做的是 , 用一台望遠鏡 , 甚至是現在設計的一台 , 向外看 , 你會看到和我們從這兒看到同樣的星系 。
and with a more powerful telescope , you'll be able to see stars , and planets .	再加上一個更強大的望遠鏡 , 你就能看到恆星 , 以及行星 。
in those galaxies , you'll be able to do astrophysics , and learn the laws of physics .	在那些星系中 , 你將能夠做到天體物理學 , 並學習物理定律 。
and locally there you could build particle accelerators , and learn elementary particle physics , and chemistry , and so on .	在當地你可以建造粒子加速器 , 並學習基本粒子物理學 , 化學等.
probably the hardest science to do would be biology field trips because it would take several hundred million years to get to the nearest lifebearing planet and back .	可能最難做得的科學是生物學領域之旅 , 因為要花上好幾億年才能到達最近的有生命的星球 , 再回來 。
but i have to tell you and sorry , richard but i never did like biology field trips much , and i think we can just about make do with one every few hundred million years .	但是我必須告訴你--對不起richard--但是我從來都不喜歡生物學的實地考察我認為我們可以每隔幾億年就做一次
so in fact , intergalactic space does contain all the prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge . any such cube , anywhere in the universe , could become the same kind of hub that we are , if the knowledge of how to do so were present there .	所以事實上 , 星系間的空間包含了開放式的知識的前提條件 。 任何這樣的立方體 , 任何在宇宙的任何地方 , 都可以成為和我們相同的樞紐 , 只要我們知道如何做是存在的 。
so we're not in a uniquely hospitable place .	所以我們不是在一個特別適宜人居的地方 。
if intergalactic space is capable of creating an openended stream of explanations , then so is almost every other environment . so is the earth . so is a polluted earth .	如果星系間的空間可以創造出一串開放式的解釋 , 那麼幾乎所有其他的環境 , 那麼地球也是一樣 。 受污染的地球 。
and the limiting factor , there and here , is not resources , because they're plentiful , but knowledge , which is scarce .	而限制性因素 , 這裡和這裡 , 不是資源 , 因為資源很充沛 , 但知識 , 很稀少 。
now this cosmic knowledgebased view may and i think ought to make us feel very special . but it should also make us feel vulnerable , because it means that without the specific knowledge that's needed to survive the ongoing challenges of the universe , we won't survive them .	這種以知識為基礎的宇宙觀也許--而我認為應該讓我們感覺十分特殊 。 但同時也應該讓我們感到脆弱 , 因為這意味著 , 若沒有特定的知識需要我們生存於宇宙中不斷面臨的挑戰 , 我們將無法存活 。
all it takes is for a supernova to go off a few light years away , and we'll all be dead !	僅僅是幾光年外的一個超新星 , 我們都會死 !
martin rees has recently written a book about our vulnerability to all sorts of things , from astrophysics , to scientific experiments gone wrong , and most importantly to terrorism with weapons of mass destruction .	馬丁.瑞斯最近寫了一本關於我們人類對各種事物的脆弱性的書 , 從天體物理學 , 到科學實驗都出錯 , 最重要的是用大規模毀滅性武器的恐怖主義 。
and he thinks that civilization has only a 50 percent chance of surviving this century .	他認為 , 文明只有50%的機率能在這個世紀生存 。
i think he's going to talk about that later in the conference .	我想他等會兒再在會議上會談到這個話題 。
now i don't think that probability is the right category to discuss this issue in .	現在我不認為機率是正確的分類可以討論這個議題
but i do agree with him about this . we can survive , and we can fail to survive .	但我確實同意他的看法 。 我們能生存下來 , 我們也可能無法生存下去 。
but it depends not on chance , but on whether we create the relevant knowledge in time .	但這並不取決於機會 , 而是我們是否能及時創造相關的知識 。
the danger is not at all unprecedented . species go extinct all the time .	危險完全不是從前所未 , 物種隨時會滅絕 。
civilizations end . the overwhelming majority of all species and all civilizations that have ever existed are now history .	文明終究會結束 。 絕大多數曾經存在過的物種和所有的文明都是歷史 。
and if we want to be the exception to that , then logically our only hope is to make use of the one feature that distinguishes our species , and our civilization , from all the others namely , our special relationship with the laws of physics , our ability to create new explanations , new knowledge to be a hub of existence .	如果我們想成為例外的話 , 邏輯上我們唯一的希望就是利用這個特點來區分我們這個物種和我們的文明 , 與其他所有人類--也就是 , 我們與物理定律的特殊關係我們的能力創造新的解釋 , 新的知識成為存在的中心
so let me now apply this to a current controversy , not because i want to advocate any particular solution , but just to illustrate the kind of thing i mean .	所以 , 讓我現在把這件事用在當前的爭議上 , 不是因為我想提倡任何特定的解決方案 , 而只是用來闡述我所指的那類事情 。
and the controversy is global warming .	而爭議是全球暖化 。
now , i'm a physicist , but i'm not the right kind of physicist . in regard to global warming , i'm just a layman . and the rational thing for a layman to do is to take seriously the prevailing scientific theory . and according to that theory , it's already too late to avoid a disaster .	我是物理學家 , 但是我不是正確的物理學家 。 關於全球暖化 , 我只是個懶漢 。 對於一個拉爾曼來說 , 理性是:認真對待那些普遍存在的科學理論 。 根據那個理論 , 已經太遲 , 以致於無法避免災難 。
because if it's true that our best option at the moment is to prevent co2 emissions with something like the kyoto protocol , with its constraints on economic activity and its enormous cost of hundreds of billions of dollars or whatever it is , then that is already a disaster by any reasonable measure .	因為如果它是當下我們最好的選擇就是用像京都議定書之類的東西來防止二氧化碳排放 , 限制經濟活動 , 花費數千億美元之類的 , 那麼任何合理的措施都將造成災難 。
and the actions that are advocated are not even purported to solve the problem , merely to postpone it by a little . so it's already too late to avoid it , and it probably has been too late to avoid it ever since before anyone realized the danger .	所提倡的行動 , 甚至沒有為解決問題而出力 , 僅僅是稍微推遲一下 。 所以 , 已經太遲 , 無法避免它 , 自從有人發現危險之前 , 可能已經太遲了 。
it was probably already too late in the 1970s , when the best available scientific theory was telling us that industrial emissions were about to precipitate a new ice age in which billions would die .	可能在1970年代就已經太晚了 , 最好的科學理論告訴我們 , 工業排放即將降臨一個新的冰河時期 , 數十億人將會死亡 。
now the lesson of that seems clear to me , and i don't know why it isn't informing public debate .	這堂課讓我很清楚 , 我也不知道為什麼它沒有提供公眾辯論的資訊 。
it is that we can't always know . when we know of an impending disaster , and how to solve it at a cost less than the cost of the disaster itself , then there's not going to be much argument , really .	就是我們不能一直都知道 。 當我們知道一個即將發生的災難 , 以及如何以費用低於災難本身的成本解決 , 那麼就真的不會有太多爭論了 。
but no precautions , and no precautionary principle , can avoid problems that we do not yet foresee .	但沒有預防措施 , 也沒有預防原則 , 就可以避免我們尚未預見的問題 。
hence , we need a stance of problemfixing , not just problemavoidance .	因此 , 我們需要解決問題的立場 , 而不只是解決問題 。
and it's true that an ounce of prevention equals a pound of cure , but that's only if we know what to prevent .	一盎司的預防等於一盎司的解藥但是這只有我們知道預防什麼的
if you've been punched on the nose , then the science of medicine does not consist of teaching you how to avoid punches .	如果你被打到鼻子上 , 那麼醫學的科學就不會教你如何避免打孔 。
if medical science stopped seeking cures and concentrated on prevention only , then it would achieve very little of either .	如果醫學科學不再尋求治療 , 只專注在預防 , 它也幾乎不會達成 。
the world is buzzing at the moment with plans to force reductions in gas emissions at all costs .	此刻世界正不斷地努力計畫 , 不計代價大幅降低氣排放 。
it ought to be buzzing with plans to reduce the temperature , and with plans to live at the higher temperature and not at all costs , but efficiently and cheaply . and some such plans exist , things like swarms of mirrors in space to deflect the sunlight away , and encouraging aquatic organisms to eat more carbon dioxide .	它應該與計畫配合降低溫度並駕馭更高溫的計畫而不是不計代價但效率又便宜 。 而且有些計畫存在 , 例如一群鏡子在太空中偏離太陽光 , 並且鼓勵水生生物吃更多的二氧化碳 。
at the moment , these things are fringe research .	在當下這些東西是fringe研究
they're not central to the human effort to face this problem , or problems in general .	他們不是人類投入心力去面對這個問題 , 或是一般性的問題 。
and with problems that we are not aware of yet , the ability to put right not the sheer good luck of avoiding indefinitely is our only hope , not just of solving problems , but of survival .	對於我們尚未意識到的問題 , 放錯的能力不是無限期的好運 , 是我們唯一的希望 , 不僅僅是解決問題 , 還包括生存 。
so take two stone tablets , and carve on them .	拿兩塊石板 , 然後刻在上面 。
on one of them , carve: " problems are soluble . "	其中一個說法是雕刻: " 問題是可以解決的 "
and on the other one carve: " problems are inevitable . "	另一部雕刻上寫著: 「 問題是不可避免的 。 」
how can a struggling country break out of poverty if it's trapped in a system of bad rules ? economist paul romer unveils a bold idea: " charter cities , " cityscale administrative zones governed by a coalition of nations .	一個掙扎生活的國家要怎樣才能脫離貧窮 , 如果它被困在一個不良規則的體制 ? 經濟學家保羅默揭示了一個大膽的想法: 「 特區城市 」 , 以城市規模統治的行政區 , 由一個國家聯盟來管理 。
business , culture , economics , global issues , politics	商業、文化、全球議題、政治、
paul romer's radical idea: charter cities	paulromer的激進想法:特區市 。
take a look at this picture .	請看這張照片 。
it poses a very fascinating puzzle for us .	它給我們帶來了一個非常引人入勝的謎題 。
these african students are doing their homework under streetlights at the airport in the capital city because they don't have any electricity at home .	這些非洲學生在首都機場的街燈下做功課 , 因為他們家裡沒有電 。
now , i haven't met these particular students , but i've met students like them .	我還沒見過這些特殊的學生 , 但我碰過像他們一樣的學生 。
let's just pick one for example , the one in the green shirt .	舉個例子 , 綠色上衣的那個 。
let's give him a name , too: nelson .	咱們來幫他取個名字:尼爾森 。
i'll bet nelson has a cellphone .	我敢說尼爾森有一支手機 。
so here is the puzzle .	所以謎題是這樣的:
why is it that nelson has access to a cuttingedge technology , like the cellphone , but doesn't have access to a 100yearold technology for generating electric light in the home ?	為什麼尼爾森可以接觸到像手機這樣尖端的科技 , 但是卻沒有一個一百年的科技可以在家裡產生電燈 ?
now , in a word , the answer is " rules . "	簡單來說 , 答案就是 「 規則 」 。
bad rules can prevent the kind of winwin solution that's available when people can bring new technologies in and make them available to someone like nelson .	不良的規則能夠防止雙贏的解決方案 , 當人們能夠將新技術帶進像尼爾森這樣的人手中 , 使他們有機會接觸到像尼爾森這樣的人 。
what kinds of rules ?	什麼樣的規則 ?
the electric company in this nation operates under a rule , which says that it has to sell electricity at a very low , subsidized price in fact , a price that is so low it loses money on every unit that it sells .	這個國家的電力公司運作規則是說它必須以極低的價格銷售電力--事實上 , 電價太低--每賣一單位都要損失金錢 。
so it has neither the resources , nor the incentives , to hook up many other users .	所以 , 它既沒有資源 , 也沒有誘因 , 可以吸引許多其他用戶 。
the president wanted to change this rule .	總統想要改變這條規則 ,
he's seen that it's possible to have a different set of rules , rules where businesses earn a small profit , so they have an incentive to sign up more customers .	他知道 , 有可能有不同的規則 , 企業從中賺取小額利潤的規則 , 所以他們有動機去簽署更多客戶 。
that's the kind of rules that the cellphone company that nelson purchases his telephony from operates under .	nelson公司採用的手機業者就是這種規則 , 不受監聽 。
the president has seen how those rules worked well .	總統見識過那些規則是如何運作的很好 。
so he tried to change the rules for pricing on electricity , but ran into a firestorm of protest from businesses and consumers who wanted to preserve the existing subsidized rates .	所以他嘗試改變用電價制定的規則 , 但卻引發了一場激烈的抗議 , 抗議來自企業和消費者 , 想要保存既有的補助率 。
so he was stuck with rules that prevented him from letting the winwin solution help his country .	所以他被困在規則中 , 阻止了他讓雙贏解決方案幫助他的國家 。
and nelson is stuck studying under the streetlights .	尼爾森被困在街燈下進行研究 ,
the real challenge then , is to try to figure out how we can change rules .	真正的挑戰是 , 試著找出我們該如何改變規則 。
are there some rules we can develop for changing rules ?	是否有一些規則我們可以發展用來改變規則 ?
i want to argue that there is a general abstract insight that we can make practical , which is that , if we can give more choices to people , and more choices to leaders who , in many countries , are also people .	我想要說明的是 , 有一個一般抽象的見解就是我們可以做實務 , 那就是 , 如果我們能給予人們更多選擇 , 給那些在許多國家裡 , 領導者更多的選擇 , 他們也是人民 。
but , it's useful to present the opposition between these two .	但是 , 要呈現出兩者間的反對意見 , 是很有用的 。
because the kind of choice you might want to give to a leader , a choice like giving the president the choice to raise prices on electricity , takes away a choice that people in the economy want .	因為你可能想給領導者什麼樣的選擇 , 比如給總統一個選擇 , 提高電價的選擇 , 剝奪了人們想要的一個選擇 。
they want the choice to be able to continue consuming subsidized electric power .	他們希望能選擇繼續使用補貼電力 。
so if you give just to one side or the other , you'll have tension or friction .	所以如果你只給予一方或者另一方 , 你會有張力或摩擦力 。
but if we can find ways to give more choices to both , that will give us a set of rules for changing rules that get us out of traps .	但如果我們能想辦法給雙方更多的選擇這會給我們一組規則用來改變規則使我們脫離陷阱
now , nelson also has access to the internet .	尼爾森也有網路用 。
and he says that if you want to see the damaging effects of rules , the ways that rules can keep people in the dark , look at the pictures from nasa of the earth at night .	他說 , 如果你想看到規則所造成的損害 , 規則所能讓人們留在黑暗中的方式 , 看看美國太空總署在夜間所看到的圖片 。
in particular check out asia .	特別是在亞洲 。
if you zoom in here , you can see north korea , in outline here , which is like a black hole compared to its neighbors .	如果你放大這裡 , 你可以看到北韓 , 位於輪廓上 , 它就像是鄰近地區的黑洞 。
now , you won't be surprised to learn that the rules in north korea keep people there in the dark .	現在 , 你不會驚訝地發現 , 北韓的規則讓那裡的人保持在黑暗中 。
but it is important to recognize that north korea and south korea started out with identical sets of rules in both the sense of laws and regulations , but also in the deeper senses of understandings , norms , culture , values and beliefs .	但很重要的是 , 要了解北韓和南韓一開始是用一套相同的規則在法律和法規的意義上 , 也要能更深入了解、規範、文化、價值和信念 。
when they separated , they made choices that led to very divergent paths for their sets of rules .	當他們分開時 , 他們做出了選擇 , 導致了非常多樣化的路徑 , 用於他們的規則 。
so we can change we as humans can change the rules that we use to interact with each other , for better , or for worse .	所以 , 我們可以改變我們人類可以改變我們用來和彼此互動的規則 , 做得更好 , 或做得更壞 。
now let's look at another region , the caribbean .	現在我們來看看另一個地區 , 加勒比海
zoom in on haiti , in outline here .	放大海地 , 在這裡 。
haiti is also dark , compared to its neighbor here , the dominican republic , which has about the same number of residents .	海地也很暗 , 與這裡的鄰居相比 , 多明尼加共和國也差不多數量的居民 。
both of these countries are dark compared to puerto rico , which has half as many residents as either haiti or the dominican republic .	這兩個國家相對於波多黎各來說 , 兩國的狀況都很黑暗 , 這個國家有一半的居民 , 不論是海地或多明尼加共和國 。
what haiti warns us is that rules can be bad because governments are weak .	海地警告我們的是 , 規則可能會有不好的情況 , 因為政府的軟弱 。
it's not just that the rules are bad because the government is too strong and oppressive , as in north korea .	不僅僅因為政府實在太強大 , 太過壓迫 , 就像北韓的情況一樣 。
so that if we want to create environments with good rules , we can't just tear down .	所以如果我們想要創造出有良好體制的環境 , 我們就不能就這樣撕下來 。
we've got to find ways to build up , as well .	我們也得找出方法來建立
now , china dramatically demonstrates both the potential and the challenges of working with rules .	現在 , 中國戲劇性地展示了與規則合作的潛力與挑戰 。
back in the beginning of the data presented in this chart , china was the world's hightechnology leader .	回到資料表的一開始 , 中國是世界高科技領導人 。
chinese had pioneered technologies like steel , printing , gunpowder .	中國人擁有先驅科技 , 像是鋼鐵、印刷、火藥 。
but the chinese never adopted , at least in that period , effective rules for encouraging the spread of those ideas a profit motive that could have encouraged the spread .	但中國人從未採用這種制度 , 至少在那個時期 , 有效的制度來鼓勵這些想法的散播 , 一個有利潤的動機 , 可以促使這個觀念的傳播 。
and they soon adopted rules which slowed down innovation and cut china off from the rest of the world .	他們很快就採用了規則 , 讓創新慢下來 , 讓中國遠離世界 。
so as other countries in the world innovated , in the sense both of developing newer technologies , but also developing newer rules , the chinese were cut off from those advances .	所以 , 隨著世界上其他國家的創新 , 在這方面 , 開發出更新的技術 , 同時開發出更新的規則 , 中國也被那些進步所阻斷 。
income there stayed stagnant , as it zoomed ahead in the rest of the world .	國民所得停滯不前 , 世界其他地方的收入停滯不前 。
this next chart looks at more recent data .	接下來這張圖表是比較近期的資料
it plots income , average income in china as a percentage of average income in the united states .	它策劃了所得 , 中國的平均所得佔了美國平均所得的百分比 。
in the '50s and '60s you can see that it was hovering at about three percent .	在50、60年代 , 你可以看到這個數字大約是3% 。
but then in the late '70s something changed .	但在70年代末期 , 有些事情改變了 。
growth took off in china . the chinese started catching up very quickly with the united states .	中國的成長開始在中國爆發了 , 中國人開始趕上美國 。
if you go back to the map at night , you can get a clue to the process that lead to the dramatic change in rules in china .	如果你在夜晚回到地圖上 , 你就能得到一個線索 , 這個過程會導致中國的大幅改變規則 。
the brightest spot in china , which you can see on the edge of the outline here , is hong kong .	中國最亮的這點 , 你們可以在輪廓邊上看到 , 就是香港 。
hong kong was a small bit of china that , for most of the 20th century , operated under a very different set of rules than the rest of mainland china rules that were copied from working market economies of the time , and administered by the british .	香港本來是中國的一小部分在20世紀大部分的時候都是用一套非常不同的規則來運作這套制度是用當時的勞動市場經濟制度所複製而成的
in the 1950s , hong kong was a place where millions of people could go , from the mainland , to start in jobs like sewing shirts , making toys .	在1950年代 , 香港是一個有數百萬人可以去的地方 , 從大地到大地 , 到從工作開始 , 像是縫衣、做玩具 。
but , to get on a process of increasing income , increasing skills led to very rapid growth there .	但 , 為了增加收入 , 增加技能就會帶來非常快速的成長 。
hong kong was also the model which leaders like deng xiaoping could copy , when they decided to move all of the mainland towards the market model .	香港當時也是一個範本 , 領導人如鄧小平可以複製的範本 , 當時他們決定把所有土地都移到主要市場模式上 。
but deng xiaoping instinctively understood the importance of offering choices to his people .	但鄧小平直覺地了解到提供人民選擇的重要性 。
so instead of forcing everyone in china to shift immediately to the market model , they proceeded by creating some special zones that could do , in a sense , what britain did: make the opportunity to go work with the market rules available to the people who wanted to opt in there .	所以 , 與其強迫所有中國人立即轉型到市場模式上 , 他們採取的方式是創建某些特區 , 某種程度上來說 , 英國所做到的:讓有機會和市場規則的人一同上班 , 讓想要選擇在那裏的人能有所貢獻 。
so they created four special economic zones around hong kong: zones where chinese could come and work , and cities grew up very rapidly there ; also zones where foreign firms could come in and make things .	所以他們在香港周圍建了四個特別的經濟特區:中國人可以來到這個區塊 , 中國人可以來到這個區塊 , 城市可以很快地在那裡成長 ; 也可以讓外國公司來到這個區間 , 做一些事情 。
one of the zones next to hong kong has a city called shenzhen .	在香港旁邊的一個地方有一個城市叫深圳
in that city there is a taiwanese firm that made the iphone that many of you have , and they made it with labor from chinese who moved there to shenzhen .	在那個城市裡 , 有個台灣公司 , 製作了你們當中許多人所擁有的iphone , 他們製作了從中國人到深圳的勞動力 。
so after the four special zones , there were 14 coastal cites that were open in the same sense , and eventually demonstrated successes in these places that people could opt in to , that they flocked to because of the advantages they offered .	所以 , 在四個特區之後 , 有14個海岸風箏 , 以同樣的方式在開放 , 最終在這些地方都能展現出成功 , 讓人們能夠選擇去做 , 讓他們團結起來 , 因為他們提供的優勢而被解放出來 。
demonstrated successes there led to a consensus for a move toward the market model for the entire economy .	在那裡獲得了成功 , 帶來了一致的共識 , 讓它朝向市場經濟模式前進 。
now the chinese example shows us several points .	中國的例子顯示了好幾點 。
one is: preserve choices for people .	其一是:為人們的選擇保存下來 。
two: operate on the right scale .	二:運作在正確的尺度上 。
if you try to change the rules in a village , you could do that , but a village would be too small to get the kinds of benefits you can get if you have millions of people all working under good rules .	如果你嘗試改變一個村落的規則 , 你可以這麼做 , 但是一個村落會變得太小 , 以至於得到好處 , 如果你有數百萬人在有良好體制下工作 。
on the other hand , the nation is too big .	另一方面 , 國家過於重大 ,
if you try to change the rules in the nation , you can't give some people a chance to hold back , see how things turn out , and let others zoom ahead and try the new rules .	如果你嘗試改變國家的規則 , 你不能給某些人一個機會 , 看看事情的結果如何 , 然後讓其他人放大 , 嘗試新的規則 。
but cities give you this opportunity to create new places , with new rules that people can opt in to .	但 , 城市給你這個機會 , 可以創造新的地方 , 只要有新的規則 , 大家就能夠選擇 。
and they're large enough to get all of the benefits that we can have when millions of us work together under good rules .	它們夠大 , 能取得當數百萬人在有良好規則下一起工作的所有利益 。
so the proposal is that we conceive of something called a charter city .	所以提議是我們對所謂 " 特區市 " 的概念
we start with a charter that specifies all the rules required to attract the people who we'll need to build the city .	我們從一份特許書開始 , 特定所有規則 , 來吸引我們建造這座城市所需要的人 。
we'll need to attract the investors who will build out the infrastructure the power system , the roads , the port , the airport , the buildings .	我們得要吸引投資者 , 他們要建造基礎設施 , 電力系統、道路、港口、機場、建築物 。
you'll need to attract firms , who will come hire the people who move there first .	你會需要吸引公司的員工 , 誰會先請來那兒的員工 。
and you'll need to attract families , the residents who will come and live there permanently , raise their children , get an education for their children , and get their first job .	而且你會需要吸引家家人 , 那些將來會永久住在那裡的居民 , 養育他們的孩子 , 為他們的孩子取得教育 , 取得他們的第一份工作 。
with that charter , people will move there .	有了那個憲章 , 人們會搬到那裡去 。
the city can be built .	城市可以被建造起來 。
and we can scale this model .	並且能夠將這個模型的規模
we can go do it over and over again .	我們可以一而再 , 再而三地做 。
to make it work , we need good rules . we've already discussed that .	要讓它可行 , 我們需要好的規則 。 我們已經討論過了 。
those are captured in the charter .	那些在憲法中被捕捉到 ,
we also need the choices for people .	我們也需要人民的選擇
that's really built into the model if we allow for the possibility of building cities on uninhabited land .	如果我們能在沒有人居住的土地上建造城市的可能性 , 那就真的建在模型中了 。
you start from uninhabited territory .	你從不為人知的領域開始 。
people can come live under the new charter , but no one is forced to live under it .	人們可以來到新的憲章底下 , 但沒有人是被迫要活在它底下的 。
the final thing we need are choices for leaders .	最後我們需要的是給領導者的選擇 。
and , to achieve the kind of choices we want for leaders we need to allow for the potential for partnerships between nations: cases where nations work together , in effect , de facto , the way china and britain worked together to build , first a little enclave of the market model , and then scale it throughout china .	為了達成我們希望領導者的那種選擇 , 我們需要讓各國合作的可能性:讓各國合作的案件 , 實際上 , deeo , 中國和英國合作建立的方式 , 先是建立一個小小的封閉式的市場模式 , 然後再擴展到整個中國 。
in a sense , britain , inadvertently , through its actions in hong kong , did more to reduce world poverty than all the aid programs that we've undertaken in the last century .	在某種意義上 , 英國不經意間 , 透過它在香港所做的行動 , 減少了世界貧窮 , 比上個世紀所有援助計畫加起來還要多 。
so if we allow for these kind of partnerships to replicate this again , we can get those kinds of benefits scaled throughout the world .	所以如果我們能讓這樣的夥伴再複製一次 , 我們就能讓這類的利益擴展到全世界 。
in some cases this will involve a delegation of responsibility , a delegation of control from one country to another to take over certain kinds of administrative responsibilities .	在某些情況下 , 這會牽涉到一個權力代表團 , 一個權力代表團 , 從一個國家到另一個國家的控制權 , 去負起某些責任 。
now , when i say that , some of you are starting to think , " well , is this just bringing back colonialism ? "	現在 , 當我這樣說的時候 , 你們其中一些人開始想 , " 嗯 , 這只是帶回殖民主義嗎 ? "
it's not . but it's important to recognize that the kind of emotions that come up when we start to think about these things , can get in the way , can make us pull back , can shut down our ability , and our interest in trying to explore new ideas .	它不是 。 但很重要的是 , 要體認當我們開始思考這些事情時所產生的那種情緒 , 可以阻擋我們 , 可以讓我們倒退 , 可以阻擋我們的能力 , 以及我們對探索新想法的興趣 。
why is this not like colonialism ?	為什麼這不像殖民主義 ?
the thing that was bad about colonialism , and the thing which is residually bad in some of our aid programs , is that it involved elements of coercion and condescension .	殖民主義不好的地方 , 在一些援助計畫中 , 有些還剩不好的東西 , 就是它涉及到強制和優越的元素 。
this model is all about choices , both for leaders and for the people who will live in these new places .	這個模式是關於選擇的一切 , 包括領導者 , 以及將來居住在這些新地方的人 。
and , choice is the antidote to coercion and condescension .	選擇是強制執行和執行的解藥 。
so let's talk about how this could play out in practice .	我們來談談這如何能實踐 。
let's take a particular leader , raul castro , who is the leader of cuba .	讓我們以一個特定的領導人 , 拉爾•卡斯楚 , 他是古巴的領袖 。
it must have occurred to castro that he has the chance to do for cuba what deng xiaoping did for china , but he doesn't have a hong kong there on the island in cuba .	卡斯楚一定也想過他有機會為古巴做到像鄧小平為中國做到的事不過他在古巴的島嶼上沒有香港
he does , though , have a little bit of light down in the south that has a very special status .	不過 , 他南方的點光有很特別的地位 。
there is a zone there , around guantanamo bay , where a treaty gives the united states administrative responsibility for a piece of land that's about twice the size of manhattan .	在關塔那摩灣周圍有一區 , 在那裡 , 一塊條約給予美國政府責任 , 一塊土地大約是曼哈頓的兩倍大 。
castro goes to the prime minister of canada and says , " look , the yankees have a terrible pr problem .	卡斯楚跑去找加拿大總理 , 說: 「 聽好 , 雅克斯有可怕的pr問題 。
they want to get out .	他們想要脫身 。
why don't you , canada , take over ?	你為什麼不 , 加拿大 , 接管 ?
build run a special administrative zone .	營運一個特殊的管理區 。
allow a new city to be built up there .	讓一座新的城市建設在那裡 。
allow many people to come in .	讓許多人進來
let us have a hong kong nearby .	讓我們附近有一個香港
some of my citizens will move into that city as well .	我的一些市民也會搬進那個城市 。
others will hold back . but this will be the gateway that will connect the modern economy and the modern world to my country . "	其他人會保持不動產 。 但這將是那條通往我國家的現代經濟和現代世界的通道 。 」
now , where else might this model be tried ?	這個模式還能在哪裡試驗呢 ?
well , africa . i've talked with leaders in africa .	嗯 , 非洲 。 我曾和領導人談過
many of them totally get the notion of a special zone that people can opt into as a rule .	他們中的很多人完全懂得特殊區域的概念 , 人們可以選擇將其視為一種規則 。
it's a rule for changing rules .	是改變規則的規則 。
it's a way to create new rules , and let people optin without coercion , and the opposition that coercion can force .	這是一種創造新規則的方式 , 並且讓人民有不受迫害的意見 , 及對抗不利的意見都能強迫 。
they also totally get the idea that in some instances they can make more credible promises to longterm investors the kind of investors who will come build the port , build the roads , in a new city they can make more credible promises if they do it along with a partner nation .	他們也完全了解 , 在某些情況下 , 他們能對長期投資者做出更有保障的承諾 , 像是投資者會來建港口、建造道路的那種 , 在一個新的城市中 , 他們能做出更有保障的承諾 , 只要他們能和一個夥伴國家合作 。
perhaps even in some arrangement that's a little bit like an escrow account , where you put land in the escrow account and the partner nation takes responsibility for it .	也許在某些安排中 , 這有點像是寄宿帳戶 , 把土地放在信託帳戶裡 , 合夥的國家需要為此負責 。
there is also lots of land in africa where new cities could be built .	非洲有很多的土地可以建設新城市 。
this is a picture i took when i was flying along the coast .	這是我沿著海岸飛行時所拍攝的照片
there are immense stretches of land like this land where hundreds of millions of people could live .	像這樣的大陸有著巨大的延伸 , 能讓數以億計的人居住 。
now , if we generalize this and think about not just one or two charter cites , but dozens cities that will help create places for the many hundreds of millions , perhaps billions of people who will move to cities in the coming century is there enough land for them ?	現在 , 如果我們總結一下 , 想一想 , 不僅僅是一、二個特區市 , 還有數十個城市 , 將有助於為數以億計、數十億人搬到城市 , 在未來的這個世紀 , 有足夠的土地容納他們嗎 ?
well , throughout the world , if we look at the lights at night , the one thing that's misleading is that , visually , it looks like most of the world is already built out .	嗯 , 在全世界 , 如果我們在晚上看這些燈時 , 有一件事是誤導了 , 那就是 , 視覺上來說 , 看來 , 全世界大部分的人都已經是內建出來的 。
so let me show you why that's wrong .	所以 , 讓我來告訴你為什麼那是錯的 。
take this representation of all of the land .	把這代表所有的土地
turn it into a square that stands for all the arable land on earth .	把它變成一個方塊代表地球上所有的可耕地
and let these dots represent the land that's already taken up by the cities that three billion people now live in .	讓這些點代表已經有三十億人居住的城市所需要的土地 。
if you move the dots down to the bottom of the rectangle you can see that the cities for the existing three billion urban residents take up only three percent of the arable land on earth .	如果你把這些點移到這個長方形的底部你可以看到有30億城市居民的城市只佔了地球上可耕地面積的3%
so if we wanted to build cities for another billion people , they would be dots like this .	所以如果我們想為另外十億人建造城市 , 他們會是像這樣的點 。
we'd go from three percent of the arable land , to four percent .	我們將從百分之三的可耕地 , 降到百分之四 。
we'd dramatically reduce the human footprint on earth by building more cities that people can move to .	我們大幅降低了地球上人類的足跡 , 藉由建造更多人們可以遷移的城市 。
and if these are cities governed by good rules , they can be cities where people are safe from crime , safe from disease and bad sanitation , where people have a chance to get a job .	如果這些城市是受良好體制管理的城市 , 他們可以是讓人民安全的城市 , 不受犯罪、疾病和不良的衛生設施傷害 , 這樣人們就有機會得到工作 。
they can get basic utilities like electricity .	能獲得像電力這樣基礎的公共設施
their kids can get an education .	他們的孩子可以接受教育
so what will it take to get started building the first charter cities , scaling this so we build many more ?	所以 , 要花什麼才能開始建造第一座特許城市 , 擴大規模 , 以便我們還能建造更多呢 ?
it would help to have a manual .	這有助於使用手冊 。
what university professors could do is write some details that might go into this manual .	大學教授們可以做的就是撰寫一些細節 , 可能進入這本手冊 。
you wouldn't want to let us run the cities , go out and design them .	你不會想讓我們管理城市 , 走出去設計它們 。
you wouldn't let academics out in the wild .	你不會讓學者們在野外
but , you could set us to work thinking about questions like , suppose it isn't just canada that does the deal with raul castro .	但 , 你可以讓我們去思考一些問題 , 比如 , 假設不只加拿大會對抗拉斯楚 。
perhaps brazil comes in as a participant , and spain as well . and perhaps cuba wants to be one of the partners in a fourway joint venture .	或許巴西也參一腳西班牙 , 或許古巴想成為四邊合作夥伴之一
how would we write the treaty to do that ?	我們要如何制定條約 , 才能做到 ?
there is less precedent for that , but that could easily be worked out .	比較沒有先例可循 , 但那很容易就能解決 。
how would we finance this ?	我們要如何資助這件事 ?
turns out singapore and hong kong are cities that made huge gains on the value of the land that they owned when they got started .	其實 , 新加坡和香港是一開始就有土地價值的城市 。
you could use the gains on the value of the land to pay for things like the police , the courts , but the school system and the health care system too , which make this a more attractive place to live , makes this a place where people have higher incomes which , incidentally , makes the land more valuable .	你可以利用土地的收益來支付像警察、法庭等費用 , 但學校體制和健康照護體制 , 這也是一個更吸引人的地方 , 讓這個地方的居民能有更高的收入 , 更順帶一提 , 讓土地更有價值 。
so the incentives for the people helping to construct this zone and build it , and set up the basic rules , go very much in the right direction .	所以 , 提供建設區塊的人們動機 , 並建立起基本規則 , 往對的方向前進 。
so there are many other details like this .	所以還有許多其它類似的細節 。
how could we have buildings that are low cost and affordable for people who work in a first job , assembling something like an iphone , but make those buildings energy efficient , and make sure that they are safe , so they don't fall down in an earthquake or a hurricane .	我們如何能有低成本的建築物 , 讓第一份工作需要負擔得起的建築物 , 組裝成類似iphone的東西 , 但讓那些建築物能有效率生產能源 , 確保它們安全 , 不會因為地震或是颶風而倒下 。
many technical details to be worked out , but those of us who are already starting to pursue these things can already tell that there is no roadblock , there's no impediment , other than a failure of imagination , that will keep us from delivering on a truly global winwin solution .	許多技術細節尚待解決 , 但是我們這些已經開始追求這些事的人 , 已經可以得知 , 沒有道路 , 沒有阻礙 , 除了一個失敗的想像力之外 , 還會讓我們無法實現真正的全球性的雙贏辦法 。
let me conclude with this picture .	讓我用這張照片做個總結 。
the reason we can be so well off , even though there is so many people on earth , is because of the power of ideas .	我們之所以如此幸福 , 儘管地球上有這麼多人 , 是因為思想的力量 。
we can share ideas with other people , and when they discover them , they share with us .	我們可以跟別人分享想法 , 當他們發現想法時 , 他們也會跟我們分享 。
it's not like scarce objects , where sharing means we each get less .	它不像稀有物品 , 分享的意義是我們都變得更少了 。
when we share ideas we all get more .	當我們分享想法時我們都會得到更多 。
when we think about ideas in that way , we usually think about technologies .	當我們用那種方式思考想法時 , 我們通常會想到科技 。
but there is another class of ideas: the rules that govern how we interact with each other ; rules like , let's have a tax system that supports a research university that gives away certain kinds of knowledge for free .	但還有另一種想法:規則在規則規則上管理我們如何和彼此互動 ; 例如 , 讓我們訂個賦稅制 , 來支撐一個研究大學 , 免費提供某些知識 。
let's have a system where we have ownership of land that is registered in a government office , that people can pledge as collateral .	讓我們有一個體制 , 我們擁有擁有土地在政府辦公室登記的土地 , 人民可以向政府部門索證 。
if we can keep innovating on our space of rules , and particularly innovate in the sense of coming up with rules for changing rules , so we don't get stuck with bad rules , then we can keep moving progress forward and truly make the world a better place , so that people like nelson and his friends don't have to study any longer under the streetlights . thank you .	如果我們能不斷在規則空間上創新 , 特別是在創新的意義上 , 來制定改變規則的規則 , 讓我們不會卡在不良的規則中 , 那麼我們就能不斷進步真正讓世界變得更好 , 讓像尼爾森和他的朋友再也不用在路燈下讀書了 。 謝謝 。
genomics pioneer craig venter takes a break from his epic roundtheworld expedition to talk about the millions of genes his team has discovered so far in its quest to map the ocean’s biodiversity .	基因組學先驅克萊格•凡特仰賴他的史詩般的遠征隊 , 來談談他團隊所發現的數百萬個基因 , 到目前為止 , 用來描繪海洋的生物多樣性 。
dna , biosphere , biotech , entrepreneur , genetics , invention , oceans , science , technology	dna、生物圈、生物科技、企業家、基因、發明、海洋、科學、科技、
craig venter on dna and the sea	craigventer在dna和海上
at the break , i was asked by several people about my comments about the aging debate .	演講結束後 , 我被幾個人問到我對於老化辯論的看法 。
and this will be my only comment on it .	這將是我對它唯一的評論 。
and that is , i understand that optimists greatly outlive pessimists .	那就是 , 我了解樂觀主義者活得比悲觀者好 。
what i'm going to tell you about in my 18 minutes is how we're about to switch from reading the genetic code to the first stages of beginning to write the code ourselves .	我在這18分鐘內要告訴你們的 , 就是我們將如何從讀取基因編碼轉換到開始自己編寫基因編碼的最初階段 。
it's only 10 years ago this month when we published the first sequence of a freeliving organism , that of haemophilus influenzae .	僅僅是10年前這個月我們才出版第一批免費生物體的序列 , 也就是流感嗜血桿菌 。
that took a genome project from 13 years down to four months .	花了13年到4個月的基因組計劃 。
we can now do that same genome project in the order of two to eight hours .	我們現在可以在二到八小時內完成同樣的基因組計畫 。
so in the last decade , a large number of genomes have been added: most human pathogens , a couple of plants , several insects and several mammals , including the human genome .	所以 , 在過去十年間 , 大量的基因組被加上了:大部份的人類病原體、幾種植物、幾種昆蟲和幾種哺乳類的基因組 , 包括人類基因組 。
genomics at this stage of the thinking from a little over 10 years ago was , by the end of this year , we might have between three and five genomes sequenced ; it's on the order of several hundred .	此時的基因組學 , 從大約10多年前開始 , 到今年底 , 我們可能有3到5組基因組的測序 , 大約是幾百組 。
we just got a grant from the gordon and betty moore foundation to sequence 130 genomes this year , as a side project from environmental organisms .	今年 , 我們剛剛從戈登和貝蒂•摩爾基金獲得一項資助 , 將130組基因組的基因組排序視為環境有機體的副作用 。
so the rate of reading the genetic code has changed .	所以讀取基因編碼的速率就改變了 。
but as we look , what's out there , we've barely scratched the surface on what is available on this planet .	但當我們看著 , 外面的世界有什麼 , 我們幾乎都沒有抓住這顆行星上可用的表面 。
most people don't realize it , because they're invisible , but microbes make up about a half of the earth's biomass , whereas all animals only make up about one onethousandth of all the biomass .	大多數人不會意識到它 , 因為它們是隱形的 , 但微生物構成了地球一半的生物量 , 而所有動物的數量只佔所有生物總數的1/3 。
and maybe it's something that people in oxford don't do very often , but if you ever make it to the sea , and you swallow a mouthful of seawater , keep in mind that each milliliter has about a million bacteria and on the order of 10 million viruses .	也許這種事是牛津居民不太常做 , 但如果你曾經到海裡 , 吞一口海水 , 請記住每一毫升的海水中都有大約一百萬個細菌和一千萬個病毒 。
less than 5 , 000 microbial species have been characterized as of two years ago , and so we decided to do something about it .	少於5 , 000種微生物物種在兩年前就被分類了 , 所以我們決定採取行動 。
and we started the sorcerer ii expedition , where we were , as with great oceanographic expeditions , trying to sample the ocean every 200 miles .	我們開始了第二期的srceri探險 , 我們在那裡進行了很棒的海洋探險 , 嘗試每隔200英哩進行一次採樣 。
we started in bermuda for our test project , then moved up to halifax , working down the u . s . east coast , the caribbean sea , the panama canal , through to the galapagos , then across the pacific , and we're in the process now of working our way across the indian ocean .	我們從百慕達開始做我們的測試計畫 , 接著移到哈利法克斯 , 在美國東岸 , 加勒比海 , 巴拿馬運河 , 穿過加拉帕戈斯 , 橫越太平洋 , 我們現在正在橫越印度洋 。
it's very tough duty ; we're doing this on a sailing vessel , in part to help excite young people about going into science .	這是很艱難的任務 ; 我們在帆船上進行此項任務 , 有一部分能協助引導年輕人進入科學領域 。
the experiments are incredibly simple .	實驗非常簡單 。
we just take seawater and we filter it , and we collect different size organisms on different filters , and then take their dna back to our lab in rockville , where we can sequence a hundred million letters of the genetic code every 24 hours .	我們只採集海水並過濾它 , 然後在不同的濾網上搜集不同大小的生物 , 然後把它們的dna帶回我們在岩ville的實驗室 , 在那裡 , 我們每24小時可以對一億個基因編碼進行測序 。
and with doing this , we've made some amazing discoveries .	這麼做之後 , 我們有了驚人的發現 。
for example , it was thought that the visual pigments that are in our eyes there was only one or two organisms in the environment that had these same pigments .	舉例來說 , 當時認為我們眼中的視覺色素在環境中只有一兩種有機體具有相同的色素 。
it turns out , almost every species in the upper parts of the ocean in warm parts of the world have these same photoreceptors , and use sunlight as the source of their energy and communication .	結果是 , 世界上大部分海洋中 , 溫暖部分的海洋中 , 幾乎所有的物種都有這些相同的光感接收器 , 並將陽光當作它們能量和溝通的來源 。
from one site , from one barrel of seawater , we discovered 1 . 3 million new genes and as many as 50 , 000 new species .	從一個地點 , 從一桶海水中 , 我們發現了一百三十萬個新基因和多達五萬個新物種 。
we've extended this to the air now with a grant from the sloan foundation .	我們現在已經把這個計畫用sloan基金會的資助來把這個計畫延伸到空中 。
we're measuring how many viruses and bacteria all of us are breathing in and out every day , particularly on airplanes or closed auditoriums .	我們正在測量我們每天所呼吸的病毒和細菌數量 , 特別是在飛機或密閉的講堂上 。
we filter through some simple apparatuses ; we collect on the order of a billion microbes from just a day filtering on top of a building in new york city .	我們透過一些簡單的儀器過濾 ; 我們僅僅一天內就收集到十億微生物的數量 , 在紐約的一棟大樓上過濾 。
and we're in the process of sequencing all that at the present time .	在目前我們對這一切進行排序的過程中 ,
just on the data collection side , just where we are through the galapagos , we're finding that almost every 200 miles , we see tremendous diversity in the samples in the ocean .	就在收集資料的這一邊 , 我們透過加拉帕戈斯群眾 , 發現幾乎每隔200英里 , 我們就在海裡樣本中看到極大的多樣性 。
some of these make logical sense , in terms of different temperature gradients .	有些在邏輯上合理的說法是不同溫度的梯度
so this is a satellite photograph based on temperatures red being warm , blue being cold and we found there's a tremendous difference between the warm water samples and the cold water samples , in terms of abundant species .	這是一張衛星照片 , 以溫度為基礎 , 紅色是溫暖的 , 藍色則是寒冷的 , 我們發現溫暖的水樣和很冷的水樣本之間有著極大的差異 , 以豐富的物種而言 。
the other thing that surprised us quite a bit is these photoreceptors detect different wavelengths of light , and we can predict that based on their amino acid sequence .	另一件讓我們相當驚訝的是這些光感測器探測不同波長的光 , 我們可以根據它們的氨基酸序列來預測 。
and these vary tremendously from region to region .	這些不同區域的變化非常大 。
maybe not surprisingly , in the deep ocean , where it's mostly blue , the photoreceptors tend to see blue light .	或許不意外地 , 在深海裡 , 大部分是藍色的 , 感光細胞傾向於看見藍光 。
when there's a lot of chlorophyll around , they see a lot of green light .	當周圍有大量葉綠素時 , 它們會看見很多綠光 。
but they vary even more , possibly moving towards infrared and ultraviolet in the extremes .	但它們可能有更多的變化 , 可能在極端的情況下 , 朝紅外線和紫外線前進 。
just to try and get an assessment of what our gene repertoire was , we assembled all the data including all of ours thus far from the expedition , which represents more than half of all the gene data on the planet and it totaled around 29 million genes .	為了評估基因庫的量 , 我們把所有資料組合起來 , 包括所有我們目前在探險的資料 , 總計大約有一半以上的基因資料 , 總計大約有兩千九百萬個基因 。
and we tried to put these into gene families to see what these discoveries are: are we just discovering new members of known families , or are we discovering new families ?	我們試著把這些基因放到基因家庭中 , 看看這些發現是什麼:我們是發現已知家庭的新成員嗎 ? 還是我們發現了新的家庭 ?
and it turns out we have about 50 , 000 major gene families , but every new sample we take in the environment adds in a linear fashion to these new families .	結果我們大約有五萬個主要的基因族群 , 但我們在環境中所採取的每一個新樣本 , 都會以排列的方式帶給這些新族群 。
so we're at the earliest stages of discovery about basic genes , components and life on this planet .	所以我們正處於發現基礎基因、組成物及生命的最早階段 。
when we look at the socalled evolutionary tree , we're up on the upper righthand corner with the animals .	當我們看到所謂的演化樹 , 我們就在右上角 , 和動物一起 。
of those roughly 29 million genes , we only have around 24 , 000 in our genome .	那些大約有2千9百萬個基因 , 我們的基因組只有大約2萬4千種 。
and if you take all animals together , we probably share less than 30 , 000 and probably maybe a dozen or more thousand different gene families .	如果你把所有動物放在一起看 , 我們可能只有不到三萬種 , 可能只有十幾種或更多的基因族群 。
i view that these genes are now not only the design components of evolution .	我認為 , 這些基因現在不僅僅是演化的設計要素 。
and we think in a genecentric view maybe going back to richard dawkins' ideas than in a genomecentric view , which are different constructs of these gene components .	我們以基因為中心的觀點來看 , 或許回到了理查•道金斯的想法 , 而不是以基因為中心的觀點來看 , 這些基因組成的不同構造 。
synthetic dna , the ability to synthesize dna , has changed at sort of the same pace that dna sequencing has over the last decade or two , and is getting very rapid and very cheap .	合成dna , 即dna合成的能力 , 已經在某種程度上改變了 , dna測序的速度在過去十年或二十年間 , 已經變得非常快速、非常便宜 。
our first thought about synthetic genomics came when we sequenced the second genome back in 1995 , and that from mycoplasma genitalium .	我們最初想到 「 合成基因組 」 的想法是從1995年我們在為第二組基因組定序之後 , 想到它是從菌絲體生殖器取得的 。
and we have really nice tshirts that say , you know , " i heart my genitalium . "	我們有很棒的t恤上面寫著: 「 我愛我的生殖器 。 」
this is actually just a microorganism .	這其實只是一種微生物 。
but it has roughly 500 genes .	但有大約500個基因 。
haemophilus had 1 , 800 genes .	嗜血桿菌有1800個基因 。
and we simply asked the question , if one species needs 800 , another 500 , is there a smaller set of genes that might comprise a minimal operating system ?	我們只是問了個問題 , 如果有一種物種需要800種 , 另外500種 , 有一組基因比較小 , 可能是由最小的作業系統所組成的 ?
so we started doing transposon mutagenesis .	所以我們開始進行轉位子的突變 。
transposons are just small pieces of dna that randomly insert in the genetic code .	轉位子只是隨機插入基因編碼的小段的dna 。
and if they insert in the middle of the gene , they disrupt its function .	而如果它們插入基因的正中間 , 干擾它的功能 ,
so we made a map of all the genes that could take transposon insertions and we called those " nonessential genes . "	所以我們製作了所有可以接受轉位子插入的基因圖譜 , 我們稱之為 「 非必要基因 」 。
but it turns out the environment is very critical for this , and you can only define an essential or nonessential gene based on exactly what's in the environment .	但結果發現 , 環境對此是非常關鍵的 , 你只能根據環境中到底是什麼來定義一個必要或非必要的基因 。
we also tried to take a more directly intellectual approach with the genomes of 13 related organisms , and we tried to compare all of those , to see what they had in common .	我們也嘗試將一個更直接的方法 , 和13種相關有機體的基因組做比較 , 我們嘗試將它們的一切比較 , 看看它們之間有什麼共同點 。
and we got these overlapping circles . and we found only 173 genes common to all 13 organisms .	我們得到了這些重疊的圓 。 我們發現 , 只有173個基因在13種有機體中共有 。
the pool expanded a little bit if we ignored one intracellular parasite ; it expanded even more when we looked at core sets of genes of around 310 or so .	如果我們忽略了一組細胞寄生蟲 , 水池會膨脹一點 , 大約310左右會增加更多 。
so we think that we can expand or contract genomes , depending on your point of view here , to maybe 300 to 400 genes from the minimal of 500 .	所以我們認為我們可以擴張或收縮基因組 , 取決於你在這裡的觀點 , 將300到400個基因從最少的500個基因擴張到400個基因 。
the only way to prove these ideas was to construct an artificial chromosome with those genes in them , and we had to do this in a cassettebased fashion .	唯一可以證明這些想法的方法是製造一條人造染色體 , 裡面有那些基因 , 我們必須以定型為基礎來做這件事 。
we found that synthesizing accurate dna in large pieces was extremely difficult .	我們發現在大型的片斷中合成出精確的dna是極其困難的 。
ham smith and clyde hutchison , my colleagues on this , developed an exciting new method that allowed us to synthesize a 5 , 000base pair virus in only a twoweek period that was 100 percent accurate , in terms of its sequence and its biology .	hamsmith和clydehutchison , 是我的同事 , 研發出令人振奮的新方法 , 讓我們在兩週內合成一個5000個鹼基對的病毒 , 只有兩週的準確度 , 是100%的準確度 , 以它的序列和生物學來說 。
it was a quite exciting experiment when we just took the synthetic piece of dna , injected it in the bacteria and all of a sudden , that dna started driving the production of the virus particles that turned around and then killed the bacteria .	這是個令人興奮的實驗 , 當我們把合成的dna注射到細菌中 , 突然間 , dna開始導致病毒粒子轉過身 , 然後殺死了細菌 。
this was not the first synthetic virus a polio virus had been made a year before but it was only one tenthousandth as active and it took three years to do .	這不是人造病毒的第一種合成 , 小兒麻痺病毒在一年之前被製造出來 , 但它只有萬分之一的活躍病毒且花了三年時間 。
this is a cartoon of the structure of phi x 174 .	這是phix174的結構卡通 。
this is a case where the software now builds its own hardware , and that's the notions that we have with biology .	這是一個軟體現在建構自己的硬體的例子 , 也是我們和生物學產生的概念 。
people immediately jump to concerns about biological warfare , and i had recent testimony before a senate committee , and a special committee the u . s . government has set up to review this area .	人們立刻轉而關注生物戰 , 我最近在參議院委員會舉行前發表了證詞 , 美國政府設立了一個專門委員會 , 來審查這一區域 。
and i think it's important to keep reality in mind , versus what happens with people's imaginations .	我認為很重要的是要讓現實記住 , 與其讓人們的想像力保持在心中 。
basically , any virus that's been sequenced today that genome can be made .	基本上 , 任何今天已經完成基因組定序的病毒都可以製造
and people immediately freak out about things about ebola or smallpox , but the dna from this organism is not infective .	大家會立刻對伊波拉病毒或天花感到驚訝 , 但這個有機體的dna沒有感染力 。
so even if somebody made the smallpox genome , that dna itself would not cause infections .	所以 , 即使有人做了天花的基因組 , dna本身也不會造成感染 。
the real concern that security departments have is designer viruses .	真正讓國安部門擔憂的是設計師病毒 。
and there's only two countries , the u . s . and the former soviet union , that had major efforts on trying to create biological warfare agents .	並且只有兩個國家 , 美國和前蘇聯兩國 , 他們在試圖創造生物武器時 , 曾有過重大的努力 。
if that research is truly discontinued , there should be very little activity on the knowhow to make designer viruses in the future .	如果那項研究真的被終結了 , 將來在製造設計病毒上 , 應該不會有非常少的活動 。
i think singlecell organisms are possible within two years .	我認為 , 在兩年內 , 單細胞生物就有可能
and possibly eukaryotic cells , those that we have , are possible within a decade .	有可能真核細胞 , 那些我們已經擁有的細胞 , 在十年內是可能實現的 。
so we're now making several dozen different constructs , because we can vary the cassettes and the genes that go into this artificial chromosome .	所以我們現在正在製作數十種不同的構造 , 因為我們可以改變放大器的放大器和基因 , 進入人造染色體 。
the key is , how do you put all of the others ?	關鍵在於 , 如何將所有其他人
we start with these fragments , and then we have a homologous recombination system that reassembles those into a chromosome .	我們從這些碎片開始 , 然後我們有一個同源重組系統 , 將這些碎片重新組合成一個染色體 。
this is derived from an organism , deinococcus radiodurans , that can take three million rads of radiation and not be killed .	這是從一個有機體衍生出來的 , deinocococcusradiodurans說 , 它可以承受三百萬拉德輻射 , 且不會被殺死 。
it reassembles its genome after this radiation burst in about 12 to 24 hours , after its chromosomes are literally blown apart .	在輻射爆發後它會在12至24小時內重組它的基因 , 在它的染色體被完全炸開之後 。
this organism is ubiquitous on the planet , and exists perhaps now in outer space due to all our travel there .	這種生物在地球上無所不在 , 或許現在因為我們在那裡的旅行而存在於外太空 。
this is a glass beaker after about half a million rads of radiation .	這是由約50萬拉德輻射照射而產生的玻璃杯 。
the glass started to burn and crack , while the microbes sitting in the bottom just got happier and happier .	玻璃開始發燒且發出啪聲 , 而在底部的微生物卻變得更快樂 。
here's an actual picture of what happens: the top of this shows the genome after 1 . 7 million rads of radiation .	這張是實際狀況的照片上方顯示輻射的基因組是在170萬拉德輻射之後
the chromosome is literally blown apart .	染色體被完全分解了 。
and here's that same dna automatically reassembled 24 hours later .	這是同一種dna在24小時後自動重新組合 。
it's truly stunning that these organisms can do that , and we probably have thousands , if not tens of thousands , of different species on this planet that are capable of doing that .	真的很令人震驚 , 這些生物能夠做到這件事 , 我們可能有成千上萬的 , 如果不是數以萬計的不同的物種 , 才有能力做到這一點 。
after these genomes are synthesized , the first step is just transplanting them into a cell without a genome .	在這些基因組被綜合後 , 第一步就是將它們移植進一個沒有基因組的細胞 。
so we think synthetic cells are going to have tremendous potential , not only for understanding the basis of biology but for hopefully environmental and society issues .	所以我們認為合成細胞將會有極大的潛力 , 不僅是為了瞭解生物學的基礎 , 同時也為了環境和社會議題 。
for example , from the third organism we sequenced , methanococcus jannaschii it lives in boiling water temperatures ; its energy source is hydrogen and all its carbon comes from co2 it captures back from the environment .	舉例來說 , 從我們所測序的第三個生物上 , 甲烷janoccusjannasisii住在沸騰的水溫 ; 它的能量來源是氫原子 , 它的碳是來自於二氧化碳 , 它是從周圍環境中捕捉回來的 。
so we know lots of different pathways , thousands of different organisms now that live off of co2 , and can capture that back .	所以我們知道許多不同的途徑 , 成千上萬種不同的生物以二氧化碳為生 , 可以捕捉回來 。
so instead of using carbon from oil for synthetic processes , we have the chance of using carbon and capturing it back from the atmosphere , converting that into biopolymers or other products .	所以 , 與其從使用從石油中取得的碳 , 不如從大氣中採用碳 , 將碳從大氣層中捕捉回來 , 將它轉換成生物聚合物或其他產品 。
we have one organism that lives off of carbon monoxide , and we use as a reducing power to split water to produce hydrogen and oxygen .	我們有一種生物是依靠一氧化碳來維生的 , 我們用作一種降低能量來分解水來產生氫氣和氧氣 。
also , there's numerous pathways that can be engineered metabolizing methane .	此外 , 還有無數的途徑 , 都可以把甲烷給改造成 。
and dupont has a major program with statoil in norway to capture and convert the methane from the gas fields there into useful products .	杜邦對挪威石油公司有一項重大的計畫要把來自天然氣田的甲烷轉換成為有用的產品
within a short while , i think there's going to be a new field called " combinatorial genomics , " because with these new synthesis capabilities , these vast gene array repertoires and the homologous recombination , we think we can design a robot to make maybe a million different chromosomes a day .	短時間內 , 我認為將會有一個新的領域 , 叫做 「 組合基因組學 」 , 因為有這些新的合成能力 , 這些廣大的基因陣列和同源重組 , 我們認為我們可以設計一個機器人 , 讓每天可能製造一百萬種不同的染色體 。
and therefore , as with all biology , you get selection through screening , whether you're screening for hydrogen production , or chemical production , or just viability .	因此 , 就像所有生物學一樣 , 透過篩選 , 無論是對氫化生產做篩選 , 或化學生產 , 或僅僅是可行性 。
to understand the role of these genes is going to be well within reach .	要了解這些基因所扮演的角色 , 將來會很好的接觸 。
we're trying to modify photosynthesis to produce hydrogen directly from sunlight .	我們正在嘗試修改光合作用的過程 , 直接從陽光中產生氫氣 。
photosynthesis is modulated by oxygen , and we have an oxygeninsensitive hydrogenase that we think will totally change this process .	光合作用是由氧氣來調節的 , 我們認為有一種氧不敏感的催化酶將會完全改變這個過程 。
we're also combining cellulases , the enzymes that break down complex sugars into simple sugars and fermentation in the same cell for producing ethanol .	我們也在結合細胞酶 , 將複雜糖分解成簡單糖在同一個細胞裡 , 發酵來製造乙醇 。
pharmaceutical production is already under way in major laboratories using microbes .	用微生物進行製藥生產已經在主要實驗室中進行了 。
the chemistry from compounds in the environment is orders of magnitude more complex than our best chemists can produce .	環境中的化合物所產生的化學作用 , 會比我們最好的化學家所製造的還要複雜許多 。
i think future engineered species could be the source of food , hopefully a source of energy , environmental remediation and perhaps replacing the petrochemical industry .	我認為未來工程的物種可以成為食物的來源 , 希望成為能源的來源 , 環境的補救措施 , 或許還能取代石化工業 。
let me just close with ethical and policy studies .	讓我以倫理和政策的研究來作總結 。
we delayed the start of our experiments in 1999 until we completed a yearandahalf bioethical review as to whether we should try and make an artificial species .	在1999年 , 我們延遲了實驗的開始 , 直到我們完成了一個一年半的生物倫理審查 , 討論我們是否應該嘗試製造一個人造物種 。
every major religion participated in this .	每個主要宗教都參與了這個項目
it was actually a very strange study , because the various religious leaders were using their scriptures as law books , and they couldn't find anything in them prohibiting making life , so it must be ok . the only ultimate concerns were biological warfare aspects of this , but gave us the go ahead to start these experiments for the reasons we were doing them .	這其實是個很奇怪的研究 , 因為各種宗教領袖都把他們的經文當成是法律書籍 , 卻找不到任何東西來禁止製作生命 , 所以這一定是沒問題的 。 唯一的最終關注是生物戰的面向 , 卻給我們未來的開始這些實驗的理由 。
right now the sloan foundation has just funded a multiinstitutional study on this , to work out what the risk and benefits to society are , and the rules that scientific teams such as my own should be using in this area , and we're trying to set good examples as we go forward .	目前史隆基金會剛剛資助一個多機構的研究 , 來找出對社會的風險和益處 , 以及像我這樣的科學團隊所應該採用的規則 , 在這個領域中 , 我們在努力建立好的範例 。
these are complex issues .	這些都是複雜的問題 。
except for the threat of bioterrorism , they're very simple issues in terms of , can we design things to produce clean energy , perhaps revolutionizing what developing countries can do and provide through various simple processes .	除了生物恐怖主義的威脅之外 , 它們是很簡單的議題 , 我們是否能設計東西來產生清潔能源 , 或許能改革開發中國家的做法 , 並透過各種簡單的過程來提供 。
psychologist philip zimbardo says happiness and success are rooted in a trait most of us disregard: the way we orient toward the past , present and future . he suggests we calibrate our outlook on time as a first step to improving our lives .	心理學家菲利普津巴多說 , 快樂和成功來自一個我們大部分人都不在乎的特質:我們朝向過去、現在和未來的方向前進 。 他建議我們校正自己的過往 , 讓我們用時間的第一步來改善生活 。
brain , business , happiness , mind , psychology , science	大腦、商業、快樂、思想、心理學、科學
philip zimbardo prescribes a healthy take on time	菲利浦•津巴多開出健康的 「 準時 」 會 ,
i want to share with you some ideas about the secret power of time , in a very short time .	我想和大家分享一些關於時間的秘密力量的想法 , 在很短的時間內 。
video: all right , start the clock please . 30 seconds studio .	影片:好吧 , 開始計時器 。 三十秒的工作室 。
keep it quiet please . settle down .	保持安靜 , 安頓下來 。
it's about time . end sequence . take one .	時間差不多 , 終結排序 , 拿一個
10 , nine , eight , seven , six , five , four , three , two . . .	10 , 9 , 8 , 7 , 6 , 5 , 4 , 3 , 2......
philip zimbardo: let's tune into the conversation of the principals in adam's temptation .	菲利浦津巴多:咱們先調查亞當的誘惑性對談 。
" come on adam , don't be so wishywashy . take a bite . " " i did . "	「 來吧 , 亞當 , 別那麼胡說八道 。 咬一口 。 」 「 我做到了 。 」
" one bite , adam . don't abandon eve . "	「 一口 , 亞當 。 不要拋棄伊娃 。 」
" i don't know , guys .	「 我不知道 , 各位 。
i don't want to get in trouble . "	我不想惹麻煩 。 」
" okay . one bite . what the hell ? "	「 好吧 。 一口 。 到底怎麼了 ? 」
life is temptation . it's all about yielding , resisting , yes , no , now , later , impulsive , reflective , present focus and future focus .	生活充滿誘惑感 。 一切有關節拍、抗拒 , 是的 , 是的 , 不是 , 現在 , 以後 , 衝動 , 專注 , 現在以及未來的重點 。
promised virtues fall prey to the passions of the moment .	承諾美德會墮落到當下的熱情
of teenage girls who pledged sexual abstinence and virginity until marriage thank you george bush the majority , 60 percent , yielded to sexual temptations within one year .	那些曾宣誓要在婚前 , 實踐性慾、貞操的少女 , 多虧了大多數人 , 約有60% , 會在一年內達到性誘惑 。
and most of them did so without using birth control .	大部份都在不使用節育器 。
so much for promises .	為了承諾好多 。
now lets tempt fouryearolds , giving them a treat .	現在讓誘使四歲的孩子 , 給他們一個條約 。
they can have one marshmallow now . but if they wait until the experimenter comes back , they can have two .	他們現在可以有一顆棉花糖 。 但如果他們等到實驗人員回來 , 他們會有兩顆 。
of course it pays , if you like marshmallows , to wait .	當然 , 如果你喜歡棉花糖的話 , 它會付錢 , 等一下 。
what happens is twothirds of the kids give in to temptation .	三分之二的孩子用於誘惑 。
they cannot wait . the others , of course , wait .	他們不能等 。 其他人 , 當然 , 等等 。
they resist the temptation . they delay the now for later .	他們抗拒誘惑 , 延後推 。
walter mischel , my colleague at stanford , went back 14 years later , to try to discover what was different about those kids .	沃爾特.米舍爾 , 我斯坦福大學的同事 , 14年後又回去找那些孩子們的不同之處 。
there were enormous differences between kids who resisted and kids who yielded , in many ways .	在很多方面 , 抵制的孩子和被量產的孩子之間存在著巨大的差異 。
the kids who resisted scored 250 points higher on the sat .	那些抵制sat考試的孩子 , 成績提高了250分 。
that's enormous . that's like a whole set of different iq points .	那是巨大的 。 那就像是一整組不同的智商點 。
they didn't get in as much trouble . they were better students .	他們沒有惹上多少麻煩 , 而是更好的學生 。
they were selfconfident and determined . and the key for me today , the key for you , is , they were futurefocused rather than presentfocused .	他們自信又堅定 。 而對我來說 , 最重要的是 , 他們是 「 未來 」 , 而不是 「 現在式 」 。
so what is time perspective ? that's what i'm going to talk about today .	所以 , 時間觀點是什麼 ? 這就是我今天要談的 。
time perspective is the study of how individuals , all of us , divide the flow of your human experience into time zones or time categories .	從時間角度來研究 , 針對個人 , 我們所有人 , 將你人類經驗的流動 , 分成時間區域或時間類別 。
and you do it automatically and nonconsciously .	而且你會自動和無意識地做 。
they vary between cultures , between nations , between individuals , between social classes , between education levels .	文化、國家、個人、社會階級 , 教育程度都不同 。
and the problem is that they can become biased , because you learn to overuse some of them and underuse the others .	問題是 , 它們會變得偏頗 , 因為你學會了多用點、少用點 「 別人 」 。
what determines any decision you make ?	是什麼決定了你做了什麼決定 ?
you make a decision on which you're going to base an action .	你要決定哪些事會讓你採取行動 。
for some people it's only about what is in the immediate situation , what other people are doing and what you're feeling .	對某些人來說 , 只有在當下情況下 , 其他人在做什麼以及你感受到了什麼 。
and those people , when they make their decisions in that format we're going to call them " presentoriented , " because their focus is what is now .	那些人 , 當他們在那種格式中做決策時 , 我們會稱他們為 「 正當性 」 , 因為他們專注在當下 。
for others , the present is irrelevant .	對其他人來說 , 現在並不重要 。
it's always about " what is this situation like that i've experienced in the past ? "	總是要說: 「 我過去的經歷是怎樣的情況 ? 」
so that their decisions are based on past memories .	所以他們的決定基於過去的記憶 。
and we're going to call those people " pastoriented , " because they focus on what was .	我們要稱這些人為 「 過去式 」 , 因為他們把焦點放在什麼上面 。
for others it's not the past , it's not the present , it's only about the future .	對其他人來說 , 這不是過去 , 也不是現在 , 只關乎未來 。
their focus is always about anticipated consequences .	他們的焦點總是關於期待的結果 。
we're going to call them " futureoriented . " their focus is on what will be .	我們要稱他們為 「 未來導向 」 。 他們的重點在於將來會變成什麼 。
so , time paradox , i want to argue , the paradox of time perspective , is something that influences every decision you make , you're totally unaware of .	所以 , 時間悖論 , 我想說 , 時間觀點的悖論是會影響你所做的每一個決定 , 你是完全沒有意識到的 。
namely , the extent to which you have one of these biased time perspectives .	換句話說 , 你的視角是有偏見的 。
well there is actually six of them . there are two ways to be presentoriented .	嗯 , 其實有六種 。 有兩種方式可以用 。
there is two ways to be pastoriented , two ways to be future .	有兩種方式可以放牧 , 兩種方式可以是未來 。
you can focus on pastpositive , or pastnegative .	你可以注重 " 正面懷舊 " 或 " 負面懷舊 "
you can be presenthedonistic , namely you focus on the joys of life , or presentfatalist it doesn't matter , your life is controlled .	你可以是 " 享受主義者 " , 也就是專注於生活的喜悅 , 或是現在的主義者--這並不重要 , 你的生活是受控制的 。
you can be futureoriented , setting goals .	你可以是 「 未來 」 、 「 設定目標 」 。
or you can be transcendental future: namely , life begins after death .	或者你也可以是超然的未來:也就是說 , 生命是從死後開始的
developing the mental flexibility to shift time perspectives fluidly depending on the demands of the situation , that's what you've got to learn to do .	發展思維的靈活性 , 以流暢的角度看待時間觀點依據局勢的要求 , 那才是你要學會做的 。
so , very quickly , what is the optimal time profile ?	很快地 , 最好的時間檔案是什麼 ?
high on pastpositive . moderately high on future .	高度 " 正面懷舊 " 、適度未來的高度 。
and moderate on presenthedonism .	以及調節現有主義 。
and always low on pastnegative and presentfatalism .	永遠放低 " 負面懷舊 " 和 " 現世主義 "
so the optimal temporal mix is what you get from the past pastpositive gives you roots . you connect your family , identity and your self .	所以最好的臨時混合就是你從過去積極正面帶給你的根源 。 你連結你的家人、身份和你的自我 。
what you get from the future is wings to soar to new destinations , new challenges .	未來你會得到的 , 是翅膀要能翱翔到新的目的地 , 新的挑戰 。
what you get from the present hedonism is the energy , the energy to explore yourself , places , people , sensuality .	從現在的享樂主義得到的就是能量 , 能量去探索自己 , 地方 , 人 , 感性 。
any time perspective in excess has more negatives than positives .	比起正面的觀點 , 任何時間點 , 都比正面的觀點更多 。
what do futures sacrifice for success ?	未來要犧牲什麼才能成功 ?
they sacrifice family time . they sacrifice friend time .	犧牲家庭時間、犧牲朋友時間、
they sacrifice fun time . they sacrifice personal indulgence .	犧牲快樂的時間 , 犧牲個人的安慰
they sacrifice hobbies . and they sacrifice sleep . so it affects their health .	他們犧牲了嗜好 。 犧牲了睡眠 。 所以這會影響他們的健康 。
and they live for work , achievement and control .	並且為了工作、成就和控制生活
i'm sure that resonates with some of the tedsters .	我敢肯定 , 和一些ted人有所共鳴 。
and it resonated for me . i grew up as a poor kid in the south bronx ghetto , a sicilian family everyone lived in the past and present .	讓我有所共鳴 。 我在南布朗克斯區貧窮的孩子長大 , 一個西西里島家庭--所有人都生活在過去和現在 。
i'm here as a futureoriented person who went over the top , who did all these sacrifices because teachers intervened , and made me future oriented .	我來這裡是一位未來帶領我前進的頂尖人士 , 他們做了這些犧牲 , 因為老師介入了 , 讓我有了未來的方向 。
told me don't eat that marshmallow , because if you wait you're going to get two of them , until i learned to balance out .	告訴我不要吃那顆棉花糖 , 因為如果你等著你拿到其中兩個 , 直到我學會了平衡 。
i've added presenthedonism , i've added a focus on the pastpositive , so , at 76 years old , i am more energetic than ever , more productive , and i'm happier than i have ever been .	我加上現在的享樂主義 , 加上過往積極的關注 , 所以 , 在76歲 , 我比以往更有活力 , 更有生產力 , 我比以往更快樂 。
i just want to say that we are applying this to many world problems: changing the dropout rates of school kids , combating addictions , enhancing teen health , curing vets' ptsd with time metaphors getting miracle cures promoting sustainability and conservation , reducing physical rehabilitation where there is a 50percent drop out rate , altering appeals to suicidal terrorists , and modifying family conflicts as timezone clashes .	我只是想說 , 我們正把這個方法用在許多世界問題上:改變校園輟學率、結合毒癮、增強青少年健康、利用時間隱喻法治癒退伍軍人的創傷後壓力症候群 , 用時間隱喻法治療奇蹟──促進可持續性和保育 , 減低身體復原率 , 讓有50%退休金 , 改變自殺式恐怖份子的訴求 , 以及修正家庭衝突的時間區 。
so i want to end by saying: many of life's puzzles can be solved by understanding your time perspective and that of others .	最後我想說 , 生活中的許多謎題都可以藉由了解你的時間角度和其他人的時間角度來解決 。
and the idea is so simple , so obvious , but i think the consequences are really profound .	這個想法很簡單 , 顯而易見 , 但我認為後果真的很深遠 。
how many of today's headlines will matter in 100 years ? 1000 ? kirk citron's " long news " project collects stories that not only matter today , but will resonate for decades even centuries to come . at ted2010 , he highlights recent headlines with the potential to shape our future .	百年後 , 有多少頭條會很重要 ? 1000年後 ? kirkcitron的《長期新聞》專案計畫收集不但在今日 , 甚至數十年後才會引起共鳴 。 在ted2010 , 他強調的是近期的頭條標題 , 有著塑造我們未來的潛力 。
future , global issues , media , news , science	未來 , 全球議題、媒體、新聞、科學 。
kirk citron: and now , the real news	kirkcitron:而現在 , 真正的新聞是
we are drowning in news .	我們淹沒在新聞裡 。
reuters alone puts out three and a half million news stories a year .	單是路透社一家一年就發佈350萬則新聞
that's just one source .	那只是其中一個來源 。
my question is: how many of those stories are actually going to matter in the long run ?	我的問題是:長期來看 , 那些故事有多少變得很重要 ?
that's the idea behind the long news .	這就是 「 長遠新聞 」 背後的想法 。
it's a project by the long now foundation , which was founded by tedsters including kevin kelly and stewart brand .	這是長久以來基金會的計畫 , 由tedsters所創立 , 包括凱文凱文凱利和史都華布蘭德 。
and what we're looking for is news stories that might still matter 50 or 100 or 10 , 000 years from now .	我們在尋找的 , 是那些在50、100 , 000或10 , 000年後仍然很重要的新聞故事 。
and when you look at the news through that filter , a lot falls by the wayside .	當你透過過濾器看新聞時 , 很多地方會倒下來 。
to take the top stories from the a . p . this last year , is this going to matter in a decade ?	去年 , 從a.p.這頂尖的故事中 , 這在十年內會很重要嗎 ?
is this going to matter in 50 or 100 years ?	這在50或100年後會很重要嗎 ?
okay , that was kind of cool .	好吧 , 那有點酷 。
but the top story of this past year was the economy , and i'm just betting that , sooner or later , this particular recession is going to be old news .	但過去一年裡最頂尖的故事就是經濟 , 我只是打賭 , 遲早 , 這種經濟衰退 , 將會是老消息 。
so , what kind of stories might make a difference for the future ?	所以 , 什麼樣的故事可以為未來帶來改變 ?
well , let's take science .	嗯 , 我們拿科學來說吧 。
someday , little robots will go through our bloodstreams fixing things .	有一天 , 小機器人會經過我們的血液中 , 去修理東西 。
that someday is already here if you're a mouse .	如果你是一隻老鼠的話 , 有一天你就已經在這裡了 。
some recent stories: nanobees zap tumors with real bee venom ; they're sending genes into the brain ; a robot they built that can crawl through the human body .	一些最近的故事:奈米蜜蜂用真蜂毒液來打zap腫瘤 ; 它們將基因送入大腦 , 一個他們建造的機器人 , 能在人體上爬行 。
what about resources ? how are we going to feed nine billion people ?	資源方面呢 ? 我們要如何餵飽90億人口 ?
we're having trouble feeding six billion today .	今天我們餵養六十億人是很困難的 。
as we heard yesterday , there's over a billion people hungry .	正如我們昨天聽到的 , 有超過10億人在挨餓 。
britain will starve without genetically modified crops .	英國如果沒有基因改造的作物 , 就會餓死 。
bill gates , fortunately , has bet a billion on [agricultural] research .	幸運的是 , 比爾蓋茲有10億人在農業研究上 。
what about global politics ?	全球政治呢 ?
the world's going to be very different when and if china sets the agenda , and they may .	世界會變得非常不同 , 如果中國設定了議程 , 他們也可能 。
they've overtaken the u . s . as the world's biggest car market , they've overtaken germany as the largest exporter , and they've started doing dna tests on kids to choose their careers .	他們已經超過美國成為世界上最大的汽車市場 , 他們已經超過德國成為最大的出口國 , 他們已經開始在孩子上做dna測試 , 來選擇他們的事業 。
we're finding all kinds of ways to push back the limits of what we know .	我們找到各種方法 , 把我們所知的極限往回推 。
some recent discoveries: there's an ant colony from argentina that has now spread to every continent but antarctica ; there's a selfdirected robot scientist that's made a discovery soon , science may no longer need us , and life may no longer need us either ; a microbe wakes up after 120 , 000 years .	一些最近的發現:阿根廷有一個蟻群 , 現在已經傳播到各大洲 , 但南極洲 , 有個自我導向的機器人科學家 , 很快就有了新的發現 , 科學可能不再需要我們了 , 生命也可能不再需要我們了 ; 一個微生物在120 , 000年被喚醒了 。
it seems that with or without us , life will go on .	看來與否 , 生命會延續下去 。
but my pick for the top long news story of this past year was this one: water found on the moon .	但在過去一年 , 我選擇了一則長篇新聞 , 內容是這一個:水是在月球上發現的 。
makes it a lot easier to put a colony up there .	讓殖民地更容易放到上面 。
and if nasa doesn't do it , china might , or somebody in this room might write a big check .	如果nasa不做 , 中國可能會 , 或在座的某人可能會寫下很大的支票 。
my point is this: in the long run , some news stories are more important than others .	我的重點是:長遠來看 , 某些新聞故事比其他新聞更重要 。
planetary scientist carolyn porco shows images from the cassini voyage to saturn , focusing on its largest moon , titan , and on frozen enceladus , which seems to shoot jets of ice .	行星科學家carolynporco展示的圖片 , 從卡西尼航行到土星 , 著重在它最大的衛星 , 土衛六上 , 以及冰凍的土衛六上 , 似乎是對冰的噴射機造成很大的影響 。
nasa , design , exploration , science , space , technology , universe , visualizations	美國太空總署、設計、探索、科學、太空、科技、宇宙、視覺化呈現 。
carolyn porco flies us to saturn	carolynporco讓我們飛到土星去
in the next 18 minutes , i'm going to take you on a journey .	在接下來的18分鐘裡 , 我要帶大家踏上一段旅程 。
and it's a journey that you and i have been on for many years now , and it began some 50 years ago , when humans first stepped off our planet .	你和我已經踏上這趟旅程很多年了 , 50年前 , 人類第一次踏出我們的星球 。
