and in those 50 years , not only did we literally , physically set foot on the moon , but we have dispatched robotic spacecraft to all the planets all eight of them and we have landed on asteroids , we have rendezvoused with comets , and , at this point in time , we have a spacecraft on its way to pluto , the body formerly known as a planet .	在這50年裡 , 我們不僅真的登上了月球 , 還把機器人的太空船發射到所有星球去 , 其中有八顆行星 , 我們在小行星上登陸 , 我們還與彗星有著緊密的距離 , 此時 , 我們有一架太空飛行器正在往冥王星的方向去 , 屍體被稱為行星 。
and all of these robotic missions are part of a bigger human journey: a voyage to understand something , to get a sense of our cosmic place , to understand something of our origins , and how earth , our planet , and we , living on it , came to be .	這些機械任務都是人類更大旅程的一部分:一趟航程 , 去了解一些事情 , 去了解我們的宇宙 , 去了解我們的本源 , 以及地球 , 我們居住的地球 , 都變成這樣 。
and of all the places in the solar system that we might go to and search for answers to questions like this , there's saturn . and we have been to saturn before we visited saturn in the early 1980s but our investigations of saturn have become far more indepth in detail since the cassini spacecraft , traveling across interplanetary space for seven years , glided into orbit around saturn in the summer of 2004 , and became at that point the farthest robotic outpost that humanity had ever established around the sun .	在太陽系的所有地方 , 我們也許會去搜索像這樣的問題 , 這是土星 。 我們曾經到過土星 。 1980年代早期我們探訪過土星 。 但是我們對土星的調查 , 自從卡西尼號太空船的研究 , 跨越行星際空間的旅行 , 在2004年夏天橫越過土星軌道 , 成為人類最遠的機器人出口 。
now , the saturn system is a rich planetary system .	現在 , 土星系統是豐富的行星系統 。
it offers mystery , scientific insight and obviously splendor beyond compare , and the investigation of this system has enormous cosmic reach .	它提供了神秘、科學的洞見 , 以及明顯超越了對比的魅力 , 而這個系統的調查有著巨大的宇宙成就 。
in fact , just studying the rings alone , we stand to learn a lot about the discs of stars and gas that we call the spiral galaxies .	事實上 , 光是研究光環 , 我們就能學到很多關於恆星和氣體的圓盤 , 我們稱之為 「 螺旋星系 」 。
and here's a beautiful picture of the andromeda nebula , which is our closest , largest spiral galaxy to the milky way .	這張美麗的照片是andromeda星雲 , 這是我們與銀河系最接近、最大的螺旋狀星系 。
and then , here's a beautiful composite of the whirlpool galaxy , taken by the hubble space telescope .	這裡有個旋渦星系的美麗成分 , 由哈伯太空望遠鏡所拍攝 。
so the journey back to saturn is really part of and is also a metaphor for a much larger human voyage to understand the interconnectedness of everything around us , and also how humans fit into that picture .	所以 , 返回土星的旅程 , 其實也是一個比喻 , 比喻了更大的人類旅程 , 去了解我們身邊所有事物的相互關聯性 , 和人類如何融入那個畫面 。
and it pains me that i can't tell you all that we have learned with cassini .	我很痛苦 , 我無法告訴你們我們用卡西尼號學到的 。
i can't show you all the beautiful pictures that we've taken in the last two and a half years , because i simply don't have the time .	我沒辦法給你們看我們過去兩年半所拍攝的所有美麗圖片 , 因為我根本沒有時間 。
so i'm going to concentrate on two of the most exciting stories that have emerged out of this major exploratory expedition that we are conducting around saturn , and have been for the past two and a half years .	所以我將重點放在其中兩個最令人興奮的故事 , 在這次重大探索之旅中 , 我們正在土星周邊進行 , 並且已經進行了兩年半的探險 。
saturn is accompanied by a very large and diverse collection of moons .	伴隨著土星龐大而多樣化的登月計畫 。
they range in size from a few kilometers across to as big across as the u . s .	它們的大小範圍從幾公里大 , 到美國整體 。
most of the beautiful pictures we've taken of saturn , in fact , show saturn in accompaniment with some of its moons . here's saturn with dione , and then , here's saturn showing the rings edgeon , showing you just how vertically thin they are , with the moon enceladus .	大部分我們拍攝的土星美麗圖片事實上是土星與它的衛星伴隨的景象這裡是土星和土星 , 土星和土星和土星和土星的表面這裡是土星的光環帶它向我們展示了它們的環狀切面光環 , 它們有多薄 , 多麼有著月球的厚度
now , two of the 47 moons that saturn has are standouts .	現在土星47顆衛星中有兩顆是固定的 ,
and those are titan and enceladus . titan is saturn's largest moon , and , until cassini had arrived there , was the largest single expanse of unexplored terrain that we had remaining in our solar system .	這些土衛六和土衛二 。 土衛六是土星最大的衛星 , 直到卡西尼號到達之前 , 它是我們太陽系中最大的一個尚未被探索的地形 。
and it is a body that has long intrigued people who've watched the planets .	這個身體長期以來一直引人入勝的行星都被監視著 。
it has a very large , thick atmosphere , and in fact , its surface environment was believed to be more like the environment we have here on the earth , or at least had in the past , than any other body in the solar system .	它有很大、很厚的大氣層 , 事實上 , 它的地表環境被認為比較像是我們在地球上所存在的環境 , 至少過去是那樣 , 比起太陽系裡的其他天體 。
its atmosphere is largely molecular nitrogen , like you are breathing here in this room , except that its atmosphere is suffused with simple organic materials like methane and propane and ethane .	它的大氣層主要是分子氮 , 就像在座各位所呼吸的 , 只不過它的大氣層充斥著簡單的有機物質 , 如甲烷、丙烷和乙烷 。
and these molecules high up in the atmosphere of titan get broken down , and their products join together to make haze particles .	而這些分子高於土衛六的大氣層 , 會被分解 , 他們的產品會加入一起製造霧狀顆粒 。
this haze is ubiquitous . it's completely global and enveloping titan .	這個霧狀物無處不在 , 它完全是全球化的 , 包圍著土衛六 。
and that's why you cannot see down to the surface with our eyes in the visible region of the spectrum .	那就是為什麼你無法用肉眼看到的光譜來看見表面 。
but these haze particles , it was surmised , before we got there with cassini , over billions and billions of years , gently drifted down to the surface and coated the surface in a thick organic sludge .	但這些霧狀顆粒 , 它在我們和卡西尼一起到達卡西尼號之前 , 被保存了數十億年 , 溫和地表溫和地表 , 覆蓋著厚厚有機泥土的表面 。
so like the equivalent , the titan equivalent , of tar , or oil , or what we didn't know what .	就像泰坦上的焦油或石油 , 或我們不知道的一樣 。
but this is what we suspected . and these molecules , especially methane and ethane , can be liquids at the surface temperatures of titan .	但這是我們懷疑的 。 而這些分子 , 尤其是甲烷和乙烷 , 可以是土衛六地表溫度的液體 。
and so it turns out that methane is to titan what water is to the earth .	結果發現 , 甲烷是要讓土衛六到地球 。
it's a condensable in the atmosphere , and so recognizing this circumstance brought to the fore a whole world of bizarre possibilities . you can have methane clouds , ok , and above those clouds , you have this hundreds of kilometers of haze , which prevent any sunlight from getting to the surface .	它在大氣中是會冷凝的 , 所以 , 認知到這種情況 , 會帶來一整個怪異的可能性 。 你可以有甲烷雲 , 在這些雲之上 , 你可以有數百公里的霧狀物 , 阻止任何陽光無法到達地表 。
the temperature at the surface is some 350 degrees below zero fahrenheit .	地表的溫度是華氏零下350度 。
but despite that cold , you could have rain falling down on the surface of titan .	儘管有那樣的寒冷 , 土衛六上還是有可能會下雨 。
and doing on titan what rain does on the earth: it carves gullies ; it forms rivers and cataracts ; it can create canyons ; it can pool in large basins and craters .	在土衛六上下的雨水像土衛六地一樣 , 它會雕刻地殼 , 形成河流和白漿 ; 它能創造出峽谷 ; 它能在大盆地和隕石坑中游泳 。
it can wash the sludge off high mountain peaks and hills , down into the lowlands . so stop and think for a minute .	它可以把泥漿清洗掉高山丘 , 往下沖進低地帶 。 所以停下來思考一下 。
try to imagine what the surface of titan might look like .	試著想像土衛六的表面長什麼樣子
it's dark . high noon on titan is as dark as deep earth twilight on the earth .	那裡一片漆黑 。 中午 , 土衛六上的黑暗與地球上一片漆黑一樣 。
it's cold , it's eerie , it's misty , it might be raining , and you might be standing on the shores of lake michigan brimming with paint thinner .	那裡很冷 , 很邪惡 , 很嚴重 , 可能會下雨 , 你可能會站在密歇根湖岸邊 , 用油漆布林納 。
that is the view that we had of the surface of titan before we got there with cassini , and i can tell you that what we have found on titan , though it is not the same in detail , is every bit as fascinating as that story is .	這是我們在卡西尼號到達土衛六之前的表面 , 我可以告訴各位 , 我們在土衛六上所發現的 , 雖然在細節上並不相同 , 但故事是如此地吸引人 。
and for us , it has been like the cassini people it has been like a jules verne adventure come true .	對我們來說 , 卡西尼號的居民就像是叢林裡的凡爾納旅行 。
as i said , it has a thick , extensive atmosphere .	就像我說的 , 它有很厚、很廣的大氣層 。
this is a picture of titan , backlit by the sun , with the rings as a beautiful backdrop .	這是土衛六的照片 , 太陽照後照的 , 光環是很漂亮的背景 。
and yet another moon there i don't even know which one it is . it's a very extensive atmosphere .	然而 , 另一個月球--我甚至不知道它是哪一個 , 它是一個非常廣泛的大氣層 。
we have instruments on cassini which can see down to the surface through this atmosphere , and my camera system is one of them .	我們在卡西尼號上有儀器可以透過大氣層看到表面 , 我的相機系統就是其中之一 。
and we have taken pictures like this .	我們拍了像這樣的照片 。
and what you see is bright and dark regions , and that's about as far as it got for us .	你所看到的是明亮、黑暗的區域 , 對我們來說 , 差不多到這一步了 。
it was so mystifying: we couldn't make out what we were seeing on titan .	這實在是太神秘了:我們無法在土衛六上看到的景象 。
when you look closer at this region , you start to see things like sinuous channels we didn't know . you see a few round things .	當你更近一點看這個區域 , 你會開始看到像席間的通道──我們不知道 。 你看到的是一些圓形的東西 。
this , we later found out , is , in fact , a crater , but there are very few craters on the surface of titan , meaning it's a very young surface .	這個 , 我們後來發現 , 事實上是個隕石坑 , 但土衛六表面的隕石坑數量很少 , 意思是說 , 它是個很年輕的表面 。
and there are features that look tectonic .	並且有著看起來板塊的特徵 。
they look like they've been pulled apart .	它們看起來好像被分開了 。
whenever you see anything linear on a planet , it means there's been a fracture , like a fault .	每當你看到一個星球上有線形的物體 , 就代表有一個斷裂 , 像個斷層一樣 。
and so it's been tectonically altered .	由於它的地殼變化 ,
but we couldn't make sense of our images , until , six months after we got into orbit , an event occurred that many have regarded as the highlight of cassini's investigation of titan .	但我們無法理解我們的影像 , 直到我們進入軌道六個月後 , 一件重大事件發生了 , 許多人都認為卡西尼探測土衛六的重要事件 。
and that was the deployment of the huygens probe , the europeanbuilt huygens probe that cassini had carried for seven years across the solar system . we deployed it to the atmosphere of titan , it took two and a half hours to descend , and it landed on the surface .	那就是惠更斯號探測器的部署 , 歐洲建造的惠更斯號探測器 , 卡西尼號在整個太陽系共有七年 。 我們把它部署到土衛六的大氣 , 花了兩個半小時才降落 , 降落在地表上 。
and i just want to emphasize how significant an event this is .	我只是想強調一下這個事件有多重大 。
this is a device of human making , and it landed in the outer solar system for the first time in human history .	這是人類製造的裝置 , 它在外太陽系登陸 , 這是人類歷史上第一次 。
it is so significant that , in my mind , this was an event that should have been celebrated with ticker tape parades in every city across the u . s . and europe , and sadly , that wasn't the case .	這件事意義重大 , 以致於在我心目中 , 這個活動本來就該與美國各個城市的搔癢帶遊行和遊行 , 可悲的是 , 事實並非如此 。
it was significant for another reason . this is an international mission , and this event was celebrated in europe , in germany , and the celebratory presentations were given in english accents , and american accents , and german accents , and french and italian and dutch accents .	這是另一個原因 。 這是個國際的任務 。 這個活動在歐洲、德國都被讚頌 , 而慶祝的演說則是用英語的口音 , 美國的口音 , 德語的口音 , 德語的口音 , 法語、意大利語和荷蘭口音 。
it was a moving demonstration of what the words " united nations " are supposed to mean: a true union of nations joined together in a colossal effort for good .	這是一場關於 「 聯合國 」 一詞的動人展示 , 應該是這個字的意思:一個真正的國度團結在一起 , 一起為美好而努力 。
and , in this case , it was a massive undertaking to explore a planet , and to come to understand a planetary system that , for all of human history , had been unreachable , and now humans had actually touched it .	在這個案例中 , 探索一個行星是一個巨大的任務 。 去理解一個行星系統 , 這個行星在人類歷史上 , 一直是無法理解的 , 而現在人類真的碰觸到了它 。
so it was i mean , i'm getting goose bumps just talking about it .	所以 , 我是說 , 我開始起雞皮疙瘩的話題 。
it was a tremendously emotional event , and it's something that i will personally never forget , and you shouldn't either .	那是個極度情緒化的事件 , 也是我個人永遠不會忘記的事 , 你也不應該如此 。
but anyway , the probe took measurements of the atmosphere on the way down , and it also took panoramic pictures .	但不管怎樣 , 探測器在降下過程中對大氣進行了測量 , 也拍了全景圖 。
and i can't tell you what it was like to see the first pictures of titan's surface from the probe . and this is what we saw .	我無法告訴你第一次看到土衛六地表的照片是什麼樣子 。 這是我們所看到的景象 。
and it was a shocker , because it was everything we wanted those other pictures taken from orbit to be .	這真是令人震驚 , 因為我們希望從軌道上拍攝的其他照片也是 。
it was an unambiguous pattern , a geological pattern .	那是個很明顯的模式 , 地質的模式 。
it's a dendritic drainage pattern that can be formed only by the flow of liquids .	這是一種只靠液體流動而形成的水滴圖案 。
and you can follow these channels and you can see how they all converge .	你可以沿著這些溝渠找到它們的匯合點 。
and they converge into this channel here , which drains into this region .	它們匯合到這條通道 , 排放到這個區域 。
you are looking at a shoreline .	你現在看到的是一條海岸線 ,
was this a shoreline of fluids ? we didn't know .	這是液體的海岸線嗎 ? 我們不知道 。
but this is somewhat of a shoreline .	但這有點像海岸線 。
this picture is taken at 16 kilometers .	這張照片拍攝於16公里
this is the picture taken at eight kilometers , ok ? again , the shoreline .	這是在八公里的高度所拍攝的 , 好嗎 ? 再一次 , 海岸線 。
okay , now , 16 kilometers , eight kilometers this is roughly an airline altitude .	好 , 現在 , 16公里 , 8公里--這大約是航空公司的飛行高度 。
if you were going to take an airplane trip across the u . s . , you would be flying at these altitudes .	如果你要搭飛機橫跨美國 , 你一定會飛到這些高度 。
so , this is the picture you would have at the window of titanian airlines as you fly across the surface of titan .	這張照片是鐵達尼亞航空公司穿越土星表面時 , 你會看到的景象 。
and then finally , the probe came to rest on the surface , and i'm going to show you , ladies and gentlemen , the first picture ever taken from the surface of a moon in the outer solar system .	最後 , 探測器得以在表面上休息 , 我要向各位展示 , 各位先生女士 , 第一張從外太陽系的月球表面拍攝的照片 。
and here is the horizon , ok ?	這裡是地平線 , 好嗎 ?
these are probably water ice pebbles , yes ?	這些很可能是冰鵝卵石 , 對吧 ?
and obviously , it landed in one of these flat , dark regions and it didn't sink out of sight . so it wasn't fluid that we landed in .	很明顯地 , 它落在了其中一個平坦、深色的區域 , 且它沒有沉沒在視線之下 。 所以 , 它不是我們落入的液體 。
what the probe came down in was basically the titan equivalent of a mud flat .	基本上 , 探測器被探測到的就是土衛六相當於一座泥土平原 。
this is an unconsolidated ground that is suffused with liquid methane .	這是個無鞏固的地帶 , 充滿了液態甲烷 。
and it's probably the case that this material has washed off the highlands of titan through these channels that we saw , and has drained over billions of years to fill in lowlying basins .	很可能這材料是用我們看到的這些通道洗掉土衛六上的高地 , 排放了數十億年 , 來填補低窪地帶的盆地 。
and that is what the huygens probe landed in .	這就是惠更斯號探測器著陸的地方 。
but still , there was no sign in our images , or even in the huygens' images , of any large , open bodies of fluids .	但 , 我們的影像仍然是惠更斯號圖像中沒有任何大型、開放的液體 。
where were they ? it got even more puzzling when we found dunes .	他們在哪裡 ? 當我們發現沙丘時 , 這個問題變得更加令人困惑 。
ok , so this is our movie of the equatorial region of titan , showing these dunes . these are dunes that are 100 meters tall , separated by a few kilometers , and they go on for miles and miles and miles .	好 , 這是我們關於土衛六赤道的電影 。 這些沙丘是100公尺高的 , 被幾公里高的沙丘隔絕 , 會持續好幾英里 。
there's hundreds , up to a 1 , 000 or 1 , 200 miles of dunes .	有幾百、一千或一千兩百英里的沙丘 。
this is the saharan desert of titan .	這是土衛六的撒哈拉沙漠 。
it's obviously a place which is very dry , or you wouldn't get dunes .	這顯然是一個非常乾燥的地方 , 或者你不會有沙丘 。
so again , it got puzzling that there were no bodies of fluid , until finally , we saw lakes in the polar regions .	所以 , 再一次 , 牠讓人不禁疑惑 , 沒有體液 , 直到最後 , 我們看到了極地的湖泊 。
and there is a lake scene in the south polar region of titan .	這是土衛六南極的一個湖 。
it's about the size of lake ontario .	大小和安大略湖差不多 。
and then , only a week and a half ago , we flew over the north pole of titan and found , again , we found a feature here the size of the caspian sea .	接著 , 一個半星期前 , 我們飛過了土衛六的北極 , 再次發現 , 這裡有著和卡薩皮亞海一樣大的特徵 。
so it seems that the liquids , for some reason we don't understand , or during at least this season , are apparently at the poles of titan .	所以 , 似乎液體 , 為了某些我們不了解的原因 , 或至少這個季節 , 很明顯地 , 土衛六上的兩極 。
and i think you would agree that we have found titan is a remarkable , mystical place . it's exotic , it's alien , but yet strangely earthlike , and having earthlike geological formations and a tremendous geographical diversity , and is a fascinating world whose only rival in the solar system for complexity and richness is the earth itself .	我想你們應該會同意 , 我們發現土衛六是一個不可思議的神秘地方 。 它很奇特 , 它是外星人 , 但又和地球很相似 , 而且有著像地球般的地質多樣性 , 和一個巨大的地質多樣性 , 而且是個令人著迷的世界 , 它只能在太陽系中與太陽系相對應的複雜性和豐富性 , 就是地球本身 。
and so now we go onto enceladus . enceladus is a small moon , it's about a tenth the size of titan . and you can see it here next to england , just to show you the size . this is not meant to be a threat .	所以現在我們到土衛二看看 。 土衛二是一個小衛星 , 大小大約是土衛六的十分之一 。 你可以看到它在英格蘭旁邊 , 只是為了展示它的大小 。 這不是一個威脅 。
and enceladus is very white , it's very bright , and its surface is obviously wrecked with fractures .	而土衛二是非常白的 , 非常耀眼 , 它的表面很明顯是有裂痕的 。
it is a very geologically active body .	它是個非常地質活動的身體 。
but the mother lode of discoveries on enceladus was found at the south pole and we're looking at the south pole here where we found this system of fractures .	但在土衛二上的發現大多出現在南極 , 我們現在看到的是南極 , 我們發現了地形骨折 。
and they're a different color because they're a different composition .	它們的顏色不同 , 是因為它們的構成不同 。
they are coated . these fractures are coated with organic materials .	它們被塗滿 。 這些碎片被有機物質包裹著 。
moreover , this whole , entire region , the south polar region , has elevated temperatures . it's the hottest place on the planet , on the body .	此外 , 這整個南極區域的整體溫度也上升了 。 這是地球上最熱的地方 , 在身體上 。
that's as bizarre as finding that the antarctic on the earth is hotter than the tropics .	這就如同發現地球南極洲比熱帶地區還熱帶地區一樣奇怪 。
and then , when we took additional pictures , we discovered that from these fractures are issuing jets of fine , icy particles extending hundreds of miles into space .	接著 , 當我們拍攝了額外的照片 , 我們發現 , 從這些裂縫產生出來的噴射流束 , 冰柱粒會延伸數百英里 , 進入太空 。
and when we colorcode this image , to bring out the faint light levels , we see that these jets feed a plume that , in fact , we see , in other images , goes thousands of miles into the space above enceladus .	當我們將圖片上色 , 以產生微弱光線 , 我們可以看到 , 這些噴流在螢幕上方 , 事實上 , 我們看到 , 在其他的圖片 , 會在土衛六上方數千英里的空間裡 , 進入土衛二 。
my team and i have examined images like this , and like this one , and have thought about the other results from cassini .	我和我的團隊針對圖片做過測試 , 就像這張圖片 , 考慮到來自卡西尼號的另一個結果 。
and we have arrived at the conclusion that these jets may be erupting from pockets of liquid water under the surface of enceladus .	我們得到的結論是 , 這些噴射流在土衛二表面下的液態水可能噴發著液態水 。
so we have , possibly , liquid water , organic materials and excess heat .	所以我們有的 , 可能是液態水 , 有機物質和過剩的熱 。
in other words , we have possibly stumbled upon the holy grail of modern day planetary exploration , or in other words , an environment that is potentially suitable for living organisms .	換句話說 , 我們很可能偶然發現了現代行星探索的聖杯 , 換句話說 , 一個適合生物生存的環境 。
and i don't think i need to tell you that the discovery of life elsewhere in our solar system , whether it be on enceladus or elsewhere , would have enormous cultural and scientific implications .	我不認為我需要告訴你們 , 我們太陽系中其他地方生物的發現 , 不論是在土衛二或其它地方 , 都會有巨大的文化和科學上的影響 。
because if we could demonstrate that genesis had occurred not once , but twice , independently , in our solar system , then that means , by inference , it has occurred a staggering number of times throughout the universe and its 13 . 7 billion year history .	因為如果我們能證明 , 創意已經發生不止一次 , 而是兩次 , 在我們的太陽系中 , 那就表示 , 根據我們的推論 , 它在整個宇宙和它137億年的歷史中 , 已經出現了很驚人的次數 。
right now , earth is the only planet still that we know is teeming with life .	目前 , 地球仍是唯一一顆充滿生命的星球 。
it is precious , it is unique , it is still , so far , the only home we've ever known .	它很珍貴 , 它很獨特 , 到目前為止 , 它仍然是我們唯一的家 。
and if any of you were alert and coherent during the 1960s and we'd forgive you , if you weren't , ok you would remember this very famous picture taken by the apollo 8 astronauts in 1968 .	如果你們之中有人在1960年代時警覺和連貫我們原諒你們 , 如果不是的話 , 好 , 你會記得這張1968年由阿波羅八號太空人所拍攝的有名的照片 。
it was the first time that earth was imaged from space , and it had an enormous impact on our sense of place in the universe , and our sense of responsibility for the protection of our own planet .	那是第一次從太空拍攝的地球 , 它對於我們在宇宙中的位置產生了巨大的衝擊 , 我們對於保護我們自己星球的責任感 。
well , we on cassini have taken an equivalent first , a picture that no human eye has ever seen before .	我們現在在卡西尼號拍的就等於是一張前所未見的人類眼睛
it is a total eclipse of the sun , seen from the other side of saturn .	這是日全食的日全食 , 從土星的另一側可以看到 。
and in this impossibly beautiful picture , you see the main rings backlit by the sun , you see the refracted image of the sun and you see this ring created , in fact , by the exhalations of enceladus .	在這張無與倫比的照片中 , 你看到背著太陽的主要環狀光環 , 你看到太陽折射後的影像 , 而你看到土衛二的表面 , 事實上是被表明出來的 。
but as if that weren't brilliant enough , we can spot , in this beautiful image , sight of our own planet , cradled in the arms of saturn's rings .	但 , 好像還不夠聰明 , 我們可以發現 , 在這個美麗的圖像中 , 看見我們自己的星球 , 塞在土星環的臂彎中 。
now , there is something deeply moving about seeing ourselves from afar , and capturing the sight of our little , blueocean planet in the skies of other worlds .	看到我們自己深深地感動 , 捕捉我們小小、藍西的星球 , 到其它星球的天空 。
and that , and the perspective of ourselves that we gain from that , may be , in the end , the finest reward that we earn from this journey of discovery that started half a century ago .	而我們自己 , 從中得到的看法 , 可能就是 , 到最後 , 我們從這次探索之旅中得到的最好的奬勵 , 這段旅程始於半個世紀前 。
as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped . this slows the delivery of aid after a disaster and hides the economic potential of unused lands and unknown roads . in this short talk , google's lalitesh katragadda demos map maker , a group mapmaking tool that people around the globe are using to map their world .	直到2005年 , 只有15%的世界已被繪製 。 這會減緩災難後的援助 , 並隱藏無用的土地和未知的道路潛力 。 在這個簡短的演講中 , 谷歌已故的卡特加達加達式的自造者所繪製的地圖 , 一個團體繪製的工具 , 全世界的人都用地圖繪製他們的世界地圖 。
collaboration , design , map , technology	合作、設計、地圖、科技、地圖、
lalitesh katragadda: making maps to fight disaster , build economies	已故的katragada:製作地圖來對抗災難 , 建立經濟體 。
in 2008 , cyclone nargis devastated myanmar .	2008年 , 氣旋納吉斯破壞了緬甸 。
millions of people were in severe need of help .	數百萬人急需協助 。
the u . n . wanted to rush people and supplies to the area .	聯合國想要趕人和供應商前往該地區
but there were no maps , no maps of roads , no maps showing hospitals , no way for help to reach the cyclone victims .	但沒有地圖、沒有道路的地圖、沒有地圖顯示醫院 , 也沒有辦法幫忙達到受難者的地圖 。
when we look at a map of los angeles or london , it is hard to believe that as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped to a geocodable level of detail .	當我們看到洛杉磯或倫敦的地圖時 , 很難相信在2005年 , 世界上只有15%的地區在地理位置上有差異 。
the u . n . ran headfirst into a problem that the majority of the world's populous faces: not having detailed maps .	聯合國在世界大部分的人口面孔上都碰到一個問題:沒有詳盡的地圖 。
but help was coming .	但救援即將來臨 。
at google , 40 volunteers used a new software to map 120 , 000 kilometers of roads , 3 , 000 hospitals , logistics and relief points .	在google , 40位志願者使用了一個新軟體 , 繪製了12萬公里的道路、3000間醫院、後勤和救護站 。
and it took them four days .	而他們花了四天的時間
the new software they used ? google mapmaker .	他們用的新軟體 ? googlemapmaker
google mapmaker is a technology that empowers each of us to map what we know locally .	googlemapmaker是一個能夠賦予我們每個人力量的科技 , 將我們每個人在當地所知的事物繪製在地圖上 。
people have used this software to map everything from roads to rivers , from schools to local businesses , and video stores to the corner store .	人們使用這套軟體來繪製所有東西 , 從道路到河流、從學校到當地企業到當地的商業 , 還有錄影店 , 到角落的商店 。
nobel prize nominee hernando de soto recognized that the key to economic liftoff for most developing countries is to tap the vast amounts of uncapitalized land .	諾貝爾獎提名人hernandodesotto認爲開發中國家要實現經濟效益的關鍵是要調節大量未清除的土地
for example , a trillion dollars of real estate remains uncapitalized in india alone .	比如 , 光在印度 , 一兆美元的房地產仍然不死 。
in the last year alone , thousands of users in 170 countries have mapped millions of pieces of information , and created a map of a level of detail never thought viable .	光是在去年 , 就有170個國家數千個使用者就繪製了數百萬筆資訊 , 創造了一張程度的細節圖 , 從來沒有想過是可行的 。
and this was made possible by the power of passionate users everywhere .	藉由各地熱情的使用者的力量 , 這一切得以實現 。
let's look at some of the maps being created by users right now .	我們來看一些現在使用者製作的地圖 。
so , as we speak , people are mapping the world in these 170 countries .	所以 , 我們在說話的同時 , 在這170個國家裡 , 人們正在對映這個世界 。
you can see bridget in africa who just mapped a road in senegal .	你可以看到在非洲的bridget剛為塞內加爾標註了一條路
and , closer to home , chalua , an n . g . road in bangalore .	還有 , 離家近一點 , chalua , 那是一條在班加羅爾的n.g.路 。
this is the result of computational geometry , gesture recognition , and machine learning .	這是計算幾何學的結果 , 手勢辨識 , 以及機器學習的結果 。
this is a victory of thousands of users , in hundreds of cities , one user , one edit at a time .	這是數百個使用者的勝利 , 在數百個城市中 , 一個使用者 , 一次一個編輯 。
this is an invitation to the 70 percent of our unmapped planet .	這是一個給我們70%未被包覆的星球的邀請 。
welcome to the new world .	歡迎來到新世界 。
in 2003 , the palestinian village of budrus mounted a 10monthlong nonviolent protest to stop a barrier being built across their olive groves . did you hear about it ? didn't think so . brazilian filmmaker julia bacha asks why we only pay attention to violence in the israelpalestine conflict and not to the nonviolent leaders who may one day bring peace .	2003年 , 巴勒斯坦村莊在一場10個月的非暴力抗議活動中 , 阻止一個隔閡被建在他們的橄欖屋上 。 你聽說過嗎 ? 不這樣想 。 巴西製片家族巴西製片家族巴迪亞•巴哈查問我們為何只關注以色列衝突的暴力 , 而不是沒有暴力的領袖有一天會帶來和平 。
arts , communication , compassion , entertainment , film , peace , violence , war	藝術、溝通、同情、娛樂、電影、和平、暴力、戰爭 。
julia bacha: pay attention to nonviolence	朱莉亞•巴查:注意非暴力的發生 。
for the last 8 years , i have dedicated my life to documenting the work of israelis and palestinians who are trying to end the conflict using peaceful means .	過去八年來 , 我致力於記錄以色列人和巴勒斯坦人的工作 , 他們試圖用和平手段來結束衝突 。
when i travel with my work across europe and the united states , one question always comes up: where is the palestinian gandhi ?	當我在歐洲和美國旅行時 , 總有一個問題:巴勒斯坦的甘地在哪裡 ?
why aren't palestinians using nonviolent resistance ?	為什麼巴勒斯坦人不用非暴力的方式抗爭呢 ?
the challenge i face when i hear this question is that often i have just returned from the middle east where i spent my time filming dozens of palestinians who are using nonviolence to defend their lands and water resources from israeli soldiers and settlers .	我在聽到這個問題時所面臨的挑戰 , 通常我才剛從中東回國 , 在那裡我花時間拍攝數十位巴勒斯坦人 , 他們用非暴力的方式來捍衛他們的土地和水資源 , 來自以色列士兵和移民者 。
these leaders are trying to forge a massive national nonviolent movement to end the occupation and build peace in the region .	這些領導人試著著手一項大規模的全國性非暴力運動 , 以終止佔領並在該地區建立和平 。
yet , most of you have probably never heard about them .	但大部分人可能都沒聽說過他們 。
this divide between what's happening on the ground and perceptions abroad is one of the key reasons why we don't have yet a palestinian peaceful resistance movement that has been successful .	這種分歧存在於地面上和國外的認知之間這是我們目前尚未能成功的巴勒斯坦和平抗爭運動的主要原因之一 。
so i'm here today to talk about the power of attention , the power of your attention , and the emergence and development of nonviolent movements in the west bank , gaza and elsewhere but today , my case study is going to be palestine .	所以我今天要來談談關注的力量、關注的力量、以及非暴力運動的出現與發展 , 在西岸、加薩 , 以及其他地方 , 但現今 , 我的案例研究將會是巴勒斯坦 。
i believe that what's mostly missing for nonviolence to grow is not for palestinians to start adopting nonviolence , but for us to start paying attention to those who already are .	我相信 , 成長所缺少的 , 絕大多數是讓巴勒斯坦人開始採用非暴力手段 , 而是讓我們開始注意到那些已經擁有暴力的人 。
allow me to illustrate this point by taking you to this village called budrus .	讓我來說明這一點 , 藉由把你們帶到這個名為布德魯斯的村落 。
about seven years ago , they faced extinction , because israel announced it would build a separation barrier , and part of this barrier would be built on top of the village .	大約七年前 , 他們面臨著滅絕 , 因為以色列宣佈它會建造出隔音屏障 , 部分的障礙會建在村莊上 。
they would lose 40 percent of their land and be surrounded , so they would lose free access to the rest of the west bank .	他們會失去40%的土地 , 並且被包圍著 , 所以他們會失去免費的接觸權利 , 進入到約旦河西岸其他地方 。
through inspired local leadership , they launched a peaceful resistance campaign to stop that from happening .	通過當地的領導 , 他們發起了和平抗爭活動 , 以阻止這發生 。
let me show you some brief clips , so you have a sense for what that actually looked like on the ground .	讓我給你們看一些短片 , 讓你們了解一下 , 那些在地面上看起來是什麼樣子 。
palestinian woman: we were told the wall would separate palestine from israel .	巴勒斯坦女人:我們被告知圍牆會將巴勒斯坦與以色列分隔開來 。
here in budrus , we realized the wall would steal our land .	在布德魯斯 , 我們發現這道牆將竊取我們的土地 。
israeli man: the fence has , in fact , created a solution to terror .	以色列男性:這道圍籬事實上創造了恐懼的解答
man: today you're invited to a peaceful march .	男性:今天你受邀參加和平的遊行 。
you are joined by dozens of your israeli brothers and sisters .	你被數十位你的以色列兄弟姐妹加入 。
israeli activist: nothing scares the army more than nonviolent opposition .	以色列激進份子:軍隊最嚇人的就是非暴力對抗 。
woman: we saw the men trying to push the soldiers , but none of them could do that .	女子:我們看見男人嘗試推開士兵 , 但他們都不可以這樣做 。
but i think the girls could do it .	但我認為女孩們做得到 。
fatah party member: we must empty our minds of traditional thinking .	法塔赫黨員:我們必須空想著傳統思維 。
hamas party member: we were in complete harmony , and we wanted to spread it to all of palestine .	哈馬斯黨員:我們完全和諧了 , 我們想要將它散播到全巴勒斯坦 。
chanting: one united nation .	口號:一個聯合國 。
fatah , hamas and the popular front !	法塔赫、哈馬斯和受歡迎的前面 !
news anchor: the clashes over the fence continue .	主持人:這道籬笆繼續
reporter: israeli border police were sent to disperse the crowd .	記者:以色列邊界警察被派來驅散群眾 。
they were allowed to use any force necessary .	他們被允許使用任何必要的武力
man: these are live bullets .	男人:這些是活彈 。
it's like fallujah . shooting everywhere .	就像在fallujah , 到處拍攝
israeli activist: i was sure we were all going to die .	以色列活躍人士:我很確定我們都會死 。
but there were others around me who weren't even cowering .	但在我身邊還有其他甚至在我心中都不為所欲 。
israeli soldier: a nonviolent protest is not going to stop the [unclear] .	以色列士兵:非暴力抗爭是無法阻止這【不清楚】
protester: this is a peaceful march .	抗議者:這是和平的遊行 。
there is no need to use violence .	不需要使用暴力 。
chanting: we can do it ! we can do it !	口號聲:我們做得到 ! 我們辦得到 !
julia bacha: when i first heard about the story of budrus , i was surprised that the international media had failed to cover the extraordinary set of events that happened seven years ago , in 2003 .	茱莉亞•巴夏:當我第一次聽到布德魯斯的故事時 , 我很驚訝國際媒體竟然沒有報導這一連串不凡的事件 , 發生在2003年 。
what was even more surprising was the fact that budrus was successful .	更令人驚訝的是布德魯斯成功的事實
the residents , after 10 months of peaceful resistance , convinced the israeli government to move the route of the barrier off their lands and to the green line , which is the internationally recognized boundary between israel and the palestinian territories .	居民 , 經過了十個月的和平反抗 , 說服了以色列政府將這道屏障搬離他們的土地 , 移到綠線上 , 也就是國際公認的以色列與巴勒斯坦領土之間的界線 。
the resistance in budrus has since spread to villages across the west bank and to palestinian neighborhoods in jerusalem .	布德鲁斯村的抗爭自此傳遍全約旦河西岸的村子以及耶路撒冷境內巴勒斯坦人居住的街坊
yet the media remains mostly silent on these stories .	然而媒體還是在這些故事裡保持沉默
this silence carries profound consequences for the likelihood that nonviolence can grow , or even survive , in palestine .	這種沉默會帶來很深刻的後果 , 讓非暴力行為能成長的可能性 , 甚至在巴勒斯坦能存活下來 。
violent resistance and nonviolent resistance share one very important thing in common ; they are both a form of theater seeking an audience to their cause .	暴力抗爭和非暴力抗爭都有一個非常重要的共通點 , 他們都是劇場的一種形式 , 尋求觀眾的理由 。
if violent actors are the only ones constantly getting frontpage covers and attracting international attention to the palestinian issue , it becomes very hard for nonviolent leaders to make the case to their communities that civil disobedience is a viable option in addressing their plight .	如果暴力演員是唯一經常上門的演員 , 並吸引國際關注巴勒斯坦的議題 , 對於非暴力領袖來說 , 要向他們的社區提案 , 「 公民不服從 」 是很可行的選項 , 要處理他們的困境 。
the power of attention is probably going to come as no surprise to the parents in the room .	關注的力量可能對在場的父母都不會感到驚訝 。
the surest way to make your child throw increasingly louder tantrums is by giving him attention the first time he throws a fit .	最好的辦法是讓你的小孩大聲丟出 , 讓他有機會注意他第一次丟出一個適當的身影 。
the tantrum will become what childhood psychologists call a functional behavior , since the child has learned that he can get parental attention out of it .	這種螞蟻將成為童年心理學家所謂的功能性行為 , 因為孩子們學到了 , 他可以藉此得到父母親的注意力 。
parents can incentivize or disincentivize behavior simply by giving or withdrawing attention to their children .	父母能透過給予或吸引注意來獎勵或減輕孩子的行為 。
but that's true for adults too .	但對成年人也是如此 。
in fact , the behavior of entire communities and countries can be influenced , depending on where the international community chooses to focus its attention .	事實上 , 整個社區和國家的行為都可能受到影響 , 取決於國際社會選擇聚焦在那裡的地方 。
i believe that at the core of ending the conflict in the middle east and bringing peace is for us to transform nonviolence into a functional behavior by giving a lot more attention to the nonviolent leaders on the ground today .	我相信 , 終結中東地區的衝突的核心 , 為我們將非暴力行為轉化為一個功能性行為 , 藉由讓更多關注在地面上的非暴力領導人 。
in the course of taking my film to villages in the west bank , in gaza and in east jerusalem , i have seen the impact that even one documentary film can have in influencing the transformation .	帶我到約旦河西岸的村子裡 , 在加薩和東耶路撒冷拍攝 , 我見識到就算只是一部紀錄片也能影響到轉型 。
in a village called wallajeh , which sits very close to jerusalem , the community was facing a very similar plight to budrus .	在一個名叫瓦拉杰的村子裡 , 這個村子座落在耶路撒冷附近 , 這個社區正面臨跟布德鲁斯村非常相似的困境 。
they were going to be surrounded , lose a lot of their lands and not have freedom of access , either to the west bank or jerusalem .	他們將被包圍 , 失去許多土地也沒有取得的自由 , 無論是到西岸還是耶路撒冷 。
they had been using nonviolence for about two years but had grown disenchanted since nobody was paying attention .	他們已經使用非暴力手段大約兩年了 , 但他們漸漸放棄了 , 因為沒有人注意他們 。
so we organized a screening .	於是我們組織了一種篩選 。
a week later , they held the most wellattended and disciplined demonstration to date .	一個禮拜後 , 他們舉行了到目前為止最有熱情和紀律的示威 。
the organizers say that the villagers , upon seeing the story of budrus documented in a film , felt that there were indeed people following what they were doing , that people cared .	主辦單位說村民看到布德鲁斯村的故事被記錄在電影中 , 覺得確實有人在追隨他們正在做的事 , 人們在乎 。
so they kept on going .	所以他們繼續前進 。
on the israeli side , there is a new peace movement called solidariot , which means solidarity in hebrew .	在以色列那邊 , 有一項新的和平運動 , 叫做solidariot , 它在希伯來語中表示團結 。
the leaders of this movement have been using budrus as one of their primary recruiting tools .	這項運動的領袖一直在用布德魯斯為他們的主要招募工具之一 。
they report that israelis who had never been active before , upon seeing the film , understand the power of nonviolence and start joining their activities .	他們報告說 , 以色列人從未活躍過 , 在看過影片的時候 , 了解非暴力的力量 , 並開始加入他們的活動 。
the examples of wallajeh and the solidariot movement show that even a smallbudget independent film can play a role in transforming nonviolence into a functional behavior .	瓦拉杰和索里德拉爾特的舉例顯示即便是一部小型的獨立製片也能將非暴力行為轉化為一種功能性行為
now imagine the power that big media players could have if they started covering the weekly nonviolent demonstrations happening in villages like bil'in , ni'lin , wallajeh , in jerusalem neighborhoods like sheikh jarrah and silwan the nonviolent leaders would become more visible , valued and effective in their work .	想像一下 , 大型媒體玩家能夠擁有的力量 , 如果他們開始在村子裡做報導 , 像比爾、尼因拉、瓦拉杰村 , 在耶路撒冷的街坊中 , 如謝赫賈拉和西爾瓦恩 , 非暴力領導人會在他們的作品中變得更有價值、更有效 。
i believe that the most important thing is to understand that if we don't pay attention to these efforts , they are invisible , and it's as if they never happened .	我相信 , 最重要的是要去理解 , 如果我們不去注意這些努力 , 它們是隱形的 , 而且就好像它們從未發生一樣 。
but i have seen first hand that if we do , they will multiply .	但我親眼見到如果我們有 , 他們會相乘 。
if they multiply , their influence will grow in the overall israelipalestinian conflict .	如果他們倍增 , 他們的影響會在以色列以巴衝突中長大 。
and theirs is the kind of influence that can finally unblock the situation .	而他們的影響力就是那種終於可以解開局面的影響力 。
these leaders have proven that nonviolence works in places like budrus .	這些領導人證明了非暴力手段在布德鲁斯村這樣的地方起了作用
let's give them attention so they can prove it works everywhere .	來給他們關注 , 讓他們能夠證明它無所不在 。
simon sinek has a simple but powerful model for inspirational leadership all starting with a golden circle and the question " why ? " his examples include apple , martin luther king , and the wright brothers . . .	西蒙•辛克有一個簡單但強大的領導模式 , 始於金色的圈子 , 以及他所說的 「 為什麼 」 問題 , 包括蘋果、馬丁•路德•金 , 以及萊特兄弟......
bullseye , business , entrepreneur , leadership , sales , selling , success	bullseye , 商業 , 企業家 , 領導人 , 銷售 , 成功的銷售 ,
simon sinek: how great leaders inspire action	西蒙•史蒂克:偉大的領袖如何激發行動 。
how do you explain when things don't go as we assume ?	你要怎麼解釋當事情不如我們所想的一樣時 ?
or better , how do you explain when others are able to achieve things that seem to defy all of the assumptions ?	或者更好的是 , 你如何解釋當其他人能夠完成似乎違反所有假設的事時 ?
for example: why is apple so innovative ?	例如:為什麼蘋果電腦這麼創新 ?
year after year , after year , after year , they're more innovative than all their competition .	年復一年 , 年復一年 , 他們的創新度比他們所有的競爭對手都要高 。
and yet , they're just a computer company .	然而 , 他們只是個電腦公司 。
they're just like everyone else .	他們和其他人一樣 ,
they have the same access to the same talent , the same agencies , the same consultants , the same media .	他們有著相同的管道接觸同樣的人才 , 同樣的機構 , 同樣的顧問 , 同樣的媒體 。
then why is it that they seem to have something different ?	那為什麼他們似乎有些不同 ?
why is it that martin luther king led the civil rights movement ?	為什麼是馬丁路德金恩領導黑人民權運動 ?
he wasn't the only man who suffered in a precivil rights america , and he certainly wasn't the only great orator of the day .	他不是唯一一個在美國公民權利中受苦的人他肯定不是當時最偉大的演說家
and why is it that the wright brothers were able to figure out controlled , powered man flight when there were certainly other teams who were better qualified , better funded . . .	為什麼萊特兄弟能夠想出控制力量 , 飛行能力很明顯有其他團隊更有資格、更好的資金......
and they didn't achieve powered man flight , and the wright brothers beat them to it .	而他們沒有達成強大的飛行任務 , 萊特兄弟則打敗了他們 。
there's something else at play here .	這裏還有別的東西在玩 。
about three and a half years ago i made a discovery .	大約三年半前 , 我做了一個發現 。
and this discovery profoundly changed my view on how i thought the world worked , and it even profoundly changed the way in which i operate in it .	這個發現深深地改變了我對世界運作方式的看法 , 甚至深深改變了我在其中運作的方式 。
as it turns out , there's a pattern .	結果發現 , 有一種模式
as it turns out , all the great and inspiring leaders and organizations in the world whether it's apple or martin luther king or the wright brothers they all think , act and communicate the exact same way .	結果是 , 所有偉大且具有啟發性的領袖以及世界上的組織 , 不論是蘋果電腦、馬丁路德金恩或萊特兄弟他們都認為 , 採取行動 , 用同樣的方式來溝通 。
and it's the complete opposite to everyone else .	而且完全與其他人相反 。
all i did was codify it , and it's probably the world's simplest idea .	我所做的只是將它編碼 , 而這可能是世界上最簡單的想法 。
i call it the golden circle .	我稱之為黃金圈 。
why ? how ? what ?	為什麼 ? 如何 ? 什麼 ?
this little idea explains why some organizations and some leaders are able to inspire where others aren't .	這個小小的想法解釋了為什麼有些組織和有些領導者能夠激勵別人不在哪裡 。
let me define the terms really quickly .	讓我很快地定義一下名詞 。
every single person , every single organization on the planet knows what they do , 100 percent .	每一個人 , 地球上的每一個組織都知道他們在做什麼 , 百分之百 。
some know how they do it , whether you call it your differentiated value proposition or your proprietary process or your usp .	有些人知道他們怎麼做 , 不論你稱它為不同的價值主張 , 或是你的屬性過程 , 或你的usp 。
but very , very few people or organizations know why they do what they do .	但極少數人或組織 , 知道他們為什麼要做他們的工作 。
and by " why " i don't mean " to make a profit . "	我所謂的 「 為什麼 」 指的並不是 「 為了賺錢 」 。
that's a result . it's always a result .	這就是成果 。 總是成果 。
by " why , " i mean: what's your purpose ?	所謂 「 為什麼 」 , 我的意思是:你的目的是什麼 ?
what's your cause ? what's your belief ?	你的成因是什麼 ? 你的信念是什麼 ?
why does your organization exist ?	為什麼你的組織還存在 ?
why do you get out of bed in the morning ?	為什麼早上要起床 ?
and why should anyone care ?	為什麼有人要在乎 ?
well , as a result , the way we think , the way we act , the way we communicate is from the outside in .	嗯 , 結果是 , 我們思考、行動的方式 , 我們溝通的方式是從外而內的 。
it's obvious . we go from the clearest thing to the fuzziest thing .	很明顯 。 我們從最清楚的變成最模糊的東西 。
but the inspired leaders and the inspired organizations regardless of their size , regardless of their industry all think , act and communicate from the inside out .	但激勵人的領袖和激勵人心的組織不論它們的規模如何 , 不管它們的產業如何從內部去思考、行動與溝通
let me give you an example .	讓我舉個例子 。
i use apple because they're easy to understand and everybody gets it .	我用蘋果電腦是因為它們很容易理解 , 每個人都懂 。
if apple were like everyone else , a marketing message from them might sound like this: " we make great computers .	如果蘋果電腦和其他人一樣 , 來自它們的行銷訊息可能聽起來是這樣的: 「 我們製造出很棒的電腦 。
they're beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	它們設計得很美 , 簡單到可以使用 , 以及使用者友好 。
want to buy one ? " " meh . "	想買一台嗎 ? " 嗯 。 "
and that's how most of us communicate .	這也是我們大多數人溝通的方式 。
that's how most marketing is done , that's how most sales is done and that's how most of us communicate interpersonally .	這就是多數行銷的方式 , 多數業務就是這樣進行的 , 這也是我們多數人與人之間溝通的方式 。
we say what we do , we say how we're different or how we're better and we expect some sort of a behavior , a purchase , a vote , something like that .	我們說我們做了什麼 , 我們說我們如何不同或我們如何比較好 , 我們期待某種行為、購買、投票等等 。
here's our new law firm: we have the best lawyers with the biggest clients , we always perform for our clients who do business with us .	這裡是我們的新法律公司:我們有最好的律師和最大的客戶 , 我們總是在表演 , 為和我們做生意的客戶 。
here's our new car: it gets great gas mileage , it has leather seats , buy our car .	這是我們的新車:它的里程數很大 , 它有皮革製的座椅 , 買我們的車 。
here's how apple actually communicates .	這裡有蘋果電腦實際溝通的方式:
" everything we do , we believe in challenging the status quo .	" 我們所做的一切 , 都相信挑戰現狀
we believe in thinking differently .	我們相信用不同的角度思考
the way we challenge the status quo is by making our products beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	我們挑戰現狀的方式是讓我們的產品有美好的設計、簡單的使用 , 和使用者友好 。
we just happen to make great computers .	我們只是恰巧做出了不起的電腦 。
want to buy one ? "	想買一台嗎 ? 」
totally different right ? you're ready to buy a computer from me .	完全不一樣吧 ? 你準備好向我買一台電腦了 。
all i did was reverse the order of the information .	我所做的 , 只是將資訊的順序反過來 。
what it proves to us is that people don't buy what you do ; people buy why you do it .	它向我們證明的是人們不會買你做什麼 ; 人們買你為什麼做它 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼
this explains why every single person in this room is perfectly comfortable buying a computer from apple .	這解釋了為什麼在座的每一位買一台蘋果電腦的人 , 都很舒服 。
but we're also perfectly comfortable buying an mp3 player from apple , or a phone from apple , or a dvr from apple .	但我們也很完美的買下蘋果電腦的mp3播放器 , 或是蘋果電腦的手機 , 或是蘋果公司的dvr 。
but , as i said before , apple's just a computer company .	但 , 如我之前所說 , 蘋果電腦只是一家電腦公司 。
there's nothing that distinguishes them structurally from any of their competitors .	沒有什麼能把它們在結構上區別開來 , 與它們的競爭者大不相同 。
their competitors are all equally qualified to make all of these products .	他們的競爭者都同樣有資格製造所有這些產品 。
in fact , they tried .	事實上 , 他們試過
a few years ago , gateway came out with flat screen tvs .	幾年前 , gateway推出的平面螢幕電視
they're eminently qualified to make flat screen tvs .	他們很明顯很有資格做平面螢幕電視 。
they've been making flat screen monitors for years .	多年來 , 他們都在做平面螢幕監測 。
dell came out with mp3 players and pdas , and they make great quality products , and they can make perfectly welldesigned products and nobody bought one .	戴爾電腦推出mp3播放器和pda.它們製造出很棒的品質產品 , 它們能製造出完美設計良好的產品 , 沒有人買 。
in fact , talking about it now , we can't even imagine buying an mp3 player from dell .	事實上 , 說到現在 , 我們甚至無法想像從戴爾電腦購買mp3播放器 。
why would you buy an mp3 player from a computer company ?	為什麼你會從電腦公司買一台mp3播放器 ?
but we do it every day .	但我們每天都這麼做 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼
the goal is not to do business with everybody who needs what you have .	目標不是和每個需要你有什麼的人做生意 。
the goal is to do business with people who believe what you believe .	目標是要和那些相信你所相信的人們做生意
here's the best part: none of what i'm telling you is my opinion .	以下是最棒的部分:我告訴各位的都不是我個人的意見 。
it's all grounded in the tenets of biology .	都以生物學的角度為基礎
not psychology , biology .	不是心理學、生物學、
if you look at a crosssection of the human brain , looking from the top down , what you see is the human brain is actually broken into three major components that correlate perfectly with the golden circle .	如果你看人腦的橫切面 , 從上往下看你會看到人腦其實是由三個主要部分組成完美地與黃金圈有關
our newest brain , our homo sapien brain , our neocortex , corresponds with the " what " level .	我們最新的腦 , 我們的智人大腦我們的大腦新皮層對應的是 " 什麼 " 的層次
the neocortex is responsible for all of our rational and analytical thought and language .	大腦新皮質負責我們所有的理性、分析的想法和語言
the middle two sections make up our limbic brains , and our limbic brains are responsible for all of our feelings , like trust and loyalty .	中間兩區構成了我們的邊緣腦 , 我們的邊緣腦負責我們所有的感覺 , 像是信任和忠誠 。
it's also responsible for all human behavior , all decisionmaking , and it has no capacity for language .	它也要為所有人類的行為負責 , 所有的決策 , 而且它沒有語言的能力 。
in other words , when we communicate from the outside in , yes , people can understand vast amounts of complicated information like features and benefits and facts and figures .	換句話說 , 當我們從外而內地溝通時 , 是的 , 人們可以理解大量複雜的資訊 , 像是特徵、受益、事實和數據 。
it just doesn't drive behavior .	它就是不驅動行為 。
when we can communicate from the inside out , we're talking directly to the part of the brain that controls behavior , and then we allow people to rationalize it with the tangible things we say and do .	當我們能由內而外溝通時 , 我們就直接與控制行為的腦對話 , 然後我們讓人們合理化它 , 用我們說的和做的有形的東西 。
this is where gut decisions come from .	這是膽識的由來 。
you know , sometimes you can give somebody all the facts and figures , and they say , " i know what all the facts and details say , but it just doesn't feel right . "	你知道的 , 有時候你可以提供一些事實和數據 , 他們會說: 「 我知道事實和細節說了什麼 , 但那只是感覺不對而已 。 」
why would we use that verb , it doesn't " feel " right ?	為什麼我們會用這個動詞 , 它不會是 「 感覺 」 的 , 對吧 ?
because the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking doesn't control language .	因為控制決策的腦並不能控制語言
and the best we can muster up is , " i don't know . it just doesn't feel right . "	我們最多能整理出的就是: 「 我不知道 , 只是感覺不對 。 」
or sometimes you say you're leading with your heart , or you're leading with your soul .	或者 , 有時你說你帶著你的心引領 , 或者你帶領你的靈魂 。
well , i hate to break it to you , those aren't other body parts controlling your behavior .	嗯 , 我很討厭把它弄壞 , 那些都不是身體的其他部分在控制你的行為 。
it's all happening here in your limbic brain , the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking and not language .	這一切都發生在你的邊緣腦中 , 也就是控制決策而非語言的那個部分 。
but if you don't know why you do what you do , and people respond to why you do what you do , then how will you ever get people to vote for you , or buy something from you , or , more importantly , be loyal and want to be a part of what it is that you do .	但如果你不知道你為什麼做你所做的事 , 大家就會回應你為什麼做你所做的 , 那麼你要如何讓別人投票給你 , 或是從你身上買東西 , 或者 , 更重要的是 , 忠誠一點 , 想要成為你所做的一部分 。
again , the goal is not just to sell to people who need what you have ; the goal is to sell to people who believe what you believe .	再一次 , 目標不是僅僅是賣給需要你才擁有的人 ; 目標是要賣給那些相信你所相信的人們 。
the goal is not just to hire people who need a job ; it's to hire people who believe what you believe .	目標不只是要雇用需要工作的人而是要雇用那些相信你所相信的人們
i always say that , you know , if you hire people just because they can do a job , they'll work for your money , but if you hire people who believe what you believe , they'll work for you with blood and sweat and tears .	我總是這麼說 , 你知道 , 如果你雇用人僅僅是因為他們能做一份工作 , 他們會為了你的錢而工作 , 但如果你雇用那些相信你所相信的事的人 , 他們會為你工作 , 他們會帶著血汗、汗水和淚水 。
and nowhere else is there a better example of this than with the wright brothers .	除此之外 , 沒有別的例子 , 比起萊特兄弟 ,
most people don't know about samuel pierpont langley .	大部分人並不知道samuelpierpontlangley
and back in the early 20th century , the pursuit of powered man flight was like the dot com of the day .	回到二十世紀初 , 追求有權力的人飛行就像今天的網路公司一樣 。
everybody was trying it .	每個人都在嘗試 。
and samuel pierpont langley had , what we assume , to be the recipe for success .	而samuelpierpontlangley曾經擁有 , 我們假設的成功的訣竅是
i mean , even now , you ask people , " why did your product or why did your company fail ? "	我的意思是 , 即使是現在 , 你問人們: 「 為什麼你的產品 , 或是你的公司為什麼失敗 ? 」
and people always give you the same permutation of the same three things: undercapitalized , the wrong people , bad market conditions .	人們總是給你相同的這三樣東西:資金不足、錯誤的人、市場狀況 。
it's always the same three things , so let's explore that .	總是相同的三件事 , 所以我們來探討一下 。
samuel pierpont langley was given 50 , 000 dollars by the war department to figure out this flying machine .	samuelpierpontlangley透過戰爭部門捐了5萬美元來搞清楚這個飛行機器
money was no problem .	錢沒有問題 。
he held a seat at harvard and worked at the smithsonian and was extremely wellconnected ; he knew all the big minds of the day .	他在哈佛任職 , 在史密森尼亞工作 , 且他有非常完善的聯繫 ; 他知道當時所有的大型心靈 。
he hired the best minds money could find and the market conditions were fantastic .	他雇用了最好的思想人才也能找到市場條件很棒 。
the new york times followed him around everywhere , and everyone was rooting for langley .	紐約時報跟著他到處跑 , 每個人都為langley加油 。
then how come we've never heard of samuel pierpont langley ?	為什麼我們從來沒有聽過samuelpierpontlangley ?
a few hundred miles away in dayton ohio , orville and wilbur wright , they had none of what we consider to be the recipe for success .	幾百英哩之外 , 俄亥俄州、奧維爾和威爾伯特萊特 , 他們都沒有我們認為的成功的訣竅 。
they had no money ; they paid for their dream with the proceeds from their bicycle shop ; not a single person on the wright brothers' team had a college education , not even orville or wilbur ; and the new york times followed them around nowhere .	他們沒有錢 , 以腳踏車店的價格支付他們的夢想 ; 沒有一個人在萊特兄弟的團隊中 , 接受大學教育 , 甚至沒有奧維爾或威爾伯 ; 紐約時報跟著他們到處跑 。
the difference was , orville and wilbur were driven by a cause , by a purpose , by a belief .	不同的是 , 奧維爾和威爾伯被一個目的、一個信念所驅使 。
they believed that if they could figure out this flying machine , it'll change the course of the world .	他們相信如果他們能想出這架飛行機器這將改變世界的軌道
samuel pierpont langley was different .	samuelpierpontlangley不同
he wanted to be rich , and he wanted to be famous .	他想變得富有而且他想成名
he was in pursuit of the result .	他在追求結果 。
he was in pursuit of the riches .	他在追求富人時
and lo and behold , look what happened .	然後看 , 看看發生了什麼事 。
the people who believed in the wright brothers' dream worked with them with blood and sweat and tears .	相信萊特兄弟的夢想和他們一起工作的人有血汗、汗水和淚水 。
the others just worked for the paycheck .	另一些人只是為支付費用而工作 。
and they tell stories of how every time the wright brothers went out , they would have to take five sets of parts , because that's how many times they would crash before they came in for supper .	他們說的故事是每次萊特兄弟出門他們就得帶上五套零件因為這是他們出去吃晚餐前會墜機的次數
and , eventually , on december 17th , 1903 , the wright brothers took flight , and no one was there to even experience it .	最後 , 1903年12月17日萊特兄弟起飛 , 根本沒人在那兒經歷這種事 。
we found out about it a few days later .	我們幾天後發現
and further proof that langley was motivated by the wrong thing: the day the wright brothers took flight , he quit .	進一步證明langley是錯的動機那天萊特兄弟起飛了 , 他放棄了
he could have said , " that's an amazing discovery , guys , and i will improve upon your technology , " but he didn't .	他可能會說: 「 各位 , 我會改善你的技術 。 」 但他沒有 。
he wasn't first , he didn't get rich , he didn't get famous so he quit .	他不是第一 , 他沒有變有錢 , 他沒有變有名 , 所以他退出 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼
and if you talk about what you believe , you will attract those who believe what you believe .	如果你談到你所相信的你會吸引到那些相信你所相信的人們
but why is it important to attract those who believe what you believe ?	但為什麼吸引那些相信你所相信的人們很重要 ?
something called the law of diffusion of innovation , and if you don't know the law , you definitely know the terminology .	所謂創新的散播法則 , 如果你不知道這個法則 , 你絕對會知道這個術語 。
the first two and a half percent of our population are our innovators .	我們人口的前2.5%都是我們的創新者 。
the next 13 and a half percent of our population are our early adopters .	接下來的13.5%人口是我們早期的採用者 。
the next 34 percent are your early majority , your late majority and your laggards .	接下來的34%是早期的大多數 , 晚期的大多數以及落後者 。
the only reason these people buy touch tone phones is because you can't buy rotary phones anymore .	這些人買觸控式手機的唯一原因 , 是因為你再也無法購買轉子手機了 。
we all sit at various places at various times on this scale , but what the law of diffusion of innovation tells us is that if you want massmarket success or massmarket acceptance of an idea , you cannot have it until you achieve this tipping point between 15 and 18 percent market penetration , and then the system tips .	我們都位於這個尺度的不同地點 , 但創新的散播法則告訴我們 , 如果你想要大眾市場成功或大眾市場接受一個想法 , 你就不可能擁有它 , 直到你達到百分之十五到百分之十八的市場佔有率 , 然後系統才會開始 。
and i love asking businesses , " what's your conversion on new business ? "	我喜歡問企業: 「 你新企業的轉換是什麼 ? 」
and they love to tell you , " oh , it's about 10 percent , " proudly .	而且他們很喜歡跟你說: 「 喔 , 大概是10%吧 。 」 很驕傲的 。
well , you can trip over 10 percent of the customers .	嗯 , 你可以讓超過百分之十的客戶絆腳 。
we all have about 10 percent who just " get it . "	我們都有大約10%的 「 懂 」 。
that's how we describe them , right ?	這就是我們如何形容他們 , 對吧 ?
that's like that gut feeling , " oh , they just get it . "	就像那種直覺 , 「 噢 , 他們就是懂的 。 」
the problem is: how do you find the ones that get it before you're doing business with them versus the ones who don't get it ?	問題是:如何在你和他們做生意之前 , 找到那些得不到的 ?
so it's this here , this little gap that you have to close , as jeffrey moore calls it , " crossing the chasm " because , you see , the early majority will not try something until someone else has tried it first .	所以就是這個 , 這個小小的差距 , 你必須結束 , 正如jeffreymoore所說的 , " 跨越隔閡 " 因為 , 你看 , 早期的大多數不會嘗試一些事情 , 直到其他人已經先嘗試 。
and these guys , the innovators and the early adopters , they're comfortable making those gut decisions .	而這些人 , 創新者以及早期的採用者 , 他們對做那些腸道的決定感到很自在 。
they're more comfortable making those intuitive decisions that are driven by what they believe about the world and not just what product is available .	他們對做這些直覺的決策感到更自在也就是他們對世界的信念所驅使的 , 而不僅僅是產品可以取得的 。
these are the people who stood in line for six hours to buy an iphone when they first came out , when you could have just walked into the store the next week and bought one off the shelf .	這些是排隊排了六個小時買iphone的人 , 他們第一次出櫃時 , 你可以在下一週走進店裡買一部在架上買一部 。
these are the people who spent 40 , 000 dollars on flat screen tvs when they first came out , even though the technology was substandard .	這些是花4萬美元在平面螢幕電視上的人 , 剛上市的時候 , 儘管當時的科技是次要的 。
and , by the way , they didn't do it because the technology was so great ; they did it for themselves .	而且 , 順帶一提 , 他們這麼做並不是因為這項科技如此偉大他們這麼做是為了他們自己
it's because they wanted to be first .	是因為他們想先
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it and what you do simply proves what you believe .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼做 , 以及你做什麼就證明了你相信什麼 。
in fact , people will do the things that prove what they believe .	事實上 , 人們會去做證明他們所相信的事 。
the reason that person bought the iphone in the first six hours , stood in line for six hours , was because of what they believed about the world , and how they wanted everybody to see them: they were first .	那個人買iphone在前六個小時排隊排六個小時 , 是因為他們所相信的世界 , 以及他們希望每個人如何看待他們:他們是第一個 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼
so let me give you a famous example , a famous failure and a famous success of the law of diffusion of innovation .	讓我舉一個有名的例子 , 一個有名的失敗以及一個有名的成功關於創新法則的散播 。
first , the famous failure .	第一 , 知名的失敗 。
it's a commercial example .	這是個商業的例子 。
as we said before , a second ago , the recipe for success is money and the right people and the right market conditions , right ? you should have success then .	正如我們之前所說 , 一秒鐘前成功的方案就是金錢和對的人以及對的市場狀況 , 對嗎 ? 你應該要那樣成功 。
from the time tivo came out about eight or nine years ago to this current day , they are the single highestquality product on the market , hands down , there is no dispute .	從tivo上市時間大約是八、九年前到現在 , 它們是市場上唯一高品質的產品 , 手下來 , 沒有爭議 。
they were extremely wellfunded .	他們獲得很好的資金 。
market conditions were fantastic .	市場的狀況很棒 。
i mean , we use tivo as verb .	我的意思是 , 我們用tivo當動詞
i tivo stuff on my piece of junk time warner dvr all the time .	我常常在垃圾之中tivo東西放在dvr上
but tivo's a commercial failure .	但tivo卻是個商業上的失敗者
they've never made money .	他們從來沒有賺過錢 。
and when they went ipo , their stock was at about 30 or 40 dollars and then plummeted , and it's never traded above 10 .	當他們上ipo公司時 , 他們的股價約30到40美元 , 接著跌倒 , 從沒在10美元以上交易 。
in fact , i don't think it's even traded above six , except for a couple of little spikes .	事實上 , 我不認為它會在6以上進行交易 , 除了幾項小漲幅 。
because you see , when tivo launched their product they told us all what they had .	因為你看 , 當tivo推出他們的產品他們告訴我們他們有的是什麼
they said , " we have a product that pauses live tv , skips commercials , rewinds live tv and memorizes your viewing habits without you even asking . "	他們說: 「 我們有一個可以暫停現場電視的產品 , 跳過商業廣告 , 倒帶一下現場電視 , 記下你的收視習慣 , 連問都不問 。 」
and the cynical majority said , " we don't believe you .	憤世嫉俗的多數人說: 「 我們不相信你 。
we don't need it . we don't like it .	我們不需要 , 我們不喜歡 。
you're scaring us . "	你嚇壞了我們 。 」
what if they had said , " if you're the kind of person who likes to have total control over every aspect of your life , boy , do we have a product for you .	如果他們說: 「 如果你是那種喜歡完全掌控生活各個層面的人 , 那我們有給你的產品 。
it pauses live tv , skips commercials , memorizes your viewing habits , etc . , etc . "	它會暫停現場電視、跳過商業廣告、記下你的收視習慣等等 。 」
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it , and what you do simply serves as the proof of what you believe .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你為什麼做 , 而你所做的就只是證明你相信什麼 。
now let me give you a successful example of the law of diffusion of innovation .	現在讓我給你們一個成功的例子關於創新法則的擴散法則 。
in the summer of 1963 , 250 , 000 people showed up on the mall in washington to hear dr . king speak .	在1963年夏天 , 二十五萬人出現在華盛頓的廣場上 , 聽金恩博士的演說 。
they sent out no invitations , and there was no website to check the date .	他們沒有寄出任何邀請函而當時也沒有網站去查看日期
how do you do that ?	怎麼做呢 ?
well , dr . king wasn't the only man in america who was a great orator .	金恩博士不是美國唯一一個偉大的演說家 ,
he wasn't the only man in america who suffered in a precivil rights america .	他不是在美國唯一一個受到不公平待遇的美國人 。
in fact , some of his ideas were bad .	事實上 , 他的一些想法很爛 。
but he had a gift .	但他有一個禮物 。
he didn't go around telling people what needed to change in america .	他沒有到處告訴人們在美國什麼需要改變 。
he went around and told people what he believed .	他到處告訴人們他所相信的
" i believe , i believe , i believe , " he told people .	「 我相信 , 我相信 , 我相信 , 」 他告訴人們 ,
and people who believed what he believed took his cause , and they made it their own , and they told people .	而那些相信他所相信的人們將他的理想化 , 成為他們自己的理想 , 並且告訴人們 ,
and some of those people created structures to get the word out to even more people .	而其中一些人創造了結構 , 讓這個字能傳遞出去給更多人 。
and lo and behold , 250 , 000 people showed up on the right day at the right time to hear him speak .	另外 , 二十五萬人在對的日子出現 , 聽他說話 。
how many of them showed up for him ?	有多少人為了他而出現 ?
they showed up for themselves .	他們為了自己而現身 。
it's what they believed about america that got them to travel in a bus for eight hours to stand in the sun in washington in the middle of august .	這是他們所相信的美國讓他們坐了八小時的巴士穿梭於八月中間在華盛頓的陽光下穿梭
it's what they believed , and it wasn't about black versus white: 25 percent of the audience was white .	這是他們所相信的 , 這不是關於黑人與白人25%的觀眾是白人 。
dr . king believed that there are two types of laws in this world: those that are made by a higher authority and those that are made by man .	金恩博士相信在這個世界上有兩種不同的法律那些由較高權威制定的法律和那些由人類所定的法律
and not until all the laws that are made by man are consistent with the laws that are made by the higher authority will we live in a just world .	直到所有由人類所定的法律都與由更高權威制定的法律一致時 , 我們才會活在一個公正的世界 。
it just so happened that the civil rights movement was the perfect thing to help him bring his cause to life .	剛好 , 民權運動就是最完美的幫助他將自己的理想帶入生活 。
we followed , not for him , but for ourselves .	我們跟隨 , 不是為了他 , 而是為了我們自己 。
and , by the way , he gave the " i have a dream " speech , not the " i have a plan " speech .	順帶一提 , 他給了這個 「 我有一個夢想 」 演講而不是 「 我有一個計畫 」 演講 。
listen to politicians now , with their comprehensive 12point plans .	聽現在的政治人物 , 有著他們全面性的12點計畫 。
they're not inspiring anybody .	他們沒有激勵任何人 。
because there are leaders and there are those who lead .	因為有領導者和領導者
leaders hold a position of power or authority , but those who lead inspire us .	領導者持有權力或權威的位置 , 但那些領導的人啟發我們 。
whether they're individuals or organizations , we follow those who lead , not because we have to , but because we want to .	不論是個人或組織 , 我們會追隨那些領導的人 , 不是因為我們必須 , 而是因為我們想要 。
we follow those who lead , not for them , but for ourselves .	我們跟隨那些領導的人 , 不是為了他們 , 而是為了我們自己 。
and it's those who start with " why " that have the ability to inspire those around them or find others who inspire them .	正是那些以 「 為什麼 」 開始的人有能力去啟發他們周圍的人 , 或是去找啟發他們的人 。
how do you remember where you parked your car ? how do you know if you're moving in the right direction ? neuroscientist neil burgess studies the neural mechanisms that map the space around us , and how they link to memory and imagination .	你怎麼還記得你把車子停在哪裡 ? 你怎麼知道你是朝正確的方向前進 ? 神經科學家尼爾•內爾研究出描繪我們周圍空間的神經機制 , 以及它們如何與記憶、想像力緊密相連 。
brain , cognitive science , exploration , neuroscience , science	大腦、認知科學、探索神經科學、科學
neil burgess: how your brain tells you where you are	neilburges:你的大腦如何告訴你你現在所在的位置 。
when we park in a big parking lot , how do we remember where we parked our car ?	當我們停在一個大停車場 , 我們如何記得我們車子停在哪裡 ?
here's the problem facing homer .	荷馬面臨的問題是:
and we're going to try to understand what's happening in his brain .	然後我們會試著去了解他的大腦發生了什麼事 。
so we'll start with the hippocampus , shown in yellow , which is the organ of memory .	所以 , 我們先從海馬迴開始 , 以黃色標示 , 也就是記憶的器官 。
if you have damage there , like in alzheimer's , you can't remember things including where you parked your car .	如果你有所損傷 , 像是阿茲海默症你會記不得東西包括你把車子停在那裡
it's named after latin for " seahorse , " which it resembles .	它的名字是拉丁文中的 「 海馬 」 , 和它的 「 海馬 」 。
and like the rest of the brain , it's made of neurons .	和大腦的其他部分一樣 , 它是由神經元細胞組成的 。
so the human brain has about a hundred billion neurons in it .	所以人腦內有大約一千億個神經元
and the neurons communicate with each other by sending little pulses or spikes of electricity via connections to each other .	神經元會互相交流藉由發送小脈衝或帶電的突波會透過彼此連結
the hippocampus is formed of two sheets of cells , which are very densely interconnected .	海馬體是由兩片細胞間非常緊密的連結組成
and scientists have begun to understand how spatial memory works by recording from individual neurons in rats or mice while they forage or explore an environment looking for food .	科學家們已經開始了解到空間記憶是如何運作的藉由記錄老鼠在尋找食物時的個別神經元或老鼠們
so we're going to imagine we're recording from a single neuron in the hippocampus of this rat here .	所以我們會想像我們記錄一個單一神經元在這隻老鼠的海馬體內 。
and when it fires a little spike of electricity , there's going to be a red dot and a click .	當它發出一個電的突波 , 將會有一個紅點和一個點 。
so what we see is that this neuron knows whenever the rat has gone into one particular place in its environment .	所以我們可以看到 , 這個神經元知道老鼠何時進入某一個特定的環境 。
and it signals to the rest of the brain by sending a little electrical spike .	藉由發送電的突波 , 訊號傳送到大腦的其他部分 。
so we could show the firing rate of that neuron as a function of the animal's location .	所以我們可以將神經元的發射率作為動物所在位置的函數 。
and if we record from lots of different neurons , we'll see that different neurons fire when the animal goes in different parts of its environment , like in this square box shown here .	如果我們從許多不同的神經元中紀錄我們會發現當動物進入週遭環境的不同區域時 , 不同的神經元會發出訊號 , 就像這個方盒顯示的那樣 。
so together they form a map for the rest of the brain , telling the brain continually , " where am i now within my environment ? "	所以他們一起 , 組成一張大腦的地圖 , 持續告訴大腦: 「 我現在在我的環境中的哪裡 ? 」
place cells are also being recorded in humans .	位置細胞也被紀錄在人類身上 。
so epilepsy patients sometimes need the electrical activity in their brain monitoring .	所以癲癇患者有時需要腦部監測的電子活動 。
and some of these patients played a video game where they drive around a small town .	有些病患會玩一個電玩遊戲讓他們在一個小城內開車閒晃
and place cells in their hippocampi would fire , become active , start sending electrical impulses whenever they drove through a particular location in that town .	當他們開車經過一個小鎮時 , 身體裡的位置細胞會發出活力 , 開始發出電子脈衝 。
so how does a place cell know where the rat or person is within its environment ?	那麼一個地方細胞如何得知老鼠或人的環境在哪裡呢 ?
well these two cells here show us that the boundaries of the environment are particularly important .	這裡的這兩個細胞告訴我們環境的界限特別重要 。
so the one on the top likes to fire sort of midway between the walls of the box that their rat's in .	上方那張圖顯示老鼠在兩面牆之間的中央情形
and when you expand the box , the firing location expands .	而當你將箱子擴張時 , 發射位置就會擴張 。
the one below likes to fire whenever there's a wall close by to the south .	下面的這個則喜歡發射每當有一面牆靠近南方 ,
and if you put another wall inside the box , then the cell fires in both place wherever there's a wall to the south as the animal explores around in its box .	如果你在盒子裡放另一道牆 , 那麼細胞在兩個地方都會發射一道牆 , 當動物在箱子裡探索時 , 會向南方移動 。
so this predicts that sensing the distances and directions of boundaries around you extended buildings and so on is particularly important for the hippocampus .	所以這可以預測 , 去感知你周圍的界線和方向 , 延伸建築物等等的距離 , 對於海馬體是特別重要的 。
and indeed , on the inputs to the hippocampus , cells are found which project into the hippocampus , which do respond exactly to detecting boundaries or edges at particular distances and directions from the rat or mouse as it's exploring around .	的確 , 在海馬體的輸入上 , 發現海馬體的細胞 , 海馬體是哪個項目 , 海馬體的確會在特定的距離或邊緣上有特定的距離和方向 , 從老鼠或老鼠的四處移動 。
so the cell on the left , you can see , it fires whenever the animal gets near to a wall or a boundary to the east , whether it's the edge or the wall of a square box or the circular wall of the circular box or even the drop at the edge of a table , which the animals are running around .	所以左邊的細胞你可以看到 , 任何時候動物都會被激發到接近牆壁或是東邊的界線 , 不論是方形盒子的邊緣或是圓形的牆 , 甚至是桌子的邊緣 , 動物都在四處奔跑 。
and the cell on the right there fires whenever there's a boundary to the south , whether it's the drop at the edge of the table or a wall or even the gap between two tables that are pulled apart .	那裡右邊的細胞當有一條界線向南移動時 , 無論是桌邊或是牆邊的邊緣或是兩張桌子的縫隙都會被拉開 。
so that's one way in which we think place cells determine where the animal is as it's exploring around .	這是其中一個方法 , 我們認為位置細胞可以決定動物所在的方位 。
we can also test where we think objects are , like this goal flag , in simple environments or indeed , where your car would be .	我們也可以測試我們認為物品的位置 , 像是這個目標旗子 , 在簡單的環境中 , 或者說 , 你的車子會在哪裡 。
so we can have people explore an environment and see the location they have to remember .	所以 , 我們可以讓人們探索一個環境 , 看到他們必須記得的地點 。
and then , if we put them back in the environment , generally they're quite good at putting a marker down where they thought that flag or their car was .	接著 , 如果我們把它們放回環境中 , 一般來說 , 它們非常擅長放一個標記下來 , 讓他們以為那面旗子或車子是哪裡 。
but on some trials , we could change the shape and size of the environment like we did with the place cell .	但在一些試驗中 , 我們可以改變環境的形狀和大小 , 就像我們對位置細胞所做的一樣 。
in that case , we can see how where they think the flag had been changes as a function of how you change the shape and size of the environment .	在那樣的情況下 , 我們可以看到他們認為旗幟位置的改變是如何改變環境的形狀和大小的改變 。
and what you see , for example , if the flag was where that cross was in a small square environment , and then if you ask people where it was , but you've made the environment bigger , where they think the flag had been stretches out in exactly the same way that the place cell firing stretched out .	舉例來說 , 如果國旗處在一個小方形的環境中 , 然後如果你問人們那裡的位置 , 但你讓環境變大了 , 他們認為國旗的位置和位置細胞被激發的地方差不多 。
it's as if you remember where the flag was by storing the pattern of firing across all of your place cells at that location , and then you can get back to that location by moving around so that you best match the current pattern of firing of your place cells with that stored pattern .	這就好像你還記得旗幟的所在位置 , 藉由在那個位置的位置細胞把激發的模式儲存起來 , 然後你就可以藉由四處移動 , 回到那個位置 , 這樣你就可以把目前位置細胞激發出來的模式與儲存的模式去匹配 。
that guides you back to the location that you want to remember .	引導你回到你想記住的地點 。
but we also know where we are through movement .	但我們也知道 , 透過運動 , 我們在哪裡 。
so if we take some outbound path perhaps we park and we wander off we know because our own movements , which we can integrate over this path roughly what the heading direction is to go back .	所以如果我們能停車或離開我們知道的路徑 , 是因為我們自己的動作 , 我們可以整合這條路徑 , 大約是前進的方向 。
and place cells also get this kind of path integration input from a kind of cell called a grid cell .	位置細胞也會從一個叫做 「 網格細胞 」 的細胞中得到這種整合 。
now grid cells are found , again , on the inputs to the hippocampus , and they're a bit like place cells .	網格細胞也發現海馬的輸入有點像位置細胞
but now as the rat explores around , each individual cell fires in a whole array of different locations which are laid out across the environment in an amazingly regular triangular grid .	但當老鼠四處移動時 , 各個細胞激發一系列不同的位置 , 呈現在整個環境中 , 呈現出驚人的正常三角形格狀 。
and if you record from several grid cells shown here in different colors each one has a gridlike firing pattern across the environment , and each cell's gridlike firing pattern is shifted slightly relative to the other cells .	如果你紀錄數個網格細胞以不同的顏色標示每個細胞對環境都有網格狀激發模式每個細胞的網格激發模式會相對於其他細胞則會有些微的改變
so the red one fires on this grid and the green one on this one and the blue on on this one .	紅色的會在這個格子上發射還有綠色的 , 藍色的在這個格子上 。
so together , it's as if the rat can put a virtual grid of firing locations across its environment a bit like the latitude and longitude lines that you'd find on a map , but using triangles .	所以 , 把這隻老鼠放在一起 , 就好像這隻老鼠可以放入一個虛擬的網格 , 跨越牠所在環境的發射位置 , 有點像是在地圖上所找到的緯度和長度線 , 但用的是三角形 。
and as it moves around , the electrical activity can pass from one of these cells to the next cell to keep track of where it is , so that it can use its own movements to know where it is in its environment .	隨著它四處移動 , 電流從其中一個細胞傳到下一個細胞 , 以保持追蹤位置 , 讓它可以用自己的移動來知道它在環境中的位置 。
do people have grid cells ?	人們有網格細胞嗎 ?
well because all of the gridlike firing patterns have the same axes of symmetry , the same orientations of grid , shown in orange here , it means that the net activity of all of the grid cells in a particular part of the brain should change according to whether we're running along these six directions or running along one of the six directions in between .	因為所有網格激發的對稱性都有相同的對稱軸 , 同樣的網格定位 , 在這裡以橘色顯示 , 這表示網格細胞的網格活動 , 在特定的區域 , 會根據我們是否沿這六個方向運行 , 或在中間的六個方向之一運作 。
so we can put people in an mri scanner and have them do a little video game like the one i showed you and look for this signal .	所以 , 我們可以把人放進磁共振成像掃描儀 , 讓他們玩一個小遊戲 , 像我剛剛給你們看的那種 , 去尋找這個信號 。
and indeed , you do see it in the human entorhinal cortex , which is the same part of the brain that you see grid cells in rats .	的確 , 你確實在人體內看到的是同一區域的網格細胞在老鼠腦內
so back to homer .	回到荷馬 。
he's probably remembering where his car was in terms of the distances and directions to extended buildings and boundaries around the location where he parked .	他可能還記得他的車子在哪裡 , 前進的距離和方向 , 是要把建築和界線延伸到他停車的地方 。
and that would be represented by the firing of boundarydetecting cells .	可以用邊界偵測細胞的方式來呈現 。
he's also remembering the path he took out of the car park , which would be represented in the firing of grid cells .	他也記得他從汽車公園拿出來的路徑 , 圖中以網格細胞激發的方式呈現 。
now both of these kinds of cells can make the place cells fire .	這兩種細胞都可以讓位置細胞被激發
and he can return to the location where he parked by moving so as to find where it is that best matches the firing pattern of the place cells in his brain currently with the stored pattern where he parked his car .	他可以藉由移動找到他正在停車的位置 , 找到目前位置和他大腦中儲存的位置並以儲存模式回歸位置 。
and that guides him back to that location irrespective of visual cues like whether his car's actually there .	這就引導他回到那個位置--不重視視視覺提示--比如他車子是否真的存在 。
maybe it's been towed .	可能已經被壓住了 。
but he knows where it was , so he knows to go and get it .	但他知道它在哪裡 , 所以他知道要去哪就得到它 。
so beyond spatial memory , if we look for this gridlike firing pattern throughout the whole brain , we see it in a whole series of locations which are always active when we do all kinds of autobiographical memory tasks , like remembering the last time you went to a wedding , for example .	除了空間記憶之外 , 如果我們觀察這個網格般激發模式在整個腦內 , 我們會看到它在一系列的位置 , 當我們在進行各種自傳記憶任務時 , 總是很活躍的 , 比如說你上次參加婚禮時 。
so it may be that the neural mechanisms for representing the space around us are also used for generating visual imagery so that we can recreate the spatial scene , at least , of the events that have happened to us when we want to imagine them .	所以這可能是神經機制 , 代表我們周圍的空間 , 也被用來產生視覺影像 , 如此一來 , 我們可以重新創造空間場景 , 至少 , 在我們想要想像的時候 , 發生在我們身上的事件 。
so if this was happening , your memories could start by place cells activating each other via these dense interconnections and then reactivating boundary cells to create the spatial structure of the scene around your viewpoint .	所以如果發生了這種情況 , 你的記憶就會開始於細胞藉由這些密集的介質激活彼此 , 然後重新啟動了界線細胞 , 創造出你所看到的景象周圍的空間結構 。
and grid cells could move this viewpoint through that space .	而網格細胞可以透過那個空間來移動這個視角 。
another kind of cell , head direction cells , which i didn't mention yet , they fire like a compass according to which way you're facing .	另外一種我還沒有提到的細胞頭向細胞 , 它們就像指南針一樣根據你們所面對的情況激發 。
they could define the viewing direction from which you want to generate an image for your visual imagery , so you can imagine what happened when you were at this wedding , for example .	它們可以定義視覺的方向 , 讓你想要產生一個影像 , 來呈現你的視覺影像 , 所以你可以想像你在這個婚禮時發生了什麼事 , 比如 。
so this is just one example of a new era really in cognitive neuroscience where we're beginning to understand psychological processes like how you remember or imagine or even think in terms of the actions of the billions of individual neurons that make up our brains .	這只是認知神經科學中一個新時代的例子 , 我們開始了解心理學過程 , 像是你如何記得、想像 , 甚至是思考 , 大腦中數十億個神經元的動作 。
thank you very much .	謝謝大家 。
imagine a global security driven by collaboration among agencies , government , the private sector and the public . that's not just the distant hope of opensource fans , it's the vision of james stavridis , the supreme commander of nato , who shares vivid moments from recent military history to explain why security of the future should be built with bridges rather than walls .	想像一個由各方機構、政府、私營機構和民眾共同驅動的全球安全 。 那不僅僅是來自遠方的開放電扇的希望 , 詹姆斯•斯塔迪斯的遠景 , 北約的最高指揮官 , 他在近期的軍事歷史中分享了生存的時刻 , 解釋了為什麼未來的安全應該是用橋樑而不是牆建造起來的 。
collaboration , global issues , opensource , peace , politics , social media , violence , war	合作、全球性議題、開放性議題、和平、政治、社群媒體、暴力、戰爭 。
james stavridis: how nato's supreme commander thinks about global security	詹姆斯•斯塔維迪斯:北約的最高指揮官如何看待全球安全 ?
i'm gonna talk a little bit about opensource security , because we've got to get better at security in this 21st century .	我會稍微談一談開放資源的安全性 , 因為我們在這21世紀已經有了更好的安全性 。
let me start by saying , let's look back to the 20th century , and kind of get a sense of how that style of security worked for us .	讓我先回顧一下20世紀吧 , 稍微了解一下安全的運作方式 。
this is verdun , a battlefield in france just north of the nato headquarters in belgium .	這是verdun , 一個法國的戰場 , 就在北約在比利時總部的北邊 。
at verdun , in 1916 , over a 300day period , 700 , 000 people were killed , so about 2 , 000 a day .	在verdun , 1916年 , 在一個三百天的時期 , 有七十萬人被殺 , 所以差不多有兩千人一天 。
if you roll it forward 20thcentury security into the second world war , you see the battle of stalingrad , 300 days , 2 million people killed .	如果你將它向前推進二十世紀的安全性進入第二次世界大戰 , 你會看到史達林升級的戰役 , 300天 , 2百萬人被殺 。
we go into the cold war , and we continue to try and build walls .	我們進入冷戰 , 繼續建造圍牆 。
we go from the trench warfare of the first world war to the maginot line of the second world war , and then we go into the cold war , the iron curtain , the berlin wall .	我們從第一次世界大戰的壕溝 , 到第二次世界大戰的馬蓋諾線 , 然後進入冷戰 , 鐵幕 , 柏林圍牆 。
my thesis for us today is , instead of building walls to create security , we need to build bridges .	我今天的主題是 , 與其築起圍牆來創造安全 , 我們需要建造橋樑 。
this is a famous bridge in europe .	這是歐洲有名的橋 。
it's the bridge over the drina river , the subject of a novel by ivo andrić , and it talks about how , in that very troubled part of europe and the balkans , over time there's been enormous building of walls .	這座橋在drina河上 , 由ivo和rikk的小說主題 , 它談到如何在歐洲和巴爾幹半島上 , 隨著時間流逝 , 歐洲和巴爾幹半島有著巨大的建築物 。
more recently , in the last decade , we begin to see these communities start , hesitatingly , to come together .	最近 , 在近十年 , 我們開始看到這些社區開始 , 猶豫不決地 , 團結起來 。
i would argue , again , opensource security is about connecting the international , the interagency , the privatepublic , and lashing it together with strategic communication , largely in social networks .	我會再次強調 , 開放式安全是關連國際、跨部門、私人和公共事業 , 並且將它與策略性溝通結合 , 大多是在社交網中 。
so let me talk a little bit about why we need to do that , because our global commons is under attack in a variety of ways , and none of the sources of threat to the global commons will be solved by building walls .	所以 , 讓我來談談為什麼我們需要這麼做 , 因為我們的全球公有物正在以各種方式攻擊 , 且對全球公有物的威脅都不會因為建造圍牆而受到威脅 。
now , i'm a sailor , obviously .	現在 , 我很明顯是個水手 。
this is a ship , a liner , clipping through the indian ocean .	這是一艘船 , 直線 , 橫越印度洋 。
what's wrong with this picture ?	這張照片有什麼問題 ?
it's got concertina wire along the sides of it .	沿著它的兩側上面有協奏曲線 。
that's to prevent pirates from attacking it .	也就是避免海盜襲擊它
piracy is a very active threat today around the world . this is in the indian ocean .	盜版是當今全世界都很活躍的威脅 。 這是在印度洋 。
piracy is also very active in the strait of malacca .	海盜也在馬拉加的海峽非常活躍 。
it's active in the gulf of guinea .	在幾內亞灣活躍了起來
we see it in the caribbean .	我們在加勒比海看到的
it's a $10billionayear discontinuity in the global transport system .	在全球交通運輸系統中 , 每年造成一百億美元的損失 。
last year , at this time , there were 20 vessels , 500 mariners held hostage .	去年 , 當時有20艘船 , 500名船員被挾持著 。
this is an attack on the global commons .	這是對全球公有物的攻擊 。
we need to think about how to address it .	我們需要考慮如何去處理
let's shift to a different kind of sea , the cyber sea .	讓我們轉換到另一種海洋 , 網絡海洋 。
here are photographs of two young men .	這裡有兩位年輕男子的照片 。
at the moment , they're incarcerated .	在此刻 , 他們被監禁著 。
they conducted a credit card fraud that netted them over 10 billion dollars .	他們進行了信用卡詐欺 , 還用了超過一百億美金 。
this is part of cybercrime which is a $2trillionayear discontinuity in the global economy .	這是全球經濟不連續2兆美元的網路犯罪部分 。
two trillion a year .	一年兩兆 。
that's just under the gdp of great britain .	這只是在英國的gdp底下
so this cyber sea , which we know endlessly is the fundamental piece of radical openness , is very much under threat as well .	這個我們所知無止盡的是激進開放的基本面向 , 也受到威脅 。
another thing i worry about in the global commons is the threat posed by trafficking , by the movement of narcotics , opium , here coming out of afghanistan through europe over to the united states .	全球公有物讓我擔心的另一件事 , 就是販賣的威脅 , 麻醉劑的移動 , 鴉片等 , 從阿富汗穿過歐洲到達美國 。
we worry about cocaine coming from the andean ridge north .	我們擔心從andeanridge北部運過來的可卡因 。
we worry about the movement of illegal weapons and trafficking . above all , perhaps , we worry about human trafficking , and the awful cost of it .	我們擔心非法武器的運輸和販賣的移動 。 最重要的是 , 我們擔心的是人口販賣 , 以及它的糟糕代價 。
trafficking moves largely at sea but in other parts of the global commons .	人口販賣主要是在海上遷移 , 但在全球公有物的其他地方 。
this is a photograph , and i wish i could tell you that this is a very hightech piece of us navy gear that we're using to stop the trafficking .	這是一張照片 , 我希望我能告訴你們這是一塊非常高科技的美國海軍陸戰隊用來停止販賣 。
the bad news is , this is a semisubmersible run by drug cartels .	壞消息是 , 這是一個販毒集團的半潛水器 。
it was built in the jungles of south america .	在南美洲的叢林中被建造出來 。
we caught it with that lowtech raft — — and it was carrying six tons of cocaine .	我們用那個低科技的竹筏逮到它 , 它帶著六噸的可卡因 。
crew of four . sophisticated communications sweep .	四個船員 , 精密的通訊全部掃過了 ,
this kind of trafficking , in narcotics , in humans , in weapons , god forbid , in weapons of mass destruction , is part of the threat to the global commons .	這種販賣 , 在毒品、在人身上、在武器上、在上帝面前被禁止使用大規模毀滅性的武器 , 是全球公有物的威脅之一 。
and let's pull it together in afghanistan today .	讓我們一起在今天的阿富汗 。
this is a field of poppies in afghanistan .	這是阿富汗的一片餅乾 。
eighty to 90 percent of the world's poppy , opium and heroin , comes out of afghanistan .	全世界80%到90%的大便、鴉片和海洛因來自阿富汗 。
we also see there , of course , terrorism .	我們也看到了 , 當然 , 恐怖主義
this is where al qaeda is staged from .	這是基地組織的由來 。
we also see a very strong insurgency embedded there .	我們也看到了一個很強烈的暴動就嵌在那兒 。
so this terrorism concern is also part of the global commons , and what we must address .	所以這種恐怖主義也是全球公有的一部分 , 我們必須要處理的 ,
so here we are , 21st century .	所以 , 在這裡 , 21世紀
we know our 20thcentury tools are not going to work .	我們知道我們20世紀的工具是行不通的 。
what should we do ?	我們應該怎麼做 ?
i would argue that we will not deliver security solely from the barrel of a gun .	我認為我們不能僅僅依靠槍支來傳遞安全 。
we will not deliver security solely from the barrel of a gun .	我們不能僅僅從槍口的桶子裡獲得安全遞送 。
we will need the application of military force .	我們將需要軍事力量的應用 。
when we do it , we must do it well , and competently .	當我們實行的時候 , 我們必須好好地做 , 而且要有能力 。
but my thesis is , opensource security is about international , interagency , privatepublic connection pulled together by this idea of strategic communication on the internet .	但我的論點是 , 開放式安全是關乎國際 , 跨部門 , 私人和公共的聯系 , 被這個關於網際網路戰略的思想所拉扯在一起 。
let me give you a couple of examples of how this works in a positive way .	讓我舉幾個例子來說明這如何以一個正面的方式進行 。
this is afghanistan . these are afghan soldiers .	這是阿富汗 。 這些是阿富汗士兵 。
they are all holding books .	他們都拿著書 。
you should say , " that's odd . i thought i read that this demographic , young men and women in their 20s and 30s , is largely illiterate in afghanistan . "	你應該說 , " 這太奇怪了 。 我想我讀到在這個人口 , 二十、三十幾歲的年輕男女在阿富汗是不識字的 。 "
you would be correct .	你會是對的 。
eightyfive percent cannot read when they enter the security forces of afghanistan .	85%的人進入阿富汗的安全部隊時無法閱讀 。
